when you say she's a programmer , she did do some , but the real thing is to have said the future is going to be much , much more than this .	當你說她是程式設計師時 , 她做了一些事 , 但真正的一件事是 , 說未來將會比這個更加重要 。
now , a hundred years later , this guy comes along , alan turing , and in 1936 , and invents the computer all over again .	一百年後 , 這傢伙來了 , 艾倫•圖靈在1936年發明了一台電腦 。
now , of course , babbage's machine was entirely mechanical .	當然 , babbage的機器是完全機械的 。
turing's machine was entirely theoretical .	turing的機器完全是理論的 。
both of these guys were coming from a mathematical perspective , but turing told us something very important .	這兩個人都來自數學的觀點 , 但 , 圖靈告訴我們一件很重要的事 。
he laid down the mathematical foundations for computer science , and said , " it doesn't matter how you make a computer . "	他為電腦科學奠定了數學基礎 , 說: 「 不論你如何製作電腦 。 」
it doesn't matter if your computer's mechanical , like babbage's was , or electronic , like computers are today , or perhaps in the future , cells , or , again , mechanical again , once we get into nanotechnology .	不管你電腦的機械機械 , 像是babbage , 或電子產品 , 如今 , 或未來的電腦 , 或者 , 細胞 , 或者 , 再一次 , 一旦我們進入奈米科技 。
we could go back to babbage's machine and just make it tiny . all those things are computers .	我們可以回到babbage的機器 , 讓它變小 。 所有這些東西都是電腦 。
there is in a sense a computing essence .	在某種意義上 , 電腦的本質是如此 。
this is called the church–turing thesis .	這叫做教堂繪製論文 。
and so suddenly , you get this link where you say this thing babbage had built really was a computer .	所以 , 突然間 , 你得到了這個連結 , 你說這東西babbage已經建造了一台電腦 。
in fact , it was capable of doing everything we do today with computers , only really slowly .	事實上 , 它能夠做到今天我們用電腦做所有的事情 , 只是慢慢地 。
to give you an idea of how slowly , it had about 1k of memory .	為了讓你們知道 , 記憶有多慢 。
it used punch cards , which were being fed in , and it ran about 10 , 000 times slower the first zx81 .	它用了打孔卡 , 被放進去 , 它的第一個zx81 , 000倍慢了一萬倍 。
it did have a ram pack .	它的確有一包ram包 。
you could add on a lot of extra memory if you wanted to .	如果你想的話 , 你可以加上額外的記憶 。
so , where does that bring us today ?	那麼 , 今天我們要怎麼做呢 ?
so there are plans .	這裡有計畫 。
over in swindon , the science museum archives , there are hundreds of plans and thousands of pages of notes written by charles babbage about this analytical engine .	在瑞典 , 科學博物館的檔案中 , 有數百個計劃和數千頁的筆記 , 由查爾斯巴貝奇所寫的 , 關於這個分析引擎 。
one of those is a set of plans that we call plan 28 , and that is also the name of a charity that i started with doron swade , who was the curator of computing at the science museum , and also the person who drove the project to build a difference engine , and our plan is to build it .	其中一組計劃我們稱之為計劃28 , 這也是我從doronswaade開始的慈善機構的名字 , 他是科學博物館的策展人 , 開著這個計劃來建造一個差異引擎的人 , 我們的計劃是要建造它 。
here in south kensington , we will build the analytical engine .	在南肯辛頓這裡 , 我們將建造分析引擎 。
the project has a number of parts to it .	這個計畫有許多部分 。
one was the scanning of babbage's archive .	其中一個是babbage的檔案 。
that's been done . the second is now the study of all of those plans to determine what to build .	這已經完成了 。 第二個是研究這些計畫的目的 , 來決定要建造什麼 。
the third part is a computer simulation of that machine , and the last part is to physically build it at the science museum .	第三部分是電腦模擬這台機器的模擬 , 最後一部分是要在科學博物館實體建造它 。
when it's built , you'll finally be able to understand how a computer works , because rather than having a tiny chip in front of you , you've got to look at this humongous thing and say , " ah , i see the memory operating , i see the cpu operating , i hear it operating . i probably smell it operating . "	當它被建成時 , 你終於能夠了解電腦是如何運作的 , 因為不是在你面前有一小片晶片 , 你得要看著這個巨大的東西 , 然後說: 「 啊 , 我看到記憶運作 , 我看到cpu在運作 , 我聽見它在運作 。 」
but in between that we're going to do a simulation .	但在這兩者之間我們要做一個模擬 。
babbage himself wrote , he said , as soon as the analytical engine exists , it will surely guide the future course of science .	巴比王自己寫道 , 他說 , 一旦分析引擎存在 , 它肯定會引導未來科學的軌道 。
of course , he never built it , because he was always fiddling with new plans , but when it did get built , of course , in the 1940s , everything changed .	當然 , 他從來沒有蓋過它 , 因為他總是在小心設計 , 但當它在1940年代建立時 , 一切都改變了 。
now , i'll just give you a little taste of what it looks like in motion with a video which shows just one part of the cpu mechanism working .	現在 , 我來給你們一些味覺 , 看看它在移動的樣子 , 它只顯示了cpu機制運作的一部分 。
so this is just three sets of cogs , and it's going to add . this is the adding mechanism in action , so you imagine this gigantic machine .	這只是三組齒輪 , 會加上這就是增加機制的運作所以你想像一下這個巨大的機器
so , give me five years .	給我五年 。
before the 2030s happen , we'll have it .	在2030年發生之前 , 我們將會有 。
thank you very much .	謝謝大家 。
in this imagefilled talk , yann arthusbertrand displays his three most recent projects on humanity and our habitat stunning aerial photographs in his series " the earth from above , " personal interviews from around the globe featured in his web project " 6 billion others , " and his soontobereleased movie , " home , " which documents human impact on the environment through breathtaking video .	在這張圖片中 , 雅南•阿斯伯特拉顯示了他的三項近期人性和我們的棲息地 , 令人驚訝的空拍攝 , 在他的系列《地球之上》中 , 來自世界各地的個人訪談 , 他的網路專案 「 六十億人 」 , 很快地 , 他的電影《家園》 , 記錄了人類對環境的影響 , 透過呼吸影片 , 來記錄人類的影響 。
art , climate change , environment , film , future , humanity , media , photography	藝術、氣候變遷、環境、電影、未來、人性、媒體、攝影、攝影 。
yann arthusbertrand captures fragile earth in wideangle	雅恩•阿胡斯伯特在廣角的地球上捕捉到脆弱的地球 。
i have a big impact on the planet to travel here by plane .	我對地球有很大的影響 , 可以用飛機來到這裡旅行 。
i emitted , in the atmosphere , nine tons of co2 ; that is the weight of two elephants .	我在大氣中釋放了九噸二氧化碳 ; 那是兩隻大象的重量 。
i came here to speak about ecology , and i emitted as much co2 as a frenchman in one year .	我來到這裡談論生態學 , 一年內我就把二氧化碳當作法國人 。
so what do i have to do ?	所以 , 我該怎麼做 ?
i have to kill a frenchman when i come back at home ?	當我回家時 , 我得要殺一個法國人 ?
i have to do my carbon offset in another way , like i do every time .	我得要用另一種方式來做碳排放 , 就像我每次都會做一樣 。
in fact my work is to show our impact on our planet .	事實上 , 我的工作是要展現我們對地球的影響 。
i'm going to show you some examples of the last pictures i've done in the last year .	我要給你們看一些例子 , 是我去年所拍攝的照片 。
alberta sand oil , a lot of pollution .	亞伯達•沙油 , 很多污染 。
you know the problem ; we don't want to believe what we know .	你知道問題 , 我們不想相信我們所知道的 。
in alberta people work nonstop , 24 hours by seven to extract as much oil as they can .	在亞伯達 , 人們工作了24小時 , 每七個小時 , 盡可能抽取更多的油 。
we know about the end of oil .	我們知道石油的末端 。
oil sand is not a longterm solution .	石油沙不是一個長期的解決方案 。
but we use three times more oil than we find every year .	但我們每年使用的石油量是每年所發現的三倍 。
we don't want to believe what we know .	我們不想相信我們所知道的 。
coral reef in new caledonia .	珊瑚礁位於新卡里尼亞 。
100 percent of the coral may be wiped out before 2050 because of global warming .	百分之百的珊瑚可能因為全球暖化而被滅絕 。
and you know how coral are very sensitive to temperature , and are very important for the biodiversity of the sea .	你知道珊瑚對溫度非常敏感 , 對海洋生物多樣性來說是非常重要的 。
north pole . i've done this picture last summer .	北極 。 我去年夏天拍了這張照片 。
it was impossible to do this picture 15 years ago .	15年前這張照片是不可能的 。
now there is a new way open between atlantic and pacific .	大西洋和太平洋之間有一種新的開放方式 。
the thickness of the arctic decreased more than 40 percent since 1960 .	從1960年起 , 北極的厚度降低了40% 。
there is a new face of kilimanjaro without ice .	在沒有冰的情況下 , 吉利曼jaro就有了新的面孔 。
it lost 80 percent of its ice .	它失去了80%的冰 。
according to scientists , in 100 years all the mountain glacier will be gone .	根據科學家 , 在一百年內 , 所有的冰川都會消失 。
glaciers are very important for the life on earth .	冰河對地球上的生命是非常重要的 。
like al gore told you , two billion people live on the water from the glacier of himalaya .	如同高爾所說 , 有二十億人住在喜馬拉雅的冰河上 。
return of fish men .	回來的魚類男人 。
one fifth of human kind depend on fish to live .	人類有五分之一依賴魚類生存 。
today now 70 percent of the fish stock are overexploited .	現今有70%的魚類存量過度使用 。
according to fao , if we don't change our system of fishing the main sea resources will be gone in 2050 .	根據fao , 如果我們不改變我們在2050年捕撈大海資源的系統 。
we don't want to believe what we know .	我們不想相信我們所知道的 。
the beautiful picture , by [unclear] in africa .	美麗的照片 , 在非洲 。
one human of six have not enough to eat in the world .	六個人中有六個人沒有足夠的食物可以吃 。
one billion people have not enough to eat .	十億人沒有足夠的食物可以吃 。
in africa , corn is one of the main foods in many places .	在非洲 , 玉米在許多地方是主要食物之一 。
here in america , 90 percent of the corn cultivated is used to feed animals or to do oil .	在美國 , 百分之九十的玉米培養被用來餵養動物或石油 。
palm tree plantation in borneo .	在婆羅的棕櫚樹種植 。
every year we lose 50 thousand square miles in deforestation .	每年我們在森林砍伐中損失了五萬平方英里 。
refugee camp in darfur .	達佛的難民營 。
today we have 20 million refugees in the world .	現今世界上有兩千萬難民 。
according to the u . n . , we speak about 250 million refugees in 2050 .	根據聯合國 , 我們在2050年提到大約2億5千萬難民 。
i always show my pictures in the street .	我總是在街上展示我的照片 。
we have done already 100 exhibitions in the cities .	我們已經在城市裡完成了100次展覽 。
but how to understand the world without the voice of people ?	但 , 要怎麼了解這個世界 , 卻沒有人的聲音 ?
landscape was not enough .	景觀不夠 。

12th man: if i was to go back to iraq and speak to the people , i'd have to bow down and kiss their feet .	第十二個男人:如果我回到伊拉克 , 和人民說話 , 我得要向下弓 , 親吻他們的腳 。
just as that woman tried to kiss my feet when we were taking her sons .	正如那位女士試圖親吻我的腳 , 我們帶著她的兒子 。
and i feel humbled by their strength .	他們的力量讓我感到謙卑 。
and i will forever feel a need to make reparations to iraq .	我永遠會覺得伊拉克有必要做回應 。
second woman: dad , mom , i grew up .	第二個女人:爸爸 , 媽媽 , 我長大了 。
you shouldn't worry about me . dad doesn't need to go to work .	你不該擔心我 , 爸爸不需要去工作 。
my family . . . what can i say ?	我的家人......我能說什麼 ?
at the moment , my family is very poor , my life here in shenzhen is just about showing myself that i can earn more and to let my parents stay and have something to live on .	此時 , 我的家人非常貧窮 , 我在深圳這裡的人生 , 只是要讓自己看到 , 我可以賺更多 , 讓父母留下來 , 有些事要活下去 。

now i am going to speak to you about my movie .	現在我要跟你們談談我的電影 。

the name of the movie is " home " " maison . "	這部電影的名字是 「 家 」 。
it is about the state of the planet .	它是關於地球的狀態 。

video: this earth is four and a half billion years old .	影片:地球有四十五億年的歷史 。
these plants , several hundred million years old .	這些植物 , 數億年前 。
and we humans have been walking upright for only 200 thousand years .	我們人類已經直立行走了20萬年 。
we've managed to adapt , and have conquered the whole planet .	我們成功適應了 , 並且征服了整個地球 。
for generations , we've been raising our children , not unlike millions of other species living beside us .	世代以來 , 我們一直在養育我們的孩子 , 不像其他數百萬種物種生活在我們旁邊 。
for the past 30 years i've been closely watching the earth and its dwellers from high up in the sky .	過去三十年來 , 我幾乎看過地球和它的dweller從天空上升起 。
our life is tied to the wellbeing of our planet .	我們的生活和地球的福祉綁在一起 。
we depend on water , forests , deserts , oceans .	我們仰賴水、森林、沙漠、海洋 。
fishing , breeding , farming are still the world's foremost human occupations .	捕魚、繁殖、農業仍然是世界上人類職業的最好 。
and what binds us together is far greater than what divides us .	把我們結合在一起的 , 遠比分裂我們的更大 。
we all share the same need for the earth's gifts the same wish to rise above ourselves , and become better .	我們都有一樣的需求 , 對地球的禮物 , 和上方的願望一樣 , 並且變得更好 。
and yet we carry on raising walls to keep us apart .	然而 , 我們仍在提高牆壁上 , 以保持距離 。
today our greatest battle is to protect the natural offerings of our planet .	現今 , 我們最大的戰役是保護地球的天然資源 。
in less than 50 years we've altered it more thoroughly than in the entire history of mankind .	不到50年 , 我們已經徹底改變了它 , 比人類的歷史更徹底的改變了它 。
half of the world's forests have vanished .	世界上一半的森林已經消失了 。
water resources are running low .	水資源的資源很低 。
intensive farming is depleting soils .	密集農業正在耗盡土壤 。
our energy sources are not sustainable .	我們的能源來源無法永續發展 。
the climate is changing .	氣候正在改變 。
we are endangering ourselves .	我們正在瀕臨絕種 。
we're only trying to improve our lives .	我們只想改善我們的生活 。
but the wealth gaps are growing wider .	但財富差距越來越廣 。
we haven't yet understood that we're going at a much faster pace than the planet can sustain .	我們尚未了解到 , 我們的速度比地球能維持的速度還要快 。
we know that solutions are available today .	我們知道現今的解決方案是可以取得的 。
we all have the power to change this trend for the better .	我們都有能力去更好地改變這個趨勢 。
so what are we waiting for ?	所以 , 我們還在等什麼 ?

in this accessible talk from tedxboston , richard resnick shows how cheap and fast genome sequencing is about to turn health care upside down .	在tedxboston的這場演講中 , richardresnick顯示了如何便宜且快速的基因定序即將把健康照護轉向下降 。
dna , biotech , health care , science , technology	dna、生物科技、健康照護、科學、科技、科技、科技 。
richard resnick: welcome to the genomic revolution	理查•雷斯尼克:歡迎來到基因革命 。
ladies and gentlemen , i present to you the human genome .	各位先生女士 , 我向你們展示人類基因組 。
chromosome one , top left .	染色體一 , 左上方 。
bottom right are the sex chromosomes .	右下方是性別染色體 。
women have two copies of that big x chromosome ; men have the x and , of course , that small copy of the y .	女性有兩份大型x染色體 ; 男人有x , 當然 , 那個小型的y 。
sorry boys , but it's just a tiny little thing that makes you different .	對不起男孩們 , 但這只是一個小東西 , 讓你有所不同 。
so if you zoom in on this genome , then what you see , of course , is this double helix structure the code of life spelled out with these four biochemical letters , or we call them bases , right: a , c , g and t .	所以如果你放大這個基因組 , 當然 , 你會看到這個雙螺旋結構--生命的代碼--這四個生物化學字母 , 或者我們稱之為基礎:a、c、g和t 。
how many are there in the human genome ? three billion .	人類基因組中有多少 ? 三十億 。
is that a big number ?	這是個大數字嗎 ?
well , everybody can throw around big numbers .	嗯 , 每個人都可以丟出大量的數字 。
but in fact , if i were to place one base on each pixel of this 1280 by 800 resolution screen , we would need 3 , 000 screens to take a look at the genome .	但事實上 , 如果我把這1280像素的每一個像素放到800個解析度螢幕上 , 我們就需要3000個螢幕來檢視基因組 。
so it's really quite big .	這真的很大 。
and perhaps because of its size , a group of people all , by the way , with y chromosomes decided they would want to sequence it .	也許是因為它的大小 , 順便一提 , 有一群人 , 有y染色體決定要定序它 。
and so 15 years , actually , and about four billion dollars later , the genome was sequenced and published .	事實上 , 15年後 , 大約40億美元後 , 基因組序列和出版 。
in 2003 , the final version was published , and they keep working on it .	在2003年 , 最後的版本被發表了 , 他們繼續研究它 。
that was all done on a machine that looks like this .	這一切都是用像這樣的機器完成的 。
it costs about a dollar for each base a very slow way of doing it .	每一鹼基都要花費一美元 , 非常緩慢的做法 。
well folks , i'm here to tell you that the world has completely changed and none of you know about it .	各位 , 我來這裡是要告訴各位 , 世界已經完全改變了 , 沒有人知道 。
so now what we do is we take a genome , we make maybe 50 copies of it , we cut all those copies up into little 50base reads , and then we sequence them , massively parallel .	我們現在做的是把基因組做五十本複製 , 把這些複製品切成五十頁的閱讀 , 然後我們將它們定序 , 大量平行 。
and then we bring that into software , and we reassemble it and we tell you what the story is .	然後我們把它帶到軟體中 , 把它重新組合起來 , 告訴你故事是什麼 。
and so just to give you a picture of what this looks like , the human genome project: 3 gigabases , right .	所以 , 給你們看一張圖片 , 人類基因組計劃:3gbases 。
one run on one of these machines: 200 gigabases in a week .	一台機器運行其中一台:每週有200gb 。
and that 200 is going to change to 600 this summer , and there's no sign of this pace slowing .	今年夏天將會有六百個改變 , 沒有任何步調的跡象 。
so the price of a base , to sequence a base , has fallen 100 million times .	所以 , 基地的價格、基地的價格 , 已經下降了一億倍 。
that's the equivalent of you filling up your car with gas in 1998 , waiting until 2011 , and now you can drive to jupiter and back twice .	等同於你們在1998年用氣體填滿車子 , 等到2011年 , 現在你可以開車到木星 , 再回來兩次 。
world population , pc placements , the archive of all the medical literature , moore's law , the old way of sequencing , and here's all the new stuff .	世界人口、pc定位、所有醫學文獻的檔案、摩爾定律、古老的定序方式 , 全都是新的東西 。
guys , this is a log scale ; you don't typically see lines that go up like that .	各位 , 這是一個網誌規模 , 你通常不會看到像這樣的線條 。
so the worldwide capacity to sequence human genomes is something like 50 , 000 to 100 , 000 human genomes this year .	所以 , 全世界對於人類基因組序列的能力大約是今年約五萬到十萬個人類基因組 。
and we know this based on the machines that are being placed .	我們知道這個基於被安置的機器 。
this is expected to double , triple or maybe quadruple year over year for the foreseeable future .	預期這會增加兩倍 , 三倍或四倍 , 可能是未來可預見的未來一年 。
in fact , there's one lab in particular that represents 20 percent of all that capacity .	事實上 , 特別是有一個實驗室 , 代表了20%的能力 。
it's called the beijing genomics institute .	它叫做北京基因組學研究所 。
the chinese are absolutely winning this race to the new moon , by the way .	中國人絕對贏得了新月球的比賽 。
what does this mean for medicine ?	這對醫學來說是什麼意思 ?
so a woman is age 37 .	女性年齡是37歲 。
she presents with stage 2 estrogen receptorpositive breast cancer .	她呈現了第二階段雌激素受體乳癌 。
she is treated with surgery , chemotherapy and radiation .	她接受手術、化療和放射線治療 。
two years later , she comes back with stage three c ovarian cancer .	兩年後 , 她帶著三c的卵巢癌回來 。
unfortunately , treated again with surgery and chemotherapy .	不幸的是 , 手術和化療再次治療 。
she comes back three years later at age 42 with more ovarian cancer , more chemotherapy .	三年後她回到42歲 , 患有更多卵巢癌 , 更多化療 。
six months later , she comes back with acute myeloid leukemia .	六個月後 , 她又帶著急性白血病回來 。
she goes into respiratory failure and dies eight days later .	八天後 , 她進入呼吸道失敗 。
so first , the way in which this woman was treated , in as little as 10 years , will look like bloodletting .	首先 , 這位女士被治療的方式 , 不到十年的時間 , 看起來會像血液流動 。
and it's because of people like my colleague , rick wilson , at the genome institute at washington university , who decided to take a look at this woman postmortem .	因為像我同事rickwilson這樣的人 , 在華盛頓大學的基因研究所 , 他決定要看這位女士後遺症 。
and he sequenced , he took skin cells , healthy skin , and cancerous bone marrow , and he sequenced the whole genomes of both of them in a couple of weeks , no big deal .	他定序了 , 他拿了皮膚細胞 , 健康的皮膚 , 癌症的骨髓 , 他定序了兩種基因組 , 在幾個星期內 , 沒什麼大不了的 。
and then he compared those two genomes in software , and what he found , among other things , was a deletion , a 2 , 000base deletion across three billion bases in a particular gene called tp53 .	接著 , 他把這兩種基因和軟體比較 , 他發現 , 在其它東西當中 , 有兩千多個鹼基 , 一個特定的基因 , 叫做tp53 。
if you have this deleterious mutation in this gene , you're 90 percent likely to get cancer in your life .	如果你的基因中有這種致命的突變 , 你的人生可能有90%會罹患癌症 。
so unfortunately , this doesn't help this woman , but it does have severe , profound if you will , implications to her family .	不幸的是 , 這對這位女士沒有幫助 , 但如果你願意的話 , 這對她的家庭有很嚴重的影響 。
i mean , if they have the same mutation , and they get this genetic test , and they understand it , then they can go and get regular screens , and they can catch cancer early and potentially live a significantly longer life .	我的意思是 , 如果他們有相同的突變 , 他們得到了這個基因測驗 , 然後他們明白了 , 那麼他們就可以定期篩選癌症 , 可能活得更久 。
let me introduce you now to the beery twins , diagnosed with cerebral palsy at the age of two .	讓我介紹一下啤酒雙胞胎 , 在兩歲時被診斷出腦性麻痺症 。
their mom is a very brave woman who didn't believe that the symptoms weren't matching up , and through some heroic efforts and a lot of internet searching , she was able to convince the medical community that , in fact , they had something else .	他們的母親是一位非常勇敢的女人 , 她不相信症狀不符合 , 透過一些英勇的努力和網路搜尋 , 她能夠說服醫學界 , 事實上 , 他們還有其他東西 。
what they had was doparesponsive dystonia .	他們所擁有的是雙關語的雙關語 。
and so they were given ldopa , and their symptoms did improve , but they weren't totally asymptomatic .	所以他們得到了dopa , 他們的症狀確實改善了 , 但他們並沒有完全的症狀 。
turns out the gentleman in this picture is a guy named joe beery , who was lucky enough to be the cio of a company called life technologies .	這張照片中的先生是一位叫joebeery的傢伙他很幸運能成為一家叫做生命科技的公司
they're one of the two companies that makes these massive whole genome sequencing tools .	它們是兩家公司之一 , 製造這些大量的基因組定序工具 。
and so what he did was he got his kids sequenced .	所以他所做的是 , 他讓他的孩子做定序 。
and what they found was a series of mutations in a gene called spr , which is responsible for producing serotonin , among other things .	他們發現一系列的突變 , 在一個叫做 「 春天 」 的基因中 , 負責產生血清素 , 其它東西 。
so on top of ldopa , they gave these kids a serotonin precursor drug , and they're effectively normal now .	所以 , 在dopa之上 , 他們給這些孩子一種血清素先驅藥物 , 現在他們很正常 。
guys , this would never have happened without whole genome sequencing .	各位 , 如果沒有完整的基因組定序 , 這絕對不會發生 。
and at the time this was a few years ago it cost $100 , 000 .	幾年前 , 那時是10萬美金 。
today it's $10 , 000 . next year it's $1 , 000 .	今天是一萬美金 , 明年是一千美金 。
the year after it's $100 , give or take a year .	在100元後的那一年 , 或一年 。
that's how fast this is moving .	這就是移動的速度 。
so here's little nick likes batman and squirt guns .	這裡有小小的nick喜歡蝙蝠俠和松鼠槍 。
and it turns out nick shows up at the children's hospital with this distended belly like a famine victim .	結果發現 , 尼克在兒童醫院出現 , 腹部像個饑荒受害者一樣 。
and it's not that he's not eating , it's that when he eats , his intestine basically opens up and feces spill out into his gut .	並不是說他不吃東西 , 而是當他吃的時候 , 他的腸道基本上會打開 , 糞便會流出他的腸道 。
so a hundred surgeries later , he looks at his mom and says , " mom , please pray for me . i'm in so much pain . "	幾百次手術後 , 他看著他的媽媽說: 「 媽 , 請為我祈禱 , 我非常痛苦 。 」
his pediatrician happens to have a background in clinical genetics and he has no idea what's going on , but he says , " let's get this kid's genome sequenced . "	他的小兒科醫生剛好有臨床遺傳學的背景 , 他完全不知道發生了什麼事 , 但他說: 「 我們來找這個孩子的基因序列 。 」
and what they find is a singlepoint mutation in a gene responsible for controlling programmed cell death .	他們發現 , 一個單點突變 , 負責控制細胞死亡的基因 。
so the theory is that he's having some immunological reaction to what's going on to the food essentially , and that's a natural reaction , which causes some programmed cell death .	所以 , 理論是 , 他正在對食物的反應有一些免疫反應 , 基本上 , 這是一種自然反應 , 導致一些編程的細胞死亡 。
but the gene that regulates that down is broken .	但管制下的基因已經壞掉了 。

daniel kraft demos his marrow miner a new device that quickly harvests lifesaving bone marrow with minimal pain to the donor . he emphasizes that the adult stem cells found in bone marrow can be used to treat many terminal conditions , from parkinson's to heart disease .	丹尼爾•克拉夫示範他的骨髓礦工一個新的裝置 , 能快速收集生命的骨髓 , 和捐贈者的最小痛苦 。 他強調的是 , 在骨髓中發現的成人幹細胞可以被用來治療許多終極條件 , 從帕金森氏症到心臟疾病 。
