so actually how do we harvest this bone marrow ?	所以實際上 , 我們要如何收集這些骨髓 ?
well we have a whole o . r . team , general anesthesia , nurses , and another doctor across from me .	我們有一整間o.r.團隊 , 麻醉 , 護士 , 還有另一位醫生在我身邊 。
bob's on the table , and we take this sort of small needle , you know , not too big .	鮑勃站在桌上 , 我們採用這種小針 , 你知道的 , 不太大 。
and the way we do this is we basically place this through the soft tissue , and kind of punch it into the hard bone , into the tuchus that's a technical term and aspirate about 10 mls of bone marrow out , each time , with a syringe .	我們做這件事的方式基本上就是把這個裝置放在軟組織裡 , 把它打進硬骨頭 , 進入突丘腦 , 每次用針筒 , 只要用針筒 , 就可以達到10個骨髓 。
and hand it off to the nurse . she squirts it into a tin .	然後把它交給護士 , 她將它放進一個小東西裡 。
hands it back to me . and we do that again and again .	把它交給我 。 我們一而再再而三地這樣做 。
about 200 times usually .	通常是200次 。
and by the end of this my arm is sore , i've got a callus on my hand , let alone bob , whose rear end looks something more like this , like swiss cheese .	在我手臂的尾聲是如此 , 我手上有一通電話 , 更不用說鮑勃 , 他的屁股看起來像這樣 , 像是瑞士起司 。
so i'm thinking , you know , this procedure hasn't changed in about 40 years .	所以我在想 , 你知道的 , 這個手術在40年內沒有改變 。
and there is probably a better way to do this .	可能還有更好的方法來做這件事 。
so i thought of a minimally invasive approach , and a new device that we call the marrow miner .	所以我想到一個最低入侵的方法 , 我們稱之為 「 骨髓礦工 」 。
and the marrow miner , the way it works is shown here .	而骨髓礦工 , 它的運作方式是在這裡展示的 。
our standard seethrough patient .	我們的標準看診病人 。
instead of entering the bone dozens of times , we enter just once , into the front of the hip or the back of the hip .	與其進入骨骼的數十次 , 我們就只是進入髖骨的前面或髖骨的後面 。
and we have a flexible , powered catheter with a special wire loop tip that stays inside the crunchy part of the marrow and follows the contours of the hip , as it moves around .	我們有彈性、發電的導管 , 用特殊的電線管 , 留在馬羅的殘酷部分 , 然後追蹤髖骨的輪廓 , 當它移動時 。
so it enables you to very rapidly aspirate , or suck out , rich bone marrow very quickly through one hole .	所以它能讓你非常快速地吸入骨髓 , 或是吸出一個洞 , 很快地 , 豐富的骨髓 。
we can do multiple passes through that same entry .	我們可以通過相同的入口 。
and , so , very quickly , bob can just get one puncture , local anesthesia , and do this harvest as an outpatient .	所以 , 很快地 , 鮑勃只能拿到一個針筒 , 當地麻醉劑 , 並把這個收穫當作一個門診 。
so i did a few prototypes . i got a small little grant at stanford .	所以我做了一些原型 , 我在史丹佛拿到一個小小的格子 。
and played around with this a little bit .	再多玩一點 。
and our team members developed this technology .	我們的團隊成員開發了這項技術 。
and eventually we got two large animals , and pig studies .	最終 , 我們有兩個大型動物和豬研究 。
and we found , to our surprise , that we not only got bone marrow out , but we got 10 times the stem cell activity in the marrow from the marrow miner , compared to the normal device .	我們發現 , 意外的是 , 我們不只得到骨髓 , 我們還得到骨髓中幹細胞活動的十倍 , 相較於正常的裝置 。
this device was just fda approved in the last year .	這個裝置在去年才被核准 。
here is a live patient . you can see it following the flexible curves around .	這是個活體病患 。 你可以看到它在附近的彈性曲線 。
there will be two passes here , in the same patient , from the same hole .	同一個病人 , 同一個洞 , 就會有兩個通過 。
this was done under local anesthesia , as an outpatient .	這是在當地麻醉劑的情況下所做的 , 做成是門診 。
and we got , again , about three to six times more stem cells than the standard approach done on the same patient .	同樣的 , 我們得到的幹細胞數量是同一個病人的標準方法的三到六倍 。
so why should you care ? bone marrow is a very rich source of adult stem cells .	所以 , 你為什麼要在乎 ? 骨髓是個非常豐富的成人幹細胞 。
you all know about embryonic stem cells .	你們都知道胚胎幹細胞 。
they've got great potential but haven't yet entered clinical trials .	他們有很大的潛力 , 但還沒有進入臨床試驗 。
adult stem cells are throughout our body , including the bloodforming stem cells in our bone marrow , which we've been using as a form of stemcell therapy for over 40 years .	成人幹細胞在全身各處 , 包括我們骨髓中的血液幹細胞 , 我們已經用它作為幹細胞治療的形式 , 已經超過四十年了 。
in the last decade there's been an explosion of use of bone marrow stem cells to treat the patient's other diseases such as heart disease , vascular disease , orthopedics , tissue engineering , even in neurology to treat parkinson's and diabetes .	在過去十年間 , 使用骨髓幹細胞的爆炸 , 來治療病人其他疾病 , 像是心臟病、血管疾病、組織工程 , 甚至在神經系統中 , 來治療帕金森氏症和糖尿病 。
we've just come out , we're commercializing , this year , generation 2 . 0 of the marrow miner .	我們剛剛推出 , 我們正在商業化 , 今年 , 第二代的骨髓礦工 。
the hope is that this gets more stem cells out , which translates to better outcomes .	希望這能讓更多的幹細胞被翻譯成更好的結果 。
it may encourage more people to sign up to be potential livesaving bone marrow donors .	它可能會鼓勵更多人參與成為可能救命的骨髓捐贈者 。
it may even enable you to bank your own marrow stem cells , when you're younger and healthier , to use in the future should you need it .	甚至可能讓你可以銀行你自己的骨髓幹細胞 , 當你更年輕、更健康的時候 , 讓你可以在未來使用它 。
and ultimately and here's a picture of our bone marrow transplant survivors , who come together for a reunion each year at stanford .	最終 , 這是我們的骨髓移植者的照片 , 他們每年在史丹佛聚會 。
hopefully this technology will let us have more of these survivors in the future .	希望這項技術能讓我們在未來有更多的倖存者 。
physicist and surfer garrett lisi presents a controversial new model of the universe that just maybe answers all the big questions . if nothing else , it's the most beautiful 8dimensional model of elementary particles and forces you've ever seen .	物理學家和波斯弗雷特•蓋瑞特•賴西在宇宙中提出一個爭議性的新模型 , 可能只能回答所有大問題 。 如果沒有其他東西 , 它是最美麗的8維元元元元元元素模型 , 強迫你見過 。
physics , science , technology	物理、科學、科技、科技、
garrett lisi on his theory of everything	garretlisi理論是所有東西的理論 。
whoa , dude . check out those killer equations . sweet .	哇 , 老兄 , 看看那些殺手方程式 。
actually , for the next 18 minutes i'm going to do the best i can to describe the beauty of particle physics without equations .	事實上 , 在接下來的18分鐘裡 , 我要盡我所能地描述無方程式的粒子物理的美麗 。
it turns out there's a lot we can learn from coral .	結果發現 , 我們可以從珊瑚身上學到很多東西 。
coral is a very beautiful and unusual animal .	珊瑚是非常美麗且不尋常的動物 。
each coral head consists of thousand of individual polyps .	每個珊瑚的頭包含數以千計的珊瑚蟲 。
these polyps are continually budding and branching into genetically identical neighbors .	這些珊瑚蟲不斷地在基因上生長 , 分枝成一模一樣的鄰居 。
if we imagine this to be a hyperintelligent coral , we can single out an individual and ask him a reasonable question .	如果我們想像這是個超智能的珊瑚 , 我們可以單獨找出一個人 , 並問他一個合理的問題 。
we can ask how exactly he got to be in this particular location compared to his neighbors if it was just chance , or destiny , or what ?	我們可以問他在這個特定的地點與他的鄰居相比 , 如果只是偶然 , 或命運 , 或什麼 ?
now , after admonishing us for turning the temperature up too high , he would tell us that our question was completely stupid .	把溫度調高了之後 , 他會告訴我們 , 我們的問題完全愚蠢 。
these corals can be quite kind of mean , you see , and i have surfing scars to prove that .	這些珊瑚可以是很有意思的 , 你看 , 我有衝浪疤痕來證明這一點 。
but this polyp would continue and tell us that his neighbors were quite clearly identical copies of him .	但這隻珊瑚蟲會繼續告訴我們 , 牠的鄰居很明顯是同類的複製品 。
that he was in all these other locations as well , but experiencing them as separate individuals .	他也在其他的位置裡 , 但體驗它們和獨立的個體是不同的 。
for a coral , branching into different copies is the most natural thing in the world .	對珊瑚而言 , 分枝到不同的複製品是世界上最自然的東西 。
unlike us , a hyperintelligent coral would be uniquely prepared to understand quantum mechanics .	不像我們 , 超級聰明的珊瑚會特別準備好了解量子力學 。
the mathematics of quantum mechanics very accurately describes how our universe works .	量子力學的數學非常準確地描述我們的宇宙是如何運作的 。
and it tells us our reality is continually branching into different possibilities , just like a coral .	它告訴我們 , 我們的現實不斷地被分為不同的可能性 , 就像珊瑚一樣 。
it's a weird thing for us humans to wrap our minds around , since we only ever get to experience one possibility .	這對我們人類來說是很奇怪的事 , 因為我們只能體驗一個可能性 。
this quantum weirdness was first described by erwin schrödinger and his cat .	這種量子奇怪的現象首先被erwinschrdinger和他的貓描述 。
the cat likes this version better .	貓比較喜歡這個版本 。
in this setup , schrödinger is in a box with a radioactive sample that , by the laws of quantum mechanics , branches into a state in which it is radiated and a state in which it is not .	在這個組合中 , 薛丁格在一個有放射性樣本的盒子裡 , 通過量子力學的定律 , 分支進入一個狀態 , 一個不存在的狀態 。
in the branch in which the sample radiates , it sets off a trigger that releases poison and schrödinger is dead .	在採集樣本的分支中 , 釋放出毒藥和薛丁格爾已經死了 。
but in the other branch of reality , he remains alive .	但在現實的另一種領域中 , 他仍然活著 。
these realities are experienced separately by each individual .	這些實相被分開了 。
as far as either can tell , the other one doesn't exist .	到目前為止 , 另一種並不存在 。
this seems weird to us , because each of us only experiences an individual existence , and we don't get to see other branches .	這對我們來說似乎很奇怪 , 因為我們每個人都只經歷個人存在 , 而我們無法看到其他的分支 。
it's as if each of us , like schrödinger here , are a kind of coral branching into different possibilities .	這就好像我們每一個人 , 如薛丁格 , 都是珊瑚分支成不同的可能性 。
the mathematics of quantum mechanics tells us this is how the world works at tiny scales .	量子力學的數學告訴我們 , 世界的運作方式很小 。
it can be summed up in a single sentence: everything that can happen , does .	它可以用單一句話來總結:所有可能發生的事情 , 確實 。
but this does not mean everything happens .	但這並不表示一切都會發生 。
the rest of physics is about describing what can happen and what can't .	其他的物理則是描述可能發生什麼事 , 以及什麼都不能 。
what physics tells us is that everything comes down to geometry and the interactions of elementary particles .	物理學告訴我們 , 一切都歸功於幾何和基本粒子的互動 。
and things can happen only if these interactions are perfectly balanced .	只有這些互動是完全平衡的 。
now i'll go ahead and describe how we know about these particles , what they are and how this balance works .	現在我來說明我們對這些粒子的了解 , 它們是什麼 , 以及平衡如何運作 。
in this machine , a beam of protons and antiprotons are accelerated to near the speed of light and brought together in a collision , producing a burst of pure energy .	在這個機器中 , 一束質子和反質子會加速接近光速 , 以碰撞產生出純能量的爆炸 。
this energy is immediately converted into a spray of subatomic particles , with detectors and computers used to figure out their properties .	這種能量馬上被轉換成亞原子粒子的噴射 , 探測器和電腦用來找出它們的特性 。
this enormous machine the large hadron collider at cern in geneva has a circumference of 17 miles and , when it's operating , draws five times as much power as the city of monterey .	這台巨大的機器 , 位於日內瓦的大型強子對撞機有17英里的圍欄 , 當它在運作時 , 比蒙特雷市的城市還要多五倍 。
we can't predict specifically what particles will be produced in any individual collision .	我們無法準確預測哪些粒子會在任何個別碰撞中產生 。
quantum mechanics tells us all possibilities are realized .	量子力學告訴我們所有可能性 。
but physics does tell us what particles can be produced .	但物理告訴我們粒子能產生什麼 。
these particles must have just as much mass and energy as is carried in by the proton and antiproton .	這些粒子必須的質量和能量就跟質子和反質子一樣 。
any particles more massive than this energy limit aren't produced , and remain invisible to us .	任何比這能源限制更大的粒子 , 都不會產生出來 , 且對我們來說仍然是看不見的 。
this is why this new particle accelerator is so exciting .	這就是為什麼這個新的粒子加速器非常令人興奮 。
it's going to push this energy limit seven times beyond what's ever been done before , so we're going to get to see some new particles very soon .	它會推動這個能量限制前七倍之多 , 所以我們很快就會看到一些新的粒子 。
but before talking about what we might see , let me describe the particles we already know of .	但在談我們可能看到的之前 , 讓我來描述我們已經知道的粒子 。
there's a whole zoo of subatomic particles .	有一大堆亞原子粒子的動物 。
most of us are familiar with electrons .	我們大部份人熟悉電子 。
a lot of people in this room make a good living pushing them around .	許多人在這個房間裡養活得很好 。
but the electron also has a neutral partner called the neutrino , with no electric charge and a very tiny mass .	但電子也有中性伴侶 , 叫做微中子 , 沒有電荷和非常小的質量 。
in contrast , the upanddown quarks have very large masses , and combine in threes to make the protons and neutrons inside atoms .	相對的 , 上方夸克的質量非常大 , 三分之二的結合 , 將質子和中子組合成原子 。
all of these matter particles come in left and righthanded varieties , and have antiparticle partners that carry opposite charges .	所有這些粒子都來自左邊和右邊的多樣性 , 並且有相反載荷的抗粒子伴侶 。
these familiar particles also have less familiar second and third generations , which have the same charges as the first but have much higher masses .	這些熟悉的粒子也有較少熟悉的第二代和第三代 , 和第一代相同的載荷相同 , 但質量較高 。
these matter particles all interact with the various force particles .	這些粒子都和各種力粒子互動 。
the electromagnetic force interacts with electrically charged matter via particles called photons .	電磁力通過光子所引電的粒子相互作用 。
there is also a very weak force called , rather unimaginatively , the weak force , that interacts only with lefthanded matter .	還有一種很弱的力量 , 叫做 「 不想像力 」 , 它只和左撇子物質相互作用 。
the strong force acts between quarks which carry a different kind of charge , called color charge , and come in three different varieties: red , green and blue .	夸克的強力作用在夸克帶有一種不同的載荷 , 叫做顏色充電 , 三種不同的種類:紅、綠、藍 。
you can blame murray gellmann for these names they're his fault .	你可以責怪murraygellmann , 他們是他的錯 。
finally , there's the force of gravity , which interacts with matter via its mass and spin .	最後 , 重力的力量 , 透過質量和旋轉來互動 。
the most important thing to understand here is that there's a different kind of charge associated with each of these forces .	最重要的是 , 每一股力量有不同的載荷 。
these four different forces interact with matter according to the corresponding charges that each particle has .	這四種不同的力相互作用 , 根據每個粒子都有的相對應載荷 。
a particle that hasn't been seen yet , but we're pretty sure exists , is the higgs particle , which gives masses to all these other particles .	一個尚未見過的粒子 , 但我們很確定存在的粒子 , 就是希格斯粒子 , 讓所有其他粒子產生質量 。
the main purpose of the large hadron collider is to see this higgs particle , and we're almost certain it will .	大型強子對撞機的主要目的是要看到這個希格斯粒子 , 我們幾乎確定它會發生 。
but the greatest mystery is what else we might see .	但最偉大的奧秘是我們還能看到的 。
and i'm going to show you one beautiful possibility towards the end of this talk .	我將向你們展示一個美麗的可能性 , 來到這場演說的結尾 。
now , if we count up all these different particles using their various spins and charges , there are 226 .	如果我們用不同的旋轉和載荷來計算這些不同的粒子 , 就會有226顆 。
that's a lot of particles to keep track of .	要追蹤很多粒子 。
and it seems strange that nature would have so many elementary particles .	大自然似乎有這麼多基本粒子 。
but if we plot them out according to their charges , some beautiful patterns emerge .	但如果我們根據他們的載荷來繪製它們 , 有些美麗的圖案會浮現出來 。
the most familiar charge is electric charge .	最熟悉的載荷是電荷 。
electrons have an electric charge , a negative one , and quarks have electric charges in thirds .	電子有電荷 , 負電 , 夸克有三分之一的電荷 。
so when two up quarks and a down quark are combined to make a proton , it has a total electric charge of plus one .	所以 , 當兩個夸克和下夸克組合成一個質子時 , 總電荷總電荷總共只有一個 。
these particles also have antiparticles , which have opposite charges .	這些粒子也有反粒子 , 有相反的載荷 。
now , it turns out the electric charge is actually a combination of two other charges: hypercharge and weak charge .	結果發現電荷實際上是另外兩個載荷組合:超載荷和弱載荷 。
if we spread out the hypercharge and weak charge and plot the charges of particles in this twodimensional charge space , the electric charge is where these particles sit along the vertical direction .	如果我們把超級充電和弱電荷散開 , 在這二度載荷空間中繪製出粒子的載荷 , 電荷就是這些粒子在垂直方向的位置 。
the electromagnetic and weak forces interact with matter according to their hypercharge and weak charge , which make this pattern .	電磁力和弱力相互作用 , 根據他們的超載和弱載荷 , 會產生這種模式 。
this is called the unified electroweak model , and it was put together back in 1967 .	這就是所謂的 「 民選模式 」 , 它在1967年被組合起來 。
the reason most of us are only familiar with electric charge and not both of these is because of the higgs particle .	我們大多數人只熟悉電荷 , 而不是兩者都是因為希格斯粒子 。
the higgs , over here on the left , has a large mass and breaks the symmetry of this electroweak pattern .	左邊這裡的希格斯有很大的質量 , 打破了這個發電模式的對稱性 。
it makes the weak force very weak by giving the weak particles a large mass .	它讓弱力變弱 , 讓弱粒子變成大質量 。
since this massive higgs sits along the horizontal direction in this diagram , the photons of electromagnetism remain massless and interact with electric charge along the vertical direction in this charge space .	由於這個巨大的希格斯位於水平方向 , 電磁力學的光子仍然沒有質量 , 在這個載荷空間中與電荷之間的互動 。
so the electromagnetic and weak forces are described by this pattern of particle charges in twodimensional space .	所以電磁力和弱力被這二維空間中的粒子載荷所描述 。
we can include the strong force by spreading out its two charge directions and plotting the charges of the force particles in quarks along these directions .	我們可以把強力推廣出兩個載荷方向並在這些方向上繪製出夸克力粒子的載荷
the charges of all known particles can be plotted in a fourdimensional charge space , and projected down to two dimensions like this so we can see them .	所有已知粒子的載荷可以在四度載荷空間中繪製 , 投射到像這樣的二維空間 , 這樣我們就能看見它們 。
whenever particles interact , nature keeps things in a perfect balance along all four of these charge directions .	每當粒子相互作用時 , 大自然就會保持完美的平衡 , 和這四種載荷方向的平衡 。
if a particle and an antiparticle collide , it creates a burst of energy and a total charge of zero in all four charge directions .	如果粒子和抗粒子碰撞 , 它會造成能量的爆炸 , 以及四個載荷方向的總載荷 。
at this point , anything can be created as long as it has the same energy and maintains a total charge of zero .	在這個時點 , 任何東西只要它有相同的能量 , 維持零的總載荷 。
for example , this weak force particle and its antiparticle can be created in a collision .	例如 , 這種弱力粒子和它的反粒子可以在碰撞中產生 。
in further interactions , the charges must always balance .	在更進一步的互動中 , 指控總是平衡 。
one of the weak particles could decay into an electron and an antineutrino , and these three still add to zero total charge .	其中一個微小的粒子可以分解成電子和一顆中子 , 這三個粒子仍然加上0的總載荷 。
nature always keeps a perfect balance .	大自然總是保持完美的平衡 。
so these patterns of charges are not just pretty .	所以這些載荷的模式不只漂亮 。
they tell us what interactions are allowed to happen .	他們告訴我們 , 哪些互動被允許發生 。
and we can rotate this charge space in four dimensions to get a better look at the strong interaction , which has this nice hexagonal symmetry .	我們可以在四維空間旋轉這個載荷空間 , 來更好地觀察強烈的交互作用 , 這種六角形對稱性 。
in a strong interaction , a strong force particle , such as this one , interacts with a colored quark , such as this green one , to give a quark with a different color charge this red one .	在強烈的互動中 , 強力粒子 , 例如這個 , 與有顏色的夸克互動 , 例如 , 綠色夸克 , 用不同顏色表示這個紅色 。
and strong interactions are happening millions of times each second in every atom of our bodies , holding the atomic nuclei together .	強烈的互動每一秒就會發生數百萬次 , 以我們身體的每個原子組合 , 將原子核結合在一起 。
but these four charges corresponding to three forces are not the end of the story .	但這四個載荷對應到三種力量並不是故事的結尾 。
we can also include two more charges corresponding to the gravitational force .	我們還可以把兩個載荷和重力相對應 。
when we include these , each matter particle has two different spin charges , spinup and spindown .	當我們把它們納入 , 每個粒子都有兩種不同的旋轉指控、旋轉和旋轉 。
so they all split , and give a nice pattern in sixdimensional charge space .	所以它們都分開 , 在六度載荷空間中給一個很棒的圖案 。
we can rotate this pattern in six dimensions , and see that it's quite pretty .	我們可以在六維空間旋轉這個模式 , 看到它是相當漂亮的 。
right now , this pattern matches our best current knowledge of how nature is built at the tiny scales of these elementary particles .	目前 , 這個模式符合我們目前所知的大自然在這些元素粒子的微小尺度 。
this is what we know for certain .	這就是我們所知的 。
some of these particles are at the very limit of what we've been able to reach with experiments .	有些粒子在實驗中能達到的極限 。
from this pattern , we already know the particle physics of these tiny scales . the way the universe works with these tiny scales is very beautiful .	從這個模式 , 我們已經知道這些微小的粒子物理學 。 宇宙和這些微小的尺度是非常漂亮的 。
but now i'm going to discuss some new and old ideas about things we don't know yet .	但現在我要來談談一些我們還不知道的新點子 。
we want to expand this pattern using mathematics alone , and see if we can get our hands on the whole enchilada .	我們只想用數學來拓展這個模式 , 看看我們能否掌握整個恩基達的手 。
we want to find all the particles and forces that make a complete picture of our universe .	我們想找到所有構成我們宇宙的粒子和力量 。
and we want to use this picture to predict new particles that we'll see when experiments reach higher energies .	我們想用這張照片來預測新的粒子在實驗達到更高能量時會看到的粒子 。
so there's an old idea in particle physics that this known pattern of charges , which is not very symmetric , could emerge from a more perfect pattern that gets broken similar to how the higgs particle breaks the electroweak pattern to give electromagnetism .	粒子物理學有一個古老的想法 , 這種已知的載荷模式 , 不對稱 , 可以從更完美的模式中產生出來 , 就像希格斯粒子打破電路模式 , 來產生電磁力 。
in order to do this , we need to introduce new forces with new charge directions .	為了做到這一點 , 我們需要引進新的載荷方向 。
when we introduce a new direction , we get to guess what charges the particles have along this direction , and then we can rotate it in with the others .	當我們引進一個新的方向 , 我們會猜測粒子在這個方向的載荷 , 然後我們可以把它旋轉到另一個方向 。
if we guess wisely , we can construct the standard charges in six charge dimensions as a broken symmetry of this more perfect pattern in seven charge dimensions .	如果我們明智地猜測 , 我們就能在六度載荷空間中建構出標準載荷的對稱性 , 以七度載荷的形式 , 來對應這個更完美的圖案 。
this particular choice corresponds to a grand unified theory introduced by pati and salam in 1973 .	這種選擇對應到1973年由帕蒂和薩拉姆提出的大統一理論 。
when we look at this new unified pattern , we can see a couple of gaps where particles seem to be missing .	當我們觀察這個新的統一模式時 , 我們可以看到一些缺口 , 粒子似乎缺少了 。
this is the way theories of unification work .	這就是統一理論的運作方式 。
a physicist looks for larger , more symmetric patterns that include the established pattern as a subset .	物理學家尋找更大、更對稱的圖案 , 包含了特定的圖案 。
the larger pattern allows us to predict the existence of particles that have never been seen .	更大的模式讓我們能夠預測那些從未見過的粒子存在 。
this unification model predicts the existence of these two new force particles , which should act a lot like the weak force , only weaker .	這個統一模型預測了這兩個新的粒子存在 , 它應該很像弱力 , 只有弱力 。
now we can rotate this set of charges in seven dimensions and consider an odd fact about the matter particles: the second and third generations of matter have exactly the same charges in sixdimensional charge space as the first generation .	現在我們可以在七維空間中旋轉這組載荷 , 並考慮到物質粒子的奇怪事實:第二和第三代物質在六度載荷空間中有完全一樣的載荷 。
these particles are not uniquely identified by their six charges .	這些粒子並非獨一無二的被六個載荷所辨識出來 。
they sit on top of one another in the standard charge space .	他們坐在標準載荷空間的頂端 。
however , if we work in eightdimensional charge space , then we can assign unique new charges to each particle .	然而 , 如果我們在八度載荷空間中工作 , 我們就能分配每個粒子獨特的新載荷 。
then we can spin these in eight dimensions , and see what the whole pattern looks like .	然後我們可以在八度空間中轉動 , 看看整個圖案是什麼樣子 。
here we can see the second and third generations of matter now related to the first generation by a symmetry called " triality . "	在這裡 , 我們可以看到第二和第三代相關的物質 , 由所謂的 「 審判 」 的對稱性 。
this particular pattern of charges in eight dimensions is actually part of the most beautiful geometric structure in mathematics .	這種八度空間的載荷模式實際上是數學中最美麗的幾何結構之一 。
it's a pattern of the largest exceptional lie group , e8 .	它是最大例外的謊言團體e8 。
this lie group is a smooth , curved shape with 248 dimensions .	這個謊言團體是平滑的 , 曲線形狀有248維度 。
each point in this pattern corresponds to a symmetry of this very complex and beautiful shape .	在這個圖案中的每一點都與這個複雜且美麗的形狀相對應 。
one small part of this e8 shape can be used to describe the curved spacetime of einstein's general relativity , explaining gravity .	這個e8形狀的一小部分可以用來描述愛因斯坦廣義相對論的曲線時空 , 解釋重力 。
together with quantum mechanics , the geometry of this shape could describe everything about how the universe works at the tiniest scales .	與量子力學結合 , 這個形狀的幾何形狀可以描述宇宙是如何運作的 。
the pattern of this shape living in eightdimensional charge space is exquisitely beautiful , and it summarizes thousands of possible interactions between these elementary particles , each of which is just a facet of this complicated shape .	這種形狀的圖案 , 生活在八度載荷空間是非常美麗的 , 它總結了數千個可能的相互作用 , 每一個都是這個複雜的形狀 。
as we spin it , we can see many of the other intricate patterns contained in this one .	當我們轉動它時 , 我們可以看到其中許多複雜的圖案 。
and with a particular rotation , we can look down through this pattern in eight dimensions along a symmetry axis and see all the particles at once .	有了特定的旋轉 , 我們就能在八度空間中觀察這個圖案 , 同時觀察所有粒子 。
it's a very beautiful object , and as with any unification , we can see some holes where new particles are required by this pattern .	它是一個非常美麗的物體 , 如同任何一個物體一樣 , 我們可以看到這些特定的新粒子所需要的 。
there are 20 gaps where new particles should be , two of which have been filled by the patisalam particles .	有20個落差 , 新的粒子應該是 , 其中兩個被帕塔拉瓦粒子填滿 。
from their location in this pattern , we know that these new particles should be scalar fields like the higgs particle , but have color charge and interact with the strong force .	從這個模式的位置 , 我們知道這些新的粒子應該會像希格斯粒子一樣大 , 但有顏色的載荷 , 和強力互動 。
filling in these new particles completes this pattern , giving us the full e8 .	填入這些新粒子 , 完成了這個模式 , 給了我們全e8 。
this e8 pattern has very deep mathematical roots .	這個e8圖案有很深的數學根源 。
it's considered by many to be the most beautiful structure in mathematics .	它被許多人認為是數學中最美麗的結構 。
it's a fantastic prospect that this object of great mathematical beauty could describe the truth of particle interactions at the smallest scales imaginable .	這個偉大數學美的物體可以用最小的尺度描述粒子互動的真相 。
and this idea that nature is described by mathematics is not at all new .	而這個想法 , 大自然被數學所描述 , 並非全新的 。
in 1623 , galileo wrote this: " nature's grand book , which stands continually open to our gaze , is written in the language of mathematics .	在1623年 , 伽利略寫了這句話: 「 大自然的偉大之書 , 不斷地對我們的觀點打開 , 寫在數學的語言中 。
its characters are triangles , circles and other geometrical figures , without which it is humanly impossible to understand a single word of it ; without these , one is wandering around in a dark labyrinth . "	它的角色是三角形、圓形和其他幾何圖形 , 沒有任何一個字是人道不可能理解的 ; 沒有這些 , 一個是在黑暗的迷宮中漫遊 。 」
i believe this to be true , and i've tried to follow galileo's guidance in describing the mathematics of particle physics using only triangles , circles and other geometrical figures .	我相信這是真的 , 我試著遵循伽利略的指導 , 描述粒子物理的數學 , 只用三角形、圓形和其他幾何數字 。
of course , when other physicists and i actually work on this stuff , the mathematics can resemble a dark labyrinth .	當然 , 當我和其他物理學家一起研究這些東西時 , 數學可以和黑暗的迷宮相似 。
but it's reassuring that at the heart of this mathematics is pure , beautiful geometry .	但 , 要確保數學的核心是純粹的 , 美麗的幾何學 。
joined with quantum mechanics , this mathematics describes our universe as a growing e8 coral , with particles interacting at every location in all possible ways according to a beautiful pattern .	與量子力學結合 , 這個數學將我們的宇宙描述為一個不斷成長的e8珊瑚 , 粒子以各種可能的形式進行互動 。
and as more of the pattern comes into view using new machines like the large hadron collider , we may be able to see whether nature uses this e8 pattern or a different one .	隨著更多的模式 , 使用像大型強子對撞機的新機器 , 我們可能會看到大自然使用這個e8的圖案或另一個圖案 。
this process of discovery is a wonderful adventure to be involved in .	這個發現過程是個很棒的冒險 。
if the lhc finds particles that fit this e8 pattern , that will be very , very cool .	如果lhc找到符合e8圖案的粒子 , 那就很酷了 。
if the lhc finds new particles , but they don't fit this pattern well , that will be very interesting , but bad for this e8 theory .	如果lhc能找到新的粒子 , 但它們不符合這個模式 , 那會很有趣 , 但對e8理論不好 。
and , of course , bad for me personally .	當然 , 對我個人來說是不好的 。
now how bad would that be ?	那會多糟 ?
well , pretty bad .	嗯 , 相當糟糕 。
but predicting how nature works is a very risky game .	但 , 預測大自然的運作方式是非常危險的遊戲 。
this theory and others like it are long shots .	這個理論和其他類似的理論是長時間拍攝 。
one does a lot of hard work knowing that most of these ideas probably won't end up being true about nature .	有一個很辛苦的工作 , 知道大部分這些點子可能不會成為大自然的真相 。
that's what doing theoretical physics is like: there are a lot of wipeouts .	這就是理論物理學的做法:有很多的擦力 。
in this regard , new physics theories are a lot like startup companies .	在這方面 , 新的物理理論就像新創公司一樣 。
as with any large investment , it can be emotionally difficult to abandon a line of research when it isn't working out .	就如同任何大型投資 , 在沒有成功的情況下 , 要放棄一系列的研究是很困難的 。
but in science , if something isn't working , you have to toss it out and try something else .	但在科學上 , 如果有東西行不通 , 你就得要把它拿出來嘗試其他東西 。
now , the only way to maintain sanity and achieve happiness in the midst of this uncertainty is to keep balance and perspective in life .	在不確定之下 , 維持公平和幸福的唯一方法就是保持生活的平衡和觀點 。
i've tried the best i can to live a balanced life .	我盡我所能活得平衡 。
i try to balance my life equally between physics , love and surfing my own three charge directions .	我試著平衡我的生活 , 平衡物理、愛、衝浪我自己的三個載荷方向 。
this way , even if the physics i work on comes to nothing , i still know i've lived a good life .	這樣一來 , 即使我所研究的物理都沒有 , 我仍然知道我過著美好的生活 。
and i try to live in beautiful places .	我試著生活在美麗的地方 。
for most of the past ten years i've lived on the island of maui , a very beautiful place .	過去十年 , 我住在馬伊島 , 一個非常美麗的地方 。
now it's one of the greatest mysteries in the universe to my parents how i managed to survive all that time without engaging in anything resembling fulltime employment .	這是宇宙中最偉大的奧秘之一 , 對我父母來說 , 我如何能在沒有全職員工的情況下存活下來 。
i'm going to let you in on that secret .	我將要告訴你們這個秘密 。
this was a view from my home office on maui .	這是我在馬伊的家鄉辦公室的景象 。
and you may have noticed that these beautiful views are similar , but in slightly different places .	你可能注意到這些美麗的觀點相似 , 但在稍微不同的地方 。
that's because this used to be my home and office on maui .	那是因為以前我在毛伊島的家和辦公室 。
i've chosen a very unusual life .	我選擇了一種非常不尋常的生活 。
but not worrying about rent allowed me to spend my time doing what i love .	但不用擔心房租 , 讓我花時間做我愛的事 。
living a nomadic existence has been hard at times , but it's allowed me to live in beautiful places and keep a balance in my life that i've been happy with .	有時遊牧的存在很艱苦 , 但它讓我能住在美麗的地方 , 保持平衡 , 讓我的生活變得很開心 。
it allows me to spend a lot of my time hanging out with hyperintelligent coral .	它讓我花很多時間和超級智慧的珊瑚一起出去 。
but i also greatly enjoy the company of hyperintelligent people .	但我也很享受超級聰明的人的公司 。
so i'm very happy to have been invited here to ted .	我很高興能被邀請來ted 。
chris anderson: i probably understood two percent of that , but i still absolutely loved it . so i'm going to sound dumb .	克里斯•安德森:我大概明白其中的百分之二 , 但我仍然很喜歡 。 所以我要聽起來很蠢 。
your theory of everything garrett lisi: i'm used to coral .	你的所有關於garrettlisi的理論:我習慣珊瑚 。
ca: that's right . the reason it's got a few people at least excited is because , if you're right , it brings gravity and quantum theory together .	克里斯:沒錯 , 讓少數人興奮的原因是 , 如果你對了 , 它會把重力和量子理論結合在一起 。
so are you saying that we should think of the universe , at its heart that the smallest things that there are , are somehow an e8 object of possibility ?	所以 , 你是說 , 我們應該想想宇宙 , 心臟裡有最小的東西 , 就是e8物體的可能性 ?
i mean , is there a scale to it , at the smallest scale , or . . . ?	我的意思是 , 在最小的尺度上 , 是否有一個尺寸 ?
gl: well , right now the pattern i showed you that corresponds to what we know about elementary particle physics that already corresponds to a very beautiful shape .	格林:現在我給你們看的圖案 , 和我們所知的基本粒子物理學有關 , 已經對應到一個非常美麗的形狀 。
and that's the one that i said we knew for certain .	這就是我所說的我們知道的 。
and that shape has remarkable similarities and the way it fits into this e8 pattern could be the rest of the picture .	那個形狀有著驚人的相似性 , 它融入了e8圖案 , 可能是其他的圖片 。
and these patterns of points that i've shown for you actually represent symmetries of this highdimensional object that would be warping and moving and dancing over the space time that we experience .	我給你們看的這些點 , 其實代表的是這個高維度物體的對稱性 , 會在我們體驗的時空中扭曲、移動、跳舞 。
and that would be what explains all these elementary particles that we see .	這會解釋我們所看到的所有基本粒子 。
ca: but a string theorist , as i understand it , explains electrons in terms of much smaller strings vibrating i know you don't like string theory vibrating inside it .	克里斯:但弦理論家 , 我了解它 , 用更小的弦震動來解釋電子 , 我知道你不喜歡弦理論在裡面震動 。
how should we think of an electron in relation to e8 ?	我們該怎麼看待e8的電子 ?
gl: no , it would be one of the symmetries of this e8 shape .	格林:不 , 它是e8形狀的對稱之一 。
so what's happening is , as the shape is moving over spacetime , it's twisting . and the direction it's twisting as it moves is what particle we see . so it would be ca: the size of the e8 shape , how does that relate to the electron ?	所以 , 當這個形狀在時空中移動時 , 它會轉動 。 當它移動時 , 它會轉動的方向是我們看到的粒子 。 克:e8形狀的大小 , 和電子有什麼關係 ?
i kind of feel like i need that for my picture .	我覺得我需要這張照片 。
is it bigger ? is it smaller ?	會更大嗎 ? 會更小嗎 ?
gl: well , as far as we know electrons are point particles , so this would be going down to the smallest possible scales .	格林:就我們所知的電子是點粒子 , 所以這會是最小的可能尺度 。
so the way these things are explained in quantum field theory is , all possibilities are expanding and developing at once .	所以 , 這些東西在量子場理論中解釋的方式是 , 所有可能性都同時擴張和發展 。
and this is why i use the analogy to coral .	這就是為什麼我用比喻珊瑚 。
and in this way , the way that e8 comes in is it will be as a shape that's attached at each point in spacetime .	以這種方式 , e8進來的方式 , 就是它的形狀 , 在時空中每一點都附著 。
and , as i said , the way the shape twists the directional along which way the shape is twisting as it moves over this curved surface is what the elementary particles are , themselves .	正如我所說的 , 形狀的扭曲方向在曲線表面上移動時 , 形狀扭曲的方向是基本粒子本身 。
so through quantum field theory , they manifest themselves as points and interact that way .	所以 , 透過量子場理論 , 他們把自己看成點 , 並以這種方式互動 。
i don't know if i'll be able to make this any clearer .	我不知道我能否更清楚地做這件事 。
ca: it doesn't really matter .	克里斯:這並不重要 。
it's evoking a kind of sense of wonder , and i certainly want to understand more of this .	它喚起了一種奇妙的感覺 , 我當然也想更了解這一點 。
but thank you so much for coming . that was absolutely fascinating .	但非常謝謝你來了 。 這絕對是令人著迷的 。
the legendary chimpanzee researcher jane goodall talks about tacare and her other community projects , which help people in booming african towns live sidebyside with threatened animals .	傳奇的黑猩猩研究員珍•古爾談到托兒和其它社區計畫 , 協助波普非洲市居住的人們 , 威脅到動物 。
africa , animals , biodiversity , environment , global issues , pollution , primates , science	非洲、動物、生物多樣性、環境、全球議題、污染、靈長類、科學、科學、科學、科學等問題 。
jane goodall helps humans and animals live together	珍古德能協助人類和動物一起生活 。
good afternoon , good evening , whatever .	午安 , 晚安 , 等等 。
we can go , jambo , guten abend , bonsoir , but we can also ooh , ooh , ooh , ooh , ooh , ooh , ooh , ooh , ooh .	我們可以去 , 喔 , 喔 , 喔 , ~ ~ ~ ~ ~ ~ ~ 噢 , 噢 , 噢 , 噢 , 噢 , 噢 , 噢 , 噢 , 噢 。
that is the call that chimpanzees make before they go to sleep in the evening .	這就是黑猩猩在晚上睡覺前的叫聲 。
you hear it going from one side of the valley to the other , from one group of nests to the next .	你聽到它從山谷的一邊移動到另一邊 , 從一群巢穴到下一邊 。
and i want to pick up with my talk this evening from where zeray left off yesterday .	今晚我想跟大家談談 , 昨天的zeray留下來的地方 。
he was talking about this amazing , threeyearold australopithecine child , selam .	他談到這個驚人、三歲的澳大利亞小孩塞拉姆 。
and we've also been hearing about the history , the family tree , of mankind through dna genetic profiling .	我們也聽過關於歷史、家庭樹、人類基因資料的歷史 。
and it was a paleontologist , the late louis leakey , who actually set me on the path for studying chimpanzees .	這是古生物學家 , 最近的路易斯•路易斯•萊克 , 他讓我踏上研究黑猩猩的路上 。
and it was pretty extraordinary , way back then .	當時是非常不凡的 。
it's kind of commonplace now , but his argument was because he'd been searching for the fossilized remains of early humans in africa .	現在有點常見 , 但他的論點是 , 因為他一直在尋找非洲早期人類的化石 。
and you can tell an awful lot about what those beings looked like from the fossils , from the shape of the muscle attachments , something about the way they lived from the various artifacts found with them .	可以看出那些從化石的形狀 , 從肌肉附著的形狀 , 和它們的生存方式有關 。
but what about how they behaved ? that's what he wanted to know .	但他們怎麼做呢 ? 這就是他想要知道的 。
and of course , behavior doesn't fossilize .	當然 , 行為不會化石 。
he argued and it's now a fairly common theory that if we found behavior patterns similar or the same in our closest living relatives , the great apes , and humans today , then maybe those behaviors were present in the apelike , humanlike ancestor some seven million years ago .	他主張 , 現在是個相當常見的理論 , 如果我們在最接近的物種、大猩猩和人類身上找到類似的行為模式 , 那麼也許這些行為出現在七百萬年前 , 人類祖先 。
and therefore , perhaps we had brought those characteristics with us from that ancient , ancient past .	因此 , 也許我們已經把這些特性帶到古代 , 古老的過去 。
well , if you look in textbooks today that deal with human evolution , you very often find people speculating about how early humans may have behaved , based on the behavior of chimpanzees .	嗯 , 如果你看看現今處理人類演化的教科書 , 你常常會發現人們會根據黑猩猩的行為來推測早期人類的行為 。
they are more like us than any other living creature , and we've heard about that during this ted conference .	它們比我們任何其他生物都更像我們 , 在ted會議中我們都聽說過 。
so it remains for me to comment on the ways in which chimpanzees are so like us , in certain aspects of their behavior .	所以 , 對我來說 , 對於黑猩猩和我們來說 , 黑猩猩在某些方面是如此相似的 。
every chimpanzee has his or her own personality .	每隻黑猩猩都有自己的性格 。
of course , i gave them names . they can live to be 60 years or more , although we think most of them probably don't make it to 60 in the wild .	當然 , 我會給他們名字 。 他們可以活到60年或更久 , 雖然我們認為大部分的人可能不會在野外60歲 。
mr . wurzel . the female has her first baby when she's 11 or 12 .	沃茲先生 。 女性生了她11歲或12歲時的第一個寶寶 。
thereafter , she has one baby only every five or six years , a long period of childhood dependency when the child is nursing , sleeping with the mother at night , and riding on her back .	在那裡 , 她每五、六年就有一個嬰兒 , 一個長期的童年依賴 , 當孩子在護理時 , 晚上和母親一起睡覺 , 背上騎著 。
and we believe that this long period of childhood is important for chimpanzees , just as it is for us , in relation to learning .	我們相信長期的童年對黑猩猩來說是很重要的 , 就如同對我們來說 , 與學習有關 。
as the brain becomes ever more complex during evolution in different forms of animals , so we find that learning plays an ever more important role in an individual's life history .	隨著大腦在不同的動物演化過程中變得更複雜所以我們發現學習在個人生命歷史中扮演著更重要的角色
and young chimpanzees spend a lot of time watching what their elders do .	年輕的黑猩猩花了很多時間觀察他們的長者的做法 。
we know now that they're capable of imitating behaviors that they see .	現在我們知道他們有能力模仿他們所看到的行為 。
and we believe that it's in this way that the different toolusing behaviors that have now been seen in all the different chimpanzee populations studied in africa how these are passed from one generation to the next , through observation , imitation and practice , so that we can describe these toolusing behaviors as primitive culture .	我們相信 , 這種方式 , 目前在非洲各個黑猩猩族群中所看到的不同的隔離行為 , 研究這些行為是如何從一個世代傳到下一個世代 , 透過觀察、模仿和練習 , 來形容這些獨立行為是原始文化的行為 。
chimpanzees don't have a spoken language . we've talked about that .	黑猩猩沒有口語 。 我們已經談過了 。
they do have a very rich repertoire of postures and gestures , many of which are similar , or even identical , to ours and formed in the same context . greeting chimpanzees embracing .	它們的確有非常豐富的姿勢和姿勢 , 許多都很相似 , 甚至相同的 , 在同樣的情境中形成 , 希臘的黑猩猩擁抱著 。
they also kiss , hold hands , pat one another on the back .	他們也會親吻、握手、拍手 , 在背後 。
and they swagger and they throw rocks .	牠們游泳 , 扔石頭 。
in chimpanzee society , we find many , many examples of compassion , precursors to love and true altruism .	在黑猩猩社會中 , 我們發現許多許多關於同情心的例子 , 愛和真正的利他主義 。
unfortunately , they , like us , have a dark side to their nature .	不幸的是 , 他們和我們一樣 , 對他們的天性有黑暗的一面 。
they're capable of extreme brutality , even a kind of primitive war .	他們有能力極度殘酷 , 甚至是一種原始的戰爭 。
and these really aggressive behaviors , for the most part , are directed against individuals of the neighboring social group .	這些非常積極的行為 , 大部分的情況下 , 都被指導對抗鄰近社會群體的個體 。
they are very territorially aggressive .	它們是非常激烈的 。
chimpanzees , i believe , more than any other living creature , have helped us to understand that , after all , there is no sharp line between humans and the rest of the animal kingdom .	黑猩猩 , 我相信 , 比任何其他生物都更能幫助我們了解 , 畢竟 , 人類和其他動物王國之間沒有明顯的界線 。
it's a very blurry line , and it's getting more blurry all the time as we make even more observations .	這是一條非常模糊的線 , 每當我們做更多觀察時 , 越來越模糊 。
the study that i began in 1960 is still continuing to this day .	我從1960年開始的研究至今仍持續著 。
and these chimpanzees , living their complex social lives in the wild , have helped more than anything else to make us realize we are part of , and not separated from , the amazing animals with whom we share the planet .	這些黑猩猩 , 活在野外複雜的社交生活 , 幫助我們了解到我們是其中的一部分 , 而不是和我們共享地球的偉大動物 。
so it's pretty sad to find that chimpanzees , like so many other creatures around the world , are losing their habitats .	所以 , 要找到黑猩猩 , 和世界上許多其他生物一樣 , 會失去牠們的棲息地 。
this is just one photograph from the air , and it shows you the forested highlands of gombe .	這只是一張空氣中的照片 , 它展示了戈米貝的森林高地 。
and it was when i flew over the whole area , about 16 years ago , and realized that outside the park , this forest , which in 1960 had stretched almost unbroken along the eastern shore of lake tanganyika , which is where the tiny , 30squaremile gombe national park lies , that a question came to my mind .	大約16年前 , 我飛越整個區域 , 發現在公園之外 , 這片森林在1960年 , 沿著坦尼卡東部的湖岸延伸到幾乎沒有破裂 , 也就是在那兒 , 三十平方公里的戈米爾國家公園 , 這個問題出現在我腦海中 。
" how can we even try to save these famous chimpanzees , when the people living around the national park are struggling to survive ? "	「 我們要如何拯救這些知名的黑猩猩 ? 當這些住在國家公園的人們掙扎著生存 ? 」
more people are living there than the land could possibly support .	更多人住在那裏 , 比陸地還多 。
the numbers increased by refugees pouring in from burundi and over the lake from congo .	難民湧入緬甸的數量也從剛果的湖中增加 。
and very poor people they couldn't afford to buy food from elsewhere .	非常貧窮的人 , 他們買不起其他地方的食物 。
this led to a program , which we call tacare .	這就導致了一個計畫 , 我們稱之為 「 tacare 」 。
it's a very holistic way of improving the lives of the people living in the villages around the park .	這是一種非常全面的改善居住在公園裡的人們的生活方式 。
it started small with 12 villages . it's now in 24 .	從12個村落開始 , 現在已經24歲了 。
there isn't time to go into it , but it's including things like tree nurseries , methods of farming most suitable to this now very degraded , almost desertlike land up in these mountains .	沒有時間深入研究 , 但它包括樹木護士、農業最適合的方法 , 目前在這些山區中幾乎沙漠降落 。
ways of controlling , preventing soil erosion .	控制、防止土壤侵蝕 。
ways of reclaiming overused farmland , so that within two years they can again be productive .	重建過量的農田 , 這樣一來 , 兩年內 , 再次有生產力 。
working to help the villagers obtain fresh water from wells .	為了幫助村民從井裡取得淡水 。
perhaps build some schoolrooms .	也許建造一些學校室 。
most important of all , i believe , is working with small groups of women , providing them with opportunities for microcredit loans .	最重要的是 , 我相信 , 和少數女性合作 , 提供她們機會給微型貸款 。
and we've got , as is the case around the world , about 95 percent of all loans returned .	我們有95%的貸款回來 。
empowering women , working with education , providing scholarships for girls so they can finish secondary school , in the clear understanding that , all around the world , as women's education improves , family size drops .	賦予女性權力 , 與教育合作 , 為女孩提供獎學金 , 讓他們能完成中學教育 , 清楚地了解全世界 , 身為女性的教育改善 , 家庭規模減少 。
we provide information about family planning and about hiv/aids .	我們提供家庭規劃和愛滋病的資訊 。
and as a result of this program , something's happening for conservation .	由於這個計劃的結果 , 保育正在發生 。
what's happening for conservation is that the farmers living in these 24 villages , instead of looking on us as a bunch of white people coming to study a whole bunch of monkeys and by the way , many of the staff are now tanzanian but when we began the tacare program , it was a tanzanian team going into the villages .	保育正在發生的是 , 居住在這24個村落的農夫 , 而不是把我們看成一群白人來研究一群猴子 , 順帶一提 , 許多員工現在是坦尚尼亞人 , 但當我們開始計程程時 , 這是一個坦尚尼亞的團隊進入村落 。
it was a tanzanian team talking to the villagers , asking what they were interested in .	那是坦尚尼亞的團隊 , 和村民談話 , 問他們對什麼有興趣 。
were they interested in conservation ? absolutely not .	他們對保育感興趣嗎 ? 絕對不是 。
they were interested in health ; they were interested in education .	他們對健康有興趣 , 他們對教育有興趣 。
and as time went on , and as their situation began to improve , they began to understand ever more about the need for conservation .	隨著時間過去 , 當他們的情況開始改善 , 他們開始了解保育的需求 。
they began to understand that as the upper levels of the hills were denuded of trees , so you've got this terrible soil erosion and mudslides .	他們開始了解 , 隨著山丘的上層被砍伐 , 所以你就有了這種可怕的土壤侵蝕和泥土 。
today , we are developing what we call the greater gombe ecosystem .	現今 , 我們正在發展所謂的 「 更大的gombe生態系統 」 。
this is an area way outside the national park , stretching out into all these very degraded lands .	這是國家公園外的一個區域 , 向外延伸到這些非常退化的土地 。
and as these villages have a better standard of life , they are actually agreeing to put between 10 percent and 20 percent of their land in the highlands aside , so that once again , as the trees grow back , the chimpanzees will have leafy corridors through which they can travel to interact as they must for genetic viability with other remnant groups outside the national park .	當這些村落有更好的生活水準時 , 他們其實同意把10%到20%的土地放在高地旁邊 , 所以 , 當樹木長回來時 , 黑猩猩會透過這些黑猩猩的走廊 , 讓牠們可以在國家公園以外的其他殘疾團體互動 。
so tacare is a success .	所以tacare是成功的 。
we're replicating it in other parts of africa , around other wilderness areas which are faced with extreme population pressure .	我們在非洲其他地區複製 , 在其他地方 , 面對極端人口壓力 。
the problems in africa , however , as we've been discussing for the whole of these first couple of days of ted , are major problems .	然而 , 非洲的問題 , 正如我們過去幾天在ted討論的一樣 , 都是重大的問題 。
there is a great deal of poverty .	有很大的貧窮 。
and when you get large numbers of people living in land that is not that fertile , particularly when you cut down trees , and you leave the soil open to the wind for erosion , as desperate populations cut down more and more trees , so that they can try and grow food for themselves and their families , what's going to happen ? something's got to give .	當你有大量的居住地 , 不那麼肥沃 , 尤其是當你砍樹 , 把土壤開放給空氣 , 因為絕望的人口減少了更多的樹木 , 這樣他們就能為自己和家人種食物 , 有什麼事會發生 。
and the other problems in not only africa , but the rest of the developing world and , indeed , everywhere what are we doing to our planet ?	而其他的問題不只在非洲 , 還在開發中國家 , 的確 , 無所不在 , 我們對地球做了什麼 ?
you know , the famous scientist , e . o . wilson said that if every person on this planet attains the standard of living of the average european or american , we need three new planets .	著名的科學家威爾森說 , 如果地球上的每一個人都能維持普通的歐洲人或美國人的生活水準 , 我們需要三個新星球 。
today , they are saying four . but we don't have them . we've got one .	今天 , 他們說四個 , 但我們沒有 。 我們有一個 。
and what's happened ? i mean , the question here is , here we are , arguably the most intelligent being that's ever walked planet earth , with this extraordinary brain , capable of the kind of technology that is so well illustrated by these ted conferences , and yet we're destroying the only home we have .	到底發生了什麼事 ? 我的意思是 , 問題是 , 在這裡 , 我們是最聰明的人 , 擁有這個非凡的大腦 , 能夠被ted會議所描述的科技 , 然而我們卻在摧毀我們唯一的家園 。
the indigenous people around the world , before they made a major decision , used to sit around and ask themselves , " how does this decision affect our people seven generations ahead ? "	世界各地的原住民 , 在他們做了重大決策之前 , 曾經坐下來問自己: 「 這個決策會如何影響我們七個世代的人 ? 」
today , major decisions and i'm not particularly talking about africa here , but the developed world major decisions involving millions of dollars , and millions of people , are often based on , " how will this affect the next shareholders' meeting ? "	今天 , 主要的決策 , 我不是特別談論非洲 , 而是已開發國家的主要決策 , 涉及數百萬美金 , 通常都是基於 「 這會影響到下一個股東會議 ? 」
and these decisions affect africa .	這些決策會影響非洲 。
as i began traveling around africa talking about the problems faced by chimpanzees and their vanishing forests , i realized more and more how so many of africa's problems could be laid at the door of previous colonial exploitation .	當我開始在非洲四處旅行時 , 談到黑猩猩和它們消失的森林所面臨的問題 , 我了解到越來越多的非洲問題可以被限制在過去殖民地開發的大門 。
so i began traveling outside africa , talking in europe , talking in the united states , going to asia .	所以我開始在非洲外面旅行 , 在歐洲聊天 , 在美國聊天 , 去亞洲 。
and everywhere there were these terrible problems .	到處都有這些可怕的問題 。
and you know the kind i'm talking about . i'm talking about pollution .	你知道我所說的那種 , 我在談污染 。
the air that we breathe that often poisons us .	我們呼吸的空氣通常會毒害我們 。
the earth is poisoning our foods .	地球正在毒害我們的食物 。
the water water is perhaps one of the most crucial issues that we're going to face in this century and everywhere water is being polluted by agricultural , industrial and household chemicals that still are being sprayed around the world , seemingly with the inability to profit from past experience .	水源也許是我們這個世紀所要面對的最關鍵問題之一 , 及到處都有水污染 , 被農業、工業和家庭化學物質污染 , 這些化學物質仍然在世界各地噴灑 , 似乎無法從過去的經驗中獲利 。
the mangroves are being cut down ; the effects of things like the tsunami get worse .	紅樹林被砍伐 , 海嘯的效應越來越糟 。
we've talked about the soil erosion .	我們已經談過土壤侵蝕 。
we have the reckless burning of fossil fuels along with other greenhouse gasses , so called , leading to climate change .	我們對化石燃料的燃燒量和其他溫室氣體密切 , 稱為氣候變遷 。
finally , all around the world , people have begun to believe that there is something going on very wrong with our climate .	最後 , 全世界的人開始相信氣候上發生了什麼事 。
all around the world climates are mixed up .	全世界的氣候都混合了 。
and it's the poor people who are affected worse .	那些被影響更糟的窮人
it's africa that already is affected .	非洲已經受到影響了 。
in many parts of subsaharan africa , the droughts are so much worse .	在撒哈拉以南非洲的許多地區 , 乾旱變得更糟 。
and when the rain does come , it so often leads to flooding and added distress , and the cycle of poverty and hunger and disease .	當雨來臨時 , 通常會造成洪水 , 加上痛苦 , 以及貧窮、飢餓和疾病的循環 。
and the numbers of people living in an area that the land cannot support , who are too poor to buy food , who can't move away because the whole land is degraded .	住在一個無法支援的地區的人數 , 他們太貧窮了 , 無法購買食物 , 因為整片土地已經退化了 。
and so you get desertification creeping , creeping , creeping as the last of the trees are cut down .	所以你會得到沙漠化的珊瑚礁 , 如同最後一棵樹的最後一棵樹被砍掉 。
and this kind of thing is not just in africa . it's all over the world .	這種東西不只在非洲 , 全世界都有 。
so it wasn't surprising to me that as i was traveling around the world i met so many young people who seemed to have lost hope .	所以 , 我並不意外 , 當我在世界各地旅行時 , 我遇到許多年輕人似乎失去希望 。
we seem to have lost wisdom , the wisdom of the indigenous people .	我們似乎失去了智慧 , 原住民的智慧 。
i asked a question . " why ? "	我問了一個問題: 「 為什麼 ? 」
well , do you think there could be some kind of disconnect between this extraordinarily clever brain , the kind of brain that the ted technologies exemplify , and the human heart ? talking about it in the nonscientific term , in terms of love and compassion . is there some disconnect ?	嗯 , 你認為在這個非常聰明的大腦之間有某種區別嗎 ? ted科技的爆炸 , 人類的心 ? 以非科學的角度 , 談論它 , 以愛和同情的角度來說 , 有沒有其他的連結 ?
and these young people , when i talk to them , basically they were either depressed or apathetic , or bitter and angry . and they said more or less the same thing , " we feel this way because we feel you've compromised our future and there's nothing we can do about it . "	而這些年輕人 , 當我和他們談話時 , 基本上他們不是憂鬱或熱情 , 或厭惡感 , 或憤怒 。 他們說了更多的話: 「 我們會這樣感覺 , 因為我們覺得你已經妥協了我們的未來 , 而我們什麼都做不了 。 」
we have compromised their future .	我們已經妥協了他們的未來 。
i've got three little grandchildren , and every time i look at them and i think how we've harmed this beautiful planet since i was their age , i feel this desperation .	我有三個孫子 , 每當我看著他們時 , 我就會想我們如何傷害這個美麗的星球 , 從我年紀開始 , 我就感到絕望 。
and that led to this program we call roots and shoots , which began right here in tanzania and has now spread to 97 countries around the world .	這就導致了我們稱之為根與芽的計畫 , 起源於坦尚尼亞 , 現在已經擴散到全世界97個國家 。
it's symbolic . roots make a firm foundation .	它是象徵性的 。 樹根會創建一個公司基金會 。
shoots seem tiny ; to reach the sun they can break through a brick wall .	射擊看起來很小 ; 要抵達太陽 , 能穿過磚牆 。
see the brick wall as all these problems we've inflicted on the planet , environmental and social . it's a message of hope .	把磚牆看成我們在地球上所遇到的問題 , 環保和社交問題 。 這是一種希望的訊息 。
hundreds and thousands of young people around the world can break through and can make this a better world for all living things .	世界各地有成千上萬的年輕人可以打破 , 讓這個世界變得更美好 。
the most important message of roots and shoots: every single one of us makes a difference , every single day .	根與芽的最重要的訊息:我們每一個人每天都會有所改變 。
we have a choice . every one of us in this room , we have a choice as to what kind of difference we want to make .	我們有選擇 。 在座的每一個人 , 我們都有選擇 , 選擇要做出什麼樣的差異 。
the very poor have no choice . it's up to us to change things so that the poor have choice as well .	貧窮的人沒有選擇 , 決定要改變事情 , 讓窮人也有選擇 。
the roots and shoots groups all choose three projects .	根與芽團體都選擇三個計畫 。
it depends on how old they are , and which country , whether they're in a city or rural , as to what kinds of projects .	它取決於它們的年齡 , 以及哪個國家 , 不論它們在城市或鄉村 , 都要考慮到什麼樣的計畫 。
but basically , we have programs now from preschool right through university , with more and more adults starting their own roots and shoots groups .	但基本上 , 我們現在有從幼兒園到大學的計畫 , 越來越多的成人開始自己的根部和芽團體 。
and every group chooses , between them , three different kinds of project to make this a better world , recognizing that all these different problems are interconnected and impinge on each other .	每個團體選擇 , 在他們之間 , 三個不同的專案計畫 , 讓這個更好的世界變得更好 , 認知所有這些不同的問題都互相連結 , 互相影響 。
so one of their projects will be to help their own human community .	所以他們的其中一項計畫是幫助他們自己的社區 。
and then , if they're able , they may raise money to help communities in other parts of the world .	接著 , 如果他們能夠的話 , 他們可能會募到錢來協助世界上其他地方的社區 。
one of their projects will be to help animals not just wildlife , domestic animals as well .	其中一項計畫是幫助動物不只是野生動物 , 還有家畜 。
and one of their projects will be to help the environment that we all share .	其中一項計畫是幫助我們共享的環境 。
and woven throughout all of this is a message of learning to live in peace and harmony within ourselves , in our families , in our communities , between nations , between cultures , between religions and between us and the natural world .	在這一切中 , 都包含了一種訊息 , 學習在我們內心的和平和和諧 , 在我們的家庭、我們的社區、國家、文化之間、宗教之間、我們和自然界之間 。
we need the natural world . we cannot go on destroying it at the rate we are .	我們需要自然世界 。 我們不能以我們速度破壞它 。
we not do have more than this one planet .	我們沒有超過這個星球 。
just picking one or two of the projects right here in africa that the roots and shoots groups are doing , one or two projects only in tanzania , in uganda , kenya , south africa , congobrazzaville , sierra leone , cameroon and other groups . and as i say , it's in 97 countries around the world .	只選其中一兩項計畫 , 非洲的根與芽團體正在進行 , 一到兩項項項目只有在坦尚尼亞、肯亞、南非、剛果、獅子山共和國、喀麥隆和其他團體 。 如我所說的 , 世界上97個國家 。
of course , they're planting trees . they're growing organic vegetables .	當然 , 他們種植樹木 , 種植有機蔬菜 。
they're working in the refugee camps , with chickens and selling the eggs for a little amount of money , or just using them to feed their families , and feeling a sense of pride and empowerment , because they're no longer helpless and depending on others with their vegetables and their chickens .	他們在難民營工作 , 用雞和雞來賣蛋 , 或是用它們來餵養家人 , 感受到驕傲和賦權 , 因為他們不再是無助的 , 依靠蔬菜和雞肉來取代別人 。
it's being used in uganda to give some psychological help to exchild soldiers .	它被用在烏干達 , 給予一些心理幫助 , 給予外星士兵 。
doing projects like this is bringing them out of themselves .	做像這樣的專案 , 讓他們自己脫離 。
once again , they're useful members of society .	再一次 , 他們是有用的社會成員 。
we have this program in prisons as well .	我們在監獄也有這個計畫 。
so , there's no time for more roots and shoots now .	所以 , 現在沒有時間可以有更多根和芽 。
but oh , they're also working on hiv/aids .	但喔 , 他們也致力於愛滋病 。
that's a very important component of roots and shoots , with older kids talking to younger ones .	這是根與芽的重要元素 , 年長的孩子和年輕人交談 。
and unwanted pregnancies and things like that , which young people listen to better from other youth , rather than adults .	像這樣的事情 , 年輕人會傾聽其他年輕人的傾聽 , 而不是成人 。
hope . that's the question i get asked as i'm going around the world: " jane , you've seen so many terrible things , you've seen your chimpanzees decrease in number from about one million , at the turn of the century , to no more than 150 , 000 now , and the same with so many other animals .	希望 。 這就是我在世界各地被問的問題: 「 珍 , 你看過這麼多可怕的東西 , 你看過黑猩猩數量減少了 , 從一百萬年開始 , 到現在都不到十五萬 , 和許多其他動物都一樣 。
forests disappearing , deserts where once there was forest .	森林消失 , 曾經有森林的沙漠 。
do you really have hope ? " well , yes .	你真的有希望嗎 ? 」 是的 。
you can't come to a conference like ted and not have hope , can you ?	你不能參加像ted這樣的會議 , 沒有希望 , 對吧 ?
and of course , there's hope . one is this amazing human brain .	當然 , 還有希望 。 一個是令人驚嘆的人類大腦 。
and i mean , think of the technologies .	我的意思是 , 想想科技 。
and i've just been so thrilled , finally , to come to people talking about compost latrines .	最後 , 我非常激動人心 , 來談談作曲車道 。
it's one of my hobbyhorses .	這是我的嗜好之一 。
we just flush all this water down the lavatory , it's terrible .	我們把所有的水都沖到電梯裡 , 真的很糟糕 。
and then talking about renewable energy desperately important .	接著談再生能源 , 迫切重要 。
do we care about the planet for our children ?	我們是否在乎我們的孩子的星球 ?
how many of us have children or grandchildren , nieces , nephews ?	有多少人有小孩或孫子、姪女、姪女 ?
do we care about their future ?	我們是否在乎他們的未來 ?
and if we care about their future , we , as the elite around the world , we can do something about it . we can make choices as to how we live each day .	如果我們在乎他們的未來 , 我們 , 身為世界各地的菁英 , 我們能做點什麼 。 我們可以做出選擇 , 做我們每天的生活 。
what we buy . what we wear .	我們買什麼 , 穿什麼 。
and choose to make these choices with the question , how will this affect the environment around me ?	選擇用問題來做這些選擇 , 這會如何影響我周遭環境 ?
how will it affect the life of my child when he or she grows up ?	當他或她長大後 , 它會如何影響我的孩子的生活 ?
or my grandchild , or whatever it is .	或是我的孫子 , 不管是什麼 。
so the human brain , coupled with the human heart , and we join hands around the world .	人類的大腦 , 與人類的心結合 , 我們加入世界各地的手 。
and that's what ted is helping so well with , and google who help us , and esri are helping us with mapping in gombe national park .	這就是ted的幫助 , google幫助我們 , esri幫助我們繪製在國家公園的地圖 。
all of these technologies we can use .	所有這些我們能使用的科技 。
now let's link them , and it's beginning to happen , isn't it ?	現在讓我們把它們連結起來 , 開始發生 , 對吧 ?
you've heard about it this afternoon . it's beginning to happen .	你們今年下午聽說過 , 已經開始發生了 。
this change , this change . to see change that we must have if we care about the future .	這種改變 , 這種改變 。 若我們在乎未來 , 我們必須看到改變 。
and the next reason for hope nature is amazingly resilient .	而希望大自然的下一個理由是非常有彈性 。
you can take an area that's absolutely destroyed , with time and perhaps some help it can regenerate .	你可以利用一個絕對被摧毀的區域 , 隨著時間 , 或許有些幫助它再生 。
and an example is the tacare program .	一個例子是坦尚尼亞計畫 。
i told you , where a seemingly dead tree stump if you stop hacking them for firewood , which you don't need to because you have wood lots , then in five years you can have a 30foot tree .	我告訴你們 , 看似死掉的樹木 , 如果你停止把它們弄成消防栓 , 那你不需要因為樹木有很多 , 那麼在五年內你就可以有一棵三十英呎的樹 。
and animals , almost on the brink of extinction , can be given a second chance . that's my next book .	幾乎在滅絕的邊緣 , 動物可以給予第二次機會 。 這是我的下一本書 。
it's inspiring . and it brings me to my last category of hope , and we've heard about this so much in the last two days: this indomitable human spirit . this determination of people , the resilience of the human spirit , so that people who you would think would be battered by poverty , or disease , or whatever , can pull themselves up out of it , sometimes with a helping hand , and take their part in society , and take their part in changing the world .	它很鼓舞人心 。 它帶給我最後一類的希望 , 我們在過去的兩天中聽說過這一點:這個不可缺的人類精神 。 這個人類精神的決心 , 人類精神的韌性 , 如此一來 , 那些你認為會被貧窮、疾病所擊垮的人 , 或其他的 , 都可以把他們自己從中拔出來 , 有時 , 有時還能用雙手 , 來參與社會的一部分 , 改變世界的一部分 。
and just to think of one or two people out of africa who are just really inspiring .	只是想一下 , 在非洲 , 有一兩個人真的很鼓舞人心 。
we could make a very long list , but obviously nelson mandela , emerging from 17 years of hard physical labor , 23 years of imprisonment , with this amazing ability to forgive , so that he could lead his nation out the evil regime of apartheid without a bloodbath .	我們可以列出非常長的清單 , 但很顯然 , 尼爾遜•曼德拉 , 從十七年的辛苦實體勞動 , 二十三年的監禁 , 帶著寬恕的能力 , 讓他能帶領國家出種族隔離的邪惡政權 , 卻沒有血腥巴士 。
ken sarowiwa , in nigeria , who took on the giant oil companies , and although people around the world tried their best , was executed .	在奈及利亞 , 肯薩洛伊瓦 , 他採用了巨大的石油公司 , 雖然世界各地的人盡力 , 卻被處決了 。
people like this are so inspirational .	像這樣的人非常鼓舞人心 。
people like this are the role models we need for young africans .	像這樣的人是年輕非洲人所需要的典範 。
and we need some environmental role models as well , and i've been hearing some of them today .	我們也需要一些環保的榜樣 , 今天我已經聽過其中一些 。
so i'm really grateful for this opportunity to share this message again , with everyone at ted .	所以我很感激這個機會 , 能再次和ted的所有人分享這個訊息 。
and i hope that some of us can get together and talk about some of these things , especially the roots and shoots program .	我希望有些人能聚在一起討論這些事 , 特別是根與芽計畫 。
and just a last word on that the young woman who's running this entire conference center , i met her today .	最後一個字 , 那個跑完整個會議中心的年輕女子 , 我今天見到她 。
she came up so excited , with her certificate . she was [in] roots and shoots .	她很興奮 , 用她的證書 , 她是根和芽 。
she was in the leadership in dar es salaam .	她在達爾薩拉姆的領導階層 。
she said it's helped her to do what she's doing .	她說這可以幫助她做她正在做的事 。
and it was very , very exciting for me to meet her and see just one example of how young people , when they are empowered , given the opportunity to take action , to make the world a better place , truly are our hope for tomorrow .	對我來說 , 這對我來說非常令人興奮 , 看到一個例子 , 說明年輕人如何賦予權力 , 因為有機會採取行動 , 讓世界變得更美好 , 真正是我們明天的希望 。
artist dianna cohen shares some tough truths about plastic pollution in the ocean and in our lives and some thoughts on how to free ourselves from the plastic gyre .	藝術家黛安娜•柯恩分享了一些關於海洋中的塑膠污染、生活中 , 以及一些想法 , 來解放我們自己 , 避免塑膠垃圾 。
consumerism , global issues , green , mission blue , oceans , plastic	消費主義、全球議題、綠色任務、藍色、海洋、塑膠等問題、塑膠、塑膠等問題、
dianna cohen: tough truths about plastic pollution	黛安娜•柯恩:關於塑膠污染的艱難事實 。
i'm a visual artist , and i'm also one of the cofounders of the plastic pollution coalition .	我是視覺藝術家 , 我也是塑膠污染聯盟的共同創辦人之一 。
i've been working with plastic bags , which i cut up and sew back together as my primary material for my artwork for the last 20 years .	我和塑膠袋合作 , 在過去二十年間 , 我把這些塑膠袋剪起來 , 再縫合成我的作品作品 。
i turn them into two and threedimensional pieces and sculptures and installations .	我把它們變成二、三維的碎片、雕塑和裝置 。
upon working with the plastic , after about the first eight years , some of my work started to fissure and break down into smaller little bits of plastic .	與塑膠合作 , 大約八年後 , 我的一些作品開始裂縫 , 分解成更小的塑膠 。
and i thought , " great .	我心想: 「 很好 。
it's ephemeral just like us . "	就像我們一樣 。 」
upon educating myself a little further about plastics , i actually realized this was a bad thing .	在教育我自己更進一步談塑膠之後 , 我意識到這是件壞事 。
it's a bad thing that plastic breaks down into smaller little bits , because it's always still plastic .	塑膠會分解成比較小的部分 , 因為它一直都是塑膠 。
and what we're finding is that a lot of it is in the marine environment .	我們發現 , 很多是在海洋環境中 。
i then , in the last few years , learned about the pacific garbage patch and the gyre .	接著 , 在過去幾年 , 我學到了太平洋垃圾堆和垃圾堆 。
and my initial reaction and i think this is a lot of people's first reaction to learning about it is , " oh my god !	我最初的反應是 , 很多人的第一反應是: 「 天啊 !
we've got to go out there and clean this thing up . "	我們得把這東西清理乾淨 。 」
so i actually developed a proposal to go out with a cargo ship and two decommissioned fishing trawlers , a crane , a chipping machine and a coldmolding machine .	所以 , 我真的開發了一個提案 , 用貨櫃船和兩艘退貨拖網漁船 , 一台拖車 , 一台拖車 , 和一台冷貨機 。
and my intention was to go out to the gyre , raise awareness about this issue and begin to pick up the plastic , chip it into little bits and cold mold it into bricks that could potentially be used as building materials in underdeveloped communities .	我的意圖是走出這個議題 , 提高對這個議題的意識 , 開始把塑膠 , 晶片成小小的碎片 , 把它冷藏成磚塊 , 可能被用來當作低調社區內的建築材料 。
i began talking with people who actually had been out to the gyre and were studying the plastic problem in the marine environment and upon doing so , i realized actually that cleaning it up would be a very small drop in the bucket relative to how much is being generated every day around the world , and that actually i needed to back up and look at the bigger picture .	我開始和那些曾經去過健身房的人談話 , 研究海洋環境中的塑膠問題 , 以此類推 , 我了解到 , 清理它將會是非常小的一滴 , 相對於全世界每天生產多少東西 , 我需要回頭看更大的圖像 。
and the bigger picture is: we need to find a way to turn off the faucet .	更大的看法是:我們需要找到一種方法來關掉錯誤 。
we need to cut the spigot of singleuse and disposable plastics , which are entering the marine environment every day on a global scale .	我們需要切割單一和可丟棄的塑膠的位置 , 每天都要在全球的規模下進入海洋環境 。
so in looking at that , i also realized that i was really angry .	所以 , 看著這一點 , 我了解到我真的很憤怒 。
i wasn't just concerned about plastic that you're trying to imagine out in the middle of the pacific ocean of which i have learned there are now 11 gyres , potentially , of plastic in five major oceans in the world .	我不只關心塑膠 , 而是你在太平洋中間想像的 , 我所學到的 , 現在有11個健身房 , 潛在五大洋的塑膠 。
it's not just that gyre of plastic that i'm concerned about it's the gyre of plastic in the supermarket .	我所關心的塑膠不僅僅是超市的塑膠垃圾 。
i'd go to the supermarket and all of my food is packaged in plastic .	我會去超市 , 所有的食物都是塑膠包裝 。
all of my beverages are packaged in plastic , even at the health food market .	我所有的飲料都是塑膠包裝 , 即使是在健康食品市場 。
i'm also concerned about the plastic in the refrigerator , and i'm concerned about the plastic and the toxins that leach from plastic into us and into our bodies .	我也關心冰箱裡的塑膠 , 我關心的是塑膠和塑膠從塑膠進入我們體內的毒素 。
so i came together with a group of other people who were all looking at this issue , and we created the plastic pollution coalition .	所以我和一群人合作 , 他們都在研究這個議題 , 我們創造了塑膠污染聯盟 。
we have many initiatives that we're working on , but some of them are very basic .	我們有很多計畫正在進行 , 但其中有些很基本 。
one is: if 80 to 90 percent of what we're finding in the ocean of the marine debris that we're finding in the ocean is plastic , then why don't we call it what it is .	第一:如果我們在海洋中發現的80%到90%到90%的海洋碎片是塑膠 , 那為什麼我們不把它稱為它 。
recycling everybody kind of ends their books about being sustainable and greening with the idea of recycling .	回收每個人的書 , 內容是要以回收的理念來維持永續和綠化 。
you put something in a bin and you don't have to think about it again .	你把東西放到bin上 , 你不需要再想一次 。
what is the reality of that ?	到底是什麼樣的現實 ?
in the united states , less than seven percent of our plastics are recycled .	在美國 , 少於7%的塑膠回收 。
and if you really look into it , particularly when it comes to plastic bottles , most of it is only downcycled , or incinerated , or shipped to china .	如果你仔細觀察 , 尤其是當談到塑膠瓶時 , 大部分的瓶子都只會下降 , 或被送到中國 。
it is downcycled and turned into lesser things , while a glass bottle can be a glass bottle again or can be used again a plastic bottle can never be a plastic bottle again .	它被拆解 , 變成更少的東西 , 而玻璃瓶可以再次成為玻璃瓶 , 或者再次使用塑膠瓶 , 永遠不會再次成為塑膠瓶 。
so this is a big issue for us .	這對我們來說是個大問題 。
another thing that we're looking at and asking people to think about is we've added a fourth r onto the front of the " reduce , reuse , recycle , " three r's , and that is refuse .	另一件我們正在看的東西 , 要求人們思考的是 , 我們在 「 減少、再利用、回收 」 前面加上第四個環 , 也就是拒絕 。
whenever possible , refuse singleuse and disposable plastics .	無論何時 , 都會拒絕單一使用和可丟棄的塑膠 。
alternatives exist ; some of them are very oldschool .	替代方案存在 ; 有些是很古老的學者 。
i myself am now collecting these cool pyrex containers and using those instead of glad and tupperware containers to store food in .	我現在正在收集這些很酷的pyrex容器 , 而不是用它們來儲存食物 。
and i know that i am doing a service to myself and my family .	我知道我在為自己和家人服務 。
it's very easy to pick up a stainlesssteel bottle or a glass bottle , if you're traveling and you've forgotten to bring your stainlesssteel bottle and fill that up with water or filtered water , versus purchasing plastic bottled water .	如果你在旅行時 , 很容易拿到一瓶無形的瓶子 , 或一瓶玻璃瓶 , 你忘了帶著一瓶無形的鋼瓶 , 填滿水或過濾水 , 和購買塑膠瓶水 。
i guess what i want to say to everybody here and i know that you guys know a lot about this issue is that this is a huge problem in the oceans , but this is a problem that we've created as consumers and we can solve .	我猜我想在這裡對大家說些什麼 , 我知道你們對這個議題了解很多 , 就是這在海洋中是個巨大的問題 , 但這是我們作為消費者所創造的問題 , 我們可以解決的問題 。
we can solve this by raising awareness of the issue and teaching people to choose alternatives .	我們可以藉由提高意識到議題和教導人們選擇替代方案來解決這個問題 。
so whenever possible , to choose alternatives to singleuse plastics .	所以 , 無論何時 , 都選擇單一使用塑膠的替代方案 。
we can cut the stem tide the stem of this into our oceans and in doing so , save our oceans , save our planet , save ourselves .	我們可以把幹細胞切成海洋 , 這樣做 , 拯救我們的海洋、拯救我們的星球、拯救我們自己 。
this demo from pattie maes' lab at mit , spearheaded by pranav mistry was the buzz of ted . it's a wearable device with a projector that paves the way for profound interaction with our environment . imagine " minority report " and then some .	這個ptiemaes在麻省理工學院的實驗室的示範 , 由pranavyyy's推行的 , 是ted的推動裝置 。 這是一個可以穿戴的裝置 , 讓它和我們的環境產生共鳴 。 想像一下 「 少數民族報告 」 , 然後有些 。
demo , design , interface design , technology	展示、設計、介面設計、科技、科技、科技等 。
pattie maes and pranav mistry demo sixthsense	pattimaes和pranavdedemose第六感測器 。
i've been intrigued by this question of whether we could evolve or develop a sixth sense a sense that would give us seamless access and easy access to metainformation or information that may exist somewhere that may be relevant to help us make the right decision about whatever it is that we're coming across .	我對這個問題很感興趣 , 究竟我們能否進化或發展出第六感 , 一種感覺 , 可以讓我們無縫、容易取得新陳代謝 , 或資訊 , 可能存在於某處 , 可以協助我們做出正確的決定 , 去做對的決定 。
and some of you may argue , well , don't today's cell phones do that already ?	有些人可能會說 , 嗯 , 今天的手機已經這樣做了嗎 ?
but i would say no .	但我會說 「 不 」 。
when you meet someone here at ted and this is the top networking place , of course , of the year you don't shake somebody's hand and then say , " can you hold on for a moment while i take out my phone and google you ? "	當你在ted見到某人時 , 當然是最頂尖的網絡地點 , 你不會握某人的手 , 然後說: 「 你能拿出手機和谷歌嗎 ? 」
or when you go to the supermarket and you're standing there in that huge aisle of different types of toilet papers , you don't take out your cell phone , and open a browser , and go to a website to try to decide which of these different toilet papers is the most ecologically responsible purchase to make .	或當你去超市 , 站在那龐大的廁所紙堆裡 , 你不會拿出手機 , 打開瀏覽器 , 然後去一個網站 , 試著決定哪些不同的廁所紙是最環保的購買方式 。
so we don't really have easy access to all this relevant information that can just help us make optimal decisions about what to do next and what actions to take .	所以 , 我們沒有很容易取得相關資訊 , 只能協助我們做出最佳決定 , 來決定下一步該做什麼 , 以及該採取什麼行動 。
and so my research group at the media lab has been developing a series of inventions to give us access to this information in a sort of easy way , without requiring that the user changes any of their behavior .	所以我在媒體實驗室的研究小組已經開發了一系列的發明 , 讓我們以簡單的方式取得這些資訊 , 不需要使用者改變他們的行為 。
and i'm here to unveil our latest effort , and most successful effort so far , which is still very much a work in process .	我來這裡是要揭露我們最新的努力 , 目前為止 , 大部分的努力都在進行中 , 這仍然是一項工作 。
i'm actually wearing the device right now and we've sort of cobbled it together with components that are off the shelf and that , by the way , only cost 350 dollars at this point in time .	我現在穿著這個裝置 , 我們把它和櫃子上架的零件組合在一起 , 順便說一下 , 目前只有350美元 。
i'm wearing a camera , just a simple webcam , a portable , batterypowered projection system with a little mirror .	我戴著攝影機 , 只是一個簡單的網路攝影機 , 一個可攜式的電池驅動的投影系統 , 一個鏡子 。
these components communicate to my cell phone in my pocket which acts as the communication and computation device .	這些元件在我的口袋裡與我的手機溝通 , 它是溝通和計算設備 。
and in the video here we see my student pranav mistry , who's really the genius who's been implementing and designing this whole system .	在影片中 , 我們看到我的學生帕拉維•米特里 , 他是當時正在實施和設計這個系統的天才 。
and we see how this system lets him walk up to any surface and start using his hands to interact with the information that is projected in front of him .	我們看到這個系統讓他走上任何表面 , 開始用他的雙手和前面投射的資訊互動 。
the system tracks the four significant fingers .	系統追蹤了四隻手指 。
in this case , he's wearing simple marker caps that you may recognize .	在這個例子中 , 他戴著簡單的標記帽子 , 你可能認得出來 。
but if you want a more stylish version you could also paint your nails in different colors .	但如果你想要一個更健全的版本 , 你也可以用不同的顏色來繪製你的指甲 。
and the camera basically tracks these four fingers and recognizes any gestures that he's making so he can just go to , for example , a map of long beach , zoom in and out , etc .	攝影機基本上追蹤這四個手指 , 並辨識出他正在製造的任何手勢 , 例如 , 他可以去看長灘的地圖 , 放大 , 等等 。
the system also recognizes iconic gestures such as the " take a picture " gesture , and then takes a picture of whatever is in front of you .	系統也能辨識出具象徵性的姿勢 , 例如 「 拍照 」 姿勢 , 然後拍下你面前的任何東西 。
and when he then walks back to the media lab , he can just go up to any wall and project all the pictures that he's taken , sort through them and organize them , and resize them , etc . , again using all natural gestures .	當他走回媒體實驗室時 , 他可以走到任何牆上 , 投影他拍的所有照片 , 透過這些照片 , 整理它們 , 將它們放大 , 再次使用各種自然手勢 。
so , some of you most likely were here two years ago and saw the demo by jeff han or some of you may think , " well , doesn't this look like the microsoft surface table ? "	所以 , 在座有些人可能兩年前來到這裡 , 傑夫•漢或者有些人可能會想: 「 這看起來不像微軟的表面桌子嗎 ? 」
and yes , you also interact using natural gestures , both hands , etc .	是的 , 你也會用自然手勢、雙手等等互動 。
but the difference here is that you can use any surface , you can walk to up to any surface , including your hand if nothing else is available and interact with this projected data .	但這裡的差別是 , 你可以用任何表面 , 你可以走到任何表面上 , 包括你的手 , 如果沒有其他東西可以使用 , 並與這個投影資料互動 。
the device is completely portable , and can be . . .	這個裝置是完全可攜帶的 , 可以......
so one important difference is that it's totally mobile .	其中一個很重要的差別是 , 它完全是移動式的 。
another even more important difference is that in mass production this would not cost more tomorrow than today's cell phones and would actually not sort of be a bigger packaging could look a lot more stylish than this version that i'm wearing around my neck .	另外一個更重要的差別在於 , 大量生產 , 明天它不會比現今的手機還多 , 實際上 , 它不會像個更大的包裝 , 看起來會比我穿著脖子的這個版本還多 。
but other than letting some of you live out your fantasy of looking as cool as tom cruise in " minority report , " the reason why we're really excited about this device is that it really can act as one of these sixthsense devices that gives you relevant information about whatever is in front of you .	但 , 除了讓你們有些人覺得很酷的幻想 , 湯姆克魯斯在《少數報告》中 , 我們對這個裝置感到非常興奮的原因之一 , 就是它真的可以作為第六感設備的其中之一 , 讓你知道你面前的任何東西 。
so we see pranav here going into the supermarket and he's shopping for some paper towels .	我們看到帕拉走進超市 , 他在購物一些紙巾 。
and , as he picks up a product the system can recognize the product that he's picking up , using either image recognition or marker technology , and give him the green light or an orange light .	當他拿起產品時 , 系統就能辨識出他撿起的產品 , 使用影像辨識或標記技術 , 並給他綠燈或橘色燈 。
he can ask for additional information .	他可以尋求額外的資訊 。
so this particular choice here is a particularly good choice , given his personal criteria .	所以這個特定的選擇是特別好的選擇 , 因為他個人的標準 。
some of you may want the toilet paper with the most bleach in it rather than the most ecologicallyresponsible choice .	在座有些人可能想要有最多麻煩的馬桶紙而不是最環保的選擇
if he picks up a book in the bookstore , he can get an amazon rating it gets projected right on the cover of the book .	如果他在書店裡拿到一本書 , 他就可以拿到亞馬遜評分 , 書的封面就會被投射出來 。

and so , pranav turns the page of the book and can then see additional information about the book reader comments , maybe sort of information by his favorite critic , etc .	所以 , 帕拉夫轉換了這本書的頁面 , 再看看這本書讀者留言的額外信息 , 可能是他最喜歡的評論家 , 等等 。
if he turns to a particular page he finds an annotation by maybe an expert of a friend of ours that gives him a little bit of additional information about whatever is on that particular page .	如果他轉向某個特定的頁面 , 他會找到一個結論 , 可能是一位朋友的專家 , 給他一些額外的資訊 , 關於那個頁面上的任何東西 。
reading the newspaper it never has to be outdated .	閱讀報紙 , 它永遠不會過時 。
you can get video annotations of the event that you're reading about you can get the latest sports scores etc .	你可以得到你讀過的事件的視覺註解 , 你可以得到最新的運動分數等等 。
this is a more controversial one .	這是更具爭議性的 。
as you interact with someone at ted , maybe you can see a word cloud of the tags , the words that are associated with that person in their blog and personal web pages .	當你和ted的某個人互動時 , 也許你能看到一個標籤的雲 , 和那個人的部落格和個人網頁有關的字詞 。
in this case , the student is interested in cameras , etc .	在這個案例中 , 學生對攝影機感興趣等等 。
on your way to the airport , if you pick up your boarding pass , it can tell you that your flight is delayed , that the gate has changed , etc .	在你到機場的路上 , 如果你拿起你的登機 , 它可以告訴你你的飛機被延遲 , 大門已經改變了 , 等等 。
and , if you need to know what the current time is it's as simple as drawing a watch on your arm .	如果你需要知道目前的時光 , 就像在你的手臂上畫一支手錶一樣簡單 。
so that's where we're at so far in developing this sixth sense that would give us seamless access to all this relevant information about the things that we may come across .	這就是我們目前正在發展的第六感 , 讓我們能無縫地取得所有關於我們可能遇到的相關資訊 。

and his girlfriend is probably not very happy about him either .	他的女朋友可能也不高興他 。
