and who knows , maybe in another 10 years we'll be here with the ultimate sixth sense brain implant .	誰知道 , 也許再過十年 , 我們將會在這裡 , 最終的第六感植入物 。
phyllis rodriguez and aicha elwafi have a powerful friendship born of unthinkable loss . rodriguez' son was killed in the world trade center attacks on september 11 , 2001 ; elwafi's son zacarias moussaoui was convicted of a role in those attacks and is serving a life sentence . in hoping to find peace , these two moms have come to understand and respect one another .	菲利斯•羅德里斯和阿克瓦菲有著強大的友誼 , 出生於不可思議的損失 。 羅德里格斯的兒子在2001年9月11日被殺害 ; 伊爾瓦菲的兒子祖撒拉索瑞亞•莫薩波薩伊被判死於攻擊中的一個角色 , 希望能找到和平 , 這兩位母親能夠理解並尊重他人 。
culture , global issues , politics	文化、全球議題、政治議題、政治議題、
9/11 healing: the mothers who found forgiveness , friendship	9/11療癒:找到寬恕、友誼的母親 。
phyllis rodriguez: we are here today because of the fact that we have what most people consider an unusual friendship .	phyllisrodriguez:我們今天來到這裡 , 是因為我們有很多人認為不尋常的友誼 。
and yet , it feels natural to us now .	但 , 現在我們感覺很自然 。
i first learned that my son had been in the world trade center on the morning of september 11th , 2001 .	我第一次了解到 , 我兒子在2001年9月11日早上在世貿中心 。
we didn't know if he had perished yet until 36 hours later .	我們不知道他是否在36小時後死了 。
at the time , we knew that it was political .	當時 , 我們知道這是政治的 。
we were afraid of what our country was going to do in the name of our son my husband , orlando , and i and our family .	我們害怕我們的國家會以我們兒子的名字來做些什麼 , 奧蘭多 , 我和我們的家人 。
and when i saw it and yet , through the shock , the terrible shock , and the terrible explosion in our lives , literally , we were not vengeful .	但當我看到它 , 透過震驚 , 震驚 , 和我們人生中糟糕的爆炸 , 真的 , 我們沒有復仇 。
and a couple of weeks later when zacarias moussaoui was indicted on six counts of conspiracy to commit terrorism , and the u . s . government called for a death penalty for him , if convicted , my husband and i spoke out in opposition to that , publicly .	幾個禮拜後 , 當zariasmoussaoui被指示了六個陰謀 , 恐怖主義 , 美國政府要求他死刑 , 如果被定罪 , 我的丈夫和我在公開對抗這件事 。
through that and through human rights groups , we were brought together with several other victims' families .	透過這些人權團體 , 我們和其他幾個受害者的家庭結合在一起 。
when i saw aicha in the media , coming over when her son was indicted , and i thought , " what a brave woman .	當我在媒體上看到aicha , 她兒子被指控時 , 我心想: 「 什麼是勇敢的女人 。
someday i want to meet that woman when i'm stronger . "	有一天 , 我想要和那位女士見面 。 」
i was still in deep grief ; i knew i didn't have the strength .	我還在深深的悲傷中 , 我知道我沒有力量 。
i knew i would find her someday , or we would find each other .	我知道我有一天會找到她 , 或者我們會找到彼此 。
because , when people heard that my son was a victim , i got immediate sympathy .	因為 , 當人們聽到我兒子是受害者時 , 我馬上就會有同理心 。
but when people learned what her son was accused of , she didn't get that sympathy .	但當人們學會兒子被指控時 , 她沒有得到同情心 。
but her suffering is equal to mine .	但她的苦難和我一樣 。
so we met in november 2002 , and aicha will now tell you how that came about .	我們在2002年11月見面 , aicha將告訴你這如何發生 。
aicha elwafi: good afternoon , ladies and gentlemen .	aichaelwafi:午安 , 各位先生女士 。
i am the mother of zacarias moussaoui .	我是zariasmoussaoui的母親 。
and i asked the organization of human rights to put me in touch with the parents of the victims .	我要求人權組織讓我聯絡受害者的父母 。
so they introduced me to five families .	所以他們介紹我給五個家庭 。
and i saw phyllis , and i watched her .	我看到了phyllis , 我看著她 。
she was the only mother in the group .	她是群體中唯一的母親 。
the others were brothers , sisters .	其他人則是兄弟姊妹 。
and i saw in her eyes that she was a mother , just like me .	我在她的眼中看到她是母親 , 就像我一樣 。
i suffered a lot as a mother .	我身為母親 , 遭受許多苦難 。
i was married when i was 14 .	我十四歲時結婚 。
i lost a child when i was 15 , a second child when i was 16 .	我十五歲時失去了一個孩子 , 我十六歲時第二個孩子 。
so the story with zacarias was too much really .	所以zacaria的故事實在太多了 。
and i still suffer , because my son is like he's buried alive .	我仍然受苦 , 因為我的兒子就像活著一樣 。
i know she really cried for her son .	我知道她真的為她兒子哭了 。
but she knows where he is .	但她知道他在哪裡 。
my son , i don't know where he is .	我的兒子 , 我不知道他在哪裡 。
i don't know if he's alive . i don't know if he's tortured .	我不知道他是否還活著 , 我不知道他是否被折磨 。
i don't know what happened to him .	我不知道他發生什麼事 。
so that's why i decided to tell my story , so that my suffering is something positive for other women .	這就是為什麼我決定說我的故事 , 所以我的痛苦對其他女性來說是正面的 。
for all the women , all the mothers that give life , you can give back , you can change .	對所有婦女來說 , 所有給予生命的母親 , 你可以回饋 , 你可以改變 。
it's up to us women , because we are women , because we love our children .	這取決於我們女性 , 因為我們是女性 , 因為我們愛我們的孩子 。
we must be handinhand and do something together .	我們必須是手持人 , 一起做點什麼 。
it's not against women , it's for us , for us women , for our children .	不是反對女人 , 而是為了我們 , 對我們女人 , 為我們的孩子 。
i talk against violence , against terrorism .	我反對暴力、對抗恐怖主義 。
i go to schools to talk to young , muslim girls so they don't accept to be married against their will very young .	我去學校跟年輕的穆斯林女孩說話 , 他們不接受嫁給他們很年輕的意願 。
so if i can save one of the young girls , and avoid that they get married and suffer as much as i did , well this is something good .	所以 , 如果我能拯救其中一位年輕女孩 , 避免他們結婚和受苦 , 嗯 , 這是好事 。
this is why i'm here in front of you .	這就是為什麼我站在你們面前 。
pr: i would like to say that i have learned so much from aicha , starting with that day we had our very first meeting with other family members which was a very private meeting with security , because it was november 2002 , and , frankly , we were afraid of the superpatriotism of that time in the country those of us family members .	帕特.羅斯:我想說我從阿里卡學到了很多 , 從那天開始 , 我們第一次和其他家庭成員開會 , 那是個非常私人的會議 , 因為2002年11月 , 坦白說 , 我們害怕當時在這個國家 , 那些我們家庭成員 。
but we were all so nervous .	但我們都很緊張 。
" why does she want to meet us ? "	「 她為什麼要和我們見面 ? 」
and then she was nervous .	然後她緊張了 。
" why did we want to meet her ? "	「 我們為什麼要和她見面 ? 」
what did we want from each other ?	我們彼此想要什麼 ?
before we knew each others' names , or anything , we had embraced and wept .	在我們知道彼此的名字之前 , 或任何東西之前 , 我們都擁抱了和哭泣 。
then we sat in a circle with support , with help , from people experienced in this kind of reconciliation .	接著 , 我們坐在一個有幫助的圈子裡 , 從人們在這種和解的環境中經歷過 。
and aicha started , and she said , " i don't know if my son is guilty or innocent , but i want to tell you how sorry i am for what happened to your families .	aicha開始 , 她說: 「 我不知道我的兒子有沒有罪惡感或無辜 , 但我想告訴各位 , 我對你的家人有多麼抱歉 。
i know what it is to suffer , and i feel that if there is a crime , a person should be tried fairly and punished . "	我知道 , 受苦是什麼 , 我覺得如果有犯罪 , 一個人應該被公平地審判、懲罰 。 」
but she reached out to us in that way , and it was , i'd like to say , it was an icebreaker .	但她以這種方式向我們伸出援手 , 我想說的是 , 那是個冰箱 。
and what happened then is we all told our stories , and we all connected as human beings .	接下來發生的是 , 我們都說出我們的故事 , 我們都和人類連結在一起 。
by the end of the afternoon it was about three hours after lunch we'd felt as if we'd known each other forever .	下午結束時 , 午餐後約三小時 , 我們感覺好像永遠都知道彼此 。
now what i learned from her , is a woman , not only who could be so generous under these present circumstances and what it was then , and what was being done to her son , but the life she's had .	我從她身上學到的是 , 一個女人 , 不僅可以在這些當下的情況下如此慷慨 , 還有她兒子做了什麼 , 她的人生也是如此 。
i never had met someone with such a hard life , from such a totally different culture and environment from my own .	我從來沒有遇過過這麼艱苦的人生 , 來自完全不同的文化和環境 。
and i feel that we have a special connection , which i value very much .	我覺得我們有一種特殊的連結 , 我非常重視它 。
and i think it's all about being afraid of the other , but making that step and then realizing , " hey , this wasn't so hard .	我認為這一切都是為了害怕他人 , 但要踏出那一步 , 然後意識到: 「 嘿 , 這並不難 。
who else can i meet that i don't know , or that i'm so different from ? "	我還能遇到誰 , 我不知道 , 還是和我這麼不同 ? 」
so , aicha , do you have a couple of words for conclusion ?	所以 , 亞克哈 , 你有幾個字要結論嗎 ?
because our time is up .	因為我們的時間到了 。
aw: i wanted to say that we have to try to know other people , the other .	伊莎貝爾:我想說我們必須試著認識其他人 。
you have to be generous , and your hearts must be generous , your mind must be generous .	你必須要慷慨慷慨 , 你的心一定是慷慨的 , 你的心智一定是慷慨的 。
you must be tolerant .	你一定是寬容的 。
you have to fight against violence .	你必須對抗暴力 。
and i hope that someday we'll all live together in peace and respecting each other .	我希望有一天 , 我們都能一起生活在和平中 , 尊重彼此 。
this is what i wanted to say .	這是我想要說的 。
too much of the world lacks access to clean drinking water . engineer michael pritchard did something about it inventing the portable lifesaver filter , which can make the most revolting water drinkable in seconds . an amazing demo from tedglobal 2009 .	太多世界都缺乏乾淨飲用水工程師michaelpritchard做了些事情 , 發明可攜式的救生水過濾器 , 可以在幾秒鐘內製造出最可飲用的水 。 這是來自tedglobal2009年的驚人展示 。
business , demo , design , global issues , invention , technology , water	商業、展示、設計、全球議題、發明、技術、水資源、水資源、水資源、

i'd like to talk about a couple of things today .	今天我想談談幾件事 。
the first thing is water .	首先是水 。
now i see you've all been enjoying the water that's been provided for you here at the conference , over the past couple of days .	現在我看到你們都很享受在研討會上提供的水 , 在過去的幾天裡 。
and i'm sure you'll feel that it's from a safe source .	我相信你們會覺得這是安全的來源 。
but what if it wasn't ?	但如果不是這樣呢 ?
what if it was from a source like this ?	如果它是從像這樣的來源呢 ?
then statistics would actually say that half of you would now be suffering with diarrhea .	然後統計數字會說 , 你們當中有一半的人會受腹瀉所苦 。
i talked a lot in the past about statistics , and the provision of safe drinking water for all .	過去我談了很多關於統計學的議題 , 以及為所有人提供安全飲用水的條款 。
but they just don't seem to get through .	但他們似乎不會經歷 。
and i think i've worked out why .	我想我已經搞清楚為什麼了 。
it's because , using current thinking , the scale of the problem just seems too huge to contemplate solving .	因為 , 用當前的思考 , 問題的規模似乎太大了 , 無法去思考解決問題 。
so we just switch off: us , governments and aid agencies .	所以我們就關掉了:我們、政府和援助機構 。
well , today , i'd like to show you that through thinking differently , the problem has been solved .	今天 , 我想用不同的思維來告訴你 , 問題已經解決了 。
by the way , since i've been speaking , another 13 , 000 people around the world are suffering now with diarrhea .	順道一提 , 自從我開始講話 , 世界各地有1萬3千人遭受腹瀉的苦難 。
and four children have just died .	四個孩子剛死去 。
i invented lifesaver bottle because i got angry .	我發明了救生員瓶 , 因為我生氣了 。
i , like most of you , was sitting down , the day after christmas in 2004 , when i was watching the devastating news of the asian tsunami as it rolled in , playing out on tv .	我和大部分人一樣 , 2004年聖誕節過後的那一天 , 我看著亞洲海嘯發出的令人沮喪的消息 , 在電視上演出 。
the days and weeks that followed , people fleeing to the hills , being forced to drink contaminated water or face death .	接下來的幾週 , 人們逃到山丘 , 被迫喝污染的水或面臨死亡 。
that really stuck with me .	這真的困擾著我 。
then , a few months later , hurricane katrina slammed into the side of america .	幾個月後 , 颶風卡崔娜陷入美國的一邊 。
" okay , " i thought , " here's a first world country , let's see what they can do . "	「 好吧 , 」 我心想: 「 這是第一個世界國家 , 讓我們看看他們能做什麼 。 」
do you know it took five days to get water to the superdome ?	你知道要花五天才能把水送到超級大眾嗎 ?
people were shooting each other on the streets for tv sets and water .	人們在街上互相拍攝電視機和水 。
that's when i decided i had to do something .	那是我決定要做點什麼的時候 。
now i spent a lot of time in my garage , over the next weeks and months , and also in my kitchen much to the dismay of my wife .	現在我花了很多時間在我的車庫 , 在接下來的幾週和幾個月 , 在我的廚房裡 , 大多是我妻子的煩惱 。
however , after a few failed prototypes , i finally came up with this , the lifesaver bottle .	然而 , 經過幾次失敗的原型之後 , 我終於想出了這個 , 救生員瓶 。
okay , now for the science bit .	好吧 , 現在來談科學 。
before lifesaver , the best hand filters were only capable of filtering down to about 200 nanometers .	在救命之前 , 最好的手過濾器只能過濾到大約200奈米 。
the smallest bacteria is about 200 nanometers .	最小的細菌大約是200奈米 。
so a 200nanometer bacteria is going to get through a 200nanometer hole .	所以 , 一個200奈米的細菌會穿過一個200奈米的洞 。
the smallest virus , on the other hand , is about 25 nanometers .	另一方面 , 最小的病毒大約是25奈米 。
so that's definitely going to get through those 200 nanometer holes .	所以這肯定會穿過那200奈米的洞 。
lifesaver pores are 15 nanometers .	救生員只有15奈米 。
so nothing is getting through .	所以 , 什麼都沒有發生 。
okay , i'm going to give you a bit of a demonstration .	好吧 , 我要給你們一些示範 。
would you like to see that ?	你會想看到嗎 ?
i spent all the time setting this up , so i guess i should .	我花了很多時間把這些設定好 , 所以我猜我應該這樣做 。
we're in the fine city of oxford .	我們在牛津的美好城市 。
so someone's done that up .	所以 , 有人這麼做了 。
fine city of oxford , so what i've done is i've gone and got some water from the river cherwell , and the river thames , that flow through here . and this is the water .	美好的牛津城 , 所以我做的是 , 我已經從河流cherwell找到一些水 , 河流流過這裡 , 這是水 。
but i got to thinking , you know , if we were in the middle of a flood zone in bangladesh , the water wouldn't look like this .	但我想 , 如果我們在孟加拉的洪水區中央 , 水不會像這樣 。
so i've gone and got some stuff to add into it .	所以 , 我已經把一些東西加進去了 。
and this is from my pond .	這是我的池塘 。
have a smell of that , mister cameraman .	聞聞一下 , 攝影師 。
we're just going to pour that in there .	我們只是要把它倒進去 。
michael pritchard: okay . we've got some runoff from a sewage plant farm .	michaelprichard:好的 , 我們有一些從污水農場跑來的 。
so i'm just going to put that in there .	所以我要把它放進去 。
put that in there . there we go .	把它放進去 , 我們就開始了 。
and some other bits and pieces , chuck that in there .	還有一些碎片和碎片 , 把它黏在裡面 。
and i've got a gift here from a friend of mine's rabbit .	我這裡有一位朋友的兔子的禮物 。
so we're just going to put that in there as well .	我們也要把它放進去 。
the lifesaver bottle works really simply .	救生員瓶很簡單 。
you just scoop the water up .	你只能把水吸起來 。
today i'm going to use a jug just to show you all . let's get a bit of that poo in there .	今天我要用jug來展示給你們看 。 讓我們把糞便放進去 。
that's not dirty enough . let's just stir that up a little bit .	這還不夠髒 。 讓我們稍微攪拌一下 。
okay , so i'm going to take this really filthy water , and put it in here . do you want a drink yet ?	好吧 , 我要把這個非常骯髒的水放進這裡 , 你還想喝一杯嗎 ?
okay . there we go .	好了 , 開始了 。
give it a few pumps . okay ?	給它一些幫浦 。 好嗎 ?
that's all that's necessary .	這就是必要的 。
now as soon as i pop the teat , sterile drinking water is going to come out .	一旦我把茶壺拿掉 , 無菌飲用水就會出來 。
i've got to be quick . okay , ready ?	準備好了嗎 ?
there we go . mind the electrics .	就這樣 , 請注意電力 。
that is safe , sterile drinking water .	那是安全、無生命的飲用水 。
there you go chris .	來吧 , 克里斯 。
what's it taste of ?	它的味道是什麼 ?
let's see chris's program throughout the rest of the show . okay ?	我們來看看chris在其他的節目裡的節目 。 好嗎 ?
okay . lifesaver bottle is used by thousands of people around the world .	好了 , 世界上數以千計的人都用過救生龍瓶 。
it'll last for 6 , 000 liters .	它會維持6 , 000公升 。
and when it's expired , using failsafe technology , the system will shut off , protecting the user .	儘管如此 , 使用失敗的技術 , 系統會關閉 , 保護使用者 。
pop the cartridge out . pop a new one in .	把車子送出去 , 把一個新的車進去 。
it's good for another 6 , 000 liters .	另外六千公升是好的 。
so let's look at the applications .	咱們來看看這個應用 。
traditionally , in a crisis , what do we do ?	傳統上 , 在危機中 , 我們該怎麼做 ?
then , after a few weeks , we set up camps .	幾週後 , 我們設立營地 。
and people are forced to come into the camps to get their safe drinking water .	人們被迫進營地 , 來取得安全飲用水 。
what happens when 20 , 000 people congregate in a camp ?	當兩萬人聚集在營地時 , 會發生什麼事 ?
diseases spread . more resources are required .	疾病傳播 , 需要更多資源 。
the problem just becomes selfperpetuating .	問題就變成了自我繁殖 。
but by thinking differently , and shipping these , people can stay put .	但用不同的方式思考 , 運送這些東西 , 人們可以留下來 。
they can make their own sterile drinking water , and start to get on with rebuilding their homes and their lives .	他們可以製造自己的無菌飲用水 , 開始重建他們的家園和生活 。
now , it doesn't require a natural disaster for this to work .	這並不需要自然災害才能成功 。
using the old thinking , of national infrastructure and pipe work , is too expensive .	用舊的想法 , 國家基礎建設和管道工作 , 太貴了 。
when you run the numbers on a calculator , you run out of noughts .	當你在計算機上計算時 , 你就快沒了 。
so here is the " thinking different " bit .	這是 「 思考不同 」 的部分 。
instead of shipping water , and using manmade processes to do it , let's use mother nature . she's got a fantastic system .	不用運送水 , 用人造過程來做 , 讓我們使用大自然 。 她有一個很棒的系統 。
she picks the water up from there , desalinates it , for free , transports it over there , and dumps it onto the mountains , rivers , and streams .	她從上面撿起水 , 免費地將水浸在上面 , 運送到山上、河流和河流上 。
and where do people live ? near water .	人們住在哪裡 ? 靠近水 。
all we've go to do is make it sterile . how do we do that ?	我們要做的就是讓它無菌 。 我們要怎麼做 ?
well , we could use the lifesaver bottle .	嗯 , 我們可以利用救生艇瓶 。
or we could use one of these .	或者 , 我們可以使用其中一個 。
the same technology , in a jerry can .	同樣的技術 , 在jerry的罐子裡 。
this will process 25 , 000 liters of water ; that's good enough for a family of four , for three years .	這會處理2萬5千公升的水 ; 這足夠四個家庭 , 三年來 。
and how much does it cost ?	要花多少錢 ?
about half a cent a day to run .	每天大約半分錢去跑 。
so , by thinking differently , and processing water at the point of use , mothers and children no longer have to walk four hours a day to collect their water .	所以 , 用不同的方式思考 , 並處理用水 , 母親和孩童不再需要每天四個小時來收集水 。
they can get it from a source nearby .	他們可以從附近的源頭取得 。
so with just eight billion dollars , we can hit the millennium goal's target of halving the number of people without access to safe drinking water .	只要花了八十億美金 , 我們就能達到千禧目標的目標 , 目的是要消除沒有安全飲用水的人數 。
to put that into context , the u . k . government spends about 12 billion pounds a year on foreign aid .	若要將它放入情境中 , 英國政府每年花費大約一百二十億英鎊在外國援助上 。
but why stop there ?	但為什麼要停在那裡 ?
with 20 billion dollars , everyone can have access to safe drinking water .	有兩百億美金 , 每個人都可以取得安全飲用水 。
so the threeandahalf billion people that suffer every year as a result , and the two million kids that die every year , will live .	因此 , 每年有三十五億人因此受苦 , 而每年死亡的兩百萬個孩子 , 將會活下來 。
paddy ashdown claims that we are living in a moment in history where power is changing in ways it never has before . in a spellbinding talk at tedxbrussels he outlines the three major global shifts that he sees coming .	帕迪•阿什德宣稱我們生活在歷史上的一個時刻 , 權力從來沒有改變過 。 在tedxbrusel的演講中 , 在他所看到的三大轉變中 , 權力正在改變 。
foreign policy , global issues , politics , world cultures	外交政策、全球議題、政治、世界文化、文化 。
paddy ashdown: the global power shift	帕迪•阿什德:全球的權力轉移 。
there's a poem written by a very famous english poet at the end of the 19th century .	在十九世紀末 , 有一首非常有名的英文詩人寫信 。
it was said to echo in churchill's brain in the 1930s .	在1930年代 , 教堂的大腦中 , 有人說是回應 。
and the poem goes: " on the idle hill of summer , lazy with the flow of streams , hark i hear a distant drummer , drumming like a sound in dreams , far and near and low and louder on the roads of earth go by , dear to friend and food to powder , soldiers marching , soon to die . "	詩歌說: 「 在夏天的山丘上 , 和溪流流的流動 , 我聽到遠方的鼓聲 , 像夢裡的聲音、遠處、低處、低聲 , 在地球的路上 , 親愛的朋友和食物給粉末 , 很快就死了 。 」
those who are interested in poetry , the poem is " a shropshire lad " written by a . e . housman .	對於詩歌感興趣的人 , 詩是《鯊魚鯊》的作者 。
but what housman understood , and you hear it in the symphonies of nielsen too , was that the long , hot , silvan summers of stability of the 19th century were coming to a close , and that we were about to move into one of those terrifying periods of history when power changes .	但霍斯曼所了解的 , 在尼爾森的交響曲中 , 你也聽過它 , 就是19世紀的穩定度很長、很熱的夏天即將到來 , 我們即將進入歷史中最恐怖的時期之一 , 當權力改變時 ,
and these are always periods , ladies and gentlemen , accompanied by turbulence , and all too often by blood .	這些都是經期的 , 各位先生女士先生們 , 伴隨著亂流 , 血流太頻繁 。
and my message for you is that i believe we are condemned , if you like , to live at just one of those moments in history when the gimbals upon which the established order of power is beginning to change and the new look of the world , the new powers that exist in the world , are beginning to take form .	我給各位的訊息是 , 我相信 , 我們被譴責 , 如果你願意 , 生活在歷史上 , 現有的權力秩序開始改變和新的看法 , 世界上存在的新勢力開始形成形式 。
and these are and we see it very clearly today nearly always highly turbulent times , highly difficult times , and all too often very bloody times .	今天我們很清楚地看到它 , 幾乎每次都非常混亂 , 極度困難的時光 , 通常都非常血腥 。
by the way , it happens about once every century .	順道一提 , 它每世紀都會發生一次 。
you might argue that the last time it happened and that's what housman felt coming and what churchill felt too was that when power passed from the old nations , the old powers of europe , across the atlantic to the new emerging power of the united states of america the beginning of the american century .	你可能會說 , 最後一次發生了 , 那就是霍斯曼所感受到的 , 以及教堂所感受到的 , 當權力從舊國家、歐洲的舊勢力 , 跨越大西洋到美國的新興權力 , 美國一世紀初的美國 。
and of course , into the vacuum where the tooold european powers used to be were played the two bloody catastrophes of the last century the one in the first part and the one in the second part: the two great world wars .	當然 , 在真空之中 , 歐洲人曾經有過太多權力在上個世紀的兩場血腥災難中 , 第一部分和第二部分:兩場大戰 。
mao zedong used to refer to them as the european civil wars , and it's probably a more accurate way of describing them .	毛澤東曾經稱他們為歐洲內戰 , 這可能是一種更精確的描述方式 。
well , ladies and gentlemen , we live at one of those times .	各位先生女士 , 我們生活在其中之一 。
but for us , i want to talk about three factors today .	但對我們來說 , 我今天想談三個因素 。
and the first of these , the first two of these , is about a shift in power .	首先 , 這兩者是權力的轉變 。
and the second is about some new dimension which i want to refer to , which has never quite happened in the way it's happening now .	第二 , 我想要指的是新的維度 , 它從來沒有發生過 。
but let's talk about the shifts of power that are occurring to the world .	但我們來談談權力的轉變 , 會發生在世界上 。
and what is happening today is , in one sense , frightening because it's never happened before .	今天發生的事是 , 在某種意義上 , 恐怖 , 因為它從來沒有發生過 。
we have seen lateral shifts of power the power of greece passed to rome and the power shifts that occurred during the european civilizations but we are seeing something slightly different .	我們看到了後續的權力轉變了希臘的力量去羅馬 , 以及在歐洲文明中發生的權力轉變 , 但我們看到了有點不同的東西 。
for power is not just moving laterally from nation to nation .	權力不只從國家移到國家 。
it's also moving vertically .	它也垂直移動 。
what's happening today is that the power that was encased , held to accountability , held to the rule of law , within the institution of the nation state has now migrated in very large measure onto the global stage .	現今所發生的力量是 , 被採取責任的權力 , 以國家的制度 , 移民到全球舞台上 。
the globalization of power we talk about the globalization of markets , but actually it's the globalization of real power .	我們談到全球化市場的全球化 , 但它其實是全球化的權力 。
and where , at the nation state level that power is held to accountability subject to the rule of law , on the international stage it is not .	在國家層面上 , 權力是指責法規的 , 國際舞台上 , 權力不是 。
the international stage and the global stage where power now resides: the power of the internet , the power of the satellite broadcasters , the power of the money changers this vast moneygoround that circulates now 32 times the amount of money necessary for the trade it's supposed to be there to finance the money changers , if you like , the financial speculators that have brought us all to our knees quite recently , the power of the multinational corporations now developing budgets often bigger than mediumsized countries .	國際舞台和全球舞台現在的權力如下:網際網路的力量、衛星廣播的力量、金錢的權力改變了這個巨大的金錢區現在的貿易所需的32倍 , 應該是財務改變者 , 如果你喜歡的 , 金融顧問把我們全都帶到我們的膝蓋上 , 多國企業的權力 , 如今已經發展的預算能力遠大於中國家 。
these live in a global space which is largely unregulated , not subject to the rule of law , and in which people may act free of constraint .	這些人生活在一個極為不受規範的全球空間裡 , 不受法律規範的影響 , 人們可能會不受限制 。
now that suits the powerful up to a moment .	此時此刻 , 強而有力 。
it's always suitable for those who have the most power to operate in spaces without constraint , but the lesson of history is that , sooner or later , unregulated space space not subject to the rule of law becomes populated , not just by the things you wanted international trade , the internet , etc . but also by the things you don't want international criminality , international terrorism .	對那些擁有最大權力的人來說 , 總是適合在空間中運作的人 , 沒有限制 , 但歷史的教訓是 , 不久或之後 , 不受規範空間的規則影響 , 不僅僅是你想要國際貿易、網路等等的事情 。 還有你不想要國際犯罪、國際恐怖主義的東西 。
the revelation of 9/11 is that even if you are the most powerful nation on earth , nevertheless , those who inhabit that space can attack you even in your most iconic of cities one bright september morning .	9/11的揭示是 , 即使你是地球上最強大的國家 , 儘管如此 , 居住的居民 , 空間可以攻擊你 , 即使是在你最明亮的一個九月早晨的城市 。
it's said that something like 60 percent of the four million dollars that was taken to fund 9/11 actually passed through the institutions of the twin towers which 9/11 destroyed .	據說 , 大約有百分之六十的4000萬美金要資助911事件 , 實際上通過雙胞胎塔 , 911事件摧毀了 。
you see , our enemies also use this space the space of mass travel , the internet , satellite broadcasters to be able to get around their poison , which is about destroying our systems and our ways .	我們的敵人也用這個空間 , 大眾旅行、網際網路、衛星廣播人員 , 來圍繞它們的毒害 , 這關乎摧毀我們的系統和方法 。
sooner or later , sooner or later , the rule of history is that where power goes governance must follow .	更早或更早 , 歷史的規則是 , 權力必須遵守 。
and if it is therefore the case , as i believe it is , that one of the phenomenon of our time is the globalization of power , then it follows that one of the challenges of our time is to bring governance to the global space .	假如我相信我們這個時代的一個現象就是全球化的力量 , 那麼我們這個時代的其中一個挑戰就是把治理帶到全球空間 。
and i believe that the decades ahead of us now will be to a greater or lesser extent turbulent the more or less we are able to achieve that aim: to bring governance to the global space .	我相信 , 現在數十年來 , 將會是更大或更少的混亂 , 我們能達成目標:把治理帶到全球 。
now notice , i'm not talking about government .	請注意 , 我不是在談政府 。
i'm not talking about setting up some global democratic institution .	我不是在談建立一些全球民主制度 。
my own view , by the way , ladies and gentlemen , is that this is unlikely to be done by spawning more u . n . institutions .	順便說一下 , 我自己的觀點 , 女士們先生們 , 這種觀點是不太可能發生在聯合國的機構裡 。
if we didn't have the u . n . , we'd have to invent it .	如果我們沒有聯合國 , 我們就得發明它 。
the world needs an international forum .	世界需要國際論壇 。
it needs a means by which you can legitimize international action .	它需要一個能合法化國際行動的手段 。
but when it comes to governance of the global space , my guess is this won't happen through the creation of more u . n . institutions .	但當談到國際空間的治理時 , 我的猜測是 , 這不會發生在聯合國的創造中 。
it will actually happen by the powerful coming together and making treatybased systems , treatybased agreements , to govern that global space .	實際上 , 由強而有力的結合 , 創造出以治療為基礎的系統、條約為基礎的協議 , 來管理這個全球空間 。
and if you look , you can see them happening , already beginning to emerge .	如果你看 , 你可以看到它們正在發生 , 已經開始出現了 。
the world trade organization: treatybased organization , entirely treatybased , and yet , powerful enough to hold even the most powerful , the united states , to account if necessary .	世界貿易組織:條約的組織 , 完全以條約為基礎的組織 , 但 , 強大到足以維持最強大的美國 , 如果必要的話 。
kyoto: the beginnings of struggling to create a treatybased organization .	kyoto:掙扎的開端 , 創造出以約定為基礎的組織 。
the g20: we know now that we have to put together an institution which is capable of bringing governance to that financial space for financial speculation .	g20:我們現在知道 , 我們得要組合一個機構 , 它能夠把治理帶到金融空間 , 來推動金融的金融空間 。
and that's what the g20 is , a treatybased institution .	而g20就是g20所謂的 「 條約 」 機構 。
now there's a problem there , and we'll come back to it in a minute , which is that if you bring the most powerful together to make the rules in treatybased institutions , to fill that governance space , then what happens to the weak who are left out ?	現在有一個問題 , 我們等一下再回來談談一下 , 如果你把最強大的力量集合在一起 , 以以治療為基礎的機構制定規則 , 來填補治理空間 , 那會發生什麼事 ?
and that's a big problem , and we'll return to it in just a second .	那是個大問題 , 我們等一下再回來 。
so there's my first message , that if you are to pass through these turbulent times more or less turbulently , then our success in doing that will in large measure depend on our capacity to bring sensible governance to the global space .	所以 , 我的第一個訊息是 , 如果你多花一點時間通過這些亂流 , 那麼我們的成功會取決於我們的能力 , 取決於我們的能力 , 把合理的管理帶到全球 。
and watch that beginning to happen .	看著這一切開始發生 。
my second point is , and i know i don't have to talk to an audience like this about such a thing , but power is not just shifting vertically , it's also shifting horizontally .	我的第二個重點是 , 我知道我不需要跟這樣的觀眾談談這種事 , 但權力不僅僅是垂直的轉變 , 也是橫向的轉變 。
you might argue that the story , the history of civilizations , has been civilizations gathered around seas with the first ones around the mediterranean , the more recent ones in the ascendents of western power around the atlantic .	你可能會說故事、文明歷史 , 一直以來文明聚集在海洋中 , 最早在地中海地區的文明 , 更近期的西方權力在大西方的後裔 。
well it seems to me that we're now seeing a fundamental shift of power , broadly speaking , away from nations gathered around the atlantic [seaboard] to the nations gathered around the pacific rim .	在我看來 , 我們現在看到的是權力的基本轉變 , 廣泛地說 , 遠離大西洋的國家聚集在太平洋的邊緣 。
now that begins with economic power , but that's the way it always begins .	這就從經濟力量開始了 , 但這也是它始於的開始 。
you already begin to see the development of foreign policies , the augmentation of military budgets occurring in the other growing powers in the world .	你已經開始看到外交政策的發展 , 在世界上其他增長的權力中 , 軍事預算的擴增 。
i think actually this is not so much a shift from the west to the east ; something different is happening .	我認為這其實不是從西方移轉到東方 , 有些不同的事情正在發生 。
my guess is , for what it's worth , is that the united states will remain the most powerful nation on earth for the next 10 years , 15 , but the context in which she holds her power has now radically altered ; it has radically changed .	我的猜測是 , 值得一提的是 , 美國在未來十年 , 將會維持最強大的國家 , 但她擁有的權力現在已經徹底改變了 ; 它徹底改變了 。
we are coming out of 50 years , most unusual years , of history in which we have had a totally monopolar world , in which every compass needle for or against has to be referenced by its position to washington a world bestrode by a single colossus .	我們在五十年後 , 最不尋常的歷史中 , 我們有一個完全不道德的世界 , 在這個世界中 , 每一根同理心的針頭 , 都必須被華盛頓一個單一大腸桿菌所引發 。
but that's not a usual case in history .	但這不是歷史上常見的例子 。
in fact , what's now emerging is the much more normal case of history .	事實上 , 現在正在發生的是更正常的歷史 。
you're beginning to see the emergence of a multipolar world .	你開始看到多重世界的出現 。
up until now , the united states has been the dominant feature of our world .	到目前為止 , 美國是我們世界的主流特徵 。
they will remain the most powerful nation , but they will be the most powerful nation in an increasingly multipolar world .	他們仍然是最強大的國家 , 但他們將是世界各地最強大的國家 。
and you begin to see the alternative centers of power building up in china , of course , though my own guess is that china's ascent to greatness is not smooth .	你開始看到中國的另一種權力中心 , 當然 , 我的猜測是 , 中國的優秀性不是平滑的 。
it's going to be quite grumpy as china begins to democratize her society after liberalizing her economy .	當中國開始將她的社會民主化後 , 她的經濟就會很糟糕 。
but that's a subject of a different discussion .	但這是一個不同的討論題目 。
you see india , you see brazil .	你看到印度 , 你看到巴西
you see increasingly that the world now looks actually , for us europeans , much more like europe in the 19th century .	你可以看到這個世界現在看起來越來越像十九世紀的歐洲人 。
europe in the 19th century: a great british foreign secretary , lord canning , used to describe it as the " european concert of powers . "	歐洲在十九世紀:一個偉大的英國外交秘書 , 名稱是 「 歐洲權力協會 」 。
there was a balance , a fivesided balance .	有一個平衡 , 一個五邊平衡 。
britain always played to the balance .	英國一直都扮演著平衡 。
if paris got together with berlin , britain got together with vienna and rome to provide a counterbalance .	如果巴黎和柏林一起合作 , 英國與維也納和羅馬結合 , 提供一個對立的平衡 。
now notice , in a period which is dominated by a monopolar world , you have fixed alliances nato , the warsaw pact .	請注意 , 在一個由單一世界主導的時期 , 你有固定的盟友nato , 華沙特 。
a fixed polarity of power means fixed alliances .	固定的權力是固定的聯盟 。
but a multiple polarity of power means shifting and changing alliances .	但多重大的權力意味著轉移和改變聯盟 。
and that's the world we're coming into , in which we will increasingly see that our alliances are not fixed .	這就是我們要進入的世界 , 我們會逐漸看到我們的聯盟沒有修復 。
canning , the great british foreign secretary once said , " britain has a common interest , but no common allies . "	偉大的英國外交部長曾說過: 「 英國有共同的利益 , 但沒有共通的盟友 。 」
and we will see increasingly that even we in the west will reach out , have to reach out , beyond the cozy circle of the atlantic powers to make alliances with others if we want to get things done in the world .	我們會看到 , 即使西方國家也會向外伸出援手 , 超越大西洋電廠的舒適圈 , 來和他人結盟 , 如果我們想要在世上做事 。
note , that when we went into libya , it was not good enough for the west to do it alone ; we had to bring others in .	請注意 , 當我們進入利比亞時 , 西方國家不夠好 ; 我們必須讓其他人參與 。
we had to bring , in this case , the arab league in .	在這個案例中 , 我們必須引進阿拉伯聯盟 。
my guess is iraq and afghanistan are the last times when the west has tried to do it themselves , and we haven't succeeded .	我的猜測是伊拉克和阿富汗最後一次 , 西方試圖自己做這件事 , 我們還沒成功 。
my guess is that we're reaching the beginning of the end of 400 years i say 400 years because it's the end of the ottoman empire of the hegemony of western power , western institutions and western values .	我的猜測是400年後 , 我們正要達到西方權力的最初 , 西方制度和西方價值觀的終點 。
you know , up until now , if the west got its act together , it could propose and dispose in every corner of the world .	到目前為止 , 如果西方國家團結起來 , 它可以在世界各個角落提出建議 。
but that's no longer true .	但這已經不是事實了 。
take the last financial crisis after the second world war .	以第二次世界大戰後的金融危機為例 。
the west got together the bretton woods institution , world bank , international monetary fund the problem solved .	西方國家聚集了布雷頓森林機構 , 世界銀行 , 國際貨幣基金--問題解決了 。
now we have to call in others .	現在我們要打電話給別人 。
now we have to create the g20 .	現在我們必須創造g20 。
now we have to reach beyond the cozy circle of our western friends .	現在我們必須超越西方朋友的舒適圈 。
let me make a prediction for you , which is probably even more startling .	讓我預測一下 , 這可能更令人驚訝 。
i suspect we are now reaching the end of 400 years when western power was enough .	我懷疑我們現在已經到了四百年後 , 西方的權力已經足夠了 。
people say to me , " the chinese , of course , they'll never get themselves involved in peacemaking , multilateral peacemaking around the world . "	人們對我說: 「 中國 , 當然 , 他們永遠不會自己參與和平、多邊和平的調停 。 」
oh yes ? why not ?	對嗎 ? 為什麼不呢 ?
how many chinese troops are serving under the blue beret , serving under the blue flag , serving under the u . n . command in the world today ?	有多少中國軍隊在藍色貝雷特下服務 , 在藍色旗幟下服務 , 在聯合國指令下服務 ?
how many americans ? 11 .	有多少美國人 ? 11 。
what is the largest naval contingent tackling the issue of somali pirates ?	索馬利海盜最大的海軍如何處理索馬利亞海盜的問題 ?
the chinese naval contingent .	中國的海軍會議員
of course they are , they are a mercantilist nation .	當然 , 他們是商人國家 。
they want to keep the sea lanes open .	他們想要讓海道保持開放 。
increasingly , we are going to have to do business with people with whom we do not share values , but with whom , for the moment , we share common interests .	漸漸地 , 我們要和我們不共享價值的人做生意 , 同時 , 與誰一起分享共同利益 。
it's a whole new different way of looking at the world that is now emerging .	它是一種全新的看待世界的方式 , 現在正在興起 。
and here's the third factor , which is totally different .	第三個因素 , 完全不同 。
today in our modern world , because of the internet , because of the kinds of things people have been talking about here , everything is connected to everything .	現今在我們的現代世界裡 , 因為網際網路 , 人們一直在談論的事物 , 一切都與一切有關聯 。
we are now interdependent .	我們現在是相互依賴的 。
we are now interlocked , as nations , as individuals , in a way which has never been the case before , never been the case before .	我們現在被聯繫起來 , 作為國家 , 作為個體 , 在以前從來沒有發生過這種情況的情況下 , 從來沒有發生過 。
the interrelationship of nations , well it's always existed .	國家之間的關聯性 , 總是存在 。
diplomacy is about managing the interrelationship of nations .	外交是要管理國家之間的關聯性 。
but now we are intimately locked together .	但現在我們被緊密連結在一起 。
you get swine flu in mexico , it's a problem for charles de gaulle airport 24 hours later .	墨西哥的豬流感 , 24小時後查爾斯迪爾機場出了問題 。
lehman brothers goes down , the whole lot collapses .	雷曼兄弟下降 , 整個崩潰 。
there are fires in the steppes of russia , food riots in africa .	俄羅斯的步伐中有火災 , 非洲的糧食暴動 。
we are all now deeply , deeply , deeply interconnected .	我們現在都深深地相互關聯 。
and what that means is the idea of a nation state acting alone , not connected with others , not working with others , is no longer a viable proposition .	這意味著 , 一個國家單獨的行為 , 而不是和他人連結 , 不再和他人合作 , 也不再是一個可行的提案 。
because the actions of a nation state are neither confined to itself , nor is it sufficient for the nation state itself to control its own territory , because the effects outside the nation state are now beginning to affect what happens inside them .	因為一個國家的行動 , 不管是它本身 , 也不足以控制它自己的領土 , 因為在國外國家的影響已經開始影響它們的內部 。
i was a young soldier in the last of the small empire wars of britain .	我是英國最後一個小型帝國戰爭的年輕士兵 。
at that time , the defense of my country was about one thing and one thing only: how strong was our army , how strong was our air force , how strong was our navy and how strong were our allies .	那時 , 我的國家辯護的重點是一件事 , 只有一件事:我們的軍隊有多強 , 我們的空軍有多強 , 我們的海軍有多強 , 我們的盟友有多強 。
that was when the enemy was outside the walls .	那時候敵人就在牆外 。
now the enemy is inside the walls .	敵人在牆壁裡 。
now if i want to talk about the defense of my country , i have to speak to the minister of health because pandemic disease is a threat to my security , i have to speak to the minister of agriculture because food security is a threat to my security , i have to speak to the minister of industry because the fragility of our hitech infrastructure is now a point of attack for our enemies as we see from cyber warfare i have to speak to the minister of home affairs because who has entered my country , who lives in that terraced house in that inner city has a direct effect on what happens in my country as we in london saw in the 7/7 bombings .	現在 , 如果我想要談我的國家防禦 , 我得要和健康部長談談 , 因為流行病對我的安全是威脅 , 我得要和農業部談談 , 因為糧食安全對我的安全造成威脅 , 我得要和產業部談談 , 因為我們的希臘基礎建設的脆弱 , 現在我們和敵人談 , 我得要談談談 , 談到我們在網路戰役中所見到的影響 , 我得要和國內部的人談談 , 因為在我國內的衝突 , 7個國家 , 那些在我國內部的人 , 對於我們國家來說 , 那些在這個國家的影響 。
it's no longer the case that the security of a country is simply a matter for its soldiers and its ministry of defense .	國家的安全不再僅僅是軍人和國防部的問題 。
it's its capacity to lock together its institutions .	它能夠將它的機構鎖在一起 。
and this tells you something very important .	這告訴各位一件非常重要的事 。
it tells you that , in fact , our governments , vertically constructed , constructed on the economic model of the industrial revolution vertical hierarchy , specialization of tasks , command structures have got the wrong structures completely .	它告訴你 , 事實上 , 我們的政府 , 垂直建構的 , 建立在工業革命的經濟模型上 , 垂直階級制度 , 專門任務 , 指令結構完全錯誤 。
you in business know that the paradigm structure of our time , ladies and gentlemen , is the network .	各位先生女士 , 企業知道我們這個時代的範式結構 , 就是網路 。
it's your capacity to network that matters , both within your governments and externally .	這是你對網路的能力 , 無論在你的政府或外部都很重要 。
so here is ashdown's third law .	這是ashdown的第三個法則 。
by the way , don't ask me about ashdown's first law and second law because i haven't invented those yet ; it always sounds better if there's a third law , doesn't it ?	順便一提 , 不要問我 「 阿什德市第一個法律 」 和 「 第二定律 」 , 因為我還沒發明這些法律 ; 如果有第三個法律 , 聽起來會比較好嗎 ?
ashdown's third law is that in the modern age , where everything is connected to everything , the most important thing about what you can do is what you can do with others .	ashdown的第三條法則是 , 在現代 , 一切都與一切有關 , 最重要的是你能做的事 , 就是你能和他人做的事 。
the most important bit about your structure whether you're a government , whether you're an army regiment , whether you're a business is your docking points , your interconnectors , your capacity to network with others .	最重要的一點是 , 無論你是政府 , 不論你是軍隊註冊 , 不論你是企業的手段 , 你的社交人員 , 你和他人建立連結的能力 。
you understand that in industry ; governments don't .	你明白這一點 , 在工業界 , 政府不懂 。
but now one final thing .	但 , 最後一件事 。
if it is the case , ladies and gentlemen and it is that we are now locked together in a way that has never been quite the same before , then it's also the case that we share a destiny with each other .	如果是這樣的 , 各位先生女士們 , 我們現在以以前從來沒有相同的方式把在一起 , 那也是我們彼此共同命運的案例 。
suddenly and for the very first time , collective defense , the thing that has dominated us as the concept of securing our nations , is no longer enough .	突然間 , 第一次 , 集體防禦 , 主宰了我們國家安全的概念 , 不再足夠 。
it used to be the case that if my tribe was more powerful than their tribe , i was safe ; if my country was more powerful than their country , i was safe ; my alliance , like nato , was more powerful than their alliance , i was safe .	以前 , 如果我的部落比他們的部落更強大 , 我是安全的 ; 如果我的國家比他們的國家強大 , 我是安全的 ; 我的盟國 , 像nato , 比他們的盟友強大 , 我是安全的 。
it is no longer the case .	不再是這樣 。
the advent of the interconnectedness and of the weapons of mass destruction means that , increasingly , i share a destiny with my enemy .	大規模毀滅性武器的出現 , 意味著 , 越來越多 , 我和敵人的命運 。
when i was a diplomat negotiating the disarmament treaties with the soviet union in geneva in the 1970s , we succeeded because we understood we shared a destiny with them .	當我是外交官 , 和1970年代在日內瓦的蘇聯協會談判時 , 我們成功了 , 因為我們知道我們和他們分享了命運 。
collective security is not enough .	集體安全不夠 。
peace has come to northern ireland because both sides realized that the zerosum game couldn't work .	和平來到北愛爾蘭 , 因為雙方都了解到零和遊戲是行不通的 。
they shared a destiny with their enemies .	他們與敵人分享命運 。
one of the great barriers to peace in the middle east is that both sides , both israel and , i think , the palestinians , do not understand that they share a collective destiny .	中東和平的一個大障礙是以色列和巴勒斯坦人 , 不了解他們共同命運 。
and so suddenly , ladies and gentlemen , what has been the proposition of visionaries and poets down the ages becomes something we have to take seriously as a matter of public policy .	所以 , 各位先生女士們 , 一直以來 , 遠見者和詩人的主張 , 都變成了我們必須認真看待公共政策的問題 。
i started with a poem , i'll end with one .	我從一首詩開始 , 以一首詩結束 。
the great poem of john donne's .	約翰•唐恩的偉大詩作 。
" send not for whom the bell tolls . "	「 送出鐘聲給誰 。 」
the poem is called " no man is an island . "	這首詩叫做 「 沒有人是島嶼 」 。
and it goes: " every man's death affected me , for i am involved in mankind , send not to ask for whom the bell tolls , it tolls for thee . "	上面寫著: 「 每個人的死亡都影響著我 , 為了我參與人類 , 不要求鐘聲 , 它會為人發聲 。 」
for john donne , a recommendation of morality .	對約翰唐恩來說 , 道德的建議 。
for us , i think , part of the equation for our survival .	對我們來說 , 我認為 , 是我們生存的一部分 。
to find the path to long life and health , dan buettner and team study the world's " blue zones , " communities whose elders live with vim and vigor to recordsetting age . at tedxtc , he shares the 9 common diet and lifestyle habits that keep them spry past age 100 .	為了找到長壽和健康的路徑 , 丹•布特納和團隊研究世界的 「 藍色區域 」 , 他們的長者和維姆和維爾一起生活 , 在tedxtc記錄年齡的社區 , 他分享了9種常見的飲食和生活方式習慣 , 讓他們能在一百歲以上流行 。
biology , culture , exploration , food , health , life , science	生物、文化、探索、食物、健康、科學、科學、科學 , 及生命 。
dan buettner: how to live to be 100+	danbuetner:如何活到100+1 。
something called the danish twin study established that only about 10 percent of how long the average person lives , within certain biological limits , is dictated by our genes .	所謂的丹麥雙胞胎研究證實 , 只有約10%的平均壽命 , 在某些生物限制之內 , 由我們的基因決定 。
the other 90 percent is dictated by our lifestyle .	剩下的90%是由我們的生活方式決定 。
so the premise of blue zones: if we can find the optimal lifestyle of longevity we can come up with a de facto formula for longevity .	所以藍色區域的前提是:如果我們能找到長壽的最佳生活方式 , 我們就能找到一個長壽的事實公式 。
but if you ask the average american what the optimal formula of longevity is , they probably couldn't tell you .	但如果你問一般美國人 , 長壽的最佳公式是什麼 , 他們可能無法告訴你 。
they've probably heard of the south beach diet , or the atkins diet .	他們可能聽說過南海灘飲食 , 或墨水飲食 。
you have the usda food pyramid .	你有美國食品金字塔 。
there is what oprah tells us .	歐普拉告訴我們什麼 。
there is what doctor oz tells us .	奧茲醫生告訴我們什麼 。
the fact of the matter is there is a lot of confusion around what really helps us live longer better .	事實是 , 對於真正幫助我們活得更久的困惑 , 有很多的困惑 。
should you be running marathons or doing yoga ?	你應該跑馬拉松還是做瑜伽 ?
should you eat organic meats or should you be eating tofu ?	你應該吃有機肉 , 還是要吃豆腐 ?
when it comes to supplements , should you be taking them ?	談到供應 , 你應該帶他們去嗎 ?
how about these hormones or resveratrol ?	荷爾蒙或逆轉荷爾蒙呢 ?
and does purpose play into it ?	目的是否要玩呢 ?
spirituality ? and how about how we socialize ?	靈性 ? 那我們如何社交呢 ?
well , our approach to finding longevity was to team up with national geographic , and the national institute on aging , to find the four demographically confirmed areas that are geographically defined .	我們尋找長壽的方法是和國家地理頻道合作 , 國家老化研究所 , 找出四個人口統計地理定義的區域 。
and then bring a team of experts in there to methodically go through exactly what these people do , to distill down the crosscultural distillation .	接著 , 把一組專家帶到那裡來 , 用準確的方式來處理這些人的做法 , 去除跨文化的分解 。
and at the end of this i'm going to tell you what that distillation is .	最後 , 我要告訴各位這個幻想是什麼 。
but first i'd like to debunk some common myths when it comes to longevity .	但首先我想在長壽時揭露一些常見的迷思 。
and the first myth is if you try really hard you can live to be 100 .	第一個迷思是如果你真的努力去活一百歲
the problem is , only about one out of 5 , 000 people in america live to be 100 .	問題是 , 美國只有五千人當中只有一人活到一百歲 。
your chances are very low .	你的機會非常低 。
even though it's the fastest growing demographic in america , it's hard to reach 100 .	儘管它是美國成長最快的人口 , 但卻很難達到100人 。
the problem is that we're not programmed for longevity .	問題是我們不是為了長壽而設計 。
we are programmed for something called procreative success .	我們被設計為 「 繁榮成功 」 的計畫 。
i love that word .	我愛那個字 。
it reminds me of my college days .	它讓我想起我大學的日子 。
biologists term procreative success to mean the age where you have children and then another generation , the age when your children have children .	生物學家稱之為 「 繁榮成功 」 , 意思是你有孩子的年齡 , 接著是另一代 , 你的孩子有孩子的年齡 。
after that the effect of evolution completely dissipates .	在演化的效應完全消失之後 。
if you're a mammal , if you're a rat or an elephant , or a human , in between , it's the same story .	如果你是哺乳動物 , 如果你是一隻老鼠或一隻大象 , 或是人類之間 , 同樣的故事 。
so to make it to age 100 , you not only have to have had a very good lifestyle , you also have to have won the genetic lottery .	所以要讓它變成100歲 , 你不只需要有良好的生活方式 , 你還得贏得基因彩票 。
the second myth is , there are treatments that can help slow , reverse , or even stop aging .	第二個迷思是 , 有治療方法可以緩慢、反轉 , 甚至停止老化 。
when you think of it , there is 99 things that can age us .	想想看 , 有99件事情可以讓我們老化 。
deprive your brain of oxygen for just a few minutes , those brain cells die , they never come back .	短短幾分鐘 , 腦細胞死亡 , 它們永遠不會回來 。
play tennis too hard , on your knees , ruin your cartilage , the cartilage never comes back .	玩網球太硬 , 膝蓋壞了你的軟骨 , 軟骨永遠不會回來 。
our arteries can clog . our brains can gunk up with plaque , and we can get alzheimer's .	我們的動脈可以部落格 , 我們的大腦可以用斑塊連接 , 我們可以得到阿茲海默症 。
there is just too many things to go wrong .	有太多事情會出錯 。
our bodies have 35 trillion cells , trillion with a " t . " we're talking national debt numbers here .	我們的身體有35兆個細胞 , 裡面有 「 t 」 。 我們在這裡談的是國家債務數字 。
those cells turn themselves over once every eight years .	這些細胞每八年就會轉動一次 。
and every time they turn themselves over there is some damage . and that damage builds up .	每當他們把自己轉過來 , 就會造成一些損害 , 損害就會增加 。
and it builds up exponentially .	它以指數方式建造 。
it's a little bit like the days when we all had beatles albums or eagles albums and we'd make a copy of that on a cassette tape , and let our friends copy that cassette tape , and pretty soon , with successive generations that tape sounds like garbage .	這有點像我們都有披頭四或老鷹專輯的日子 , 我們會在錄音帶上做複本 , 讓我們的朋友複製錄音帶 , 很快地 , 錄音帶的世代聽起來像垃圾 。
well , the same things happen to our cells .	同樣的事也發生在我們的細胞上 。
that's why a 65yearold person is aging at a rate of about 125 times faster than a 12yearold person .	這就是為什麼一個65歲的小孩以比一個12歲的人快125倍的速度老化 。
so , if there is nothing you can do to slow your aging or stop your aging , what am i doing here ?	所以 , 如果沒有東西可以減緩老化或阻止老化 , 我在這裡做什麼 ?
well , the fact of the matter is the best science tells us that the capacity of the human body , my body , your body , is about 90 years , a little bit more for women .	事實上 , 最好的科學告訴我們 , 人體的能力 , 我的身體 , 你的身體 , 大約九十年 , 對女性有更多的幫助 。
but life expectancy in this country is only 78 .	但在這個國家的平均壽命只有78歲 。
so somewhere along the line , we're leaving about 12 good years on the table .	所以在線上某個地方 , 我們在桌子上留下了大約12年的美好年 。
these are years that we could get .	這些年是我們可以得到的 。
and research shows that they would be years largely free of chronic disease , heart disease , cancer and diabetes .	研究指出 , 大部分時間都免於慢性疾病、心臟病、癌症和糖尿病 。
we think the best way to get these missing years is to look at the cultures around the world that are actually experiencing them , areas where people are living to age 100 at rates up to 10 times greater than we are , areas where the life expectancy is an extra dozen years , the rate of middle age mortality is a fraction of what it is in this country .	我們認為把這些消失的最佳方法是看看全世界正在經歷的文化 , 人們生活的比例高達100歲 , 比我們高出10倍 , 人口預期壽命是十幾年 , 中年死亡率是這個國家中年死亡率的一部分 。
we found our first blue zone about 125 miles off the coast of italy , on the island of sardinia .	我們在義大利海岸找到了第一個藍色區域大約125英里 , 位在薩丁尼亞島 。
and not the entire island , the island is about 1 . 4 million people , but only up in the highlands , an area called the nuoro province .	不是整個島嶼 , 島嶼大約有140萬人 , 但只有在高地 , 一個叫做努羅省的地方 。
and here we have this area where men live the longest , about 10 times more centenarians than we have here in america .	在這裡 , 男性壽命最長的區域 , 比美國這裡的百歲人多出十倍 。
and this is a place where people not only reach age 100 , they do so with extraordinary vigor .	這個地方 , 人們不只達到一百歲 , 他們還用非凡的vigor來做 。
places where 102 year olds still ride their bike to work , chop wood , and can beat a guy 60 years younger than them .	在那裡 , 102歲的老年人仍騎自行車去工作 , 秋天 , 可以打敗比他們年輕60歲的人 。
their history actually goes back to about the time of christ .	他們的歷史實際上回到基督時代 。
it's actually a bronze age culture that's been isolated .	它實際上是一個被隔離的青銅時代文化 。
because the land is so infertile , they largely are shepherds , which occasions regular , lowintensity physical activity .	因為土地是如此不公平 , 它們大多是牧羊人 , 常常有低密度的身體活動 。
their diet is mostly plantbased , accentuated with foods that they can carry into the fields .	牠們的飲食主要是以植物為基礎的 , 牠們能帶到田野中 。
they came up with an unleavened whole wheat bread called carta musica made out of durum wheat , a type of cheese made from grassfed animals so the cheese is high in omega3 fatty acids instead of omega6 fatty acids from cornfed animals , and a type of wine that has three times the level of polyphenols than any known wine in the world .	他們想出一塊無遺的麵包 , 叫做carta音樂 , 由土司餵養的動物所組成 , 一種乳酪是高於omega-3脂肪酸 , 而不是omega-6脂肪酸 , 來自玉米動物的脂肪酸 , 還有一種葡萄酒含量比世界上任何人所知的葡萄酒都高三倍 。
but the real secret i think lies more in the way that they organize their society .	但我認為真正的秘密在於他們組織社會的方式 。
and one of the most salient elements of the sardinian society is how they treat older people .	薩丁尼亞社會最瘋狂的元素之一就是他們如何治療老年人 。
you ever notice here in america , social equity seems to peak at about age 24 ?	你有沒有注意到在美國 , 社會平等似乎在24歲時達到高峰 ?
just look at the advertisements .	看看廣告 。
here in sardinia , the older you get the more equity you have , the more wisdom you're celebrated for .	在薩丁尼亞 , 越老越平等 , 你就越有智慧 。
you go into the bars in sardinia , instead of seeing the sports illustrated swimsuit calendar , you see the centenarian of the month calendar .	你走進薩丁尼亞的酒吧 , 不是看到運動繪製的游泳日曆 , 而是月曆的百歲月曆 。
this , as it turns out , is not only good for your aging parents to keep them close to the family it imparts about four to six years of extra life expectancy research shows it's also good for the children of those families , who have lower rates of mortality and lower rates of disease .	事實證明 , 這不僅對你老年的父母來說是好的 , 可以讓他們靠近家人 , 提高大約四到六年的預期壽命研究顯示 , 對那些家庭的孩子來說 , 死亡率和疾病的比率也很高 。
that's called the grandmother effect .	這叫做祖母效應 。
we found our second blue zone on the other side of the planet , about 800 miles south of tokyo , on the archipelago of okinawa .	我們在地球的另一邊發現了第二個藍色區域 , 東京南部大約有800英里 , 位在俄羅斯的阿基拉哥 。
okinawa is actually 161 small islands .	okinawa其實是161個小島 。
and in the northern part of the main island , this is ground zero for world longevity .	在主島的北部 , 世界長壽是零 。
this is a place where the oldest living female population is found .	這是最古老的女性族群所在的地方 。
it's a place where people have the longest disabilityfree life expectancy in the world .	這個地方 , 人們有世界上最長壽的缺陷人數 。
they have what we want .	他們有我們想要的 。
they live a long time , and tend to die in their sleep , very quickly , and often , i can tell you , after sex .	牠們活了很長一段時間 , 往往在牠們的睡眠很快 , 通常 , 我可以告訴你 , 性過後 。
they live about seven good years longer than the average american .	他們的壽命比美國人平均要長七年 。
five times as many centenarians as we have in america .	美國有五倍於百歲人 。
one fifth the rate of colon and breast cancer , big killers here in america .	第五分之一的蟻群和乳癌比率 , 美國的大殺手 。
and one sixth the rate of cardiovascular disease .	心血管疾病的比例是第六 。
and the fact that this culture has yielded these numbers suggests strongly they have something to teach us .	事實是 , 這個文化給了這些數字 , 很明顯他們有東西可以教我們 。
what do they do ?	他們會怎麼做 ?
once again , a plantbased diet , full of vegetables with lots of color in them .	再一次 , 一個以植物為基礎的飲食 , 充滿了許多顏色 。
and they eat about eight times as much tofu as americans do .	他們吃大約八倍的豆類 。
more significant than what they eat is how they eat it .	比他們吃的東西更重要 。
they have all kinds of little strategies to keep from overeating , which , as you know , is a big problem here in america .	他們有各式各樣的小策略來避免過量 , 如你所知 , 在美國 , 是個大問題 。
a few of the strategies we observed: they eat off of smaller plates , so they tend to eat fewer calories at every sitting .	我們觀察到的一些策略:它們吃比較小的盤子 , 所以它們通常會吃比較少的卡路里 。
instead of serving family style , where you can sort of mindlessly eat as you're talking , they serve at the counter , put the food away , and then bring it to the table .	與其提供家庭風格 , 你可以在談話時不經心吃 , 他們會在櫃台上服務 , 把食物送走 , 然後把它帶到桌子上 。
they also have a 3 , 000yearold adage , which i think is the greatest sort of diet suggestion ever invented .	他們也有3000歲的小孩 , 我認為這是史上最偉大的飲食建議 。
it was invented by confucius .	它是由concius發明的 。
and that diet is known as the hara , hatchi , bu diet .	這種飲食就是所謂的 「 哈拉、哈蒂、聖地 」 。
it's simply a little saying these people say before their meal to remind them to stop eating when their stomach is [80] percent full .	簡單來說 , 這些人在吃飯前就說 , 提醒他們在胃裡的百分之八十時就停止飲食 。
it takes about a half hour for that full feeling to travel from your belly to your brain .	要花半小時的時間才能從腹部到腦部旅行 。
and by remembering to stop at 80 percent it helps keep you from doing that very thing .	記住要停在百分之八十的情況下 , 它會幫助你不做這件事 。
but , like sardinia , okinawa has a few social constructs that we can associate with longevity .	但 , 就像薩丁尼亞 , okinawa有幾個社會建設 , 我們能用長壽的方式來連結 。
we know that isolation kills .	我們知道孤立會致命 。
fifteen years ago , the average american had three good friends .	15年前 , 美國平均有三個好朋友 。
we're down to one and half right now .	我們現在已經降到一半了 。
if you were lucky enough to be born in okinawa , you were born into a system where you automatically have a half a dozen friends with whom you travel through life .	如果你夠幸運出生在俄羅來納瓦 , 你生在一個系統中 , 你自動擁有一半的朋友 , 跟你一輩子旅行 。
they call it a moai . and if you're in a moai you're expected to share the bounty if you encounter luck , and if things go bad , child gets sick , parent dies , you always have somebody who has your back .	他們稱之為 「 摩艾 」 。 如果你在摩艾州 , 你被期待要分享這個反彈 , 如果你運氣不好 , 孩子生病 , 父母死亡 , 你總是有一個人有你的背 。
this particular moai , these five ladies have been together for 97 years .	這張特別的moai , 這五位女士已經在一起了97年 。
their average age is 102 .	他們的平均年齡是102歲 。
typically in america we've divided our adult life up into two sections .	通常在美國 , 我們把成人生活分成兩部分 。
there is our work life , where we're productive .	我們的工作有生產力 。
and then one day , boom , we retire .	有一天 , 砰 , 我們退休了 。
and typically that has meant retiring to the easy chair , or going down to arizona to play golf .	一般來說 , 這意味著退休到簡單的椅子上 , 或是到亞利桑那州去玩高爾夫球 。
in the okinawan language there is not even a word for retirement .	在okinawan語言中 , 甚至沒有退休的字 。
instead there is one word that imbues your entire life , and that word is " ikigai . "	取而代之的是 , 一個詞會影響你一生 , 這個詞就是 「 ikigai 」 。
and , roughly translated , it means " the reason for which you wake up in the morning . "	大約是翻譯 , 意思是 「 早上起床的理由 。 」
for this 102yearold karate master , his ikigai was carrying forth this martial art .	對於這位102歲的卡爾特•卡爾博斯特 , 他的ikigai正帶著這場火星藝術 。
for this hundredyearold fisherman it was continuing to catch fish for his family three times a week .	對這位百歲的漁夫來說 , 每週要捕魚三次 。
and this is a question . the national institute on aging actually gave us a questionnaire to give these centenarians .	這是個問題 。 國家老化研究所給了我們一個問卷 , 給這些百歲人 。
and one of the questions , they were very culturally astute , the people who put the questionnaire .	其中一個問題 , 他們是文化上的直覺 , 那些提出問卷的人 。
one of the questions was , " what is your ikigai ? "	其中一個問題是: 「 你的ikigai是什麼 ? 」
they instantly knew why they woke up in the morning .	他們馬上就知道為什麼早上起床 。
for this 102 year old woman , her ikigai was simply her greatgreatgreatgranddaughter .	這位102歲的女子 , 她的ikigai只是她的曾曾曾曾曾孫女 。
two girls separated in age by 101 and a half years .	兩個女孩在101歲和半年間分離 。
and i asked her what it felt like to hold a greatgreatgreatgranddaughter .	我問她 , 拿著一個曾曾曾曾孫女的感覺是什麼樣子 。
and she put her head back and she said , " it feels like leaping into heaven . "	她把頭放回去 , 她說: 「 感覺就像跳進天堂 。 」
i thought that was a wonderful thought .	我覺得那是個很棒的想法 。
my editor at geographic wanted me to find america's blue zone .	我在地理雜誌的編輯希望我找到美國的藍色區域 。
and for a while we looked on the prairies of minnesota , where actually there is a very high proportion of centenarians .	有一陣子 , 我們研究明尼蘇達的草原 , 事實上 , 百歲人的比例很高 。
but that's because all the young people left .	但那是因為所有的年輕人都離開了 。
so , we turned to the data again .	所以 , 我們又轉向資料 。
and we found america's longestlived population among the seventhday adventists concentrated in and around loma linda , california .	我們發現美國最長壽的人口 , 在加州 , 七天的冒險家聚集在倫敦的洛馬林達 ,
adventists are conservative methodists .	冒險家是保守主義者 。
they celebrate their sabbath from sunset on friday till sunset on saturday .	星期五 , 他們在星期五的日落慶祝他們的安息日 。
a " 24hour sanctuary in time , " they call it .	他們稱之為 「 24小時的聖所 」 。
and they follow five little habits that conveys to them extraordinary longevity , comparatively speaking .	他們遵循了五個小習慣 , 傳達給他們非凡的長壽 , 相對來說 , 相對來說 。
in america here , life expectancy for the average woman is 80 .	在美國 , 平均女性平均壽命是80歲 。
but for an adventist woman , their life expectancy is 89 .	但對一位先進主義女性而言 , 他們的壽命是89 。
and the difference is even more pronounced among men , who are expected to live about 11 years longer than their american counterparts .	差別在於 , 比起他們的美國對手 , 他們被期待要活十一年 , 比起他們的美國對手還要久 。
now , this is a study that followed about 70 , 000 people for 30 years .	這個研究追蹤了大約七萬人三十年 。
sterling study . and i think it supremely illustrates the premise of this blue zone project .	很驚人的研究 。 我認為這幾乎說明了這個藍色區域計畫的前提 。
this is a heterogeneous community .	這是一個異性戀族群 。
it's white , black , hispanic , asian .	它是白色、黑色、西班牙裔、亞洲人 。
the only thing that they have in common are a set of very small lifestyle habits that they follow ritualistically for most of their lives .	他們唯一共有的就是一組非常小的生活習慣 , 讓他們習慣過往的生活習慣 。
they take their diet directly from the bible .	他們直接從聖經中取飲食 。
genesis: chapter one , verse [29] , where god talks about legumes and seeds , and on one more stanza about green plants , ostensibly missing is meat .	基因:第一章:第一章 , 第二章 , 上帝談到樂高和種子 , 另一項則是關於綠色植物 , 顯然缺少的是肉類 。
they take this sanctuary in time very serious .	他們認真看待這個保護區 。
for 24 hours every week , no matter how busy they are , how stressed out they are at work , where the kids need to be driven , they stop everything and they focus on their god , their social network , and then , hardwired right in the religion , are nature walks .	每週24小時 , 不論他們多忙 , 工作壓力多大 , 孩子們需要被驅使 , 他們停止一切 , 專注於上帝、社交網路 , 然後 , 在宗教中 , 基本上就是自然行走 。
and the power of this is not that it's done occasionally , the power is it's done every week for a lifetime .	這種力量的力量並不是偶爾會發生 , 它的力量是每週一次都在做 。
none of it's hard . none of it costs money .	沒有困難 , 沒有花錢 。
adventists also tend to hang out with other adventists .	進步主義者也傾向和其他進步主義者相處 。
so , if you go to an adventist's party you don't see people swilling jim beam or rolling a joint .	所以 , 如果你去參加一個冒險家的派對 , 你不會看到有人在游泳吉姆姆姆 , 或是在開關 。
instead they're talking about their next nature walk , exchanging recipes , and yes , they pray .	相反地 , 他們談的是下一個大自然走路 , 交換食譜 , 是的 , 他們祈禱 。
but they influence each other in profound and measurable ways .	但它們會以深刻且可測量的方式影響彼此 。
this is a culture that has yielded ellsworth whareham .	這個文化產出了埃爾斯沃•華瑞漢 。
ellsworth whareham is 97 years old .	埃爾斯•沃爾罕是97歲 。
he's a multimillionaire , yet when a contractor wanted 6 , 000 dollars to build a privacy fence , he said , " for that kind of money i'll do it myself . "	他是個百萬萬富翁 , 但當一個承包商想要蓋一個隱私柵欄時 , 他說: 「 為了那筆錢 , 我自己就這麼做了 。 」
so for the next three days he was out shoveling cement , and hauling poles around .	所以接下來的三天 , 他出去發射水泥 , 拖著水泥到處走 。
and predictably , perhaps , on the fourth day he ended up in the operating room .	也許 , 在第四天 , 他最後到了手術室 。
but not as the guy on the table ; the guy doing openheart surgery .	但不像桌上的那個人 , 做開心手術的人 。
at 97 he still does 20 openheart surgeries every month .	九十七歲時 , 他每個月仍然做二十次開心手術 。
ed rawlings , 103 years old now , an active cowboy , starts his morning with a swim .	愛德華•沃林斯 , 103歲 , 一位活躍的牛仔 , 早上開始了游泳 。
and on weekends he likes to put on the boards , throw up rooster tails .	在週末 , 他喜歡把板子放上去 , 扔上長尾 。
her grandson actually lives in the twin cities here .	她的孫子其實住在雙胞胎城市裡 。
she starts her day with lifting weights .	她的日子開始提升重量 。
she rides her bicycle .	她騎腳踏車 。
and then she gets in her rootbeer colored 1994 cadillac seville , and tears down the san bernardino freeway , where she still volunteers for seven different organizations .	接著 , 她進入了她的根部1994年的凱迪拉克•席維爾 , 在聖貝納多高速公路上 , 她仍然自願參與七個不同的組織 。
i've been on 19 hardcore expeditions .	我曾參加過19次的硬體探險 。
i'm probably the only person you'll ever meet who rode his bicycle across the sahara desert without sunscreen .	我可能是唯一一個你會見到穿越撒哈拉沙漠的自行車的人 。
but i'll tell you , there is no adventure more harrowing than riding shotgun with marge deton .	但我要告訴各位 , 沒有冒險比乘著馬基•德頓騎士更加傷心 。
" a stranger is a friend i haven't met yet ! " she'd say to me .	她會對我說: 「 陌生人是我還沒見過的朋友 ! 」
so , what are the common denominators in these three cultures ?	那麼 , 這三種文化中有什麼共同點呢 ?
what are the things that they all do ?	他們所做的事是什麼 ?
and we managed to boil it down to nine .	我們成功地將它歸為九種 。
in fact we've done two more blue zone expeditions since this and these common denominators hold true .	事實上 , 我們已經完成了兩次藍色區域的探險 , 自此之後 , 這些共同的決策者就成了真的 。
and the first one , and i'm about to utter a heresy here , none of them exercise , at least the way we think of exercise .	首先 , 我即將要說一下 , 這裡沒有一個運動 , 至少我們認為運動的方式 。
instead , they set up their lives so that they are constantly nudged into physical activity .	相反地 , 他們建立了自己的生命 , 使他們不斷地被激發到實體活動中 。
these 100yearold okinawan women are getting up and down off the ground , they sit on the floor , 30 or 40 times a day .	這些百歲的okinawan婦女在地上起床 , 她們每天躺在地板上 , 30或40次 。
sardinians live in vertical houses , up and down the stairs .	薩丁尼亞人住在垂直的房子裡 , 上下樓梯 。
every trip to the store , or to church or to a friend's house occasions a walk .	每次去商店、教堂 , 或給朋友的房子一個散步 。
they don't have any conveniences .	他們沒有任何便利 。
there is not a button to push to do yard work or house work .	沒有一個按鈕 , 來做園藝或房子工作 。
if they want to mix up a cake , they're doing it by hand .	如果他們想要混合蛋糕 , 他們會用手做蛋糕 。
that burns calories just as much as going on the treadmill does .	那燃燒的卡路里就跟跑步機一樣 。
when they do do intentional physical activity , it's the things they enjoy . they tend to walk , the only proven way to stave off cognitive decline , and they all tend to have a garden .	當他們做有意的身體活動時 , 他們很享受的事 。 他們傾向走路 , 唯一能證明脫離認知衰退的方法 , 他們都傾向有花園 。
they know how to set up their life in the right way so they have the right outlook .	他們知道如何以正確的方式建立他們的生活 , 讓他們有正確的外觀 。
each of these cultures take time to downshift .	每種文化都需要時間降低 。
the sardinians pray . the seventhday adventists pray .	薩丁尼亞人祈禱 , 第七天的冒險家祈禱 。
the okinawans have this ancestor veneration .	okinawans有這種祖先的復仇 。
but when you're in a hurry or stressed out , that triggers something called the inflammatory response , which is associated with everything from alzheimer's disease to cardiovascular disease .	但當你在急促或緊張時 , 會觸發一種叫 「 發炎反應 」 的反應 , 和阿茲海默症及心血管疾病有關 。
when you slow down for 15 minutes a day you turn that inflammatory state into a more antiinflammatory state .	當你每天放慢15分鐘 , 將發炎狀態轉變成更抗炎的狀態 。
they have vocabulary for sense of purpose , ikigai , like the okinawans .	他們有目的、ikigai的詞彙 , 像okinawans 。
you know the two most dangerous years in your life are the year you're born , because of infant mortality , and the year you retire .	你知道你人生中最危險的兩年是你出生的那一年 , 因為嬰兒死亡率 , 而你退休的那一年 。
these people know their sense of purpose , and they activate in their life , that's worth about seven years of extra life expectancy .	這些人知道他們的目的 , 他們活在他們的生活中 , 價值約七年的預期壽命 。
there's no longevity diet .	沒有長壽的飲食 。
instead , these people drink a little bit every day , not a hard sell to the american population .	相反地 , 這些人每天都喝一點點酒 , 而不是對美國人口來說很辛苦 。
they tend to eat a plantbased diet .	他們通常會吃植物以來的飲食 。
doesn't mean they don't eat meat , but lots of beans and nuts .	並不是說牠們不吃肉 , 而是很多豆類和堅果 。
and they have strategies to keep from overeating , little things that nudge them away from the table at the right time .	他們有策略可以避免過度 , 那些小事在對的時間點把他們推離桌子 。
and then the foundation of all this is how they connect .	然後這些基礎就是它們如何連結 。
they put their families first , take care of their children and their aging parents .	他們把家人放在第一 , 照顧他們的孩子和他們的老年人 。
they all tend to belong to a faithbased community , which is worth between four and 14 extra years of life expectancy if you do it four times a month .	他們都屬於信仰的社區 , 如果你每個月做四到十四年的預期壽命是值得的 。
and the biggest thing here is they also belong to the right tribe .	最重要的是他們也屬於對的部落 。
they were either born into or they proactively surrounded themselves with the right people .	他們不是生來就在他們身上 , 或是他們積極地把自己和對的人圍繞在一起 。
we know from the framingham studies , that if your three best friends are obese there is a 50 percent better chance that you'll be overweight .	我們從弗蘭明罕研究中得知 , 如果你三個最好的朋友都肥胖 , 你的體重過重的機率會高達50% 。
so , if you hang out with unhealthy people , that's going to have a measurable impact over time .	所以 , 如果你和不健康的人在一起 , 那會隨著時間產生很大的影響 。
instead , if your friend's idea of recreation is physical activity , bowling , or playing hockey , biking or gardening , if your friends drink a little , but not too much , and they eat right , and they're engaged , and they're trusting and trustworthy , that is going to have the biggest impact over time .	取而代之的是 , 如果你的朋友的想法是實體的活動、弓、踢泥巴、腳踏車或園藝 , 如果你的朋友喝了一點點酒 , 但他們吃得不太對 , 而且他們在信任和可信度上 , 那將會是時間最大的衝擊 。
diets don't work . no diet in the history of the world has ever worked for more than two percent of the population .	飲食是行不通的 。 在歷史上 , 沒有飲食 , 超過百分之二的人口 。
exercise programs usually start in january ; they're usually done by october .	運動計畫通常從一月開始 , 通常是十月完成的 。
when it comes to longevity there is no short term fix in a pill or anything else .	當談到長壽時 , 藥丸或其他東西都沒有短暫的修復 。
but when you think about it , your friends are longterm adventures , and therefore , perhaps the most significant thing you can do to add more years to your life , and life to your years . thank you very much .	但當你仔細想想 , 你的朋友是長期冒險 , 因此 , 也許你能做最重要的事 , 讓你能活多年 , 活多年 。 謝謝 。
ink that conducts electricity ; a window that turns from clear to opaque at the flip of a switch ; a jelly that makes music . all this stuff exists , and catarina mota says: it's time to play with it . mota leads us on a tour of surprising and cool new materials , and suggests that the way we'll figure out what they're good for is to experiment , tinker and have fun .	墨水指導電力 ; 一扇窗 , 從清晰轉換到轉換開關的不透明 ; 製造音樂的水母 。 所有這些東西都存在 , 卡塔娜•莫塔說:該是玩的時候了 。 莫塔斯帶領我們進入一個令人驚訝且酷的新材料 , 建議我們如何找出它們對實驗、調整、有趣 。
creativity , design , technology	創造力、設計、科技、科技 。
catarina mota: play with smart materials	克里娜•莫塔:玩聰明的材料 。
i have a friend in portugal whose grandfather built a vehicle out of a bicycle and a washing machine so he could transport his family .	我有個朋友在葡萄牙 , 他的祖父用腳踏車和洗衣機建造了一台車 , 讓他可以運送他的家人 。
he did it because he couldn't afford a car , but also because he knew how to build one .	他這麼做是因為他買不起車 , 但也是因為他知道如何建造一輛車 。
there was a time when we understood how things worked and how they were made , so we could build and repair them , or at the very least make informed decisions about what to buy .	曾經有段時間 , 我們了解事物是如何運作的 , 和它們是如何製造的 , 所以我們能建立並修復它們 , 或是最不知情的決定 , 來決定要買什麼 。
many of these doityourself practices were lost in the second half of the 20th century .	在20世紀後半葉 , 許多這樣的做法迷失了 。
but now , the maker community and the opensource model are bringing this kind of knowledge about how things work and what they're made of back into our lives , and i believe we need to take them to the next level , to the components things are made of .	但現在 , 製造社群和開放原始碼的模型 , 正把知識帶回我們的生活中 , 我相信我們需要把它們帶到下一層 , 帶到組成的元素中 。
for the most part , we still know what traditional materials like paper and textiles are made of and how they are produced .	大部分的時候 , 我們仍然知道紙張和紡織品的傳統材料是什麼 , 以及它們如何製造 。
but now we have these amazing , futuristic composites plastics that change shape , paints that conduct electricity , pigments that change color , fabrics that light up .	但現在我們有了這些驚人、自閉症複合材料 , 可以改變形狀、能導電的顏料、會改變顏色、會亮起來的布料 。
let me show you some examples .	讓我給你們看一些例子 。
so conductive ink allows us to paint circuits instead of using the traditional printed circuit boards or wires .	所以導電墨可以讓我們繪製電路 , 而不是使用傳統印刷電路板或電線 。
in the case of this little example i'm holding , we used it to create a touch sensor that reacts to my skin by turning on this little light .	以我手上的這個小例子為例 , 我們用它來製造接觸感測器 , 打開這個小小的光線 。
conductive ink has been used by artists , but recent developments indicate that we will soon be able to use it in laser printers and pens .	導電墨被藝術家用過 , 但近期發展指出我們很快就能用在雷射印表機和筆上 。
and this is a sheet of acrylic infused with colorless lightdiffusing particles .	這張紙是用無色的光線照射粒子編織出來的 。
what this means is that , while regular acrylic only diffuses light around the edges , this one illuminates across the entire surface when i turn on the lights around it .	這意味著 , 當我打開周圍的燈光時 , 光線只會在周圍的邊緣散開 。
two of the known applications for this material include interior design and multitouch systems .	這材料的兩種已知應用包括內部設計和多層次觸控系統 。
and thermochromic pigments change color at a given temperature .	而熱色色色素會在特定的溫度上改變顏色 。
so i'm going to place this on a hot plate that is set to a temperature only slightly higher than ambient and you can see what happens .	所以我要把這個放在一個熱板上 , 設定在一個溫度上 , 溫度只比環境高一點 , 你可以看到發生什麼事 。
so one of the principle applications for this material is , amongst other things , in baby bottles , so it indicates when the contents are cool enough to drink .	這種材料的其中一個原理是 , 在嬰兒瓶中 , 其它的原理是 , 當內容夠酷時 , 它就會顯示出內容是否能喝酒 。
so these are just a few of what are commonly known as smart materials .	這些只是我們一般所知的智慧材料 。
in a few years , they will be in many of the objects and technologies we use on a daily basis .	幾年後 , 它們會出現在我們每天所使用的許多物品和技術中 。
we may not yet have the flying cars science fiction promised us , but we can have walls that change color depending on temperature , keyboards that roll up , and windows that become opaque at the flick of a switch .	我們還可能還沒有飛行車科幻小說給我們承諾 , 但我們可以用牆來改變顏色 , 取決於溫度、鍵盤 , 以及窗戶 , 會在開關的瞬間轉動 。
so i'm a social scientist by training , so why am i here today talking about smart materials ?	我是受過訓練的社會科學家 , 為什麼我今天在這裡談論智慧型材料 ?
well first of all , because i am a maker .	首先 , 因為我是製造家 。
i'm curious about how things work and how they are made , but also because i believe we should have a deeper understanding of the components that make up our world , and right now , we don't know enough about these hightech composites our future will be made of .	我很好奇事情是如何運作的 , 也是因為我相信我們應該更深入了解構成我們的世界的元素 , 而現在 , 我們對這些高科技複合材料的了解不夠多 。
smart materials are hard to obtain in small quantities .	智能材料很難在小量中取得 。
there's barely any information available on how to use them , and very little is said about how they are produced .	幾乎沒有任何關於如何使用它們的資訊 , 且很少有談到它們是如何產生的 。
so for now , they exist mostly in this realm of trade secrets and patents only universities and corporations have access to .	所以 , 目前 , 它們主要存在於貿易秘密和專利的領域 , 只有大學和企業才能取得 。
so a little over three years ago , kirsty boyle and i started a project we called open materials .	三年前 , 凱西男孩和我開始了一個計畫 , 我們稱之為 「 開放材料 」 。
it's a website where we , and anyone else who wants to join us , share experiments , publish information , encourage others to contribute whenever they can , and aggregate resources such as research papers and tutorials by other makers like ourselves .	這是一個網站 , 我們和任何想加入我們的人 , 分享實驗 , 出版資訊 , 鼓勵他人隨時可以做出貢獻 , 並聚集資源 , 例如其他製造者的研究論文和教學 。
we would like it to become a large , collectively generated database of doityourself information on smart materials .	我們希望它成為一個龐大、集體的資料庫 , 資料庫裡的智慧材料 。
but why should we care how smart materials work and what they are made of ?	但為什麼我們要關心智慧材料如何運作 , 以及它們是由什麼組成的 ?
first of all , because we can't shape what we don't understand , and what we don't understand and use ends up shaping us .	首先 , 因為我們無法形塑我們不了解的事物 , 以及我們不了解和使用的東西 , 最終會塑造我們 。
the objects we use , the clothes we wear , the houses we live in , all have a profound impact on our behavior , health and quality of life .	我們使用的物品、衣服、我們所居住的房子 , 都對我們的行為、健康和生活品質有深遠的影響 。
so if we are to live in a world made of smart materials , we should know and understand them .	所以如果我們活在一個由智慧材料構成的世界裡 , 我們應該要知道並了解它們 。
secondly , and just as important , innovation has always been fueled by tinkerers .	第二 , 同樣重要的是 , 創新一直以來都是由小工人來燃料 。
so many times , amateurs , not experts , have been the inventors and improvers of things ranging from mountain bikes to semiconductors , personal computers , airplanes .	很多時候 , 業餘人士 , 不是專家 , 是發明家和改善了從山腳踏車到半導體、個人電腦、飛機 。
the biggest challenge is that material science is complex and requires expensive equipment .	最大的挑戰是 , 材料科學是複雜且需要昂貴的設備 。
but that's not always the case .	但事實並非如此 。
two scientists at university of illinois understood this when they published a paper on a simpler method for making conductive ink .	伊利諾大學的兩位科學家了解這一點 , 他們發表了一篇論文 , 用比較簡單的方法製造導電墨水 。
jordan bunker , who had had no experience with chemistry until then , read this paper and reproduced the experiment at his maker space using only offtheshelf substances and tools .	jordanbunker , 他一直沒有化學經驗 , 直到那時 , 讀了這篇論文 , 並在他的創作時 , 利用現成的物質和工具來繁殖這個實驗 。
he used a toaster oven , and he even made his own vortex mixer , based on a tutorial by another scientist/maker .	他用烤箱 , 甚至用了自己的旋渦混合器 , 基於另一位科學家/maker的教學 。
jordan then published his results online , including all the things he had tried and didn't work , so others could study and reproduce it .	喬登後來在網路上發表了他的結果 , 包括他曾經嘗試過的所有事情 , 卻沒有成功 , 其他人也能研究並繁殖 。
so jordan's main form of innovation was to take an experiment created in a wellequipped lab at the university and recreate it in a garage in chicago using only cheap materials and tools he made himself .	約旦的創新形式是要在大學的一個良好設備實驗室創造一個實驗 , 並在芝加哥的車庫裡重建這個實驗 , 只使用便宜的材料和工具 。
and now that he published this work , others can pick up where he left and devise even simpler processes and improvements .	現在他發表了這項工作 , 其他人可以拿出他離開的地方 , 設計出更簡單的過程和改善 。
another example i'd like to mention her project's goal is to highlight the expressive qualities of materials while focusing on the creativity and skills of the builder .	另外一個例子 , 我想提一下她的專案計畫的目標 , 是要強調材料的表達特質 , 同時要專注於製造者的創意和技能 。
electronics kits are very powerful in that they teach us how things work , but the constraints inherent in their design influence the way we learn .	電子設備是非常強大的 , 它們教我們事物如何運作 , 但它們設計的限制會影響我們學習的方式 。
so hannah's approach , on the other hand , is to formulate a series of techniques for creating unusual objects that free us from predesigned constraints by teaching us about the materials themselves .	另一方面 , 漢娜的做法是建立一系列的技術 , 來創造出不尋常的物體 , 使我們免於設計限制 , 透過教導我們材料本身 。
so amongst hannah's many impressive experiments , this is one of my favorites .	在漢娜的許多令人印象深刻的實驗中 , 這是我最喜歡的一個實驗之一 。
[ " paper speakers " ] what we're seeing here is just a piece of paper with some copper tape on it connected to an mp3 player and a magnet .	我們現在看到的只是一張紙 , 上面有一些銅膠帶 , 連接到mp3播放器和磁鐵 。
so based on the research by marcelo coelho from mit , hannah created a series of paper speakers out of a wide range of materials from simple copper tape to conductive fabric and ink .	根據麻省理工學院marcelocoelho的研究漢娜創造了一系列的論文從簡單的銅膠帶到導電的布料
just like jordan and so many other makers , hannah published her recipes and allows anyone to copy and reproduce them .	就像約旦和許多其他的製造者漢娜發表了她的食譜讓任何人都能複製並繁殖它們
but paper electronics is one of the most promising branches of material science in that it allows us to create cheaper and flexible electronics .	但紙電子是最有希望的材料科學分支之一 , 它讓我們能創造更便宜、更有彈性的電子 。
so hannah's artisanal work , and the fact that she shared her findings , opens the doors to a series of new possibilities that are both aesthetically appealing and innovative .	漢娜的手工藝作品 , 她分享了她的發現 , 為一系列新的可能性打開了一系列的門 , 這些都是美學上的吸引力和創新 。
so the interesting thing about makers is that we create out of passion and curiosity , and we are not afraid to fail .	所以 , 關於製造者有趣的是 , 我們從熱情和好奇心創造出來 , 我們不怕失敗 。
we often tackle problems from unconventional angles , and , in the process , end up discovering alternatives or even better ways to do things .	我們經常處理不穩定的角度的問題 , 在這個過程中 , 發現了替代方案 , 甚至更好的方式來做事 。
so the more people experiment with materials , the more researchers are willing to share their research , and manufacturers their knowledge , the better chances we have to create technologies that truly serve us all .	所以 , 越多人實驗材料 , 越多研究人員願意分享他們的研究 , 製造出他們的知識 , 我們就越有機會創造出真正服務我們所有人的科技 。
so i feel a bit as ted nelson must have when , in the early 1970s , he wrote , " you must understand computers now . "	我覺得有點像tednelson在1970年代初期 , 他寫道: 「 你現在必須要了解電腦 。 」
back then , computers were these large mainframes only scientists cared about , and no one dreamed of even having one at home .	當時 , 電腦是這些大型的主機 , 只有科學家在乎 , 沒有人夢想在家中有一台 。
so it's a little strange that i'm standing here and saying , " you must understand smart materials now . "	所以這有點奇怪 , 我站在這裡說: 「 你現在必須要了解智慧型材料 。 」
just keep in mind that acquiring preemptive knowledge about emerging technologies is the best way to ensure that we have a say in the making of our future .	請記住 , 取得新興科技的先例知識 , 是確保我們能在未來發聲的最佳方法 。
when we drive , we get into a glass bubble , lock the doors and press the accelerator , relying on our eyes to guide us even though we can only see the few cars ahead of and behind us . but what if cars could share data with each other about their position and velocity , and use predictive models to calculate the safest routes for everyone on the road ? jennifer healey imagines a world without accidents .	當我們開車時 , 我們會進入一個玻璃泡 , 鎖上門 , 按下加速器 , 仰賴我們的眼睛 , 引導我們即使我們只能看到前方幾輛車 , 但如果汽車能和彼此分享他們的位置和速度 , 用預測模型來計算路上所有人最安全的路線 , 珍妮佛•亨利能想像一個沒有意外的世界 。
jennifer healey: if cars could talk , accidents might be avoidable	珍妮佛療癒:如果汽車可以說話 , 意外可能是可避免的 。
let's face it: driving is dangerous .	讓我們面對現實:開車是危險的 。
it's one of the things that we don't like to think about , but the fact that religious icons and good luck charms show up on dashboards around the world betrays the fact that we know this to be true .	這是我們不喜歡思考的其中一件事 , 但事實上 , 宗教圖示和好運的圖示出現在世界各地的儀表板上 , 背叛了我們所知道的事實 。
car accidents are the leading cause of death in people ages 16 to 19 in the united states leading cause of death and 75 percent of these accidents have nothing to do with drugs or alcohol .	車禍是美國人16歲至19歲的死因 , 其中75%與毒品或酒精無關 。
no one can say for sure , but i remember my first accident .	沒有人能肯定地說 , 但我記得我的第一個意外 。
i was a young driver out on the highway , and the car in front of me , i saw the brake lights go on .	我在高速公路上是個年輕的司機 , 前面的車子 , 我看到煞車燈亮了 。
i'm like , " okay , all right , this guy is slowing down , i'll slow down too . "	我說: 「 好吧 , 這傢伙慢下來 , 我也會慢下來 。 」
i step on the brake .	我踏上煞車 。
but no , this guy isn't slowing down .	但不 , 這傢伙沒有放慢速度 。
this guy is stopping , dead stop , dead stop on the highway .	這個人在高速公路上停下來 。
it was just going 65 to zero ?	只有65歲 , 0 ?
i slammed on the brakes .	我打破了煞車 。
i felt the abs kick in , and the car is still going , and it's not going to stop , and i know it's not going to stop , and the air bag deploys , the car is totaled , and fortunately , no one was hurt .	我覺得abs進去了 , 車子還在走 , 車子不會停下來 , 我知道它不會停下來 , 空氣袋部署 , 車子總會安裝起來 , 幸運的是 , 沒有人會受傷 。
but i had no idea that car was stopping , and i think we can do a lot better than that .	但我完全不知道車停了 , 我想我們能做得更好 。
i think we can transform the driving experience by letting our cars talk to each other .	我認為我們可以改變開車體驗的方式 , 讓車子彼此交談 。
i just want you to think a little bit about what the experience of driving is like now .	我只是想讓你們思考開車的體驗現在是什麼樣子 。
get into your car . close the door . you're in a glass bubble .	走進你的車裡 , 關上門 。 你在玻璃泡裡 。
you can't really directly sense the world around you .	你無法直接感知你周遭的世界 。
you're in this extended body .	你在這個擴張的身體裡 。
you're tasked with navigating it down partiallyseen roadways , in and amongst other metal giants , at superhuman speeds .	你的工作任務是要將它導入部分的道路 , 進而在超人的速度之中 。
okay ? and all you have to guide you are your two eyes .	好嗎 ? 你只需要引導你兩個眼睛 。
