okay , so that's all you have , eyes that weren't really designed for this task , but then people ask you to do things like , you want to make a lane change , what's the first thing they ask you do ?	好吧 , 這就是你們所擁有的目光 , 不是為了這個任務而設計 , 但之後 , 人們請你做這樣的事 , 你想做一個改變 , 他們要做的第一件事是什麼 ?
take your eyes off the road . that's right .	把你的眼睛從路上脫下來 , 沒錯 。
stop looking where you're going , turn , check your blind spot , and drive down the road without looking where you're going .	停下來看看你要去哪裡 , 轉身 , 檢查你的盲點 , 開車到路上 , 看你要去哪裡 。
you and everyone else . this is the safe way to drive .	你和其他人 。 這是安全的駕駛方式 。
why do we do this ? because we have to , we have to make a choice , do i look here or do i look here ?	為什麼我們要這樣做 ? 因為我們必須做選擇 , 我看這裡還是看這裡 ?
and usually we do a fantastic job picking and choosing what we attend to on the road .	通常我們會做一個很棒的工作 , 挑選我們在路上的目的 。
but occasionally we miss something .	但偶爾我們忽略了某件事 。
occasionally we sense something wrong or too late .	偶爾 , 我們會感覺到不對或太遲 。
in countless accidents , the driver says , " i didn't see it coming . "	無數的意外 , 司機說: 「 我看不到它會來 。 」
and i believe that . i believe that .	我相信 , 我相信 。
we can only watch so much .	我們只能看得太多 。
but the technology exists now that can help us improve that .	但科技現在存在 , 可以幫助我們改善這一點 。
in the future , with cars exchanging data with each other , we will be able to see not just three cars ahead and three cars behind , to the right and left , all at the same time , bird's eye view , we will actually be able to see into those cars .	在未來 , 車子彼此交換資料 , 我們不僅能看到前面三輛車 , 後面三輛車 , 右邊和左邊 , 同時 , 鳥的視野 , 我們就能看見這些車子 。
we will be able to see the velocity of the car in front of us , to see how fast that guy's going or stopping .	我們會看到前面車輛的速度 , 看看車子要走多快 , 或停車 。
if that guy's going down to zero , i'll know .	如果那傢伙要去零 , 我會知道 。
and with computation and algorithms and predictive models , we will be able to see the future .	藉由計算、演算法和預測模型 , 我們就能看見未來 。
you may think that's impossible .	你可能認為不可能 。
how can you predict the future ? that's really hard .	你要如何預測未來 ? 這真的很困難 。
actually , no . with cars , it's not impossible .	其實 , 不 , 車子 , 不可能 。
cars are threedimensional objects that have a fixed position and velocity .	車子是三維的物體 , 有固定的位置和速度 。
they travel down roads .	他們在道路上旅行 。
often they travel on prepublished routes .	通常他們會在出版的路線上旅行 。
it's really not that hard to make reasonable predictions about where a car's going to be in the near future .	對於近期車子的未來 , 並不難做出合理的預測 。
even if , when you're in your car and some motorcyclist comes bshoom ! 85 miles an hour down , lanesplitting i know you've had this experience that guy didn't " just come out of nowhere . "	就算你在車上和一些摩托車上時速八十五英里 , 我知道你有過這樣的經驗 , 沒有 「 剛出門 」 。
that guy's been on the road probably for the last half hour .	那傢伙在路上大概已經半小時了 。
right ? i mean , somebody's seen him .	對吧 ? 我的意思是 , 有人看過他 。
ten , 20 , 30 miles back , someone's seen that guy , and as soon as one car sees that guy and puts him on the map , he's on the map position , velocity , good estimate he'll continue going 85 miles an hour .	十、二十、三十英哩後 , 有人看過這個人 , 一旦車子看到那個人 , 把他放在地圖上 , 他就位在地圖、速度、好估計 , 他每小時會持續85英里 。
you'll know , because your car will know , because that other car will have whispered something in his ear , like , " by the way , five minutes , motorcyclist , watch out . "	你們會知道 , 因為你的車會知道 , 因為那另一輛車會在他的耳中發出一些東西 , 比如: 「 順便一提 , 五分鐘 , 摩托車騎士 , 仔細看 。 」
you can make reasonable predictions about how cars behave .	你可以對汽車的行為做出合理的預測 。
i mean , they're newtonian objects .	我的意思是 , 它們是牛頓的物體 。
that's very nice about them .	這對他們很棒 。
so how do we get there ?	所以 , 我們要如何做到 ?
we can start with something as simple as sharing our position data between cars , just sharing gps .	我們可以從簡單的開始 , 像是分享汽車的位置資料 , 分享gps 。
if i have a gps and a camera in my car , i have a pretty precise idea of where i am and how fast i'm going .	如果我有gps和攝影機 , 我有一個非常精確的點子 , 知道我在哪裡 , 以及我要走多快 。
with computer vision , i can estimate where the cars around me are , sort of , and where they're going .	有了電腦視覺 , 我可以估計我身邊的車在哪裡 , 以及它們要去哪裡 。
and same with the other cars .	其他車也一樣 。
they can have a precise idea of where they are , and sort of a vague idea of where the other cars are .	他們可以精確地知道自己在哪裡 , 對於其他車子在哪裡 , 他們可以有精確的概念 。
what happens if two cars share that data , if they talk to each other ?	如果兩個汽車共享這些數據 , 如果他們彼此交談 , 會發生什麼事 ?
i can tell you exactly what happens .	我可以告訴你們發生了什麼事 。
professor bob wang and his team have done computer simulations of what happens when fuzzy estimates combine , even in light traffic , when cars just share gps data , and we've moved this research out of the computer simulation and into robot test beds that have the actual sensors that are in cars now on these robots: stereo cameras , gps , and the twodimensional laser range finders that are common in backup systems .	bobwang教授和他的團隊做了電腦模擬 , 當fuszy估計結合時 , 甚至在光速交通中 , 汽車只是分享gps的資料 , 我們把這項研究從電腦模擬中移到機器人測試的床上 , 在這些機器人上有實際的感應器:sereo、gps , 以及ps , 在後備系統中常見的雷射系統中 。
we also attach a discrete shortrange communication radio , and the robots talk to each other .	我們也將短距離通訊收音機連上 , 機器人彼此交談 。
when these robots come at each other , they track each other's position precisely , and they can avoid each other .	當這些飛行器互相撞擊時 , 它們會精確地追蹤彼此的位置 , 它們可以互相避開 。
we're now adding more and more robots into the mix , and we encountered some problems .	我們現在在混合中加入了更多機器人 , 我們遇到了一些問題 。
one of the problems , when you get too much chatter , it's hard to process all the packets , so you have to prioritize , and that's where the predictive model helps you .	其中一個問題 , 當你收到太多章節時 , 很難處理所有的包裝 , 所以你必須優先處理 , 這就是預測模式幫助你的地方 。
if your robot cars are all tracking the predicted trajectories , you don't pay as much attention to those packets .	如果你的機器人車都在追蹤預期的軌跡 , 你不太會注意那些包裝 。
you prioritize the one guy who seems to be going a little off course .	你把那個看起來有點偏離軌道的人列為優先順序 。
that guy could be a problem .	那傢伙可能是個問題 。
and you can predict the new trajectory .	你可以預測新的軌跡 。
so you don't only know that he's going off course , you know how .	所以你不只知道他會走路 , 你知道的 。
and you know which drivers you need to alert to get out of the way .	你知道哪位司機必須警告出路 。
and we wanted to do how can we best alert everyone ?	我們想做的是 , 我們要如何把每個人最佳警示給最好 ?
how can these cars whisper , " you need to get out of the way ? "	這些車子怎麼會說: 「 你得走路 ? 」
well , it depends on two things: one , the ability of the car , and second the ability of the driver .	嗯 , 它取決於兩件事:一 , 汽車的能力 , 第二 , 駕駛的能力 。
if one guy has a really great car , but they're on their phone or , you know , doing something , they're not probably in the best position to react in an emergency .	如果有個人有一輛很棒的車 , 但他們在手機上 , 或做些什麼 , 他們可能不是在緊急情況下做出最好的反應 。
so we started a separate line of research doing driver state modeling .	所以 , 我們開始了一系列的研究 , 做司機國家模型 。
and now , using a series of three cameras , we can detect if a driver is looking forward , looking away , looking down , on the phone , or having a cup of coffee .	現在 , 用了一系列三台攝影機 , 我們可以偵測到駕駛是否向前看 , 向下看 , 向下看 , 在電話上 , 或是喝杯咖啡 。
we can predict the accident and we can predict who , which cars , are in the best position to move out of the way to calculate the safest route for everyone .	我們可以預測意外 , 我們可以預測誰 , 哪些車子 , 哪些車子是最好的位置 , 去計算每個人最安全的路線 。
fundamentally , these technologies exist today .	基本上 , 這些技術現今存在 。
i think the biggest problem that we face is our own willingness to share our data .	我認為我們面臨的最大問題是我們自己的意願來分享我們的資料 。
i think it's a very disconcerting notion , this idea that our cars will be watching us , talking about us to other cars , that we'll be going down the road in a sea of gossip .	我認為這是一個非常讓人不安的概念 , 我們的車子會看著我們 , 和其他車子談談 , 我們會走在路邊 。
but i believe it can be done in a way that protects our privacy , just like right now , when i look at your car from the outside , i don't really know about you .	但我相信它可以用一種方式來保護我們的隱私 , 就像現在 , 當我從外面看你的車 , 我並不知道你 。
if i look at your license plate number , i don't really know who you are .	如果我看你的牌子數 , 我並不知道你是誰 。
i believe our cars can talk about us behind our backs .	我相信我們的車子可以在我們的背後談論我們 。
and i think it's going to be a great thing .	我認為這將會是一件很棒的事 。
i want you to consider for a moment if you really don't want the distracted teenager behind you to know that you're braking , that you're coming to a dead stop .	我想請各位思考一下 , 如果你真的不希望身後的青少年分心 , 知道你很煞車 , 你就要來了 。
by sharing our data willingly , we can do what's best for everyone .	藉由意願分享我們的資料 , 我們可以為每個人做最好的事 。
so let your car gossip about you .	所以 , 讓你的車走向你 。
it's going to make the roads a lot safer .	它會讓道路更安全 。
x prize founder peter diamandis talks about how he helped stephen hawking fulfill his dream of going to space by flying together into the upper atmosphere and experiencing weightlessness at zero g .	xprize創辦人彼得•戴曼迪亞斯談到他如何協助史蒂芬•霍金完成太空的夢想 , 透過飛行到大氣層 , 並在零g中體驗無重力 。
business , flight , science , short talk , space , technology , universe	商業、飛行、科學、短談話、太空、科技、宇宙、宇宙、宇宙 。
peter diamandis on stephen hawking in zero g	彼得•戴曼迪斯在史蒂芬•霍金的零gwen的0gk中 , 彼得•戴曼迪斯在史蒂芬
those of you who know me know how passionate i am about opening the space frontier .	在座認識我的人都知道我對開太空前線有多熱情 。
so when i had the chance to give the world's expert in gravity the experience of zero gravity , it was incredible .	所以當我有機會給世界重力的專家零重力的體驗時 , 這真是不可思議 。
and i want to tell you that story .	我想告訴各位這個故事 。
i first met him through the archon x prize for genomics .	我第一次在考古x獎中見到他 。
it's a competition we're holding , the second x prize , for the first team to sequence 100 human genomes in 10 days .	這是我們所擁有的競爭 , 第二個xprize , 第一組在10天內排序100個人類基因組 。
we have something called the genome 100 100 individuals we're sequencing as part of that .	我們有一百個人被稱為 「 基因組一百個人 」 。
craig venter chairs that event .	克萊格•凡特斯那是事件的主席 。
and i met professor hawking , and he said his dream was to travel into space .	我遇到了霍金教授 , 他說他的夢想是進入太空 。
and i said , " i can't take you there , but i can take you into weightlessness into zerog .	我說: 「 我不能帶你到那裡 , 但我可以帶你進入零 。
and he said , on the spot , " absolutely , yes . "	他說 , 在這個地方 , 「 絕對是的 。 」
well , the only way to experience zerog on earth is actually with parabolic flight , weightless flight .	唯一能在地球上體驗零的方法 , 其實是飛行 , 無重力飛行 。
you take an airplane , you fly over the top , you're weightless for 25 seconds .	你拿飛機 , 飛過頂端 , 你是無重量的25秒 。
come back down , you weigh twice as much .	回來 , 你的重量是兩倍 。
you do it again and again .	你一而再再而三地做 。
you can get eight , 10 minutes of weightlessness how nasa's trained their astronauts for so long .	你可以得到8、10分鐘的無重力 , 美國太空總署如何訓練太空人這麼久 。
we set out to do this .	我們開始做這件事 。
it took us 11 years to become operational .	我們花了11年才開始運作 。
and we announced that we were going to fly stephen hawking .	我們宣布要飛行史蒂芬霍金 。
we had one government agency and one company aircraft operator say , you're crazy , don't do that , you're going kill the guy .	我們有一個政府機構和一家公司的飛機操作員說 , 你瘋了 , 不要這樣做 , 你要殺掉那個傢伙 。
and he wanted to go .	他想要去 。
we worked hard to get all the permissions .	我們努力取得所有許可 。
and six months later , we sat down at kennedy space center .	六個月後 , 我們坐在甘迺迪太空中心 。
we had a press conference , we announced our intent to do one zerog parabola , give him 25 seconds of zerog .	我們有一場記者會議 , 我們宣佈要做一場零拋物傘 , 給他25秒的零 。
and if it went really well , we might do three parabolas .	如果真的很順利 , 我們可能會做三個拋物面玻璃 。
well , we asked him why he wanted to go up and do this .	嗯 , 我們問他為什麼要去做這件事 。
and what he said , for me , was very moving .	對我而言 , 他所說的 , 是非常感人的 。
he said , " life on earth is at an everincreasing risk of being wiped out by disaster . . .	他說: 「 地球上的生命在不斷增加的風險 , 被災難摧毀......
i think the human race doesn't have a future if it doesn't go into space .	我認為 , 如果人類沒有進入太空就沒有未來了 。
i therefore want to encourage public interest in space . "	因此我想要鼓勵公眾對太空的興趣 。 」
we took him out to the kennedy space center , up inside the nasa vehicle , into the back of the zerog airplane .	我們帶他到甘迺迪太空中心 , 進入美國太空總署的車輛 , 進入零飛機的後面 。
we had about 20 people who made donations we raised $150 , 000 in donations for children's charities who flew with us .	我們有大約20個人捐款 , 捐贈出15萬美元給兒童慈善機構的捐款 。
a few tedsters here .	這裡有幾個ted人 。
we set up a whole er .	我們設立了整間急診室 。
we had four emergency room doctors and two nurses on board the airplane .	我們有四位急診室醫生和兩位護士在飛機上 。
we were monitoring his po2 of his blood , his heart rate , his blood pressure .	我們監控他的血液、心跳率、血壓 。
we had everything all set in case of an emergency ; god knows , you don't want to hurt this worldrenowned expert .	我們的一切都以緊急事件為例:上帝知道 , 你不想傷害這個世界知名的專家 。
we took off from the shuttle landing facility , where the shuttle takes off and lands .	我們從太空梭登陸設施中取下來 , 在那裡 , 太空梭被關掉和陸地 。
and my partner byron lichtenberg and i carefully suspended him into zerog .	我的另一半雷恩•里希伯格和我仔細地把他暫停為零 。
once he was there , [we] let him go to experience what weightlessness was truly like .	一旦他到那裡 , 我們就讓他去體驗真正的無重力 。
and after that first parabola , you know , the doc said everything is great . he was smiling , and we said go .	在第一個拋物傘之後 , 你知道的 , 醫生說一切都很好 , 他微笑了 , 我們說 。
so we did a second parabola .	所以我們做了第二個拋物傘 。
we actually floated an apple in homage to sir isaac newton because professor hawking holds the same chair at cambridge that isaac newton did .	我們真的把一個蘋果漂浮到艾薩克•牛頓大學 , 因為霍金教授在劍橋的椅子上 , 和牛頓大學一樣 。
and we did a fourth , and a fifth and a sixth .	我們做了第四個 , 第五個和第六個 。
and a seventh and an eighth .	第七和第八 。
and this man does not look like a 65yearold wheelchairbound man .	這個人看起來不像一個65歲的輪椅男子 。
he was so happy .	他非常開心 。
we are living on a precious jewel , and it's during our lifetime that we're moving off this planet .	我們生活在一個珍貴的珠寶 , 在我們這一生中 , 我們從地球上移走 。
please join us in this epic adventure .	請加入我們這個史詩般的冒險 。
medical animator david bolinsky presents 3 minutes of stunning animation that show the bustling life inside a cell .	醫療動畫師大衛•鮑林斯基有3分鐘的驚人動畫 , 顯示細胞內的破壞性命 。
design , entertainment , film , health , medicine , science , technology , visualizations	設計、娛樂、電影、健康、醫學、科學、技術、視覺化、視覺化 。
david bolinsky animates a cell	davidbolinsky動畫了一個細胞
i'm a medical illustrator , and i come from a slightly different point of view .	我是醫學插圖師 , 我從一個稍微不同的角度來看 。
i've been watching , since i grew up , the expressions of truth and beauty in the arts and truth and beauty in the sciences .	自從我長大以來 , 我一直在觀察 , 藝術、真與美的表達方式在科學、真與美 。
and while these are both wonderful things in their own right they both have very wonderful things going for them truth and beauty as ideals that can be looked at by the sciences and by math are almost like the ideal conjoined twins that a scientist would want to date .	雖然這些都是他們自己的權利中美妙的事情 , 但他們都有非常美妙的事物 , 可以用科學和數學來檢視它們 , 幾乎就像是科學家想要約會的理想結合雙胞胎 。
these are expressions of truth as awefull things , by meaning they are things you can worship .	這些表達真相是令人敬畏的事物 , 意思是 , 它們是你可以崇拜的事物 。
they are ideals that are powerful . they are irreducible .	它們是有力的理想 , 它們是無能為力的 。
they are unique . they are useful sometimes , often a long time after the fact .	它們是獨一無二的 , 有時是有用的 , 通常是在事實之後很長一段時間 。
and you can actually roll some of the pictures now , because i don't want to look at me on the screen .	現在你可以把一些圖片翻滾 , 因為我不想在螢幕上看著我 。
truth and beauty are things that are often opaque to people who are not in the sciences .	真相和美是常常對那些不在科學領域的人來說是不可思議的 。
they are things that describe beauty in a way that is often only accessible if you understand the language and the syntax of the person who studies the subject in which truth and beauty is expressed .	它們是用來形容美的事物 , 通常只能用你了解語言和語法的人 , 來研究真相和美的事物 。
if you look at the math , e=mc squared , if you look at the cosmological constant , where there's an anthropic ideal , where you see that life had to evolve from the numbers that describe the universe these are things that are really difficult to understand .	如果你觀察數學 , e=mc平方 , 如果你觀察宇宙的常數 , 人類理想中 , 你可以看到生命必須從描述宇宙的數量來演化 , 這些是很難理解的 。
and what i've tried to do since i had my training as a medical illustrator since i was taught animation by my father , who was a sculptor and my visual mentor i wanted to figure out a way to help people understand truth and beauty in the biological sciences by using animation , by using pictures , by telling stories so that the things that are not necessarily evident to people can be brought forth , and can be taught , and can be understood .	自從我受過醫學插圖之後 , 我就試過要做的事 , 因為我是一位雕塑家 , 我的視覺導師 , 我想要想出一個方法 , 來協助人們了解生物科學的真與美 , 透過動畫 , 用圖片 , 說故事 , 讓人們不見得可以被引進來的事物 , 可以被教導 , 可以被理解 。
students today are often immersed in an environment where what they learn is subjects that have truth and beauty embedded in them , but the way they're taught is compartmentalized and it's drawn down to the point where the truth and beauty are not always evident .	現今的學生通常會沉浸在一個環境中 , 他們學到的是真相和美的主題 , 但他們被教導的方式是相對的 , 被吸引到事實和美的地點 。
it's almost like that old recipe for chicken soup where you boil the chicken until the flavor is just gone .	就像是雞湯的舊食譜 , 煮雞 , 直到味道消失 。
we don't want to do that to our students .	我們不想對學生這樣做 。
so we have an opportunity to really open up education .	所以我們有機會真正開放教育的機會 。
and i had a telephone call from robert lue at harvard , in the molecular and cellular biology department , a couple of years ago . he asked me if my team and i would be interested and willing to really change how medical and scientific education is done at harvard .	幾年前 , 我接到一通來自哈佛的robertlue的電話 , 在分子和細胞生物學部門 , 他問我 , 我和我的團隊是否有興趣 , 願意真正改變哈佛大學的醫療和科學教育 。
so we embarked on a project that would explore the cell that would explore the truth and beauty inherent in molecular and cellular biology so that students could understand a larger picture that they could hang all of these facts on .	所以我們開始了一個計畫 , 來探索細胞 , 探索分子和細胞生物學中的真與美 , 讓學生能了解這些事實的大相片 。
they could have a mental image of the cell as a large , bustling , hugely complicated city that's occupied by micromachines .	他們可以把細胞的心智圖像想像成一個大型、大型、複雜的城市 , 由微機所佔據 。
and these micromachines really are at the heart of life .	這些微機械真的是生命的核心 。
these micromachines , which are the envy of nanotechnologists the world over , are selfdirected , powerful , precise , accurate devices that are made out of strings of amino acids .	這些微機械 , 是世界各地的奈米科技專家的嫉妒 , 是自我導向、強大、精準、精準的設備 , 是由胺基酸組成的 。
and these micromachines power how a cell moves .	這些微機械會如何移動 。
they power how a cell replicates . they power our hearts .	它們會驅動細胞複製 , 它們會驅動我們的心 。
they power our minds .	它們能驅使我們的心智 。
and so what we wanted to do was to figure out how we could make this story into an animation that would be the centerpiece of biovisions at harvard , which is a website that harvard has for its molecular and cellular biology students that will in addition to all the textual information , in addition to all the didactic stuff put everything together visually , so that these students would have an internalized view of what a cell really is in all of its truth and beauty , and be able to study with this view in mind , so that their imaginations would be sparked , so that their passions would be sparked and so that they would be able to go on and use these visions in their head to make new discoveries and to be able to find out , really , how life works .	所以 , 我們想要做的是 , 找出如何把這個故事變成一個動畫的中心 , 它是哈佛大學的生物診斷中心 , 它是一個哈佛大學的網站 , 用來做分子和細胞生物學的學生 , 除了所有的文字資訊以外 , 讓所有的東西都能被視覺化 , 讓這些學生們能夠實現它的真實和美 , 並且能夠在心中研究這個觀點 , 這樣他們的想像力才會被激發 , 以至於他們腦海 , 以此類方式發掘它們的新事物 。
so we set out by looking at how these molecules are put together .	所以我們開始研究這些分子是如何組合在一起的 。
we worked with a theme , which is , you've got macrophages that are streaming down a capillary , and they're touching the surface of the capillary wall , and they're picking up information from cells that are on the capillary wall , and they are given this information that there's an inflammation somewhere outside , where they can't see and sense .	我們和一個主題合作 , 也就是說 , 你有大噬菌體在微血管下游 , 它們正在觸碰微血管壁的表面 , 它們從毛細管壁上收集資訊 , 它們得到的資訊 , 資訊是外面有發炎的某處 , 它們看不到和感覺 。
but they get the information that causes them to stop , causes them to internalize that they need to make all of the various parts that will cause them to change their shape , and try to get out of this capillary and find out what's going on .	但他們會得到造成它們停止的資訊 , 導致它們內化 , 使它們需要製造出各種各樣的部件 , 使它們改變形狀 , 試著脫離這種微血管 , 找出發生了什麼事 。
so these molecular motors we had to work with the harvard scientists and databank models of the atomically accurate molecules and figure out how they moved , and figure out what they did .	所以這些分子馬達 , 我們必須和哈佛大學的科學家和資料庫模型合作 , 找出它們的移動方式 , 找出它們的作用 。
and figure out how to do this in a way that was truthful in that it imparted what was going on , but not so truthful that the compact crowding in a cell would prevent the vista from happening .	想出辦法以實話的方式來做這件事 , 讓大家知道發生了什麼事 , 但事實並非如此 , 牢房裡的擁抱者會阻止病毒發生 。
and so what i'm going to show you is a threeminute reader's digest version of the first aspect of this film that we produced . it's an ongoing project that's going to go another four or five years .	所以我要給你們看的是一個三分鐘的讀者的消化版本 , 是我們製作的這部電影的第一面版本 。 這是一個正在進行的專案計畫 , 將要花四年或五年的時間 。
and i want you to look at this and see the paths that the cell manufactures these little walking machines , they're called kinesins that take these huge loads that would challenge an ant in relative size .	我希望你們看看這個 , 看看細胞製造這些步行的小機器的路徑 , 它們被稱為kinesins , 將這些巨大的載重量帶到相對大小的螞蟻身上 。
run the movie , please .	請播放這部電影 。
but these machines that power the inside of the cells are really quite amazing , and they really are the basis of all life because all of these machines interact with each other .	但這些驅動細胞內部的機器真的很了不起 , 它們真的是所有生命的基礎 , 因為這些機器互相作用 。
they pass information to each other .	它們會傳遞訊息給彼此 。
they cause different things to happen inside the cell .	它們會造成不同的事情發生在細胞內 。
and the cell will actually manufacture the parts that it needs on the fly , from information that's brought from the nucleus by molecules that read the genes .	細胞會製造果蠅需要的零件 , 來自讀取基因的資訊 。
no life , from the smallest life to everybody here , would be possible without these little micromachines .	沒有生命 , 從最小的生命到這裡的每個人 , 都可能沒有這些微生物 。
in fact , it would really , in the absence of these machines , have made the attendance here , chris , really quite sparse .	事實上 , 在沒有這些機器的情況下 , 克里斯 , 真的很矛盾 。
this is the fedex delivery guy of the cell .	這是細胞的聯邦政府遞送人員 。
this little guy is called the kinesin , and he pulls a sack that's full of brand new manufactured proteins to wherever it's needed in the cell whether it's to a membrane , whether it's to an organelle , whether it's to build something or repair something .	這個小傢伙叫做kinesin , 他拉了一包包裝了新製造的蛋白質到細胞所需的位置 , 不論是細胞膜 , 不論是組織 , 不論是用來建造東西或修復 。
and each of us has about 100 , 000 of these things running around , right now , inside each one of your 100 trillion cells .	我們每個人身上都有大約十萬個這種東西在你100兆個細胞內部運行 。
so no matter how lazy you feel , you're not really intrinsically doing nothing .	所以 , 不論你有多懶惰 , 你根本不做任何事 。
so what i want you to do when you go home is think about this , and think about how powerful our cells are .	所以 , 當你回家時 , 我希望你們想想這個 , 想想我們的細胞有多強大 。
and think about some of the things that we're learning about cellular mechanics .	想想看 , 我們學到了一些關於細胞機械的東西 。
once we figure out all that's going on and believe me , we know almost a percent of what's going on once we figure out what's going on , we're really going to be able to have a lot of control over what we do with our health , with what we do with future generations , and how long we're going to live .	一旦我們搞清楚了 , 相信我 , 我們就知道發生了什麼事 , 一旦我們搞清楚到底發生了什麼事 , 我們就真的能控制我們對健康的做法 , 和我們未來的世代做些什麼 , 以及我們未來的壽命多久 。
and hopefully we'll be able to use this to discover more truth , and more beauty .	希望我們能用這個方法來發現更多的真相 , 更美麗 。
but it's really quite amazing that these cells , these micromachines , are aware enough of what the cell needs that they do their bidding .	但令人驚訝的是這些細胞 , 這些微機械 , 已經足以察覺細胞所需要的資訊 , 足以讓它們在協助 。
they work together . they make the cell do what it needs to do .	他們一起工作 , 讓細胞做該做的事 。
and their working together helps our bodies huge entities that they will never see function properly .	他們一起合作 , 幫助我們體內巨大的實體 , 它們永遠不會看到正常的功能 。
enjoy the rest of the show . thank you .	享受剩下的節目 。 謝謝 。
becky blanton planned to live in her van for a year and see the country , but when depression set in and her freelance job ended , her camping trip turned into homelessness . in this intimate talk , she describes her experience of becoming one of america's working homeless .	貝琪布蘭頓計劃要在她的車上住一年 , 看看這個國家 , 但當憂鬱症設定了 , 她的營地終於變成無家可歸 。 在這個親密的演講中 , 她描述了她成為美國無家可歸的經驗 。
adventure , happiness , life , personal growth , poverty , social change , society , storytelling	冒險、快樂、生活、個人成長、貧窮、社會改變、說故事、說故事、說故事、說故事、人生、個人成長、貧窮、社會、社會、社會、社會、說故事、
becky blanton: the year i was homeless	貝琪布蘭頓:那一年 , 我無家可歸 。
i'm a writer and a journalist , and i'm also an insanely curious person , so in 22 years as a journalist , i've learned how to do a lot of new things .	我是一位作家和記者 , 我也是一位非常好奇的人 , 所以在22年後 , 我學會了很多新東西 。
and three years ago , one of the things i learned how to do was to become invisible .	三年前 , 我學到了一件事 , 就是變成隱形 。
i became one of the working homeless .	我成為無家可歸的無家可歸者 。
i quit my job as a newspaper editor after my father died in february of that same year , and decided to travel .	同年二月 , 我辭掉了報紙編輯的工作 , 決定去旅行 。
his death hit me pretty hard .	他的死亡對我來說很困難 。
and there were a lot of things that i wanted to feel and deal with while i was doing that .	當我在做這件事時 , 有很多我想要感受和處理的事情 。
i've camped my whole life . and i decided that living in a van for a year to do this would be like one long camping trip .	我一輩子都在露營 , 我決定住在車上一年要做這件事就像一趟漫長的露營旅行 。
so i packed my cat , my rottweiler and my camping gear into a 1975 chevy van , and drove off into the sunset , having fully failed to realize three critical things .	所以我把貓包起來 , 我的腐爛推車 , 和我的露營裝備 , 變成了1975年的車 , 開車到日落 , 完全沒能實現三件重要的事 。
one: that society equates living in a permanent structure , even a shack , with having value as a person .	第一:社會等同於生活在一個永久的結構中 , 甚至是模糊 , 擁有價值 。
two: i failed to realize how quickly the negative perceptions of other people can impact our reality , if we let it .	第二:我沒有意識到別人的負面感知有多快可以影響我們的現實 。
three: i failed to realize that homelessness is an attitude , not a lifestyle .	第三:我沒意識到 , 無家可歸是態度 , 而非生活方式 。
at first , living in the van was great .	一開始 , 住在車上是很棒的 。
i showered in campgrounds . i ate out regularly .	我在營地淋浴 , 我經常吃飯 。
and i had time to relax and to grieve .	我有時間放鬆和悲慟 。
but then the anger and the depression about my father's death set in .	但接著 , 憤怒和憂鬱的是我父親的死亡設定了 。
my freelance job ended . and i had to get a fulltime job to pay the bills .	我的自由工作結束了 。 我必須得到全職工作來支付帳單 。
what had been a really mild spring turned into a miserably hot summer .	真正溫和的春天變成了一個非常熱的夏天 。
and it became impossible to park anywhere without being very obvious that i had a cat and a dog with me , and it was really hot .	幾乎不可能停在任何地方 , 沒有很明顯地 , 我有一隻貓 , 一隻狗 , 這真的很熱 。
the cat came and went through an open window in the van .	貓來了 , 穿越了車窗 。
the doggy went into doggy day care .	狗狗跑進doggy日照顧 。
whenever i could , i used employee showers in office buildings and truck stops .	每當我能用辦公大樓的員工和卡車站 。
or i washed up in public rest rooms .	或是我在公共休息室洗澡 。
nighttime temperatures in the van rarely dropped below 80 degrees fahrenheit , making it difficult or impossible to sleep .	夜間在華氏80度以下 , 溫度幾乎低於華氏80度 , 使得睡眠難以置信 。
food rotted in the heat .	食物在熱氣中腐爛 。
ice in my ice chest melted within hours , and it was pretty miserable .	冰在冰上幾小時內融化了 , 這相當悲慘 。
i couldn't afford to find an apartment , or couldn't afford an apartment that would allow me to have the rottweiler and the cat .	我負擔不起找公寓 , 或買不起公寓 , 讓我能有腐爛的推特和貓 。
and i refused to give them up , so i stayed in the van .	我拒絕給他們放棄 , 所以我待在車上 。
and when the heat made me too sick to walk the 50 feet to the public restroom outside my van at night , i used a bucket and a trash bag as a toilet .	當熱氣使我太生病了 , 晚上在我車外的公共廁所 , 我用桶子和垃圾袋當廁所 。
when winter weather set in , the temperatures dropped below freezing . and they stayed there .	當冬天氣候出現時 , 溫度下降在冷凍狀態下 , 它們留在那裡 。
and i faced a whole new set of challenges .	我面對了全新的挑戰 。
i parked a different place every night so i would avoid being noticed and hassled by the police .	我每天晚上都停了個不一樣的地方 , 這樣我就能避免被警察察察察覺、被警察引導 。
i didn't always succeed .	我不見得都成功 。
but i felt out of control of my life .	但我覺得我無法掌控我的人生 。
and i don't know when or how it happened , but the speed at which i went from being a talented writer and journalist to being a homeless woman , living in a van , took my breath away .	我不知道何時或如何發生 , 但我的速度從一個有才華的作家和記者變成一個無家可歸的女人 , 住在一輛車裡 , 把我的呼吸帶走 。
i hadn't changed . my i . q . hadn't dropped .	我沒有改變 , 我的智商沒有下降 。
my talent , my integrity , my values , everything about me remained the same .	我的才華、我的完整性、我的價值觀 , 所有關於我的事 , 都一樣 。
but i had changed somehow .	但我不知怎麼地改變了 。
i spiraled deeper and deeper into a depression .	我把更深、更深入憂鬱 。
and eventually someone referred me to a homeless health clinic .	最終有人提到我去過無家可歸的健康診所 。
and i went . i hadn't bathed in three days .	我去了 , 三天沒洗澡 。
i was as smelly and as depressed as anyone in line .	我跟排隊的人一樣 , 被羞辱 。
i just wasn't drunk or high .	我只是不喝醉或喝醉 。
and when several of the homeless men realized that , including a former university professor , they said , " you aren't homeless . why are you really here ? "	當幾個無家可歸的人意識到 , 包括前大學教授 , 他們說: 「 你不是無家可歸 。 為什麼你真的在這裡 ? 」
other homeless people didn't see me as homeless , but i did .	其他無家可歸的人沒有把我視為無家可歸 , 但我確實如此 。
then the professor listened to my story and he said , " you have a job . you have hope .	接著 , 教授傾聽我的故事 , 他說: 「 你有工作 , 你有希望 。
the real homeless don't have hope . "	真正的無家可歸者沒有希望 。 」
a reaction to the medication the clinic gave me for my depression left me suicidal . and i remember thinking , " if i killed myself , no one would notice . "	對於藥物的反應 , 診所給我的憂鬱症留下了我自殺 。 我記得在想: 「 如果我殺了自己 , 沒有人會注意到 。 」
a friend told me , shortly after that , that she had heard that tim russert , a nationally renowned journalist , had been talking about me on national t . v .	沒多久 , 一位朋友告訴我 , 她聽說提姆•羅斯特 , 一個全國知名的記者 , 一直在談我的國家電視節目 。
an essay i'd written about my father , the year before he died , was in tim's new book .	我曾寫過一篇關於我父親的論文 , 在他死前的那一年 , 是在提姆的新書 。
and he was doing the talk show circuit . and he was talking about my writing .	他在演說節目電路 。 他在談我的寫作 。
and when i realized that tim russert , former moderator of " meet the press , " was talking about my writing , while i was living in a van in a walmart parking lot , i started laughing .	當我了解到提姆•羅斯特 , 《會見媒體》的前主持人在談論我的寫作 , 當我住在華爾瑪的停車場時 , 我開始笑 。
i started laughing because it got to the point where , was i a writer , or was i a homeless woman ?	我開始笑 , 因為它到達了哪裡 , 我是作家 , 還是一個無家可歸的女人 ?
so i went in the bookstore . and i found tim's book .	所以我去了書店 , 找到了提姆的書 。
and i stood there . and i reread my essay .	我站在那裡 , 重新寫我的文章 。
because i was a writer .	因為我是作家 。
i was a writer .	我是作家 。
shortly after that i moved back to tennessee .	在那之後 , 我搬回田納西 。
i alternated between living in a van and couch surfing with friends .	我和朋友住在車裡 , 和沙發衝浪 。
and i started writing again .	我又開始再寫作 。
by the summer of the following year i was a working journalist .	隔年夏天 , 我是個工作記者 。
i was winning awards . i was living in my own apartment .	我贏得獎項 。 我住在我自己的公寓裡 。
i was no longer homeless .	我不再是無家可歸 。
and i was no longer invisible .	我不再是隱形的 。
thousands of people work full and parttime jobs , and live in their cars .	數以千計的人全職工作 , 兼職工作 , 住在他們的車裡 。
but society continues to stigmatize and criminalize living in your vehicle or on the streets .	但社會持續汙名化生活在你的車子或街道上 。
so the homeless , the working homeless , primarily remain invisible .	所以無家可歸 , 無家可歸 , 主要仍然是看不見的 。
but if you ever meet one , engage them , encourage them , and offer them hope .	但如果你遇見一個人 , 加入他們 , 鼓勵他們 , 並提供他們希望 。
the human spirit can overcome anything if it has hope .	人類的精神能夠克服任何事情 , 如果它有希望的話 。
and i'm not here to be the poster girl for the homeless .	我不是來到這裡為無家可歸的海報 。
i'm not here to encourage you to give money to the next panhandler you meet .	我不是來鼓勵你把錢捐給下一個乞討者 。
but i am here to tell you that , based on my experience , people are not where they live , where they sleep , or what their life situation is at any given time .	但我在這裡要告訴各位 , 根據我的經驗 , 人們不是他們住的地方 , 睡在哪裡 , 或他們的生活狀況 , 隨時隨時都在 。
three years ago i was living in a van in a walmart parking lot , and today i'm speaking at ted .	三年前 , 我住在一輛沃爾瑪的停車場 , 今天我在ted演講 。
hope always , always finds a way . thank you .	希望總是找到方法 。 謝謝 。
at tedxchange , thailand's " mr . condom , " mechai viravaidya , walks us through the country's bold plan to raise its standard of living , starting in the 1970s . first step: population control . and that means a lot of frank , funny and very effective talk about condoms .	在泰國的《保險套》中 , 泰國的《保險套》 , mechaiviravaidya , 帶領我們走過國家的大膽計劃 , 提高生活的標準 , 第一步:人口控制 。 這意味著許多法蘭克 , 很有趣的 , 非常有效的談論保險套 。
culture , global issues , health , population , science	文化、全球議題、健康、人口、科學、科學、科學 。
mechai viravaidya: how mr . condom made thailand a better place	米塔維拉迪亞:保險套是如何讓泰國更好的地方成為泰國先生 。
now , when i was a young man 40 years ago , the country was very , very poor with lots and lots and lots of people living in poverty .	40年前 , 當我還是個年輕人的時候 , 這個國家非常貧窮 , 有許多人生活在貧窮中 。
we decided to do something about it , but we didn't begin with a welfare program or a poverty reduction program .	我們決定要做點什麼 , 但我們不是從福利計畫開始 , 或減少貧窮計畫 。
but we began with a familyplanning program , following a very successful maternal child health activity , sets of activities .	但我們從一個家庭平台開始 , 跟著一個非常成功的孕產婦健康活動 , 一組活動 。
so basically , no one would accept family planning if their children didn't survive .	基本上 , 如果他們的孩子沒有生存 , 沒有人會接受家庭規劃 。
so the first step: get to the children , get to the mothers , and then follow up with family planning .	第一步:去找孩子 , 去找母親 , 然後跟隨家庭規劃 。
not just child mortality alone , you need also family planning .	不僅僅是兒童死亡率 , 你還需要家庭規劃 。
now let me take you back as to why we needed to do it .	現在讓我帶各位回想一下為什麼我們需要這麼做 。
in my country , that was the case in 1974 .	在我的國家 , 那是1974年的案例 。
seven children per family tremendous growth at 3 . 3 percent .	每家人的成長率是3.3% 。
there was just no future .	沒有未來 。
we needed to reduce the population growth rate .	我們需要減少人口成長率 。
so we said , " let's do it . "	所以我們說: 「 我們來做吧 。 」
the women said , " we agree . we'll use pills , but we need a doctor to prescribe the pills , " and we had very , very few doctors .	女士說: 「 我們同意 , 我們會使用藥丸 , 但我們需要醫生來開藥 。 」 我們只有很少的醫生 。
we didn't take no as an answer ; we took no as a question .	我們不把答案視為一個答案 , 我們不問 。
we went to the nurses and the midwives , who were also women , and did a fantastic job at explaining how to use the pill .	我們去了護士和中西部 , 她們也是女性 , 在解釋如何使用藥丸時 , 做了很棒的工作 。
that was wonderful , but it covered only 20 percent of the country .	那真是太棒了 , 但它只佔全國百分之二十 。
what do we do for the other 80 percent leave them alone and say , " well , they're not medical personnel . "	我們為其他80%的人做些什麼 , 讓他們孤獨說: 「 嗯 , 他們不是醫療人員 。 」
no , we decided to do a bit more .	不 , 我們決定再多做一點 。
so we went to the ordinary people that you saw .	所以我們去了你們看到的一般人 。
actually , below that yellow sign i wish they hadn't wiped that , because there was " cocacola " there .	事實上 , 在那條黃色標誌之下 , 我真希望他們不會那麼受傷 , 因為那裡有 「 可口可樂 」 。
we were so much bigger than cocacola in those days .	當時我們比可口可樂還要大很多 。
and no difference , the people they chose were the people we chose .	沒有差別 , 他們選的人是我們選的人 。
they were wellknown in the community , they knew that customers were always right , and they were terrific , and they practiced their family planning themselves .	他們在社區中很熟悉 , 他們知道客戶總是對的 , 且他們很棒 , 他們自行練習他們的家人規劃自己 。
so they could supply pills and condoms throughout the country , in every village of the country .	所以他們可以供應全國各地的藥丸和保險套 。
so there we are . we went to the people who were seen as the cause of the problem to be the solution .	所以 , 我們就在那裡 。 我們去找被認為是解決方案的成因 。
wherever there were people and you can see boats with the women , selling things here's the floating market selling bananas and crabs and also contraceptives wherever you find people , you'll find contraceptives in thailand .	不論在哪裡 , 都看得到女人的船 , 賣的是漂浮的市場 , 賣香蕉、螃蟹 , 還有避孕用品 , 不論你在哪裡找到人 , 你都會在泰國找到避孕品 。
and then we decided , why not get to religion because in the philippines , the catholic church was pretty strong , and thai people were buddhist .	然後我們決定 , 為何不去宗教 , 因為在菲律賓 , 天主教會很強烈 , 泰國人民是佛教徒 。
we went to them and they said , " look , could you help us ? "	我們去找他們 , 他們說: 「 你能幫我們嗎 ? 」
i'm there the one in blue , not the yellow holding a bowl of holy water for the monk to sprinkle holy water on pills and condoms for the sanctity of the family .	我在藍色的那兒 , 不是黃色的 , 拿著一碗聖水 , 讓僧侶在藥丸上灑上神聖的水和保險套 , 為家庭的理由 。
and this picture was sent throughout the country .	這張照片被送到全國各地 。
so some of the monks in the villages were doing the same thing themselves .	有些村莊的僧侶在做同樣的事 。
and the women were saying , " no wonder we have no sideeffects .	那些女人說: 「 難怪我們沒有副作用 。
it's been blessed . "	它被祝福了 。 」
that was their perception .	那是他們的感知 。
and then we went to teachers .	然後我們去找老師 。
you need everybody to be involved in trying to provide whatever it is that make humanity a better place .	你需要每個人參與 , 試著提供任何讓人類更好的地方 。
so we went to the teachers .	所以我們去找老師 。
over a quarter of a million were taught about family planning with a new alphabet a , b for birth , c for condom , i for iud , v for vasectomy .	超過25萬人被教導要用新的字母來規劃家庭規劃a、出生、保險套、紫外線切除術 。
and then we had a snakes and ladders game , where you throw dice .	然後我們就有了蛇和梯子遊戲 , 你丟了骰子 。
if you land on anything profamily planning , you move ahead .	如果你降落任何預期規劃 , 你就會往前走 。
like , " mother takes the pill every night .	比如: 「 媽媽每天晚上吃藥 。
very good , mother . move ahead .	非常好 , 媽媽 , 往前走 。
uncle buys a condom . very good , uncle . move ahead .	叔叔買保險套 。 非常好 , 叔叔 , 向前走 。
uncle gets drunk , doesn't use condom . come back , start again . "	叔叔喝醉 , 不用保險套 。 回來 , 再開始吧 。 」
again , education , class entertainment .	同樣的 , 教育、娛樂 。
and the kids were doing it in school too .	孩子們也在學校做這件事 。
we had relay races with condoms , we had children's condomblowing championship .	我們和保險套有相對的競賽 , 我們有兒童保險套的冠軍 。
and before long , the condom was know as the girl's best friend .	不久之後 , 保險套就被稱為女孩最好的朋友 。
in thailand , for poor people , diamonds don't make it so the condom is the girl's best friend .	在泰國 , 對貧窮的人來說 , 鑽石不會讓保險套成為女孩最好的朋友 。
we introduced our first microcredit program in 1975 , and the women who organized it said , " we only want to lend to women who practice family planning .	我們在1975年引進了第一個微型信貸計劃 , 組織了這個計劃的女性說: 「 我們只想借給那些實踐家庭規劃的女性 。
if you're pregnant , take care of your pregnancy .	如果你懷孕了 , 照顧你的懷孕 。
if you're not pregnant , you can take a loan out from us . "	如果你沒有懷孕 , 你可以從我們身上取出貸款 。 」
and that was run by them .	那是他們經營的 。
and after 35/36 years , it's still going on .	在35/36年之後 , 它仍然在發生 。
it's a part of the village development bank ; it's not a real bank , but it's a fund microcredit .	它是村落發展銀行的一部分 , 不是真正的銀行 , 而是資金額貸款 。
and we didn't need a big organization to run it it was run by the villagers themselves .	我們不需要一個大型組織來經營這個組織 , 由村民自己經營 。
and you probably hardly see a thai man there , it's always women , women , women , women .	你可能看不到一個泰國人 , 總是女人、女人、女人 。
and then we thought we'd help america , because america's been helping everyone , whether they want help or not .	接著我們認為我們會幫助美國 , 因為美國一直在幫助每個人 , 不論他們是否想要協助 。
and this is on the fourth of july .	這是七月第四日 。
we decided to provide vasectomy to all men , but in particular , american men to the front of the queue , right up to the ambassador's residence during his [unclear] .	我們決定為所有男性提供大量昆蟲 , 但特別是 , 尤其是 , 美國男士去排隊前面 , 就在大使期間 。
and the hotel gave us the ballroom for it very appropriate room .	飯店給了我們一個非常適當的房間 。
and since it was near lunch time , they said , " all right , we'll give you some lunch .	既然快到了午餐時間 , 他們說: 「 好吧 , 我們會給你吃午餐 。
of course , it must be american cola .	當然 , 它一定是美國的可樂 。
you get two brands , coke and pepsi .	你有兩個品牌 , 可口可樂和百事可樂 。
and then the food is either hamburger or hotdog . "	然後食物是漢堡或熱狗 。 」
and i thought a hotdog will be more symbolic .	我以為熱狗會更符號 。
and here is this , then , young man called willy bohm who worked for the usaid .	接下來是這個 , 年輕人打電話給威廉•龐姆 , 他為美國人工作 。
obviously , he's had his vasectomy because his hotdog is half eaten , and he was very happy .	很顯然 , 他的胸部抽搐很大 , 因為他的熱狗被吃了一半 , 而且他很開心 。
it made a lot of news in america , and it angered some people also .	它在美國做了很多新聞 , 也讓一些人感到憤怒 。
i said , " don't worry . come over and i'll do the whole lot of you . "	我說: 「 別擔心 , 過來 , 我會幫你做很多 。 」
in all this thing , from seven children to 1 . 5 children , population growth rate of 3 . 3 to 0 . 5 .	總而言之 , 從七個孩子到1.5個孩子 , 人口成長率是3.3到0.5 。
you could call it the cocacola approach if you like it was exactly the same thing .	你可以稱它為可口可樂的方法 , 如果你喜歡它是完全一樣的 。
i'm not sure whether cocacola followed us , or we followed cocacola , but we're good friends .	我不確定可口可樂是否跟著我們追蹤 , 或是追蹤可口可樂 , 但我們是好朋友 。
and so that's the case of everyone joining in .	這就是每個人加入的例子 。
we didn't have a strong government . we didn't have lots of doctors .	我們沒有強大的政府 , 我們沒有很多醫生 。
but it's everybody's job who can change attitude and behavior .	但每個人都能改變態度和行為 。
then aids came along and hit thailand , and we had to stop doing a lot of good things to fight aids .	接著 , 愛滋病來了 , 抵達泰國 , 我們得要停止做許多好事來對抗愛滋病 。
but unfortunately , the government was in denial , denial , denial .	但不幸的是 , 政府在否認、否認、否認 。
so our work wasn't affected .	所以 , 我們的工作並沒有受到影響 。
so i thought , " well , if you can't go to the government , go to the military . "	所以我想: 「 嗯 , 如果你不能去政府 , 去軍隊 。 」
so i went to the military and asked to borrow 300 radio stations .	所以我去了軍隊 , 要求借300個電台 。
they have more than the government , and they've got more guns than the government .	他們有比政府多 , 他們的槍比政府多 。
so i asked them , could they help us in our fight against hiv .	所以我問他們 , 他們能協助我們對抗愛滋病毒 。
and after i gave them statistics , they said , " yes . okay . you can use all the radio stations , television stations . "	在我給他們統計數據後 , 他們說: 「 是的 。 你可以用所有的電台、電視台 。 」
and that's when we went onto the airwaves .	那時我們就進入了空氣波 。
and then we got a new prime minister soon after that .	在那之後 , 我們得到了一個新的首相 。
and he said , " mechai , could you come and join ? "	他說: 「 米塔 , 你能來加入嗎 ? 」
he asked me in because he liked my wife a lot .	他問我 , 因為他喜歡我太太 。
so i said , " okay . "	所以我說: 「 好吧 。 」
he became the chairman of the national aids committee and increased the budget fiftyfold .	他成為國家愛滋病委員會的主席 , 並增加預算的五倍 。
every ministry , even judges , had to be involved in aids education everyone and we said the public , institutions , religious institutions , schools everyone was involved .	每個部長 , 甚至法官 , 都必須參與愛滋病教育每個人 , 我們說大眾、機構、宗教機構、學校 , 每個人都參與其中 。
and here , every media person had to be trained for hiv .	這裡 , 每個媒體人都必須受過愛滋病的訓練 。
and we gave every station half a minute extra for advertising to earn more money .	我們給每一站一半的額外廣告 , 賺更多錢 。
so they were happy with that .	所以他們很開心 。
and then aids education in all schools , starting from university .	接著 , 所有學校的愛滋病教育從大學開始 。
and these are high school kids teaching high school kids .	這些是高中生 , 教導高中生 。
and the best teachers were the girls , not the boys , and they were terrific .	最好的老師是女孩 , 不是男孩 , 他們很棒 。
and these girls who go around teaching about safe sex and hiv were known as mother theresa .	這些在教導安全性愛和愛滋病的女孩 , 被稱為 「 泰蕾莎 」 。
and then we went down one more step .	然後我們再走下一步 。
these are primary school kids third , fourth grade going to every household in the village , every household in the whole of thailand , giving aids information and a condom to every household , given by these young kids .	這些小學三年級 , 四年級到村落的每個家庭 , 在泰國的每個家庭 , 提供愛滋病資訊和保險套給每個家庭 , 給予這些孩子 。
and no parents objected , because we were trying to save lives , and this was a lifesaver .	沒有父母反對 , 因為我們試圖拯救生命 , 這是救命 。

so you have the companies also realizing that sick staff don't work , and dead customers don't buy .	所以你也知道 , 生病人員不會工作 , 而死客戶卻不會買 。

and then we have this captain condom , with his harvard mba , going to schools and night spots .	然後我們有一套保險套 , 帶著他的哈佛mba , 去學校和夜點 。
and they loved him . you need a symbol of something .	他們很愛他 。 你需要一個符號 。
in every country , every program , you need a symbol , and this is probably the best thing he's ever done with his mba .	在每個國家 , 每個程式 , 你都需要一個符號 , 這可能是他在mba上做過最好的事 。
and then we gave condoms out everywhere on the streets everywhere , everywhere .	然後我們把保險套送到各地的街道上 , 到處都是 。

and also , in traffic , the policemen give you condoms our " cops and rubbers " programs .	此外 , 在交通上 , 警察會給你保險套 , 我們的 「 警察 」 和 「 魯bbers 」 計畫 。
so , can you imagine new york policemen giving out condoms ?	所以 , 你能想像紐約警察提供保險套嗎 ?
of course i can . and they'd enjoy it immensely ; i see them standing around right now , everywhere .	當然我可以 。 而且他們很享受 , 我現在看到他們站在任何地方 , 到處都是 。

and these were the condoms that we introduced .	這些是我們推出的保險套 。
one says , " weapon of mass protection . "	有人說: 「 大規模保護的武器 。 」

why just run around ?	為什麼要跑 ?
and then finally , in thailand we're buddhist , we don't have a god , so instead , we say , " in rubber we trust . "	最後 , 在泰國 , 我們是佛教徒 , 我們沒有上帝 , 所以我們說: 「 在橡膠裡 , 我們信任 。 」
so you can see that we added everything to our endeavor to make life better for the people .	所以你可以看到 , 我們把一切都加到我們努力的努力中 , 以讓人們更好的生活 。
we had condoms in all the refrigerators in the hotels and the schools , because alcohol impairs judgment .	我們在旅館和學校裡都有保險套 , 因為酒精損害判斷 。

otherwise there wouldn't be many thais walking around today .	否則 , 今天就不會有很多泰國人走來走去 。

and then we decided to help people out of poverty , now that we got aids somewhat out of the way this time , not with government alone , but in cooperation with the business community .	然後我們決定幫助人們脫離貧窮 , 現在我們脫離了愛滋病 , 不是只有政府 , 而是和商業界合作 。
because poor people are business people who lack business skills and access to credit .	因為窮人是商人 , 他們缺乏商業技能和取得信用 。
those are the things to be provided by the business community .	這些是商業界提供的 。
we're trying to turn them into barefoot entrepreneurs , little business people .	我們試著把它們變成赤腳企業家 , 小企業家 。
the only way out of poverty is through business enterprise .	脫離貧窮的唯一方法是企業企業 。
so , that was done .	所以 , 這已經完成了 。
the money goes from the company into the village via treeplanting .	金錢從公司變成村落的移植 。
it's not a free gift .	這不是免費的禮物 。
they plant the trees , and the money goes into their microcredit fund , which we call the village development bank .	他們種植樹木 , 金錢進入他們的微型信貸基金 , 我們稱之為村落發展銀行 。
everybody joins in , and they feel they own the bank , because they have brought the money in .	每個人都加入 , 他們覺得自己擁有銀行 , 因為他們把錢帶進來 。
and before you can borrow the money , you need to be trained .	在你借錢之前 , 你得要被訓練 。
and we believe if you want to help the poor , those who are living in poverty , access to credit must be a human right .	我們相信如果你想要幫助窮人 , 生活在貧窮中的人 , 信用一定是人權 。
access to credit must be a human right .	能取得信用一定是人權 。
otherwise they'll never get out of poverty .	否則他們永遠不會脫離貧窮 。
and then before getting a loan , you must be trained .	在取得貸款之前 , 你一定要受過訓練 。
here's what we call a " barefoot mba , " teaching people how to do business so that , when they borrow money , they'll succeed with the business .	我們稱之為 「 赤腳mba 」 , 教導人們如何做生意 , 當他們借錢時 , 他們就會成功 。
these are some of the businesses: mushrooms , crabs , vegetables , trees , fruits , and this is very interesting nike ice cream and nike biscuits ; this is a village sponsored by nike .	這些是一些企業:蘑菇、螃蟹、蔬菜、樹木、水果 , 這非常有意思 , nike冰淇淋和nike餅乾 ; 這是nike贊助的村落 。
they said , " they should stop making shoes and clothes .	他們說: 「 他們應該停止製作鞋子和衣服 。
make these better , because we can afford them . "	把這些做得更好 , 因為我們可以負擔得起 。 」

so anyone sitting in and watching tv , get in touch with me .	所以 , 任何人坐在一起看電視 , 跟我聯絡 。

your smartphone may feel like a friend but a true friend would give you a smile once in a while . at ted2013 , keller rinaudo demos romo , the smartphonepowered mini robot who can motor along with you on a walk , slide you a cup of coffee across the table , and react to you with programmable expressions .	你的智慧手機可能會感覺像朋友 , 但真正的朋友會在一陣子內給你微笑 , 在ted2013年 , 克萊納多•德摩爾德莫斯 , 智慧型手機驅動的mini機器人 , 可以和你一起行走 , 投影片給你一杯咖啡橫跨桌面 , 並對你做出可程式的表情做出反應 。
keller rinaudo: a mini robot powered by your phone	kellerrinaudo:一個微型機器人 , 由你的手機發電 ,
so just by a show of hands , how many of you all have a robot at home ?	請舉手 , 你們當中有多少人在家裡都有機器人 ?
not very many of you .	不太多人 。
okay . and actually of those hands , if you don't include roomba how many of you have a robot at home ?	好 。 其實 , 如果你不包含在家裡有多少機器人呢 ?
that's the problem that we're trying to solve at romotive that i and the other 20 nerds at romotive are obsessed with solving .	這是我們試圖解決腐敗的問題 , 我和其他20位在romotive的書呆子都很著迷於解決問題 。
so we really want to build a robot that anyone can use , whether you're eight or 80 .	所以我們真的想要建造一個任何人都可以使用的機器人 , 不論你是八、八十歲 。
and as it turns out , that's a really hard problem , because you have to build a small , portable robot that's not only really affordable , but it has to be something that people actually want to take home and have around their kids .	結果發現 , 這是一個非常困難的問題 , 因為你必須建造一個小型可攜式的機器人 , 它不只能負擔得起 , 也必須是人們真正想要回家 , 帶著他們的孩子 。
this robot can't be creepy or uncanny .	這個機器人不會很可怕或不可思議 。
he should be friendly and cute .	他應該是友善且可愛 。
romo's a robot that uses a device you already know and love your iphone as his brain .	romo的機器人 , 用你已經知道且愛你的iphone的裝置作為他的大腦 。
and by leveraging the power of the iphone's processor , we can create a robot that is wifi enabled and computer visioncapable for 150 bucks , which is about one percent of what these kinds of robots have cost in the past .	透過iphone處理器的力量 , 我們就能創造出一個機器人 , 可以用wi-fi和電腦視覺 , 可以做到150美元 , 也就是這些機器人在過去所花費的百分之一 。
when romo wakes up , he's in creature mode .	當romo醒來時 , 他正處於生物模式中 。
