grandma can log into that robot and play hideandgoseek with her granddaughter for fifteen minutes every single night , when otherwise she might only be able to get to see her granddaughter once or twice a year .	祖母可以登入那個機器人 , 和她的孫女玩躲藏腳 , 每晚十五分鐘 , 否則她可能一年只能看到她的孫女一次或兩次 。
so those are a couple of the really cool things that romo can do today .	這些是現今romo能做的一些很酷的事 。
but i just want to finish by talking about something that we're working on in the future .	但我想先談談未來我們正在做的事 。
this is actually something that one of our engineers , dom , built in a weekend .	這其實是我們其中一個工程師 , 多姆 , 一個週末建成的 。
it's built on top of a google open framework called blockly .	它是建立在google開放框架上 , 叫做 「 街區 」 。
this allows you to drag and drop these blocks of semantic code and create any behavior for this robot you want .	這樣你就可以拖著這些連續的程式碼 , 為這個機器人創造任何你想要的行為 。
you do not have to know how to code to create a behavior for romo .	你不需要知道如何編寫romo的行為 。
and you can actually simulate that behavior in the browser , which is what you see romo doing on the left .	你可以在瀏覽器中模擬這種行為 , 也就是你在左邊看到romo在做的事 。
and then if you have something you like , you can download it onto your robot and execute it in real life , run the program in real life .	如果你有你喜歡的東西 , 你可以把它下載到你的機器人上 , 並在現實生活中執行這個計畫 。
and then if you have something you're proud of , you can share it with every other person who owns a robot in the world .	如果你有你自豪的東西 , 你可以和世界上所有擁有機器人的人分享 。
so all of these wifi–enabled robots actually learn from each other .	所有這些無線網路的機器人都能互相學習 。
the reason we're so focused on building robots that everyone can train is that we think the most compelling use cases in personal robotics are personal .	我們之所以如此專注於建造每個人都能訓練的機器人 , 是因為我們認為在個人機器人中 , 最令人費解的使用案例是個人的 。
they change from person to person .	它們會從人變成人 。
so we think that if you're going to have a robot in your home , that robot ought to be a manifestation of your own imagination .	所以 , 我們認為如果你要在家裡裝一個機器人 , 機器人應該是你自己的想像力 。
so i wish that i could tell you what the future of personal robotics looks like .	所以 , 我希望我能告訴你個人機器人的未來是什麼樣子 。
to be honest , i have no idea .	老實說 , 我不知道 。
but what we do know is that it isn't 10 years or 10 billion dollars or a large humanoid robot away .	但我們確實知道的是 , 它不是10年或100億美金或大型的人類機器人 。
the future of personal robotics is happening today , and it's going to depend on small , agile robots like romo and the creativity of people like yourselves .	個人機器人的未來正在發生 , 它取決於小型、敏捷的機器人 , 比如romo , 以及像你這樣的人的創造力 。
so we can't wait to get you all robots , and we can't wait to see what you build .	所以 , 我們等不及要讓你們所有機器人 , 我們等不及看到你建造的是什麼 。
author and activist isabel allende discusses women , creativity , the definition of feminism and , of course , passion in this talk .	作者和行動主義者伊莎貝爾主管討論女性、創意、女性主義的定義 , 當然 , 這場演說的熱情 。
entertainment , global issues , love , parenting , storytelling , women , world cultures	娛樂、全球議題、愛、養育、說故事、女性、世界文化、文化 。
isabel allende tells tales of passion	伊莎貝爾•艾倫說了熱情的故事 。
thank you so much . it's really scary to be here among the smartest of the smart .	非常謝謝 。 很可怕的 , 在這裏是最聰明的 。
i'm here to tell you a few tales of passion .	我來這裡是要告訴你們一些熱情的故事 。
there's a jewish saying that i love .	有句猶太人說我愛 。
what is truer than truth ? answer: the story .	比真相更真實 ? 答案:故事 。
i'm a storyteller . i want to convey something that is truer than truth about our common humanity .	我是個說故事的人 , 我想要傳達一些比我們共同的人性更真實的東西 。
all stories interest me , and some haunt me until i end up writing them .	所有故事都感興趣我 , 有些困擾我 , 直到最後我寫這些故事 。
certain themes keep coming up: justice , loyalty , violence , death , political and social issues , freedom .	有些主題不斷出現:正義、忠誠、暴力、死亡、政治和社會議題 , 自由 。
i'm aware of the mystery around us , so i write about coincidences , premonitions , emotions , dreams , the power of nature , magic .	我意識到我們周遭的謎題 , 所以我寫了關於巧合、預期、情緒、夢想、自然的力量、魔法 。
in the last 20 years i have published a few books , but i have lived in anonymity until february of 2006 , when i carried the olympic flag in the winter olympics in italy .	在過去的20年中 , 我發表了幾本書 , 但我在匿名度過 , 直到2006年2月 , 當我在義大利的冬天奧運會舉行奧運旗 。
that made me a celebrity . now people recognize me in macy's , and my grandchildren think that i'm cool .	這讓我成為了名人 。 現在 , 人們認得我是男女 , 而我的孫子們認為我很酷 。
allow me to tell you about my four minutes of fame .	讓我來告訴你我的四分鐘的名氣 。
one of the organizers of the olympic ceremony , of the opening ceremony , called me and said that i had been selected to be one of the flagbearers .	一名奧林匹克儀式的組織者 , 打電話給我 , 說我被選為國旗手之一 。
i replied that surely this was a case of mistaken identity because i'm as far as you can get from being an athlete .	我回答說 , 這是個錯誤認同的案例 , 因為我身為運動員 , 能從你身邊得知的範例 。
actually , i wasn't even sure that i could go around the stadium without a walker .	事實上 , 我甚至不確定我可以在沒有步行者的場所四處走動 。
i was told that this was no laughing matter .	我被告知這不是笑事 。
this would be the first time that only women would carry the olympic flag .	這是第一次 , 只有女性會帶著奧運國旗 。
five women , representing five continents , and three olympic gold medal winners .	五位女性代表五大洲 , 三個奧運金牌贏家 。
my first question was , naturally , what was i going to wear ?	我的第一個問題是 , 很自然地 , 我要穿什麼 ?
a uniform , she said , and asked for my measurements .	她說 , 一個制服 , 她問我的測量 。
i had a vision of myself in a fluffy anorak , looking like the michelin man .	我對自己有遠景 , 看起來像米契林人 。
by the middle of february , i found myself in turin , where enthusiastic crowds cheered when any of the 80 olympic teams was in the street .	到了二月中期 , 我在土耳其找到了我自己 , 在那裡 , 當80個奧運隊伍都在街上歡呼 。
those athletes had sacrificed everything to compete in the games .	這些運動員犧牲了遊戲中的一切競爭 。
they all deserved to win , but there's the element of luck .	他們都值得贏 , 但還有運氣的元素 。
a speck of snow , an inch of ice , the force of the wind , can determine the result of a race or a game .	一片雪花 , 一英吋的冰 , 一英吋的風力 , 可以決定賽跑的結果或遊戲 。
however , what matters most more than training or luck is the heart .	然而 , 比訓練或運氣更重要 。
only a fearless and determined heart will get the gold medal .	只有無懼且堅定的心會得到金牌 。
it is all about passion .	重點在於熱情 。
the streets of turin were covered with red posters announcing the slogan of the olympics .	土耳其的街道上有紅色海報 , 宣佈奧運的口號 。
passion lives here . isn't it always true ?	熱情生活在這裡 , 不是一直都是真的嗎 ?
heart is what drives us and determines our fate .	心是驅使我們並決定我們的命運的原因 。
that is what i need for my characters in my books: a passionate heart .	這是我書中角色所需要的:熱情的心 。
i need mavericks , dissidents , adventurers , outsiders and rebels , who ask questions , bend the rules and take risks .	我需要mavericks、異議人士、冒險人、外來者和反叛者 , 他們問問題、扭曲規則、冒險 。
people like all of you in this room .	像在座的各位一樣 。
nice people with common sense do not make interesting characters .	那些有常識的好人並不會做出有趣的角色 。
they only make good former spouses .	它們只能製造出好的配偶 。
in the green room of the stadium , i met the other flag bearers: three athletes , and the actresses susan sarandon and sophia loren .	在體育場的綠色房間裡 , 我遇見了其他國旗熊:三位運動員 , 還有蘇珊•沙蘭登和蘇菲雅羅倫 。
also , two women with passionate hearts: wangari maathai , the nobel prizewinner from kenya who has planted 30 million trees . and by doing so , she has changed the soil , the weather , in some places in africa , and of course the economic conditions in many villages .	另外 , 兩個有熱情心的女士 , wangarimaathai , 來自肯亞的諾貝爾獎得主 , 他種了三千萬棵樹 。 通過這麼做 , 她改變了土壤、天氣 , 在非洲的某些地方 , 當然 , 還有很多村莊的經濟狀況 。
and somaly mam , a cambodian activist who fights passionately against child prostitution .	一名柬埔寨激進分子 , 他們熱衷對抗兒童賣淫 。
when she was 14 years old , her grandfather sold her to a brothel .	當她十四歲時 , 她的祖父把她賣給妓院 。
she told us of little girls raped by men who believe that having sex with a very young virgin will cure them from aids .	她告訴我們 , 小女孩被男人強暴 , 她們相信和非常年輕的處女性行為會治好她們的愛滋病 。
and of brothels where children are forced to receive five , 15 clients per day , and if they rebel , they are tortured with electricity .	在那裡 , 孩子被迫每天收到5、15個客戶 , 如果他們反抗 , 他們就會被電擊折磨 。
in the green room i received my uniform .	在綠色的房間裡 , 我收到了制服 。
it was not the kind of outfit that i normally wear , but it was far from the michelin man suit that i had anticipated . not bad , really .	我通常穿的並不是那種衣服 , 但它離我預期的米其林曼服很遠 , 真的很糟 。
i looked like a refrigerator .	我看起來像個冰箱 。
but so did most of the flagbearers , except sophia loren , the universal symbol of beauty and passion .	除了蘇菲雅羅倫 , 普遍的美和熱情符號
sophia is over 70 and she looks great .	蘇菲雅超過七十歲 , 她看起來很棒 。
she's sexy , slim and tall , with a deep tan .	她很性感 , 很滑 , 很高 , 有很深的坦白 。
now , how can you have a deep tan and have no wrinkles ?	那麼 , 你要怎麼辦到一個很深的坦克 , 沒有皺紋 ?
when asked in a tv interview , " how could she look so good ? "	當在電視面談中被問到: 「 她怎麼能看起來這麼好 ? 」
she replied , " posture . my back is always straight , and i don't make old people's noises . "	她回答: 「 姿勢 。 我的背一直都是直的 , 我不會讓老人的噪音 。 」
so , there you have some free advice from one of the most beautiful women on earth .	這裡有一些免費的建議 , 來自地球上最美麗的女性之一 。
no grunting , no coughing , no wheezing , no talking to yourselves , no farting .	沒有抓住、沒有咳嗽、沒有呼吸、不和自己說話 , 不在場 。
well , she didn't say that exactly .	嗯 , 她沒有這麼說 。
at some point around midnight , we were summoned to the wings of the stadium , and the loudspeakers announced the olympic flag , and the music started by the way , the same music that starts here , the aida march .	在午夜的時候 , 我們被召喚到體育場的翅膀 , 大聲說服者宣佈奧運旗 , 音樂始於此 , 同樣的音樂始於艾達•馬奇 。
sophia loren was right in front of me she's a foot taller than i am , not counting the poofy hair .	蘇菲雅•羅倫站在我面前 , 她是比我高高 , 不算頭髮 。
she walked elegantly , like a giraffe on the african savannah , holding the flag on her shoulder . i jogged behind on my tiptoes holding the flag on my extended arm , so that my head was actually under the damn flag .	她優雅地走路 , 像在非洲草原上的長頸鹿 , 把旗子放在肩膀上 。 我在我的腳尖上 , 把旗子放在我的手臂上 , 這樣我的頭就在丹旗下 。
all the cameras were , of course , on sophia .	當然 , 所有的攝影機都在蘇菲雅 。
that was fortunate for me , because in most press photos i appear too , although often between sophia's legs .	這對我來說很幸運 , 因為在大部分的媒體照片中 , 我也看過 , 儘管在蘇菲雅的雙腳之間 。
a place where most men would love to be .	多數男人都很想去的地方 。
the best four minutes of my entire life were those in the olympic stadium .	我一生中最棒的四分鐘都是奧林匹克運動場的人 。
my husband is offended when i say this although i have explained to him that what we do in private usually takes less than four minutes so he shouldn't take it personally .	當我說這句話時 , 我的丈夫被冒犯了 , 雖然我向他解釋 , 我們私下做的事通常只花不到四分鐘 , 所以他不應該親身做 。
i have all the press clippings of those four magnificent minutes , because i don't want to forget them when old age destroys my brain cells .	我有這四分鐘的所有媒體點擊 , 因為我不想忘記那些年紀破壞我的大腦細胞 。
i want to carry in my heart forever the key word of the olympics passion .	我心裡想永遠帶著奧運熱情的關鍵字 。
so here's a tale of passion .	這是個熱情的故事 。
the year is 1998 , the place is a prison camp for tutsi refugees in congo .	今年是1998年 , 這個地方是剛果的監獄營 。
by the way , 80 percent of all refugees and displaced people in the world are women and girls .	順便一提 , 世界上80%的難民和流離失所的人都是女性和女孩 。
we can call this place in congo a death camp , because those who are not killed will die of disease or starvation .	我們可以把這個地方命名為剛果的死營 , 因為那些沒有殺死的人 , 會死於疾病或飢餓 。
the protagonists of this story are a young woman , rose mapendo , and her children .	這個故事的主角是一位年輕女子 , 羅塞•地圖 , 還有她的孩子 。
she's pregnant and a widow .	她懷孕和寡婦 。
soldiers have forced her to watch as her husband was tortured and killed .	士兵迫使她看著她的丈夫被折磨並殺害 。
somehow she manages to keep her seven children alive , and a few months later , she gives birth to premature twins .	不知何故 , 她還能讓七個孩子活下來 , 幾個月後 , 她生下了早產的雙胞胎 。
two tiny little boys .	兩個小男孩 。
she cuts the umbilical cord with a stick , and ties it with her own hair .	她用棍子剪下麻木 , 用她自己的頭髮綁住它 。
she names the twins after the camp's commanders to gain their favor , and feeds them with black tea because her milk cannot sustain them .	她以營地指揮官的名字命名為雙胞胎 , 用黑色茶餵食牠們 , 因為她的牛奶無法維持牠們 。
when the soldiers burst in her cell to rape her oldest daughter , she grabs hold of her and refuses to let go , even when they hold a gun to her head .	當士兵在她的牢房裡打破她最老的女兒時 , 她抓住她 , 拒絕放手 , 即使他們拿著槍頭 。
somehow , the family survives for 16 months , and then , by extraordinary luck , and the passionate heart of a young american man , sasha chanoff , who manages to put her in a u . s . rescue plane , rose mapendo and her nine children end up in phoenix , arizona , where they're now living and thriving .	不知怎麼的 , 家庭存活了十六個月 , 接著 , 很棒的運氣 , 一位年輕的美國人 , 薩斯夏•查奈夫的熱情心 , 他們想辦法把她放進美國救援平機 , 羅斯地圖和她的九個孩子最後到了亞利桑納州鳳凰城 , 現在他們活著繁榮 。
mapendo , in swahili , means great love .	在斯瓦希里語的地圖 , 是很棒的愛 。
the protagonists of my books are strong and passionate women like rose mapendo .	我書的主角堅強和熱情的女性 , 像羅塞•地圖 。
i don't make them up . there's no need for that .	我不會讓他們站起來 , 沒有必要的 。
i look around and i see them everywhere .	我環顧四周 , 到處看到它們 。
i have worked with women and for women all my life .	我和我的一生都和女性和女性一起工作 。
i know them well .	我很清楚他們 。
i was born in ancient times , at the end of the world , in a patriarchal catholic and conservative family .	我出生於古代 , 在世界末日 , 在父權天主教和保守的家庭中 。
no wonder that by age five i was a raging feminist although the term had not reached chile yet , so nobody knew what the heck was wrong with me .	難怪到五歲時 , 我是個狂熱的女權主義者 , 雖然這個詞還沒到智利 , 所以沒有人知道我有什麼問題 。
i would soon find out that there was a high price to pay for my freedom , and for questioning the patriarchy .	我很快就會發現 , 我的自由有很高的代價 , 並且質疑父權制度 。
but i was happy to pay it , because for every blow that i received , i was able to deliver two .	但我很高興能付錢 , 因為每次我接到的炸彈 , 我都能遞送兩次 。
once , when my daughter paula was in her twenties , she said to me that feminism was dated , that i should move on .	有一次 , 當我女兒保羅在她二十多歲時 , 她告訴我 , 女權主義是約會的 , 我應該繼續下去 。
we had a memorable fight . feminism is dated ?	我們有一場令人難忘的戰鬥 。 女權主義是約會的 ?
yes , for privileged women like my daughter and all of us here today , but not for most of our sisters in the rest of the world who are still forced into premature marriage , prostitution , forced labor they have children that they don't want or they cannot feed .	沒錯 , 對於像我女兒一樣有特權的女性 , 如今在座的我們所有人 , 但對世界上大部分的姐妹來說 , 她們仍然被迫要婚姻、妓女、強迫她們有孩子 , 她們不想要或無法餵飽 。
they have no control over their bodies or their lives .	他們無法掌控自己的身體或生命 。
they have no education and no freedom .	他們沒有教育 , 也沒有自由 。
they are raped , beaten up and sometimes killed with impunity .	他們被強暴 , 有時被毆打 , 有時被懲罰 。
for most western young women of today , being called a feminist is an insult .	現今大多數西方的年輕女性 , 被稱為女性主義者是侮辱 。
feminism has never been sexy , but let me assure you that it never stopped me from flirting , and i have seldom suffered from lack of men .	女權主義從來沒有性感 , 但讓我向你保證 , 從來沒有阻止我調情 , 我也曾被男性缺乏 。
feminism is not dead , by no means .	女性主義沒有死亡 , 沒有意義 。
it has evolved . if you don't like the term , change it , for goddess' sake .	它已經進化了 。 如果你不喜歡這個詞 , 改變它 , 改變它 , 給上帝的 。
call it aphrodite , or venus , or bimbo , or whatever you want ; the name doesn't matter , as long as we understand what it is about , and we support it .	稱之為aphrodite , 金星 , 或bimbo , 或任何你想要的東西 ; 只要我們了解它是什麼 , 我們就支持它 。
so here's another tale of passion , and this is a sad one .	這是另一個充滿熱情的故事 , 這是悲傷的故事 。
the place is a small women's clinic in a village in bangladesh .	這個地方是孟加拉村的一間小女子診所 。
the year is 2005 .	這一年是2005年 。
jenny is a young american dental hygienist who has gone to the clinic as a volunteer during her threeweek vacation .	珍妮是年輕的美國牙醫衛生專家 , 她在三週假期間去診所 。
she's prepared to clean teeth , but when she gets there , she finds out that there are no doctors , no dentists , and the clinic is just a hut full of flies .	她準備好要乾淨牙齒 , 但當她到達那裡時 , 她發現沒有醫生 , 沒有牙醫 , 診所只是蒼蠅的小屋 。
outside , there is a line of women who have waited several hours to be treated .	在外面 , 有一系列的女性 , 等了好幾個小時才能被治療 。
the first patient is in excruciating pain because she has several rotten molars .	第一個病人處於痛苦之中 , 因為她有好幾個腐爛的分子 。
jenny realizes that the only solution is to pull out the bad teeth .	珍妮知道唯一的解決方法就是拉出不好的牙齒 。
she's not licensed for that ; she has never done it .	她沒有許可 ; 她從來沒有做過 。
she risks a lot and she's terrified .	她冒了很多險 , 她嚇壞了 。
she doesn't even have the proper instruments , but fortunately she has brought some novocaine .	她甚至沒有適當的樂器 , 但幸運的是 , 她帶來了一些麻煩 。
jenny has a brave and passionate heart .	珍妮有勇敢和熱情心 。
she murmurs a prayer and she goes ahead with the operation .	她把禱告交給禱告 , 繼續手術 。
at the end , the relieved patient kisses her hands .	最後 , 病人鬆了一口氣 , 親吻她的手 。
that day the hygienist pulls out many more teeth .	那天 , 衛生學家再抽出更多牙齒 。
the next morning , when she comes again to the socalled clinic , her first patient is waiting for her with her husband .	隔天早上 , 當她再次到所謂的診所時 , 她的第一個病人正在和丈夫等待 。
the woman's face looks like a watermelon .	這位女士的臉看起來像是水母 。
it is so swollen that you can't even see the eyes .	你甚至看不見眼睛是如此的腫脹 。
the husband , furious , threatens to kill the american .	丈夫、憤怒、威脅要殺掉美國人 。
jenny is horrified at what she has done , but then the translator explains that the patient's condition has nothing to do with the operation .	珍妮對她所做的事感到害怕 , 但接著 , 翻譯解釋病人的狀況和手術一點關係都沒有 。
the day before , her husband beat her up because she was not home in time to prepare dinner for him .	前一天 , 她丈夫打她起床 , 因為她不在家準備晚餐 。
millions of women live like this today .	現今有數百萬的女性像這樣生活 。
they are the poorest of the poor .	他們是最貧窮的人 。
although women do twothirds of the world's labor , they own less than one percent of the world's assets .	雖然世界上三分之二的女性 , 她們擁有不到百分之一的資產 。
they are paid less than men for the same work if they're paid at all , and they remain vulnerable because they have no economic independence , and they are constantly threatened by exploitation , violence and abuse .	他們的薪水低於男性 , 如果他們付錢 , 他們仍然脆弱 , 因為他們沒有經濟獨立 , 且他們不斷受到剝削、暴力和虐待的威脅 。
it is a fact that giving women education , work , the ability to control their own income , inherit and own property , benefits the society .	事實上 , 給予婦女教育、工作、掌握自己的收入、繼承、自己的財產、受益於社會 。
if a woman is empowered , her children and her family will be better off .	如果一個女人被賦予權力 , 她的孩子和她的家人就會更好 。
if families prosper , the village prospers , and eventually so does the whole country .	如果家庭繁榮 , 村落繁榮 , 最終 , 整個國家都如此 。
wangari maathai goes to a village in kenya .	wangarimaathai去肯亞的村莊 。
she talks with the women and explains that the land is barren because they have cut and sold the trees .	她和婦女談話 , 解釋土地很荒謬 , 因為他們已經砍樹 , 賣了樹木 。
she gets the women to plant new trees and water them , drop by drop .	她讓婦女種植新樹和水 , 下落 。
in a matter of five or six years , they have a forest , the soil is enriched , and the village is saved .	五、六年之內 , 他們有一片森林 , 土壤豐富 , 村落也拯救了 。
the poorest and most backward societies are always those that put women down .	最貧窮和最後退的社會 , 總是那些讓女性下台的人 。
yet this obvious truth is ignored by governments and also by philanthropy .	但這個明顯的事實卻被政府忽視 , 也被慈善事業忽視 。
for every dollar given to a women's program , 20 dollars are given to men's programs .	每一塊美金給一個婦女的計畫 , 有20塊美金給男性的方案 。
women are 51 percent of humankind .	女性是51%的人類 。
empowering them will change everything more than technology and design and entertainment .	賦予他們力量 , 改變一切 , 遠勝於科技、設計和娛樂 。
i can promise you that women working together linked , informed and educated can bring peace and prosperity to this forsaken planet .	我可以向各位保證 , 女性一起合作 , 連結、知情和教育 , 可以帶來和平和繁榮 , 帶給這個脆弱的星球 。
in any war today , most of the casualties are civilians , mainly women and children . they are collateral damage .	在任何戰爭中 , 大部分的傷亡者都是平民 , 主要是女性和孩子 。 他們是負面的傷害 。
men run the world , and look at the mess we have .	男人經營世界 , 看看我們所擁有的混亂 。
what kind of world do we want ?	我們想要什麼樣的世界 ?
this is a fundamental question that most of us are asking .	這是一個我們大部分人都在問的問題 。
does it make sense to participate in the existing world order ?	是否合理地參與現有的世界秩序 ?
we want a world where life is preserved and the quality of life is enriched for everybody , not only for the privileged .	我們想要一個生活保存和生活品質的世界 , 不僅是為了特權而豐富 。
in january i saw an exhibit of fernando botero's paintings at the uc berkeley library .	在一月 , 我看到費南多•波特羅在加州柏克萊圖書館的畫展 。
no museum or gallery in the united states , except for the new york gallery that carries botero's work , has dared to show the paintings because the theme is the abu ghraib prison .	在美國 , 沒有博物館或畫廊 , 除了紐約畫廊 , 波特羅的作品 , 還敢展示這幅畫 , 因為主題是阿布格萊布監獄 。
they are huge paintings of torture and abuse of power , in the voluminous botero style .	它們是巨大的折磨和濫用權力的畫作 , 在巨大的botero風格中 。
i have not been able to get those images out of my mind or my heart .	我無法從我的心中或心中得到這些影像 。
what i fear most is power with impunity .	我最害怕的是權力 。
i fear abuse of power , and the power to abuse .	我害怕濫用權力 , 以及濫用權力 。
in our species , the alpha males define reality , and force the rest of the pack to accept that reality and follow the rules .	在我們的物種中 , 雄性領袖定義現實 , 並迫使其餘的群體接受現實並遵循規則 。
the rules change all the time , but they always benefit them , and in this case , the trickledown effect , which does not work in economics , works perfectly .	規則不斷地改變 , 但它們總是受益 , 在這個例子中 , 棘手的效應 , 在經濟上行不通 , 完全有效 。
abuse trickles down from the top of the ladder to the bottom .	虐待會從梯子的頂端滲透到底部 。
women and children , especially the poor , are at the bottom .	女性和兒童 , 特別是窮人 , 她們在最底層 。
even the most destitute of men have someone they can abuse a woman or a child .	即使是男性中最多的人 , 也有他們能虐待女人或小孩的人 。
i'm fed up with the power that a few exert over the many through gender , income , race , and class .	我用性別、收入、種族、階級來餵食的力量 。
i think that the time is ripe to make fundamental changes in our civilization .	我認為 , 時間是對我們文明的基礎改變 。
but for real change , we need feminine energy in the management of the world .	但 , 為了真正的改變 , 我們需要全世界的女性能源管理 。
we need a critical number of women in positions of power , and we need to nurture the feminine energy in men .	我們需要有權力的女性 , 我們需要培養男性女性的女性能量 。
i'm talking about men with young minds , of course .	當然 , 我在說的是有年輕心智的人 。
old guys are hopeless ; we have to wait for them to die off .	老人沒有希望 , 我們得要等他們死 。
yes , i would love to have sophia loren's long legs and legendary breasts .	是的 , 我很想擁有蘇菲雅羅倫的長腿和傳奇的胸部 。
but given a choice , i would rather have the warrior hearts of wangari maathai , somaly mam , jenny and rose mapendo .	但 , 為了選擇 , 我寧願有勇氣的心 , 班加利馬塔伊 , 瑪瑪麗、珍妮和玫瑰地圖 。
i want to make this world good .	我想讓這個世界變得更好 。
not better , but to make it good .	不是更好 , 而是要讓它更好 。
why not ? it is possible . look around in this room all this knowledge , energy , talent and technology .	為什麼不 ? 它是可能的 。 看看這個房間裡的所有知識、能量、才華和科技 。
let's get off our fannies , roll up our sleeves and get to work , passionately , in creating an almost perfect world .	讓我們脫離我們的粉絲 , 捲起袖子 , 去工作 , 熱情地創造一個幾乎完美的世界 。
every day , in a city the size of london , 30 million meals are served . but where does all the food come from ? architect carolyn steel discusses the daily miracle of feeding a city , and shows how ancient food routes shaped the modern world .	每天 , 在倫敦大小的城市裡 , 有三千萬份餐是被服務的 。 但是 , 所有的食物是從哪裡來的 ? 建築師卡羅琳•史提爾在討論餵飽一個城市的日常奇蹟 , 顯示古老的食物如何影響現代世界 。
cities , culture , food , global issues	城市、文化、食物、全球議題 。
carolyn steel: how food shapes our cities	卡羅琳•史黛爾:食物如何塑造我們的城市 , 如何塑造我們的城市 。
how do you feed a city ?	你要如何餵飽一座城市 ?
it's one of the great questions of our time .	這是我們這個時代最棒的問題之一 。
yet it's one that's rarely asked .	但卻很少被問到 。
we take it for granted that if we go into a shop or restaurant , or indeed into this theater's foyer in about an hour's time , there is going to be food there waiting for us , having magically come from somewhere .	我們視之為理所當然 , 如果我們去一間商店或餐廳 , 或是在大約一小時的戲院裡 , 會有食物等著我們 , 神奇地從某處來 。
but when you think that every day for a city the size of london , enough food has to be produced , transported , bought and sold , cooked , eaten , disposed of , and that something similar has to happen every day for every city on earth , it's remarkable that cities get fed at all .	但當你認為每一天 , 一個倫敦大小的城市 , 足夠的食物必須被生產、運輸、購買、煮、吃飯、丟棄 , 類似的事情每天都要發生在地球上 , 對於每個城市而言 , 都市都能得到食物 。
we live in places like this as if they're the most natural things in the world , forgetting that because we're animals and that we need to eat , we're actually as dependent on the natural world as our ancient ancestors were .	我們生活在像這樣的地方 , 彷彿他們是世界上最自然的東西 , 因為我們是動物 , 而且我們需要吃 , 我們其實是依賴自然界的祖先 。
and as more of us move into cities , more of that natural world is being transformed into extraordinary landscapes like the one behind me it's soybean fields in mato grosso in brazil in order to feed us .	隨著更多人進入城市 , 更多的自然世界正在被轉變為非凡的景觀 , 就像我身後的景觀 , 它是巴西馬托格羅索的大豆田 , 為了餵飽我們 。
these are extraordinary landscapes , but few of us ever get to see them .	這些是很不尋常的景觀 , 但我們當中少數人能看到它們 。
and increasingly these landscapes are not just feeding us either .	越來越多的景觀 , 不僅僅是餵飽我們 。
as more of us move into cities , more of us are eating meat , so that a third of the annual grain crop globally now gets fed to animals rather than to us human animals .	隨著更多人進入城市 , 越來越多人吃肉 , 全球每年有三分之一的穀物被餵給動物 , 而不是給人類動物 。
and given that it takes three times as much grain actually ten times as much grain to feed a human if it's passed through an animal first , that's not a very efficient way of feeding us .	由於它需要三倍的穀物實際上是十倍的穀物來餵飽人類如果它是先通過動物的話這不是非常有效率的餵食方式
and it's an escalating problem too .	這也是一個不斷增加的問題 。
by 2050 , it's estimated that twice the number of us are going to be living in cities .	到2050年 , 估計我們將會住在城市中的兩倍 。
and it's also estimated that there is going to be twice as much meat and dairy consumed .	估計也會有兩倍的肉類和奶類消耗 。
so meat and urbanism are rising hand in hand .	所以肉類和城市主義正在舉手 。
and that's going to pose an enormous problem .	這將會是一個巨大的問題 。
six billion hungry carnivores to feed , by 2050 .	到2050年 , 飢餓的食肉動物會餵食 。
that's a big problem . and actually if we carry on as we are , it's a problem we're very unlikely to be able to solve .	這是個大問題 。 實際上 , 如果我們繼續這樣做 , 這是我們無法解決的問題 。
nineteen million hectares of rainforest are lost every year to create new arable land .	每年有九千萬公頃的雨林消失了 , 造成新的耕地 。
although at the same time we're losing an equivalent amount of existing arables to salinization and erosion .	儘管同時 , 我們也失去相當於現有的可耕種性來鹽化和氣化 。
we're very hungry for fossil fuels too .	我們也對化石燃料非常渴望 。
it takes about 10 calories to produce every calorie of food that we consume in the west .	要花十卡路里才能產出我們西方消耗的每一卡路里 。
and even though there is food that we are producing at great cost , we don't actually value it .	儘管我們有很大的成本生產的食物 , 我們卻不重視它 。
half the food produced in the usa is currently thrown away .	美國有一半的食物產量正在被丟棄 。
and to end all of this , at the end of this long process , we're not even managing to feed the planet properly .	為了結束這一切 , 在這個漫長的過程結束時 , 我們甚至沒有辦法適當地把地球餵飽 。
a billion of us are obese , while a further billion starve .	十億人肥胖 , 甚至十億人挨餓 。
none of it makes very much sense .	這一切都沒有道理 。
and when you think that 80 percent of global trade in food now is controlled by just five multinational corporations , it's a grim picture .	當你認為 , 全球百分之八十的糧食交易只受五家跨國企業掌控 , 這是一張很可怕的照片 。
as we're moving into cities , the world is also embracing a western diet .	當我們進入城市時 , 世界也在擁抱西方的飲食 。
and if we look to the future , it's an unsustainable diet .	如果我們看看未來 , 這是一種不穩定的飲食 。
so how did we get here ?	我們是怎麼走到這一步的 ?
and more importantly , what are we going to do about it ?	更重要的是 , 我們要怎麼做 ?
well , to answer the slightly easier question first , about 10 , 000 years ago , i would say , is the beginning of this process in the ancient near east , known as the fertile crescent .	首先 , 要回答稍微簡單的問題 , 大約一萬年前 , 我會說 , 這個過程是在東邊古老的這個過程 , 也就是所謂的肥沃土壤 。
because , as you can see , it was crescent shaped .	因為 , 如你所見 , 它的形狀很近 。
and it was also fertile .	它也很肥沃 。
and it was here , about 10 , 000 years ago , that two extraordinary inventions , agriculture and urbanism , happened roughly in the same place and at the same time .	大約一萬年前 , 這裡有兩項非凡的發明 , 農業和城市主義 , 發生在同一個地方 , 同時也是如此 。
this is no accident , because agriculture and cities are bound together . they need each other .	這不是偶然的 , 因為農業和城市是互相連結的 。 他們需要彼此 。
because it was discovery of grain by our ancient ancestors for the first time that produced a food source that was large enough and stable enough to support permanent settlements .	因為這是我們古老祖先第一次發現穀物 , 製造出足夠大且穩定的食物來源 , 足以支撐永久的居住地 。
and if we look at what those settlements were like , we see they were compact .	如果我們看看這些定居處是什麼樣子 , 我們會看到它們是很完整的 。
they were surrounded by productive farm land and dominated by large temple complexes like this one at ur , that were , in fact , effectively , spiritualized , central food distribution centers .	他們圍繞著有生產力的農地 , 被大型寺廟主宰 , 像這一個在烏爾的大型神廟 , 事實上 , 實際上是精神化的 , 中央食物分配中心 。
because it was the temples that organized the harvest , gathered in the grain , offered it to the gods , and then offered the grain that the gods didn't eat back to the people .	因為那是神廟組織了收成的神殿 , 聚集在穀物中 , 將它送給神 , 然後給予神沒有回來吃的穀物 。
so , if you like , the whole spiritual and physical life of these cities was dominated by the grain and the harvest that sustained them .	所以 , 如果你喜歡 , 這些城市的整個靈性和實體生活是由穀物和收穫所主導的 。
and in fact , that's true of every ancient city .	事實上 , 每個古老城市都是如此 。
but of course not all of them were that small .	但當然不是全部都這麼小 。
famously , rome had about a million citizens by the first century a . d .	著名的是 , 羅馬在第一世紀時有大約一百萬名公民 。
so how did a city like this feed itself ?	所以 , 像這樣的城市是如何養活的 ?
the answer is what i call " ancient food miles . "	答案是我所謂的 「 古老食物里程 」 。
basically , rome had access to the sea , which made it possible for it to import food from a very long way away .	基本上 , 羅馬可以接觸到海洋 , 讓它能在很遠的遠處取得進口食物 。
this is the only way it was possible to do this in the ancient world , because it was very difficult to transport food over roads , which were rough .	這是唯一可能在古代世界做這件事的方法 , 因為在道路上 , 要運送食物是非常困難的 。
and the food obviously went off very quickly .	食物顯然很快就消失了 。
so rome effectively waged war on places like carthage and egypt just to get its paws on their grain reserves .	所以 , 羅馬有效地在像卡瑟和埃及這樣的地方打仗 , 只為了取得他們的穀物儲備 。
and , in fact , you could say that the expansion of the empire was really sort of one long , drawn out militarized shopping spree , really .	事實上 , 你可以說 , 帝國的擴張真的很長一段時間 , 引出軍事化的購物速度很快 。
in fact i love the fact , i just have to mention this: rome in fact used to import oysters from london , at one stage . i think that's extraordinary .	事實上 , 我很喜歡這個事實 , 我只需要提一下:羅馬以前從倫敦的牡蠣 , 一個階段 。 我認為這很了不起 。
so rome shaped its hinterland through its appetite .	所以羅馬形塑了它的暗落 , 穿過它的胃口 。
but the interesting thing is that the other thing also happened in the preindustrial world .	但有趣的是 , 另一件事也發生在工業前的世界 。
if we look at a map of london in the 17th century , we can see that its grain , which is coming in from the thames , along the bottom of this map .	如果我們看看十七世紀倫敦的地圖 , 我們可以看到它的穀物 , 它的穀物是從這張地圖的底部來的 。
so the grain markets were to the south of the city .	所以 , 穀物市場到了城市的南部 。
and the roads leading up from them to cheapside , which was the main market , were also grain markets .	道路從它們變成廉價 , 主要市場也是穀物市場 。
and if you look at the name of one of those streets , bread street , you can tell what was going on there 300 years ago .	如果你看看其中一條街道的名字 , 布雷德街 , 你可以知道三百年前發生了什麼事 。
and the same of course was true for fish .	當然 , 對魚來說也是如此 。
fish was , of course , coming in by river as well . same thing .	當然 , 魚也是靠河流進來的 。
and of course billingsgate , famously , was london's fish market , operating onsite here until the mid1980s .	當然 , 據名的倫敦的魚市場 , 直到1980年代中期才開始運作 。
which is extraordinary , really , when you think about it .	這真是不可思議 , 真的 , 仔細想想 。
everybody else was wandering around with mobile phones that looked like bricks and sort of smelly fish happening down on the port .	其他人都在用手機走來走去 , 看起來像是磚頭 , 有點像是在港口的煙魚 。
this is another thing about food in cities: once its roots into the city are established , they very rarely move .	這是關於城市中的食物的另一件事:一旦它的根就被建立起來 , 它們很少會移動 。
meat is a very different story because , of course , animals could walk into the city .	肉類是非常不一樣的故事 , 因為 , 當然 , 動物可以走進城市 。
so much of london's meat was coming from the northwest , from scotland and wales .	倫敦大部分的肉來自西北部蘇格蘭和威爾斯 。
so it was coming in , and arriving at the city at the northwest , which is why smithfield , london's very famous meat market , was located up there .	所以它進入了 , 抵達西北部的城市 , 這就是為什麼史密斯菲爾德倫敦著名的肉市場 , 位在上面 。
poultry was coming in from east anglia and so on , to the northeast .	家禽從東加利亞來到東北部 。
i feel a bit like a weather woman doing this . anyway , and so the birds were coming in with their feet protected with little canvas shoes .	不管怎樣 , 我覺得有點像是天氣女子在做這件事 。 所以 , 鳥兒們用小的帆布來保護牠們 。
and then when they hit the eastern end of cheapside , that's where they were sold , which is why it's called poultry .	當他們抵達廉價的東邊時 , 他們就被賣掉了 , 這就是為什麼它會被稱為 「 土耳其 」 。
and , in fact , if you look at the map of any city built before the industrial age , you can trace food coming in to it .	事實上 , 如果你看看工業年齡前任何城市的地圖 , 你可以追蹤食物進來 。
you can actually see how it was physically shaped by food , both by reading the names of the streets , which give you a lot of clues .	你可以看到它是如何被食物所塑造的 , 不論是閱讀街道的名字 , 都給了你很多線索 。
friday street , in a previous life , is where you went to buy your fish on a friday .	星期五街 , 以前的生活就是你在星期五買魚的地方 。
but also you have to imagine it full of food .	但同時你也必須想像它充滿食物 。
because the streets and the public spaces were the only places where food was bought and sold .	因為街道和公共空間是食物被賣的唯一地方 。
and if we look at an image of smithfield in 1830 you can see that it would have been very difficult to live in a city like this and be unaware of where your food came from .	如果我們看一下1830年史密斯菲爾德的影像 , 你可以看到在像這樣的城市中 , 很難住在這樣的城市裡 , 不知你的食物從何而來 。
in fact , if you were having sunday lunch , the chances were it was mooing or bleating outside your window about three days earlier .	事實上 , 如果你有星期日午餐 , 可能是三天前你窗戶外流浪的機會 。
so this was obviously an organic city , part of an organic cycle .	這顯然是一個有機城市 , 一個有機循環的一部分 。
and then 10 years later everything changed .	十年後 , 一切都改變了 。
this is an image of the great western in 1840 .	這是1840年大西部的圖像 。
and as you can see , some of the earliest train passengers were pigs and sheep .	如你所見 , 最早的火車乘客是豬和羊 。
so all of a sudden , these animals are no longer walking into market .	突然間 , 這些動物不再走進市場 。
they're being slaughtered out of sight and mind , somewhere in the countryside .	他們被從視覺和心智中被屠殺 , 在鄉下的某處 。
and they're coming into the city by rail .	他們被鐵路來到城市裡 。
and this changes everything .	這改變了一切 。
to start off with , it makes it possible for the first time to grow cities , really any size and shape , in any place .	首先 , 首次要種植城市 , 大小和形狀 , 在任何地方 。
cities used to be constrained by geography ; they used to have to get their food through very difficult physical means .	以前 , 城市被地理限制 ; 過去 , 他們必須透過非常困難的實體來取得食物 。
all of a sudden they are effectively emancipated from geography .	突然間 , 它們都從地理學來解放 。
and as you can see from these maps of london , in the 90 years after the trains came , it goes from being a little blob that was quite easy to feed by animals coming in on foot , and so on , to a large splurge , that would be very , very difficult to feed with anybody on foot , either animals or people .	如你所見 , 從倫敦的這些地圖 , 在火車經過的90年後 , 它從一個小小的燈泡 , 很容易被動物從腳上餵飽 , 如此一來 , 到一個大的噴泉 , 非常非常難以滿足任何人 , 不論是動物或人類 。
and of course that was just the beginning . after the trains came cars , and really this marks the end of this process .	當然 , 這只是開端 。 火車來了 , 真的是這整個過程的終點 。
it's the final emancipation of the city from any apparent relationship with nature at all .	這是城市最後的解放 , 完全從大自然的任何明顯關係中解放 。
and this is the kind of city that's devoid of smell , devoid of mess , certainly devoid of people , because nobody would have dreamed of walking in such a landscape .	這座城市是沒有氣味、缺乏混亂的城市 , 當然也沒有人 , 因為沒有人會夢想走在這樣的景觀中 。
in fact , what they did to get food was they got in their cars , drove to a box somewhere on the outskirts , came back with a week's worth of shopping , and wondered what on earth to do with it .	事實上 , 他們為了得到食物 , 他們開車到郊區某處 , 帶回一週的購物品 , 想知道地球上要怎麼做 。
and this really is the moment when our relationship , both with food and cities , changes completely .	這真的是我們與食物和城市之間的關係 , 完全改變了 。
here we have food that used to be the center , the social core of the city at the periphery .	這裡有過去的食物是市中心的社會核心 。
it used to be a social event , buying and selling food .	它以前是社交活動 , 購買和賣食物 。
we used to cook ; now we just add water , or a little bit of an egg if you're making a cake or something .	我們以前會煮飯 , 只要加水 , 或是蛋 , 只要你做蛋糕或其他東西 。
we don't smell food to see if it's okay to eat .	我們不會聞到食物來看看它是否可以吃 。
we just read the back of a label on a packet .	我們只是讀了包裝後面的標籤 。
and we don't value food . we don't trust it .	我們不重視食物 , 我們不信任它 。
so instead of trusting it , we fear it .	所以 , 我們不再相信它 , 而是害怕它 。
and instead of valuing it , we throw it away .	而不是在評估它 , 而是丟掉它 。
one of the great ironies of modern food systems is that they've made the very thing they promised to make easier much harder .	現代食品系統的諷刺之處在於他們已經做出了他們承諾要讓更加困難的事 。
by making it possible to build cities anywhere and any place , they've actually distanced us from our most important relationship , which is that of us and nature .	藉由使我們能在任何地方建立城市 , 任何地方 , 都能讓我們遠離我們最重要的關係 , 那就是我們和大自然 。
and also they've made us dependent on systems that only they can deliver , that , as we've seen , are unsustainable .	此外 , 他們也讓我們依賴他們所能提供的系統 , 如我們所見 , 無法永續發展 。
so what are we going to do about that ?	所以 , 我們該怎麼做 ?
it's not a new question .	這不是一個新問題 。
500 years ago it's what thomas more was asking himself .	五百年前 , 湯瑪斯更多問自己 。
this is the frontispiece of his book " utopia . "	這是他的書《烏托邦》的第一集 。
and it was a series of semiindependent citystates , if that sounds remotely familiar , a day's walk from one another where everyone was basically farmingmad , and grew vegetables in their back gardens , and ate communal meals together , and so on .	那是一系列的半獨立城市 , 如果這聽起來很熟悉 , 一天的走路 , 基本上每個人都是農場主 , 並且在他們的後花園中種植蔬菜 , 吃下午餐等等 。
and i think you could argue that food is a fundamental ordering principle of utopia , even though more never framed it that way .	我認為你可以主張 , 食物是烏托邦的基本原則 , 儘管如此 , 卻從來沒有這樣框架過 。
and here is another very famous " utopian " vision , that of ebenezer howard , " the garden city . "	還有另一個著名的 「 烏托邦 」 視覺 , 埃比沙尼茲霍華 , 「 花園城市 」 。
same idea: series of semiindependent citystates , little blobs of metropolitan stuff with arable land around , joined to one another by railway .	同樣的想法:一系列的半獨立城市 , 一小塊大都市 , 附近有可耕地的小塊地 , 加入火車 。
and again , food could be said to be the ordering principle of his vision .	同樣的 , 食物可以被認為是他視力的順序原則 。
it even got built , but nothing to do with this vision that howard had .	它甚至被建造出來 , 但與霍華德的遠景無關 。
and that is the problem with these utopian ideas , that they are utopian .	這就是這些烏托邦的想法的問題 , 它們是烏托邦 。
utopia was actually a word that thomas moore used deliberately .	烏托邦其實是湯瑪斯•摩爾刻意使用的一個詞 。
it was a kind of joke , because it's got a double derivation from the greek .	這是個笑話 , 因為它是希臘人的兩倍衍生的 。
it can either mean a good place , or no place .	它可能意味著一個好地方 , 或沒有地方 。
because it's an ideal . it's an imaginary thing . we can't have it .	因為它是理想的 , 它是想像的東西 , 我們不能擁有它 。
and i think , as a conceptual tool for thinking about the very deep problem of human dwelling , that makes it not much use .	我認為 , 作為一個概念工具 , 來思考人類的深層問題 , 讓它不太有用 。
so i've come up with an alternative , which is sitopia , from the ancient greek , " sitos " for food , and " topos " for place .	所以我想出了一個替代方案 , 也就是西托邦 , 古希臘文 , 「 西托 」 為食物和 「 波斯 」 。
i believe we already live in sitopia .	我相信我們已經住在西托邦 。
we live in a world shaped by food , and if we realize that , we can use food as a really powerful tool a conceptual tool , design tool , to shape the world differently .	我們生活在一個由食物塑造的世界 , 如果我們意識到 , 我們能用食物來當作一個非常強大的工具 , 設計工具 , 來形塑這個世界 。
so if we were to do that , what might sitopia look like ?	所以如果我們這樣做 , 希托邦看起來會是什麼樣子 ?
well i think it looks a bit like this .	我想這看起來有點像這樣 。
i have to use this slide . it's just the look on the face of the dog .	我得用這張投影片 , 只是狗的臉 。
but anyway , this is it's food at the center of life , at the center of family life , being celebrated , being enjoyed , people taking time for it .	但無論如何 , 這是生活中心的食物 , 在家庭生活的中心 , 被讚頌、享受、享受、花時間 。
this is where food should be in our society .	這就是食物在我們的社會所在的地方 。
but you can't have scenes like this unless you have people like this .	但除非你有像這樣的人 , 你不能有這樣的場景 。
by the way , these can be men as well .	順道一提 , 這些也可以是男人 。
it's people who think about food , who think ahead , who plan , who can stare at a pile of raw vegetables and actually recognize them .	它是那些思考食物的人 , 想著 , 誰計劃 , 誰可以盯著一堆原始蔬菜 , 並且認出他們 。
we need these people . we're part of a network .	我們需要這些人 , 我們是網路的一部分 。
because without these kinds of people we can't have places like this .	因為若沒有這些人 , 我們就不能有這樣的地方 。
here , i deliberately chose this because it is a man buying a vegetable .	在這裡 , 我故意選這個 , 因為它是一個男人買蔬菜 。
but networks , markets where food is being grown locally .	但網絡 , 食物在當地種植的市場 。
it's common . it's fresh .	它很常見 , 很新鮮 。
it's part of the social life of the city .	它是城市社會生活的一部分 。
because without that , you can't have this kind of place , food that is grown locally and also is part of the landscape , and is not just a zerosum commodity off in some unseen hellhole .	因為 , 若沒有這些 , 你就不能有這種地方 , 當地生長的食物 , 也是地景的一部分 , 不僅僅是零和商品 , 在一些未知的地獄中 。
cows with a view .	牛的觀點是 。
steaming piles of humus .	蒸汽一堆濕瓜 。
this is basically bringing the whole thing together .	這基本上是把整個東西整合在一起 。
and this is a community project i visited recently in toronto .	這是我最近在多倫多拜訪的一個社區計畫 。
it's a greenhouse , where kids get told all about food and growing their own food .	這是一間溫室 , 孩子們會告訴所有關於食物和種植他們自己的食物 。
here is a plant called kevin , or maybe it's a plant belonging to a kid called kevin . i don't know .	這裡有一株叫做凱文的植物 , 也許是植物屬於一個叫凱文的孩子 。 我不知道 。
but anyway , these kinds of projects that are trying to reconnect us with nature is extremely important .	但無論如何 , 這些計畫試圖和大自然重新連結是非常重要的 。
so sitopia , for me , is really a way of seeing .	所以 , 對我來說 , 西托邦是種看法 。
it's basically recognizing that sitopia already exists in little pockets everywhere .	基本上 , 意識到西托邦已經存在於小口袋裡 。
the trick is to join them up , to use food as a way of seeing .	把它們加在一起 , 把食物當作一種看法 。
and if we do that , we're going to stop seeing cities as big , metropolitan , unproductive blobs , like this .	如果我們這樣做 , 我們將會停止把城市視為大型、大都會、沒有生產力的區域 , 像這樣 。
we're going to see them more like this , as part of the productive , organic framework of which they are inevitably a part , symbiotically connected .	我們將看到它們更像這樣 , 作為有生產力、有機架構的一部分 , 它們是無可避免的一部分 , 相同的連結 。
but of course , that's not a great image either , because we need not to be producing food like this anymore .	但當然 , 這也不是一個偉大的圖像 , 因為我們不需要再像這樣生產食物 。
we need to be thinking more about permaculture , which is why i think this image just sums up for me the kind of thinking we need to be doing .	我們需要多考慮永續栽培 , 這就是為什麼我認為這張圖只是為了我總結我們需要做的事 。
it's a reconceptualization of the way food shapes our lives .	它是一種重新思考食物如何塑造我們的生活方式 。
the best image i know of this is from 650 years ago .	我所知道最棒的圖像是650年前 。
it's ambrogio lorenzetti's " allegory of good government . "	阿布羅吉歐•羅倫澤蒂的《好政府的寓言》 。
it's about the relationship between the city and the countryside .	重點是城市和鄉村之間的關係 。
and i think the message of this is very clear .	我認為這訊息非常清楚 。
if the city looks after the country , the country will look after the city .	如果城市照顧這個國家 , 這個國家會照顧城市 。
and i want us to ask now , what would ambrogio lorenzetti paint if he painted this image today ?	現在我要問我們 , 阿布羅吉歐•洛倫澤蒂是否畫了這張圖呢 ?
what would an allegory of good government look like today ?	今天美好政府的寓言會是什麼樣子 ?
because i think it's an urgent question .	因為我認為這是個急迫的問題 。
it's one we have to ask , and we have to start answering .	它是我們必須問的 , 我們必須開始回答 。
we know we are what we eat .	我們知道我們吃的東西 。
we need to realize that the world is also what we eat .	我們需要了解到 , 世界也是我們所吃的 。
but if we take that idea , we can use food as a really powerful tool to shape the world better .	但如果我們採用這個想法 , 我們就可以把食物當作一個非常強大的工具來塑造世界更好 。
weeks from the charter for compassion launch , karen armstrong looks at religion's role in the 21st century: will its dogmas divide us ? or will it unite us for common good ? she reviews the catalysts that can drive the world's faiths to rediscover the golden rule .	數週後 , 凱倫•阿姆斯壯在21世紀探究宗教的角色:它的教條會讓我們分裂嗎 ? 或者它會讓我們聯繫共同利益 ? 她會檢視世界上的催化劑 , 來重新發現黃金法則 。
god , ted prize , global issues , politics , religion , tedglobal2009 , violence	上帝 , ted大獎、全球議題、政治、宗教、tedglobal-2009年、暴力事件 。
karen armstrong: let's revive the golden rule	卡倫•阿姆斯壯:咱們回想黃金法則 。
for years i've been feeling frustrated , because as a religious historian , i've become acutely aware of the centrality of compassion in all the major world faiths .	多年來 , 我感到很挫折 , 因為身為宗教歷史學家 , 我漸漸意識到 , 同情心的中心性 , 在世界的主要信仰中 。
every single one of them has evolved their own version of what's been called the golden rule .	他們每一個人都演化出他們所謂的黃金法則的版本 。
sometimes it comes in a positive version " always treat all others as you'd like to be treated yourself . "	有時會出現一個正面的版本: 「 永遠對待他人 , 就像你想治療自己一樣 。 」
and equally important is the negative version " don't do to others what you would not like them to do to you . "	同樣重要的是負面的版本: 「 不要對別人做你不希望他們做的事 。 」
look into your own heart , discover what it is that gives you pain and then refuse , under any circumstance whatsoever , to inflict that pain on anybody else .	看看你自己的心 , 發現你的痛苦是什麼 , 然後拒絕 , 在任何情況下 , 在任何情況下 , 將痛苦給任何其他人 。
and people have emphasized the importance of compassion , not just because it sounds good , but because it works .	人們強調同情心的重要性 , 不只是因為它聽起來很好 , 也因為它有效 。
people have found that when they have implemented the golden rule as confucius said , " all day and every day , " not just a question of doing your good deed for the day and then returning to a life of greed and egotism , but to do it all day and every day , you dethrone yourself from the center of your world , put another there , and you transcend yourself .	人們發現 , 當他們實施黃金法則時 , 如同concius所說: 「 整天和每一天 , 」 不只是在做好事 , 然後回到貪婪和自我主義的一生 , 日復一日 , 日復一日 , 日復一日 , 你將自己從你的世界的中心 , 放下另一人 , 超越你自己 。
and it brings you into the presence of what's been called god , nirvana , rama , tao .	它帶領你進入了所謂的 「 神 」 、 「 神 」 、 「 拉馬 」 、 「 塔羅 」 的存在 。
something that goes beyond what we know in our egobound existence .	超越我們所知的事物 , 超越了我們所知的存在 。
but you know you'd never know it a lot of the time , that this was so central to the religious life .	但你知道你從來不知道 , 這對宗教生活是如此的核心 。
because with a few wonderful exceptions , very often when religious people come together , religious leaders come together , they're arguing about abstruse doctrines or uttering a council of hatred or inveighing against homosexuality or something of that sort .	因為有了一些很棒的例外 , 當宗教團體聚在一起 , 宗教領袖聚集在一起 , 他們爭論的是墮胎教條 , 或說出仇恨的議會 , 或對抗同性戀或其他類型的人 。
often people don't really want to be compassionate .	通常 , 人們並不想要有同情心 。
i sometimes see when i'm speaking to a congregation of religious people a sort of mutinous expression crossing their faces because people often want to be right instead .	有時 , 我會看到當我和宗教人士談話時 , 有點像是跨越他們的臉 , 因為人們通常會想要是對的 。
and that of course defeats the object of the exercise .	當然 , 這也打敗了運動的物體 。
now why was i so grateful to ted ?	我為什麼很感激ted ?
because they took me very gently from my booklined study and brought me into the 21st century , enabling me to speak to a much , much wider audience than i could have ever conceived .	因為他們很溫柔地從我的書籍研究帶我進入21世紀 , 讓我能夠和更多的觀眾說話 , 比我想像中更廣泛 。
because i feel an urgency about this .	因為我對此感到急迫 。
if we don't manage to implement the golden rule globally , so that we treat all peoples , wherever and whoever they may be , as though they were as important as ourselves , i doubt that we'll have a viable world to hand on to the next generation .	如果我們無法在全球實施黃金法則 , 這樣我們就能對待所有人 , 無論他們在哪裡 , 無論他們是誰 , 就好像他們一樣重要 , 我懷疑我們會有一個可實現的世界 , 來接近下一代 。
the task of our time , one of the great tasks of our time , is to build a global society , as i said , where people can live together in peace .	我們這個時代的任務之一 , 就是要建立一個全球社會 , 如我所說 , 在那裡 , 人們可以一起生活在和平中 。
and the religions that should be making a major contribution are instead seen as part of the problem .	應該要做出重大貢獻的宗教被視為問題的一部分 。
and of course it's not just religious people who believe in the golden rule .	當然 , 不只是宗教信仰黃金法則的人 。
this is the source of all morality , this imaginative act of empathy , putting yourself in the place of another .	這是所有道德的來源 , 這種想像力的行為 , 把你自己放在另一個地方 。
and so we have a choice , it seems to me .	所以 , 我們有選擇 , 似乎對我來說 。
we can either go on bringing out or emphasizing the dogmatic and intolerant aspects of our faith , or we can go back to the rabbis . rabbi hillel , the older contemporary of jesus , who , when asked by a pagan to sum up the whole of jewish teaching while he stood on one leg , said , " that which is hateful to you , do not do to your neighbor .	我們要不就是把教義和寬容的信仰帶回來 , 要不就是我們能回到拉比 。 拉比希爾 , 更老的耶穌當代 , 當他站在一條腿上時 , 全猶太教義總結起來時 , 說: 「 這對你來說很討厭 , 不要對你的鄰居做事 。
that is the torah and everything else is only commentary . "	這就是托拉和其他一切都只是評論 。 」
and the rabbis and the early fathers of the church who said that any interpretation of scripture that bred hatred and disdain was illegitimate .	教堂早期的拉比和早期的父親說 , 任何關於仇恨和厭惡的文字的詮釋都是非法的 。
and we need to revive that spirit .	我們需要重新思考這種精神 。
and it's not just going to happen because a spirit of love wafts us down .	這不只是因為愛的靈魂讓我們失望 。
we have to make this happen , and we can do it with the modern communications that ted has introduced .	我們必須讓這一切實現 , 而且我們可以用現代的溝通來實現 。
already i've been tremendously heartened at the response of all our partners .	我已經對我們所有夥伴的回應感到非常心碎 。
in singapore , we have a group going to use the charter to heal divisions recently that have sprung up in singaporean society , and some members of the parliament want to implement it politically .	在新加坡 , 我們有一個團體會用章節來治療新加坡社會的分裂 , 議會中的一些成員想要在政治上實施它 。
in malaysia , there is going to be an art exhibition in which leading artists are going to be taking people , young people , and showing them that compassion also lies at the root of all art .	在馬來西亞 , 將會有一場藝術展覽 , 讓藝術家帶領人們、年輕人 , 並展現出同情心 , 也是所有藝術的根源 。
throughout europe , the muslim communities are holding events and discussions , are discussing the centrality of compassion in islam and in all faiths .	在整個歐洲 , 穆斯林社區正在舉辦活動和討論 , 討論的是伊斯蘭和所有信仰中的同情心中心 。
but it can't stop there . it can't stop with the launch .	但它不能停止 。 它不能停止發射 。
religious teaching , this is where we've gone so wrong , concentrating solely on believing abstruse doctrines .	宗教教義 , 這就是我們錯了的地方 , 只靠信仰abstrussstrine 。
religious teaching must always lead to action .	宗教教學一定會導致行動 。
and i intend to work on this till my dying day .	我打算在臨終日工作 。
and i want to continue with our partners to do two things educate and stimulate compassionate thinking .	我想繼續跟我們的另一半繼續做兩件事 , 教育和刺激同情心 。
education because we've so dropped out of compassion .	教育因為我們已經失去了同情心 。
people often think it simply means feeling sorry for somebody .	人們通常認為這意味著對某人感到遺憾 。
but of course you don't understand compassion if you're just going to think about it .	但 , 當然 , 如果你只是想一想 , 你不會了解同情心 。
you also have to do it .	你也必須這麼做 。
i want them to get the media involved because the media are crucial in helping to dissolve some of the stereotypical views we have of other people , which are dividing us from one another .	我希望他們能得到媒體參與 , 因為媒體是很重要的 , 協助解開一些我們有的人的刻板印象 , 將我們彼此分離出來 。
the same applies to educators .	教育者也是如此 。
i'd like youth to get a sense of the dynamism , the dynamic and challenge of a compassionate lifestyle .	我希望青少年能感受到動態、動態和挑戰著同情的生活方式 。
and also see that it demands acute intelligence , not just a gooey feeling .	此外 , 它也要求急性智能 , 不只是感覺美好 。
i'd like to call upon scholars to explore the compassionate theme in their own and in other people's traditions .	我想打電話給學者 , 來探索他們自己的同情心主題 , 以及其他人的傳統 。
and perhaps above all , to encourage a sensitivity about uncompassionate speaking , so that because people have this charter , whatever their beliefs or lack of them , they feel empowered to challenge uncompassionate speech , disdainful remarks from their religious leaders , their political leaders , from the captains of industry .	也許最重要的是 , 鼓勵不熱情說話的敏感度 , 如此一來 , 因為人們有這個特徵 , 不論他們的信仰或缺乏信仰 , 他們會覺得有能力去挑戰不熱情的言論、不穩定的言論 , 來自他們的宗教領袖、政治領袖、他們的政治領袖 。
because we can change the world , we have the ability .	因為我們可以改變世界 , 我們有能力 。
i would never have thought of putting the charter online .	我從來不會想到把章節放上網 。
i was still stuck in the old world of a whole bunch of boffins sitting together in a room and issuing yet another arcane statement .	我仍然被困在舊的世界裡 , 一大堆炸彈坐在一個房間裡 , 同時還在說另一個阿肯尼的陳述 。
and ted introduced me to a whole new way of thinking and presenting ideas .	ted向我介紹一個全新的思維和想法 。
because that is what is so wonderful about ted .	因為這就是ted的美好之處 。
in this room , all this expertise , if we joined it all together , we could change the world .	在這個房間裡 , 所有這些專業知識 , 如果我們全部加入 , 我們就能改變世界 。
and of course the problems sometimes seem insuperable .	當然 , 有時 , 問題似乎是不可思議的 。
but i'd just like to quote , finish at the end with a reference to a british author , an oxford author whom i don't quote very often , c . s . lewis .	但最後我想引用一句英國作家的話 , 一位牛津作家 , 我不常引用c.路易斯的話 。
but he wrote one thing that stuck in my mind ever since i read it when i was a schoolgirl .	但他寫了一件事 , 自從我讀書時 , 一直困擾著我 。
it's in his book " the four loves . "	它在他的書《四個愛》中 。
he said that he distinguished between erotic love , when two people gaze , spellbound , into each other's eyes .	他說他分辨出愛情 , 當兩個人凝視著咒語 , 互相交換成眼睛 。
and then he compared that to friendship , when two people stand side by side , as it were , shoulder to shoulder , with their eyes fixed on a common goal .	接著 , 他把這和友誼比較 , 當兩個人站在旁邊 , 就像肩膀一樣 , 他們的眼睛會固定在共同的目標上 。
we don't have to fall in love with each other , but we can become friends .	我們不必愛彼此 , 但我們可以成為朋友 。
and i am convinced .	我深信 。
i felt it very strongly during our little deliberations at vevey , that when people of all different persuasions come together , working side by side for a common goal , differences melt away .	我覺得很強烈 , 在我們在vey的小調查中 , 當所有不同的說服者聚在一起 , 一起工作時 , 共同目標 , 差異會融化 。
and we learn amity .	我們學習的是 「 性 」 。
and we learn to live together and to get to know one another .	我們學會一起生活 , 認識彼此 。
thank you very much .	謝謝大家 。
david macaulay relives the winding and sometimes surreal journey toward the completion of rome antics , his illustrated homage to the historic city .	davidmacaulay改造了風 , 有時 , 超現實的旅程 , 朝著羅馬運動的競爭 , 他的描繪 , 和歷史城市有關 。

anyway , the pooch gets back to the dirigible with the stuff .	總之 , 糞便會帶著這些東西回去 。
unfortunately , when she goes to unwrap the prosciutto , ajax makes a lunge for it .	不幸的是 , 當她去解開原子核時 , ajax會為它做午餐 。
she's managed to save the prosciutto , but in the process she loses the tablecloth , which you can see flying away in the upper lefthand corner .	她成功地拯救了原住民 , 但在這個過程中 , 她失去了桌布 , 你可以看到在左上角飛走 。
they continue without their tablecloth , looking for a place to land this thing so that they can actually have lunch .	他們不用桌布繼續下去 , 尋找一個地方降落這個地方 , 這樣他們才能真的吃午餐 。
they eventually discover a huge wall that's filled with small holes , ideal for docking a dirigible because you've got a place to tie up .	他們最終發現一個充滿了小洞的巨牆 , 理想的做法 , 因為你有地方綁起來 。
turns out to be the exterior wall that part of it that remains of the coliseum , so they park themselves there and have a terrific lunch and have a spectacular view .	原來是哥倫理的外牆 , 剩下的部份 , 所以他們把自己停在那裡 , 吃了一頓很棒的午餐 , 看得很棒 。
at the end of lunch , they untie the anchor , they set off through the baths of caracalla and over the walls of the city and then an abandoned gatehouse and decide to take one more look at the pyramid of cestius , which has this lightning rod on top .	午餐結束時 , 他們打開了主管 , 他們打開了卡拉卡拉的浴室 , 穿過城市的牆壁 , 然後一個廢棄的大門 , 決定再看一下cestius的金字塔 。
unfortunately , that's a problem: they get a little too close , and when you're in a dirigible you have to be very careful about spikes .	不幸的是 , 這是個問題:它們太靠近了 , 當你有潛力的時候 , 你必須非常小心地去吸一口氣 。
so that sort of brings her little story to a conclusion .	所以這就把她小故事帶到一個結論中 。
marcello , on the other hand , is sort of a lazy guy , but he's not due at work until about noon .	另一方面 , marcello有點懶人 , 但他在工作直到午上 。
so , the alarm goes off and it's five to 12 or so .	所以 , 警報響起 , 大概有5到12 。
he gets up , leaps onto his scooter , races through the city past the church of santa maria della pace , down the alleys , through the streets that tourists may be wandering through , disturbing the quiet backstreet life of rome at every turn .	他站起來 , 跳上他的摩托車 , 穿過城市的賽車 , 穿過聖塔瑪莉亞德拉的教堂 , 走下巷子 , 遊客可能在街上遊走 , 每次都破壞羅馬的安靜生活 。
that speed with which he is moving , i hope i have suggested in this little image , which , again , can be turned around and read from both sides because there's text on the bottom and text on the top , one of which is upside down in this image .	他正在移動的速度 , 我希望我在這張小圖片中提到 , 同樣的 , 可以從兩邊轉過來閱讀 , 因為上面有文字 , 上面有簡訊 , 上面寫著這張圖片上下面的圖片 。
so , he keeps on moving , approaching an unsuspecting waiter who is trying to deliver two plates of linguine in a delicate white wine clam sauce to diners who are sitting at a table just outside of a restaurant in the street .	所以 , 他繼續前進 , 接近一個毫無疑問的服務員 , 他試圖在很細緻的白葡萄酒店裡提供兩塊口味的口味 , 讓坐在餐廳外面的晚餐 。
waiter catches on , but it's too late .	服務生抓住了 , 但太晚了 。
and marcello keeps moving in his scooter .	馬歇爾多繼續走下去 。
everything he sees from this point on is slightly affected by the linguine , but keeps on moving because this guy's got a job to do .	他在這個時點所看到的一切 , 都有點受語言影響 , 但繼續下去 , 因為這個人有工作要做 。
removes some scaffolding . one of the reasons rome remains the extraordinary place it is that because of scaffolding and the determination to maintain the fabric , it is a city that continues to grow and adapt to the needs of the particular time in which it finds itself , or we find it .	除去一些支架 。 羅馬仍然不平凡的原因之一 , 因為支架和決心要維持布料的結構 , 這個城市持續成長和適應特定時間的需求 。
right through the piazza della rotonda , in front of the pantheon again wreaking havoc and finally getting to work .	穿越了帕雅茲達•羅頓達 , 在萬神殿前 , 再次威脅到工作 。
marcello , as it turns out , is the driver of the number 64 bus , and if you've been on the number 64 bus , you know that it's driven with the same kind of exuberance as marcello demonstrated on his scooter .	結果發現 , 馬賽洛是數字64輛巴士的司機 , 如果你曾上過64輛公車 , 你知道馬賽洛的駕駛和馬歇爾羅的摩托車一樣高興 。
and finally carletto . you see his apartment in the upper lefthand corner .	最後是卡萊托 。 你看到他在左上角的公寓 。
he's looking at his table ; he's planning to propose this evening to his girlfriend of 40 years , and he wants it to be perfect .	他看著他的桌子 , 今晚要向他的女朋友提議這個晚上四十年的樣子 , 他希望它是完美的 。
he's got candles out , he's got flowers in the middle and he's trying to figure out where to put the plates and the glasses .	他拿出蠟燭 , 中間有花 , 他正在想辦法把盤子和玻璃放在哪裡 。
but he's not happy ; something's wrong .	但他不快樂 , 有些問題 。
the phone rings anyway , he's called to the palazzo .	總之 , 電話響了 , 他被叫到palazo 。
he saunters he saunters at a good clip , but as compared to all the traveling we've just seen , he's sauntering .	他在一段很棒的短片中挑選 , 但比起我們剛才所看到的旅行 , 他在反射 。
everybody knows carletto , because he's in entertainment , actually ; he's in television .	大家都知道卡萊托 , 因為他在娛樂中 , 其實他在電視上 。
he's actually in television repair , which is why people know him .	他其實是在電視修復中 , 這就是為什麼大家知道他 。
so they all have his number .	所以他們都有他的數字 。
he arrives at the palazzo , arrives at the big front door .	他到達了帕拉zo , 到達了大門 。
enters the courtyard and talks to the custodian , who tells him that there's been a disaster in the palazzo ; nobody's tvs are working and there's a big soccer game coming up , and the crowd is getting a little restless and a little nervous .	進入法庭院 , 和顧客交談 , 他告訴他 , 在巴拉zo有災難 ; 沒有人在電視上播放 , 有一個大型足球比賽正在上來 , 群眾變得有點無休 , 有點緊張 。
he goes down to the basement and starts to check the wiring , and then gradually works his way up to the top of the building , apartment by apartment , checking every television , checking every connection , hoping to find out what this problem is .	他走到地下室 , 開始檢查電線 , 然後逐漸地工作到建築的頂端 , 透過公寓檢查 , 檢查每個電視 , 檢查所有連線 , 希望能找出這個問題是什麼 。
he works his way up , finally , the grand staircase and then a smaller staircase until he reaches the attic .	他爬上去 , 最後 , 爬樓梯 , 直到他抵達閣樓 。
he opens the window of the attic , of course , and there's a tablecloth wrapped around the building's television antenna .	他打開閣樓的窗戶 , 當然 , 有一張桌布包圍在大樓的電視天線上 。
he removes it , the problems are solved , everybody in the palazzo is happy .	他移除它 , 解決問題 , 巴拉zo的所有人都很快樂 。
and of course , he also solves his own problem .	當然 , 他也解決了他自己的問題 。
all he has to do now , with a perfect table , is wait for her to arrive .	他現在只需要做一個完美的桌子 , 等著她到達 。
that was the first attempt , but it didn't seem substantial enough to convey whatever it was i wanted to convey about rome .	那是第一個嘗試 , 但似乎還不夠多 , 可以傳達我想要傳達的羅馬 。
so i thought , well , i'll just do piazzas , and i'll get inside and underneath and i'll show these things growing and show why they're shaped the way they are and so on .	所以我想 , 嗯 , 我只會做帕亞薩斯 , 我會進去 , 下面我會展示這些東西 , 展示它們如何形成它們的樣子 , 等等 。
and then i thought , that's too complicated . no , i'll just take my favorite bits and pieces and i'll put them inside the pantheon but keep the scale , so you can see the top of sant'ivo and the pyramid of cestius and the tempietto of bramante all side by side in this amazing space .	然後我想 , 這太複雜了 。 不 , 我會把我最喜歡的部分和碎片放進萬神殿裡 , 這樣你就能看到聖誕節的頂端和克西斯蒂夫的金字塔 , 在這神奇的空間中 。
now that's one drawing , so i thought maybe it's time for piranesi to meet escher .	這是一幅畫 , 所以我想也許是要見escher的時候了 。
you see that i'm beginning to really lose control here and also hope .	你可以看到我開始失去控制權 , 也開始失去希望 。
there's a very thin blue line of exhaust that sort of runs through this thing that would be kind of the trail that holds it all together .	有一條非常薄的藍色的外殼 , 一路穿過這個東西 , 有點像是把它們整合在一起的軌跡 。
then i thought , " wait a minute , what am i doing ? "	然後我想: 「 等等 , 我在做什麼 ? 」
a book is not only a neat way of collecting and storing information , it's a series of layers .	書不僅是收集和儲存資訊的方式 , 而是一系列的層次 。
i mean , you always peel one layer off another ; we think of them as pages , doing it a certain way .	我的意思是 , 你總是把一層剝離另一層 ; 我們認為它們是頁面 , 以某種方式做 。
but think of them as layers . i mean , rome is a place of layers horizontal layers , vertical layers and i thought , well just peeling off a page would allow me to if i got you thinking about it the right way would allow me to sort of show you the depth of layers .	但 , 把它們想成是層層 。 我的意思是 , 羅馬是層層層的層次 , 垂直層 , 我心想 , 只要我把頁面撕掉 , 就可以讓你思考一下 , 讓我可以給你們看一些正確的層次 。
the stucco on the walls of most of the buildings in rome covers the scars ; the scars of centuries of change as these structures have been adapted rather than being torn down .	羅馬大廈的牆壁上大部分的建築都覆蓋著疤痕 , 這些結構數世紀以來 , 改變的疤痕被當作適應 , 而不是被摧毀 。
if i do a foldout page on the lefthand side and let you just unfold it , you see behind it what i mean by scar tissue .	如果我在左邊做摺紙的頁面 , 讓你展開它 , 你可以看到我所謂的疤痕組織 。
you can see that in 1635 , it became essential to make smaller windows because the bad guys were coming or whatever .	你可以看到 , 在1635年 , 製造小窗戶是必要的 , 因為壞人來了 , 不論如何 。
adaptations all get buried under the stucco .	適應措施都被埋在黏土下 。
i could peel out a page of this palazzo to show you what's going on inside of it .	我可以把這個palazzo的一頁給你們看看裡面發生了什麼事 。
but more importantly , i could also show you what it looks like at the corner of one of those magnificent buildings with all the massive stone blocks , or the fake stone blocks done with brick and stucco , which is more often the case .	但更重要的是 , 我還可以讓你們看看 , 那些偉大的建築的角落 , 上面有著巨大的石塊 , 或用磚塊做仿冒的石塊 , 通常是如此 。
so it becomes slightly threedimensional .	所以它變得有點三維 。
i could take you down one of those narrow little streets into one of those surprising piazzas by using a double gate fold double foldout page which , if you were like me reading a popup book as a child , you hopefully stick your head into .	我可以把你們其中一個狹窄的小街道帶到其中一個令人驚訝的比賽中 , 用一雙折疊的雙折頁頁頁面 , 如果你像我小時候讀一本popup的書 , 你希望能把頭伸進去 。
you wrap the pages around your head and are in that piazza for that brief period of time .	你把你頭上的頁面包裹起來 , 就在那短暫的時間內 。
and i've really not done anything much more complicated than make foldout pages .	我真的沒有做任何更複雜的事 , 比摺疊頁更複雜 。
but then i thought , maybe i could be simpler here .	但我想 , 也許我可以更簡單一點 。
let's look at the pantheon and the piazza della rotonda in front of it .	咱們來看看萬神殿和帕亞茲達面前的羅頓達 。
here's a book completely wide open .	這是一本完全開放的書 。
ok , if i don't open the book the whole way , if i just open it 90 degrees , we're looking down the front of the pantheon , and we're looking sort of at the top , more or less down on the square .	好吧 , 如果我不打開這本書 , 只要我打開它90度 , 我們就在視萬神廟的前方 , 我們就好像往上看 , 在廣場上方 , 或多或少看到 。
and if i turn the book the other way , we're looking across the square at the front of the pantheon .	如果我把書換成另一種方式 , 我們會看到萬神廟前方的廣場 。
no foldouts , no tricks just a book that isn't open the whole way .	沒有摺疊 , 沒有單純的把戲 , 沒有完全打開 。
that seemed promising . i thought , maybe i'll do it inside and i can even combine the foldouts with the only partially opened book .	這似乎很有希望 。 我想 , 也許我可以進去 , 我甚至可以將摺疊技術和唯一開放的書結合起來 。
so we get inside the pantheon and it grows and so on and so forth .	所以我們進到萬神廟裡 , 它的成長等等 。
and i thought , maybe i'm on the right track , but it sort of lost its human quality .	我心想 , 也許我在正確的軌道上 , 但它似乎失去了人類的品質 。
so i went back to the notion of story , which is always a good thing to have if you're trying to get people to pay attention to a book and pick up information along the way .	所以我回到故事的概念 , 如果你想讓人們注意一本書 , 一路上收集資訊 , 總是有好處 。
" pigeon's progress " struck me as a catchy title .	「 鴿子的進步 」 把我當作捕捉頭銜 。
if it was a homing pigeon , it would be called " homer's odyssey . "	如果這隻鴿子叫作 「 荷馬的奧德賽 」 。
but it was the journey of the . . .	但那是那段旅程......
i mean , if a title works , use it . but it would be a journey that went through rome and showed all the things that i like about rome .	我的意思是 , 如果一個標題成功 , 用它 。 但這將會是一段旅程 , 經過羅馬 , 展現我喜歡的所有羅馬的東西 。
it's a pigeon sitting on top of a church .	它是教堂頂端的鴿子 。
goes off during the day and does normal pigeon stuff . comes back , the whole place is covered with scaffolding and green netting and there's no way this pigeon can get home .	白天停下來 , 做正常的鴿子 , 回來 , 整個地方都被支架和綠色網路包覆著 , 這樣鴿子就不可能回家了 。
so it's a homeless pigeon now and it's going to have to find another place to live , and that allows me to go through my catalog of favorite things , and we start with the tall ones and so on .	它現在是無家可歸的鴿子 , 它必須找到另一個住的地方 , 這樣我才能穿越我最喜歡的東西 , 我們從最高的鴿子開始 。
maybe it has to go back and live with family members ; that's not always a good thing , but it does sort of bring pigeons together again .	也許它必須回去和家人住在一起 , 那不一定是件好事 , 但它會再次把鴿子帶回來 。
and i thought , that's sort of interesting , but maybe there's a person who should be involved in this in some way .	我心想 , 這有點有趣 , 但也許有個人應該以某種方式參與這件事 。
so i kind of came up with this old guy who spends his life looking after sick pigeons .	所以我想出了一個老人 , 他一生都在照顧生病的鴿子 。
he'll go anywhere to get them dangerous places and whatnot and they become really friends with this guy , and learn to do tricks for him and entertain him at lunchtime and stuff like that .	他會到哪裡去找他們危險的地方 , 他們會變成和這個傢伙交朋友 , 學著為他做技倆 , 在午餐時間和其他地方娛樂他 。
there's a real bond that develops between this old man and these pigeons .	在這個老人和鴿子之間 , 有一個真正的聯結 。
but unfortunately he gets sick . he gets really sick at the end of the story .	但不幸的是 , 他生病了 。 他在故事結束時真的生病了 。
he's taught them to spell his name , which is aldo .	他被教導要拼他的名字 , 艾爾多 。
they show up one day after three or four days of not seeing him he lives in this little garret and they spell his name and fly around .	三四天後 , 他們出席了一天 , 他住在這個小垃圾桶裡 , 他們把他的名字和飛來飛去 。
and he finally gets enough strength together to climb up the ladder onto the roof , and all the pigeons , a la red balloon , are there waiting for him and they carry him off over the walls of the city .	他終於得到足夠的力量 , 把梯子爬到屋頂上 , 所有的鴿子 , 紅氣球等著他 , 把他帶到城市的牆上 。
and i forgot to mention this: whenever he lost a pigeon , he would take that pigeon out beyond the walls of the city .	我忘了提到這一點:每當他失去鴿子時 , 他都會把鴿子帶到城市的牆外 。
in the old roman custom , the dead were never buried within the walls .	在古羅馬的習俗中 , 死者從來沒有被埋在牆上 。
and i thought that's a really cheery story .	我覺得這真是令人興奮的故事 。
. that's really going to go a long way .	這真的會很長一段時間 。
so anyway , i went through . . . and again , if packaging doesn't work and if the stories aren't going anywhere , i just come up with titles and hope that a title will sort of kick me off in the right direction .	總之 , 我經歷了一次 , 如果包裝不成功 , 如果故事不在任何地方 , 我只是想出了標題 , 希望有個標題會引起我走向正確的方向 。
and sometimes it does focus me enough and i'll even do a title page .	有時它會讓我專注 , 我甚至會做一個標題 。
so , these are all title pages that eventually led me to the solution i settled on , which is the story of a young woman who sends a message on a homing pigeon she lives outside the walls of the city of rome to someone in the city .	所以 , 這些都是標題圖 , 最終引領我到我定居的解決方案 , 就是一個年輕女子的故事 , 她在羅馬市外的羅馬城牆外 , 向城市中的某個人傳遞訊息 。
and the pigeon is flying down above the appian way here .	鴿子在上方飛行 。
you can see the tombs and pines and so on and so forth along the way .	你可以看到墳墓和松樹等等 , 一路走來 。
if you see the red line , you are seeing the trail of the pigeon ; if you don't see the red line , you are the pigeon .	如果你看到紅線 , 你可以看到鴿子的軌跡 ; 如果你看不到紅線 , 你就是鴿子 。
and it becomes necessary and possible , at this point , to try to convey what that sense would be like of flying over the city without actually moving .	此時此刻 , 它會變成必要且可能 , 試圖傳達出那感官在城市中飛過的是什麼樣子 , 而不動 。
past the pyramid of cestius these will seem very familiar to you , even if you haven't been to rome recently past the gatehouse .	經過cestius的金字塔 , 這對你來說是非常熟悉的 , 即使你最近還沒去過羅馬大廈 。
this is something that's a little bit unusual .	這有點不尋常 。
this pigeon does something that most homing pigeons do not do: it takes the scenic route , which was a device that i felt was necessary to actually extend this book beyond about four pages .	這種鴿子做的事 , 大部分的愛滋動物都做不到:牠需要這個場景路線 , 這是我覺得要把這本書延伸到約四頁以外的裝置 。
so , we circle around the coliseum , past the church of santa maria in cosmedin and the temple of hercules towards the river .	所以 , 我們繞著哥倫比亞的大教堂 , 穿越了哥斯姆丁的聖瑪利亞教堂 , 以及海克力士的神殿朝著河流前進 。
we almost collide with the cornice of the palazzo farnese designed by michelangelo , built of stone taken from the coliseum narrow escape .	我們幾乎和帕拉zofarzofanse所設計的米開朗基羅的石頭相撞 , 用的是哥倫比羅逃脫的石頭 。
we swoop down over the campo de' fiori .	我們在柬埔寨的菲洛里游過來 。
this is one of those things i show to my students because it's a complete bastardization a denial of any rules of perspective .	這是我給學生看的其中一件事 , 因為這是完全禁止任何觀點的規則 。
the only rule of perspective that i think matters is if it looks believable , you've succeeded .	我認為唯一重要的規則是 , 如果它看起來是可信的 , 你就成功了 。
but you try and figure out where the vanishing points meet here ; a couple are on mars and a couple of others in cremona .	但你試著找出消失點在哪裡 ; 有些是在火星和其他一些在cremona的地方 。
but into the piazza in front of santa maria della pace , where invariably a soccer game is going on , and we're hit by a soccer ball .	但 , 在聖塔瑪麗亞德拉帕斯面前 , 絕對是足球比賽正在進行 , 我們被足球撞擊 。
now this is a terrible illustration of being hit by a soccer ball .	這是被足球撞擊的可怕例子 。
i have all the pieces: there's santa maria della pace , there's a soccer ball , there's a little bit of a bird's wing nothing's happening , so i had to rethink it .	我有所有的碎片:聖塔瑪麗亞迪拉的步調 , 足球 , 鳥翅膀沒有發生什麼事 , 所以我得要重新思考 。
and if you do want to see santa maria della pace , these books are really flexible , incredibly interactive just turn it around and look at it the other way .	如果你想要看到聖誕老人瑪麗亞德拉的步調 , 這些書很有彈性 , 非常互動 , 只要把它轉過來 , 再看看另一種方式 。
through the alley , we can see the impact is captured in the red line .	透過巷子 , 我們可以看到影響力在紅線中被捕捉 。
and then bird manages to pull itself together past this medieval tower one of the few remaining medieval towers towards the church of sant'agnese and around the dome looking down into piazza navona which we've already mentioned and seen and flown over a couple of times ; there's the bernini statue of the four rivers and then past the wonderful borromini sant'ivo , stopping just long enough on the 26foot diameter oculus of the pantheon to catch our breath .	接著 , 鳥類會把自己拉過去 , 經過這個中世紀塔 , 只有少數幾個中世紀塔 , 直到聖誕老人的教堂 , 四周 , 看著帕亞札納維納維娜 , 我們已經看過並流過幾次 ; 伯尼•史塔爾特 , 還有四條河的聖地雕像 , 經過了美妙的布洛米尼•聖地山 , 停止了26英呎直徑的萬物 , 去抓住我們的呼吸 。
and then we can swoop inside and around ; and because we're flying , we don't really have to worry about gravity at this particular moment in time , so this drawing can be oriented in any way on the page .	接著 , 我們可以在裡面和周圍旋轉 , 因為我們正在飛 , 我們不需要擔心重力 , 在這個時刻 , 這幅圖可以隨時隨地呈現 。
we get a little exuberant as we pass gesu ; it's not surprising to sort of mimic the architecture in this way .	當我們通過gesu時 , 我們會變得很開心 , 這並不令人驚訝 , 以這種方式模仿建築 。
past the wonderful wall filled with the juxtaposition that i was talking about ; beautiful carvings set into the walls above the neon " ristorante " sign , and so on .	過去 , 充滿了我所說的美妙的圍牆 ; 美麗的雕刻在新生 「 暴風 」 的牆上 , 諸如此類 。
and eventually , we arrive at the courtyard of the palazzo , which is our destination .	最終 , 我們到了巴拉zo的庭院 , 那是我們的目的地 。
straight up through the courtyard into a little window into the attic , where somebody is working at the drawing board .	直接穿過庭院 , 進入閣樓 , 在那裡有人在畫板工作 。
he removes the message from the leg of the bird ; this is what it says .	他從鳥的腿上取出訊息 , 這是牠所說的 。
as we look at the drawing board , we see what he's working on is , in fact , a map of the journey that the pigeon has just taken , and the red line extends through all the sights .	當我們看著畫板時 , 我們看到他正在做的事 , 事實上 , 這趟鴿子剛拍的旅程的地圖 , 紅線穿過所有的視線 。
and if you want the information , so that we complete this cycle of understanding , all you have to do is read these paragraphs .	如果你想要資訊 , 這樣我們才能完成理解的循環 , 你只需要閱讀這些段落 。
thank you very much .	謝謝大家 。
mit researcher skylar tibbits works on selfassembly the idea that instead of building something , we can create materials that build themselves , much the way a strand of dna zips itself together . it's a big concept at early stages ; tibbits shows us three inthelab projects that hint at what a selfassembling future might look like .	麻省理工學院的研究者skylartibbit是自我組裝的概念 , 我們能創造出自身的材料 , 大多是dnazips本身的一股概念 。 這是早期的一個大概念 ; tibbit向我們展示了三項自我組裝的未來 。
skylar tibbits: can we make things that make themselves ?	skylartibbit:我們能製造製造自己的東西嗎 ?
today i'd like to show you the future of the way we make things .	今天我想向你們展示我們製造東西的未來 。
i believe that soon our buildings and machines will be selfassembling , replicating and repairing themselves .	我相信很快我們的建築和機器會自我組裝、複製、修復自己 。
so i'm going to show you what i believe is the current state of manufacturing , and then compare that to some natural systems .	所以我要向你們展示我相信目前的製造狀態 , 然後將它和一些自然系統比較 。
so in the current state of manufacturing , we have skyscrapers two and a half years [of assembly time] , 500 , 000 to a million parts , fairly complex , new , exciting technologies in steel , concrete , glass .	在目前的製造業狀態 , 我們有摩天大樓 , 兩年半的時間 , 五十萬到一百萬個零件 , 相當複雜、嶄新的、令人興奮的科技 , 在鋼鐵、混凝土、玻璃 。
we have exciting machines that can take us into space five years [of assembly time] , 2 . 5 million parts .	我們有令人興奮的機器可以帶我們進入太空五年 , 即250萬個零件 。
but on the other side , if you look at the natural systems , we have proteins that have two million types , can fold in 10 , 000 nanoseconds , or dna with three billion base pairs we can replicate in roughly an hour .	但另一方面 , 如果你看一下自然系統 , 我們有兩百萬種類型的蛋白質 , 可以在一萬奈秒摺疊 , 或是dna有三十億個鹼基對的dna , 我們可以在大約一小時內複製 。
so there's all of this complexity in our natural systems , but they're extremely efficient , far more efficient than anything we can build , far more complex than anything we can build .	所以 , 我們自然系統的複雜性 , 但它們非常有效率 , 比任何我們能建造的東西還要有效率 , 遠遠比任何我們能建造的東西都還要複雜 。
they're far more efficient in terms of energy .	在能源方面 , 它們更有效率 。
they hardly ever make mistakes .	他們幾乎沒有犯錯 。
and they can repair themselves for longevity .	他們可以長壽地修復自己 。
so there's something super interesting about natural systems .	自然系統有個很有趣的東西 。
and if we can translate that into our built environment , then there's some exciting potential for the way that we build things .	如果我們能將它翻譯成我們的建設環境 , 那就有一些令人興奮的潛力可以用來建造東西 。
and i think the key to that is selfassembly .	我認為關鍵在於自我組裝 。
so if we want to utilize selfassembly in our physical environment , i think there's four key factors .	所以 , 如果我們想要在我們的物理環境中自組裝 , 我認為有四個關鍵因子 。
the first is that we need to decode all of the complexity of what we want to build so our buildings and machines .	第一 , 我們需要解碼所有我們想建造的東西的複雜性 , 以便我們的建築物和機器 。
and we need to decode that into simple sequences basically the dna of how our buildings work .	我們需要將它解碼成簡單的序列 , 基本上就是我們的建築物如何運作的dna 。
then we need programmable parts that can take that sequence and use that to fold up , or reconfigure .	接著 , 我們需要可編程的零件 , 可以用這個序列來折疊 , 或重新配置 。
we need some energy that's going to allow that to activate , allow our parts to be able to fold up from the program .	我們需要一些能量來啟動 , 使我們的零件能夠從程式中摺出來 。
and we need some type of error correction redundancy to guarantee that we have successfully built what we want .	我們需要某種類型的錯誤修正 , 來確保我們成功地建立我們想要的東西 。
so i'm going to show you a number of projects that my colleagues and i at mit are working on to achieve this selfassembling future .	所以我要給你們看幾個項目 , 我和麻省理工學院的同事正在努力實現這個自我組裝的未來 。
the first two are the macrobot and decibot .	第一兩種是麥克羅伯特和狄西波特 。
so these projects are largescale reconfigurable robots 8 ft . , 12 ft . long proteins .	這些計畫是大規模的可重組的機器人 , 8英尺 , 12英尺長的蛋白質 。
they're embedded with mechanical electrical devices , sensors .	它們嵌入了機械電子裝置 , 感應器 。
you decode what you want to fold up into , into a sequence of angles so negative 120 , negative 120 , 0 , 0 , 120 , negative 120 something like that ; so a sequence of angles , or turns , and you send that sequence through the string .	你要解碼你想要摺疊的東西 , 變成一連串的角度 , 負120、120、120、120 , 負120 , 負120 , 負120個像這樣的東西 。 所以一連串的角度 , 或旋轉 , 然後你透過弦將序列發送出 。
each unit takes its message so negative 120 it rotates to that , checks if it got there and then passes it to its neighbor .	每個單位都用它的訊息 , 負120它轉向它 , 檢查是否到那裡 , 然後傳給鄰居 。
so these are the brilliant scientists , engineers , designers that worked on this project .	這些是傑出的科學家、工程師、設計師在這個專案上工作 。
and i think it really brings to light: is this really scalable ?	我認為它真的能帶來光明:這真的可擴展嗎 ?
i mean , thousands of dollars , lots of man hours made to make this eightfoot robot .	我的意思是 , 數千美元 , 許多人小時製造了這個八英尺的機器人 。
can we really scale this up ? can we really embed robotics into every part ?	我們能真的擴大規模嗎 ? 我們能真的把機械人物嵌入每一個部分嗎 ?
the next one questions that and looks at passive nature , or passively trying to have reconfiguration programmability .	下一個問題是 「 被動 」 , 或 「 被動地嘗試重組程式性 」 。
but it goes a step further , and it tries to have actual computation .	但它進一步進一步 , 試圖有實際的計算 。
it basically embeds the most fundamental building block of computing , the digital logic gate , directly into your parts .	它基本上嵌入了計算最基本的基礎 , 數位邏輯門 , 直接進入你的零件中 。
so this is a nand gate .	這是一個nand大門 。
you have one tetrahedron which is the gate that's going to do your computing , and you have two input tetrahedrons .	有一個四面體 , 也就是你計算的門 , 你有兩個輸入的四面體 。
one of them is the input from the user , as you're building your bricks .	其中一個是來自使用者的輸入 , 因為你正在建造你的磚塊 。
the other one is from the previous brick that was placed .	另外一個是從先前被放置的磚塊 。
and then it gives you an output in 3d space .	然後它會給你一個3d空間的輸出 。
so what this means is that the user can start plugging in what they want the bricks to do .	這意味著 , 使用者可以開始加入他們想要的磚塊 。
it computes on what it was doing before and what you said you wanted it to do .	它計算前所做的事和你所說的要做的事 。
and now it starts moving in threedimensional space so up or down .	現在它開始在三維空間中移動 , 向上或向下 。
so on the lefthand side , [1 , 1] input equals 0 output , which goes down .	所以在左手邊 , [1、1]輸入等於0輸出 , 結果會下降 。
on the righthand side , [0 , 0] input is a 1 output , which goes up .	在右手邊 , 0 , 輸入是1輸出 , 上升 。
and so what that really means is that our structures now contain the blueprints of what we want to build .	這意味著我們的結構現在包含了我們想要建造的藍圖 。
so they have all of the information embedded in them of what was constructed .	所以他們把所有資訊都嵌入其中 。
so that means that we can have some form of selfreplication .	這意味著我們可以有某種形式的自我複製 。
in this case i call it selfguided replication , because your structure contains the exact blueprints .	在這個案例中 , 我稱它為自動複製 , 因為你的結構包含了精確的藍圖 。
if you have errors , you can replace a part .	如果你犯錯 , 你可以取代一個部件 。
all the local information is embedded to tell you how to fix it .	所有當地的資訊都被嵌入 , 告訴你如何修復它 。
so you could have something that climbs along and reads it and can output at one to one .	所以你可以有一些可以爬上去讀的東西 , 可以輸出一個到一個 。
it's directly embedded ; there's no external instructions .	它是直接嵌入的 ; 沒有外部指令 。
so the last project i'll show is called biased chains , and it's probably the most exciting example that we have right now of passive selfassembly systems .	最後一個專案叫做偏見鏈 , 它可能是我們目前最令人興奮的例子 , 被動的自組裝系統 。
so it takes the reconfigurability and programmability and makes it a completely passive system .	所以它需要可重組和可程式性 , 讓它成為一個完全被動的系統 。
so basically you have a chain of elements .	基本上你有一連串的元素 。
each element is completely identical , and they're biased .	每個元素都是完全相同的 , 它們有偏見 。
so each chain , or each element , wants to turn right or left .	每一個鏈 , 或每一個元素 , 都想要向右轉或左轉 。
so as you assemble the chain , you're basically programming it .	所以 , 當你組裝鏈 , 你基本上是在編寫它 。
you're telling each unit if it should turn right or left .	你在告訴每個單位是否應該向右轉或左轉 。
