for others , the present is irrelevant .	對其他人來說 , 現在並不重要 。
it's always about " what is this situation like that i've experienced in the past ? "	總是關於 「 我過去所經歷過的這種情況是什麼 ? 」
so that their decisions are based on past memories .	所以 , 他們的決定基於過去記憶 。
and we're going to call those people " pastoriented , " because they focus on what was .	我們稱這些人為 「 過去式 」 , 因為他們把焦點放在什麼 。
for others it's not the past , it's not the present , it's only about the future .	對其他人來說 , 這不是過去 , 也不是現在 , 而是關於未來 。
their focus is always about anticipated consequences .	他們的焦點總是預期會有後果 。
we're going to call them " futureoriented . " their focus is on what will be .	我們將稱之為 「 未來式 」 。 他們的焦點在於會是什麼 。
so , time paradox , i want to argue , the paradox of time perspective , is something that influences every decision you make , you're totally unaware of .	所以 , 時間悖論 , 我想說的是 , 時間的悖論 , 是影響你所做的每一決定的 , 你完全不知道的 。
namely , the extent to which you have one of these biased time perspectives .	換句話說 , 你有偏見的時間觀點 。
well there is actually six of them . there are two ways to be presentoriented .	其實有六個 。 有兩種方式可以呈現出來 。
there is two ways to be pastoriented , two ways to be future .	過去有兩種方式 , 有兩種方式可以成為未來 。
you can focus on pastpositive , or pastnegative .	你可以把焦點放在正面的、負面的 。
you can be presenthedonistic , namely you focus on the joys of life , or presentfatalist it doesn't matter , your life is controlled .	你可以做個簡報 , 也就是你把焦點放在生活的喜悅上 , 或簡報主義者不重要 , 你的生活是受控制的 。
you can be futureoriented , setting goals .	你可以是未來的目標 , 設定目標 。
or you can be transcendental future: namely , life begins after death .	或者 , 你可以是超然的未來:即 , 生命從死亡開始 。
developing the mental flexibility to shift time perspectives fluidly depending on the demands of the situation , that's what you've got to learn to do .	發展靈活性 , 轉變時間的觀點 , 取決於情況的需求 , 這就是你需要學習的 。
so , very quickly , what is the optimal time profile ?	所以 , 很快地 , 最佳的時間檔案是什麼 ?
high on pastpositive . moderately high on future .	很正面 。 未來的發展很高 。
and moderate on presenthedonism .	現代主義的現代主義 。
and always low on pastnegative and presentfatalism .	總是低於負面和虛假主義 。
so the optimal temporal mix is what you get from the past pastpositive gives you roots . you connect your family , identity and your self .	所以 , 最佳的顳葉混合物是你從過去的積極帶給你根 。 你將你的家人、身份和你的自我連結起來 。
what you get from the future is wings to soar to new destinations , new challenges .	你從未來得到的 , 是翅膀到新目的地 , 新的挑戰 。
what you get from the present hedonism is the energy , the energy to explore yourself , places , people , sensuality .	你從現在的享樂主義中得到的能量 , 探索你自己、地點、人、感覺 。
any time perspective in excess has more negatives than positives .	無論多餘時間的觀點 , 都比正面的觀點還要負面 。
what do futures sacrifice for success ?	未來對成功的犧牲是什麼 ?
they sacrifice family time . they sacrifice friend time .	他們犧牲家庭時間、犧牲朋友時間 。
they sacrifice fun time . they sacrifice personal indulgence .	他們犧牲有趣的時間 , 犧牲個人的衝突 。
they sacrifice hobbies . and they sacrifice sleep . so it affects their health .	他們犧牲嗜好、犧牲睡眠 , 影響他們的健康 。
and they live for work , achievement and control .	他們為工作、成就和控制權而生活 。
i'm sure that resonates with some of the tedsters .	我相信 , 和一些ted者共鳴 。
and it resonated for me . i grew up as a poor kid in the south bronx ghetto , a sicilian family everyone lived in the past and present .	對我來說 , 我是南布朗克斯ghetto貧窮的小孩 , 一個西西里的家庭 , 住在過去和現在 。
i'm here as a futureoriented person who went over the top , who did all these sacrifices because teachers intervened , and made me future oriented .	我來這裡是一位有著未來的人 , 走過頂端 , 因為老師們採取了這些犧牲 , 讓我成為未來的方向 。
told me don't eat that marshmallow , because if you wait you're going to get two of them , until i learned to balance out .	告訴我 , 不要吃棉花糖 , 因為如果你等著你會拿到兩個 , 直到我學會了平衡 。
i've added presenthedonism , i've added a focus on the pastpositive , so , at 76 years old , i am more energetic than ever , more productive , and i'm happier than i have ever been .	我加上了當代主義 , 我把焦點放在過去的積極 , 所以 , 在76歲時 , 我比以往更有活力 , 更有生產力 , 而且我比以前更快樂 。
i just want to say that we are applying this to many world problems: changing the dropout rates of school kids , combating addictions , enhancing teen health , curing vets' ptsd with time metaphors getting miracle cures promoting sustainability and conservation , reducing physical rehabilitation where there is a 50percent drop out rate , altering appeals to suicidal terrorists , and modifying family conflicts as timezone clashes .	我只是想說 , 我們正應用在許多世界問題上:改變學校的輟學率、結合成癮、提升青少年健康、用時間隱喻來治療vets的創傷後壓力症候群 , 促進永續性和保育 , 減少實體復健率 , 增加了50%的輟學率、改變吸引自殺的恐怖分子 , 以及修改家庭衝突 。
so i want to end by saying: many of life's puzzles can be solved by understanding your time perspective and that of others .	最後我想說的是 , 許多生命的謎題可以透過了解你的時間的觀點和其他的觀點來解決 。
and the idea is so simple , so obvious , but i think the consequences are really profound .	這個想法很簡單 , 很明顯 , 但我認為結果非常深遠 。
how many of today's headlines will matter in 100 years ? 1000 ? kirk citron's " long news " project collects stories that not only matter today , but will resonate for decades even centuries to come . at ted2010 , he highlights recent headlines with the potential to shape our future .	一百年後 , 有多少頭條新聞會造成影響 ? 一百年後 ? 克勞倫的 「 長期新聞計畫 」 收集這些故事 , 不僅僅是現今重要的 , 還要花數十年才會出現 。 在ted2010年 , 他提出近期的頭條新聞 , 有潛在影響我們未來的潛力 。
future , global issues , media , news , science	未來、全球議題、媒體、新聞、科學、科學、科學問題、
kirk citron: and now , the real news	kirkcitron:現在 , 真正的消息是:
we are drowning in news .	新聞淹沒了我們 。
reuters alone puts out three and a half million news stories a year .	光是通勤者每年就有350萬個新聞報導 。
that's just one source .	這只是其中一個來源 。
my question is: how many of those stories are actually going to matter in the long run ?	我的問題是:在長期間 , 到底有多少故事會很重要 ?
that's the idea behind the long news .	這就是長期新聞背後的想法 。
it's a project by the long now foundation , which was founded by tedsters including kevin kelly and stewart brand .	由tedster所創立的一個計畫 , 包括凱文凱利和史都華•布蘭德 。
and what we're looking for is news stories that might still matter 50 or 100 or 10 , 000 years from now .	我們正在尋找的新聞報導 , 新聞報導可能在50或1000年後仍然很重要 。
and when you look at the news through that filter , a lot falls by the wayside .	當你透過那個過濾器看新聞時 , 有很多的落差 。
to take the top stories from the a . p . this last year , is this going to matter in a decade ?	去年從a.p.的頂尖故事來看 , 這在過去十年是很重要的嗎 ?
is this going to matter in 50 or 100 years ?	這在50或100年內會有什麼影響嗎 ?
okay , that was kind of cool .	好吧 , 這有點酷 。
but the top story of this past year was the economy , and i'm just betting that , sooner or later , this particular recession is going to be old news .	但過去一年的主題是經濟 , 我敢打賭 , 不久後 , 這個衰退將會是舊消息 。
so , what kind of stories might make a difference for the future ?	所以 , 未來可能會造成什麼樣的改變 ?
well , let's take science .	嗯 , 咱們來談科學 。
someday , little robots will go through our bloodstreams fixing things .	有一天 , 小機器人會穿過我們的血液處理東西 。
that someday is already here if you're a mouse .	某一天 , 如果你是一隻老鼠 , 就已經存在了 。
some recent stories: nanobees zap tumors with real bee venom ; they're sending genes into the brain ; a robot they built that can crawl through the human body .	一些最近的故事:奈米蜜蜂帶有真正的蜜蜂毒液 ; 它們把基因送到大腦中 ; 一個可以爬過人體的機器人 。
what about resources ? how are we going to feed nine billion people ?	那麼資源呢 ? 我們要如何餵飽九十億人 ?
we're having trouble feeding six billion today .	我們現在正面臨60億人的糧食問題 。
as we heard yesterday , there's over a billion people hungry .	正如我們昨天聽到的 , 有超過十億人挨餓 。
britain will starve without genetically modified crops .	英國不會有基因改造的作物來餓死 。
bill gates , fortunately , has bet a billion on [agricultural] research .	幸運的是 , 比爾蓋茲在研究中有十億人 。
what about global politics ?	那麼全球政治呢 ?
the world's going to be very different when and if china sets the agenda , and they may .	當中國設定議程時 , 世界會變得非常不同 , 他們可能 。
they've overtaken the u . s . as the world's biggest car market , they've overtaken germany as the largest exporter , and they've started doing dna tests on kids to choose their careers .	他們把美國當作世界上最大的汽車市場 , 他們把德國當作最大的出口國 , 他們開始在孩子身上做dna檢測 , 來選擇職業生涯 。
we're finding all kinds of ways to push back the limits of what we know .	我們找到各式各樣的方法 , 來推回我們所知的極限 。
some recent discoveries: there's an ant colony from argentina that has now spread to every continent but antarctica ; there's a selfdirected robot scientist that's made a discovery soon , science may no longer need us , and life may no longer need us either ; a microbe wakes up after 120 , 000 years .	最近的一些發現:阿根廷的蟻群現在已經擴散到每一塊大陸 , 但南極洲 , 有一個自動導向的機器人科學家 , 很快就發現了 , 科學不再需要我們 , 生命也不再需要我們 ; 一個微生物在十二萬年之後就醒來了 。
it seems that with or without us , life will go on .	似乎沒有我們 , 生命會持續下去 。
but my pick for the top long news story of this past year was this one: water found on the moon .	但過去一年 , 我對這個長期新聞的選擇是這個:水在月球上找到 。
makes it a lot easier to put a colony up there .	讓蟻群更容易放到上面 。
and if nasa doesn't do it , china might , or somebody in this room might write a big check .	如果太空總署不做 , 中國可能 , 或在座的某個人可能會寫一支大支票 。
my point is this: in the long run , some news stories are more important than others .	我的重點是:在長期來看 , 有些新聞故事比其他新聞更重要 。
planetary scientist carolyn porco shows images from the cassini voyage to saturn , focusing on its largest moon , titan , and on frozen enceladus , which seems to shoot jets of ice .	地球科學家carolynporco展示了卡西尼航行到土星的影像 , 把焦點放在最大的衛星、土衛二 , 和冰凍土衛二的土衛二 , 這似乎是冰的射線 。
nasa , design , exploration , science , space , technology , universe , visualizations	nasa、設計、探索、科學、太空、科技、宇宙、視覺化、視覺化 。
carolyn porco flies us to saturn	卡羅琳•普洛柯讓我們飛來土星飛來飛去 。
in the next 18 minutes , i'm going to take you on a journey .	在接下來的18分鐘裡 , 我要帶你們踏上一段旅程 。
and it's a journey that you and i have been on for many years now , and it began some 50 years ago , when humans first stepped off our planet .	這段旅程是你和我已經經歷了好幾年了 , 五十年前 , 人類第一次踏出我們的星球 。
and in those 50 years , not only did we literally , physically set foot on the moon , but we have dispatched robotic spacecraft to all the planets all eight of them and we have landed on asteroids , we have rendezvoused with comets , and , at this point in time , we have a spacecraft on its way to pluto , the body formerly known as a planet .	在那50年裡 , 我們不僅僅是踏上月球 , 我們還把機械太空船分散到所有行星中 , 我們已經登上了小行星 , 在此時此刻 , 我們有了一艘太空船 , 運送到冥王星的路上 , 前所知的身形是行星 。
and all of these robotic missions are part of a bigger human journey: a voyage to understand something , to get a sense of our cosmic place , to understand something of our origins , and how earth , our planet , and we , living on it , came to be .	所有這些機械任務都是人類旅程的一部分:一趟旅程 , 去了解某件事 , 去了解我們的宇宙 , 去了解我們的起源 , 了解我們的地球 , 以及我們的星球 , 以及我們生活在它身上的一部分 。
and of all the places in the solar system that we might go to and search for answers to questions like this , there's saturn . and we have been to saturn before we visited saturn in the early 1980s but our investigations of saturn have become far more indepth in detail since the cassini spacecraft , traveling across interplanetary space for seven years , glided into orbit around saturn in the summer of 2004 , and became at that point the farthest robotic outpost that humanity had ever established around the sun .	在太陽系中 , 我們可能去尋找像這樣的問題的答案 , 我們曾去過土星 。 我們去過土星 , 在1980年代初期 , 我們去過土星探訪 , 但我們對土星的調查已經變得更加深刻 , 從卡西尼號太空船到星際太空飛行的七年後 , 在2004年夏天就開始繞行土星運行 , 當時人類在太陽周圍的最遙遠的機械設施 。
now , the saturn system is a rich planetary system .	土星系統是個很豐富的行星系統 。
it offers mystery , scientific insight and obviously splendor beyond compare , and the investigation of this system has enormous cosmic reach .	它提供了神秘的、科學的洞察 , 顯然超越比較之外 , 對於這個系統的調查有巨大的宇宙 。
in fact , just studying the rings alone , we stand to learn a lot about the discs of stars and gas that we call the spiral galaxies .	事實上 , 光靠研究圓圈 , 我們就得要了解很多星星的圓圈和氣體的圓圈 , 我們稱之為螺旋星系 。
and here's a beautiful picture of the andromeda nebula , which is our closest , largest spiral galaxy to the milky way .	這張美麗的照片是andromedanebula這是我們最接近銀河的最大螺旋星系
and then , here's a beautiful composite of the whirlpool galaxy , taken by the hubble space telescope .	接著 , 這是由哈伯太空望遠鏡所拍攝的美麗的複合物 。
so the journey back to saturn is really part of and is also a metaphor for a much larger human voyage to understand the interconnectedness of everything around us , and also how humans fit into that picture .	所以 , 回到土星的旅程其實是人類旅程的一部分 , 也是一個比喻 , 來了解我們周遭的事物之間的關聯性 , 以及人類如何融入這張照片 。
and it pains me that i can't tell you all that we have learned with cassini .	這讓我感到痛苦 , 我無法告訴你們 , 我們已經學過卡西尼 。
i can't show you all the beautiful pictures that we've taken in the last two and a half years , because i simply don't have the time .	我無法向你們展示我們過去兩年半所拍攝的美麗照片 , 因為我沒有時間 。
so i'm going to concentrate on two of the most exciting stories that have emerged out of this major exploratory expedition that we are conducting around saturn , and have been for the past two and a half years .	所以 , 我將專注於這次重大的探險探險旅程中 , 兩個最令人興奮的故事 , 我們正在進行土星的探險 , 過去兩年半以來都是如此 。
saturn is accompanied by a very large and diverse collection of moons .	土星伴隨著非常大量且多樣化的衛星收集 。
they range in size from a few kilometers across to as big across as the u . s .	它們的大小範圍從幾公里長到像美國一樣大 。
most of the beautiful pictures we've taken of saturn , in fact , show saturn in accompaniment with some of its moons . here's saturn with dione , and then , here's saturn showing the rings edgeon , showing you just how vertically thin they are , with the moon enceladus .	我們拍過土星的美麗照片事實上 , 大部分的土星與一些衛星共存 , 這裡是土星的土星 , 這裡是土星的土星 , 這裡是土星的邊緣 , 展示了它們的垂直薄度 , 它們是月球土衛二 。
now , two of the 47 moons that saturn has are standouts .	土星47顆衛星中有兩個是站著的 。
and those are titan and enceladus . titan is saturn's largest moon , and , until cassini had arrived there , was the largest single expanse of unexplored terrain that we had remaining in our solar system .	這些是土衛二和土衛二 。 土衛六是土星最大的衛星 , 直到卡西尼抵達那裡 , 是我們太陽系中最大的一個未被探索的地形 。
and it is a body that has long intrigued people who've watched the planets .	這個身體有很長的好奇心 , 看過這個星球的人 。
it has a very large , thick atmosphere , and in fact , its surface environment was believed to be more like the environment we have here on the earth , or at least had in the past , than any other body in the solar system .	它的大氣層非常厚 , 事實上 , 它的表面環境被認為比較像我們在地球上所擁有的環境 , 或至少在過去 , 比太陽系中任何其他的身體都還要複雜 。
its atmosphere is largely molecular nitrogen , like you are breathing here in this room , except that its atmosphere is suffused with simple organic materials like methane and propane and ethane .	它的大氣主要是分子氮 , 就像你在這個房間裡呼吸一樣 , 除了它的大氣中有機物質 , 像是甲烷、丙烷和乙烷 。
and these molecules high up in the atmosphere of titan get broken down , and their products join together to make haze particles .	這些分子在土衛六大氣層中高度被破壞 , 它們的產品結合在一起 , 製造哈西米粒子 。
this haze is ubiquitous . it's completely global and enveloping titan .	這種帽子無所不在 , 完全是全球性的 , 包含土衛六 。
and that's why you cannot see down to the surface with our eyes in the visible region of the spectrum .	這就是為什麼你看不見我們的眼睛在可見的光譜範圍內的表面 。
but these haze particles , it was surmised , before we got there with cassini , over billions and billions of years , gently drifted down to the surface and coated the surface in a thick organic sludge .	但這些迷宮粒子 , 在我們到達卡西尼之前 , 已經有數十億年了 , 溫和地面漂移 , 將表面覆蓋在厚厚的有機水泥中 。
so like the equivalent , the titan equivalent , of tar , or oil , or what we didn't know what .	如同土衛六 , 土衛六等同於焦油或石油 , 或我們不知道的 。
but this is what we suspected . and these molecules , especially methane and ethane , can be liquids at the surface temperatures of titan .	但這是我們懷疑的 。 這些分子 , 特別是甲烷和乙烷 , 可以在泰坦的表面溫度上成為液體 。
and so it turns out that methane is to titan what water is to the earth .	結果發現 , 甲烷就是土衛六的水對地球的影響 。
it's a condensable in the atmosphere , and so recognizing this circumstance brought to the fore a whole world of bizarre possibilities . you can have methane clouds , ok , and above those clouds , you have this hundreds of kilometers of haze , which prevent any sunlight from getting to the surface .	它在大氣層中是可容忍的 , 所以意識到這種情況會帶來整個世界奇怪的可能性 。 你可以有甲烷雲 , 好 , 在這些雲層之上 , 你有這數百公里的哈米 , 防止陽光到達地表 。
the temperature at the surface is some 350 degrees below zero fahrenheit .	表面的溫度低於華氏零度的350度 。
but despite that cold , you could have rain falling down on the surface of titan .	儘管如此寒冷 , 土衛六表面的雨下降 。
and doing on titan what rain does on the earth: it carves gullies ; it forms rivers and cataracts ; it can create canyons ; it can pool in large basins and craters .	在土衛六下雨的作用:它雕刻了幾條河流和洞穴 ; 它能創造峽谷 ; 它能在大盆地和大隕石中池塘 。
it can wash the sludge off high mountain peaks and hills , down into the lowlands . so stop and think for a minute .	它可以把高山峰和山丘洗掉 , 沖到低地 。 停下來 , 思考一下 。
try to imagine what the surface of titan might look like .	試想一下土衛六的表面看起來是什麼樣子 。
it's dark . high noon on titan is as dark as deep earth twilight on the earth .	它是黑暗的 。 鐵達尼號的高度和地球深海一樣黑暗 。
it's cold , it's eerie , it's misty , it might be raining , and you might be standing on the shores of lake michigan brimming with paint thinner .	它很冷 , 很糟糕 , 很糟糕 , 可能是下雨 , 你可能會站在密西根湖岸邊 , 用油漆刷刷 。
that is the view that we had of the surface of titan before we got there with cassini , and i can tell you that what we have found on titan , though it is not the same in detail , is every bit as fascinating as that story is .	這是我們在土衛六到達之前的土衛六表面 , 我可以告訴你們 , 我們在土衛六上發現的 , 雖然在細節上並沒有一樣的細節 , 和這個故事一樣吸引人 。
and for us , it has been like the cassini people it has been like a jules verne adventure come true .	對我們來說 , 這就像是卡西尼人一樣 , 曾是青少年凡爾納探險成真 。
as i said , it has a thick , extensive atmosphere .	如我所說 , 它有很厚的大氣層 。
this is a picture of titan , backlit by the sun , with the rings as a beautiful backdrop .	這張照片是土衛六的背景 , 背景是一幅美麗的背景 。
and yet another moon there i don't even know which one it is . it's a very extensive atmosphere .	另外一個月球 , 我甚至不知道它是哪一個 。 它是一個非常廣泛的大氣層 。
we have instruments on cassini which can see down to the surface through this atmosphere , and my camera system is one of them .	我們有卡西尼號的儀器可以透過大氣層看到表面 , 我的攝影機系統是其中之一 。
and we have taken pictures like this .	我們拍了像這樣的照片 。
and what you see is bright and dark regions , and that's about as far as it got for us .	你看到的是明亮又暗的區域 , 就跟我們一樣 。
it was so mystifying: we couldn't make out what we were seeing on titan .	這太神秘了:我們無法在泰坦看到什麼 。
when you look closer at this region , you start to see things like sinuous channels we didn't know . you see a few round things .	當你仔細看這個區域 , 你會開始看到我們不知道的東西 。 你可以看到一些圓形的東西 。
this , we later found out , is , in fact , a crater , but there are very few craters on the surface of titan , meaning it's a very young surface .	後來我們發現 , 事實上 , 其實是坑洞 , 但土衛六表面上有很少的坑坑 , 意思是它是個很年輕的表面 。
and there are features that look tectonic .	有些特徵看起來像地形 。
they look like they've been pulled apart .	他們看起來好像被拉開了 。
whenever you see anything linear on a planet , it means there's been a fracture , like a fault .	每當你看到星球上的任何線性 , 就意味著有破裂 , 像錯 。
and so it's been tectonically altered .	所以它的結構已經改變了 。
but we couldn't make sense of our images , until , six months after we got into orbit , an event occurred that many have regarded as the highlight of cassini's investigation of titan .	但是我們無法理解我們的影像 , 直到我們進入軌道六個月後 , 發生了一件事件 , 發生在許多人認為是卡西尼對土衛六的高峰之後 。
and that was the deployment of the huygens probe , the europeanbuilt huygens probe that cassini had carried for seven years across the solar system . we deployed it to the atmosphere of titan , it took two and a half hours to descend , and it landed on the surface .	那就是蜂巢探測器的部署 , 歐洲建造的蜂箱 , 卡西尼號在太陽系運行了七年 。 我們把它部署到泰坦的大氣層 , 花了兩半小時的時間在地表上 。
and i just want to emphasize how significant an event this is .	我想強調一下這個事件有多重要 。
this is a device of human making , and it landed in the outer solar system for the first time in human history .	這是人類製造的裝置 , 它是人類史上第一次登陸的太陽系 。
it is so significant that , in my mind , this was an event that should have been celebrated with ticker tape parades in every city across the u . s . and europe , and sadly , that wasn't the case .	在我心中 , 這件事非常重要 , 在我腦海中 , 這個事件應該被標記在美國和歐洲的每一個城市裡 , 不幸的是 , 這並非如此 。
it was significant for another reason . this is an international mission , and this event was celebrated in europe , in germany , and the celebratory presentations were given in english accents , and american accents , and german accents , and french and italian and dutch accents .	這是另一個原因 。 這是國際使命 , 這個事件在歐洲、德國 , 以及慶祝的演講在英文口音、美國口音、德國口音、法語、義大利語和荷蘭口音 。
it was a moving demonstration of what the words " united nations " are supposed to mean: a true union of nations joined together in a colossal effort for good .	它是一個動人的示範 , 說明了聯合國應該要說的是什麼:一個真正的聯合國在一個大規模的努力中加入在一起 。
and , in this case , it was a massive undertaking to explore a planet , and to come to understand a planetary system that , for all of human history , had been unreachable , and now humans had actually touched it .	在這個例子中 , 要探索一個星球 , 要了解一個行星的行星系統 , 在人類歷史上 , 一直無法達成 , 現在人類已經碰到它了 。
so it was i mean , i'm getting goose bumps just talking about it .	我的意思是 , 我只是在談論它 。
it was a tremendously emotional event , and it's something that i will personally never forget , and you shouldn't either .	那是個極大的情感事件 , 我個人永遠不會忘記 , 你也不該忘記 。
but anyway , the probe took measurements of the atmosphere on the way down , and it also took panoramic pictures .	總之 , 探測器在降低大氣層的測量結果也拍攝了全景照片 。
and i can't tell you what it was like to see the first pictures of titan's surface from the probe . and this is what we saw .	我無法告訴各位 , 第一次從探測器看到泰坦的表面是什麼樣子 。 這是我們所看到的 。
and it was a shocker , because it was everything we wanted those other pictures taken from orbit to be .	這是個令人震驚的事件 , 因為我們希望這些照片從軌道上拍下來 。
it was an unambiguous pattern , a geological pattern .	它是一個不確定的模式 , 一個地質的模式 。
it's a dendritic drainage pattern that can be formed only by the flow of liquids .	它是一種傾斜的排水模式 , 只有液體的流動才能形成 。
and you can follow these channels and you can see how they all converge .	你可以跟著這些管道 , 你可以看到它們是如何融合的 。
and they converge into this channel here , which drains into this region .	他們把這個管道轉換成這個區域 。
you are looking at a shoreline .	你看到的是海岸線 。
was this a shoreline of fluids ? we didn't know .	這是流體的海岸線嗎 ? 我們不知道 。
but this is somewhat of a shoreline .	但這是一條海岸線 。
this picture is taken at 16 kilometers .	這張照片拍攝於16公里 。
this is the picture taken at eight kilometers , ok ? again , the shoreline .	這張照片拍攝於8公里 , 好嗎 ? 同樣的 , 海岸線 。
okay , now , 16 kilometers , eight kilometers this is roughly an airline altitude .	好 , 現在 , 16公里 , 8公里--這大概是一架飛機的高度 。
if you were going to take an airplane trip across the u . s . , you would be flying at these altitudes .	如果你要搭飛機橫跨美國 , 你會在這些高度飛行 。
so , this is the picture you would have at the window of titanian airlines as you fly across the surface of titan .	這張照片是你在鐵達尼亞航空的窗戶 , 當你飛越鐵達尼號表面時 , 你會看到的 。
and then finally , the probe came to rest on the surface , and i'm going to show you , ladies and gentlemen , the first picture ever taken from the surface of a moon in the outer solar system .	最後 , 探測器到了表面上 , 我要給你們看的是 , 女士們先生們 , 這是從外太陽系表面拍的第一張照片 。
and here is the horizon , ok ?	這是地平線 , 好嗎 ?
these are probably water ice pebbles , yes ?	這些可能是冰石 , 是嗎 ?
and obviously , it landed in one of these flat , dark regions and it didn't sink out of sight . so it wasn't fluid that we landed in .	很顯然 , 它落在一個平坦、黑暗的區域中 , 且它沒有從視線下沉 。 所以它不是我們登陸的流體 。
what the probe came down in was basically the titan equivalent of a mud flat .	探測器的來源基本上等同於泥土的平面 。
this is an unconsolidated ground that is suffused with liquid methane .	這是一個沒有隔離的地面 , 上面有液態甲烷 。
and it's probably the case that this material has washed off the highlands of titan through these channels that we saw , and has drained over billions of years to fill in lowlying basins .	可能是這種情況 , 這種材料已經從土衛六的高地上洗掉 , 經過我們看到的這些管道 , 已經耗盡了數十億年的時間 , 來填補低盆地 。
and that is what the huygens probe landed in .	這就是赤道探測器登陸的樣子 。
but still , there was no sign in our images , or even in the huygens' images , of any large , open bodies of fluids .	但仍然 , 我們的影像中沒有任何徵兆 , 甚至在huygen的影像中 , 任何大型、開放的液體 。
where were they ? it got even more puzzling when we found dunes .	它們在哪裡 ? 當我們發現沙丘時 , 它變得更讓人困惑 。
ok , so this is our movie of the equatorial region of titan , showing these dunes . these are dunes that are 100 meters tall , separated by a few kilometers , and they go on for miles and miles and miles .	好 , 這是我們在泰坦赤道的電影 , 展示了這些沙丘 , 這些沙丘高達100公尺 , 分離了幾公里 , 數英里長 。
there's hundreds , up to a 1 , 000 or 1 , 200 miles of dunes .	有數百英里高達一千或一百英里的沙丘 。
this is the saharan desert of titan .	這是泰坦撒哈拉沙漠 。
it's obviously a place which is very dry , or you wouldn't get dunes .	很顯然 , 這個地方很乾燥 , 或你沒辦法弄沙丘 。
so again , it got puzzling that there were no bodies of fluid , until finally , we saw lakes in the polar regions .	所以 , 再一次 , 這讓人困惑的是 , 沒有液體 , 直到終於 , 我們看到北極地區的湖 。
and there is a lake scene in the south polar region of titan .	在土衛六南極有個湖景 。
it's about the size of lake ontario .	大約是安大略湖的大小 。
and then , only a week and a half ago , we flew over the north pole of titan and found , again , we found a feature here the size of the caspian sea .	接著 , 半年前 , 我們飛越了土衛六的北極 , 再次發現 , 我們發現了卡普安海的特徵 。
so it seems that the liquids , for some reason we don't understand , or during at least this season , are apparently at the poles of titan .	所以 , 似乎液體 , 基於某些原因 , 至少在這個季節 , 很明顯地位在泰坦的極地 。
and i think you would agree that we have found titan is a remarkable , mystical place . it's exotic , it's alien , but yet strangely earthlike , and having earthlike geological formations and a tremendous geographical diversity , and is a fascinating world whose only rival in the solar system for complexity and richness is the earth itself .	我想你會同意我們發現土衛六是一個很奇特、神秘的地方 。 它是外星人 , 但卻是很奇怪的地球形態 , 像地球一樣 , 地球形態和一個極大的地理多樣性 , 一個令人著迷的世界 , 一個在複雜和豐富的太陽系中 , 只有地球本身 。
and so now we go onto enceladus . enceladus is a small moon , it's about a tenth the size of titan . and you can see it here next to england , just to show you the size . this is not meant to be a threat .	現在我們來到土衛二 。 土衛二是一個小月球 , 它的大小大約是土衛六的十分之一 。 你可以看到它旁邊的英格蘭 , 只為了向你展示大小 。 這不是威脅 。
and enceladus is very white , it's very bright , and its surface is obviously wrecked with fractures .	土衛二非常白 , 非常明亮 , 它的表面很明顯地破碎了 。
it is a very geologically active body .	它是地質活躍的身體 。
but the mother lode of discoveries on enceladus was found at the south pole and we're looking at the south pole here where we found this system of fractures .	但在土衛二的發現之母就在南極找到了 , 我們現在看到的是南極 , 在那裡 , 我們發現了破裂系統 。
and they're a different color because they're a different composition .	它們是不同的顏色 , 因為它們是不同的組成 。
they are coated . these fractures are coated with organic materials .	它們被覆蓋 。 這些碎片被有機材料覆蓋 。
moreover , this whole , entire region , the south polar region , has elevated temperatures . it's the hottest place on the planet , on the body .	此外 , 整個南極區域已經升高了溫度 。 這是地球上最熱的地方 。
that's as bizarre as finding that the antarctic on the earth is hotter than the tropics .	這有點奇怪 , 發現地球上南極洲比熱帶地區更熱 。
and then , when we took additional pictures , we discovered that from these fractures are issuing jets of fine , icy particles extending hundreds of miles into space .	接著 , 當我們拍攝額外的照片時 , 我們發現從這些碎片中 , 正引發好的噴射機 , 冰粒會延伸數百英里的空間 。
and when we colorcode this image , to bring out the faint light levels , we see that these jets feed a plume that , in fact , we see , in other images , goes thousands of miles into the space above enceladus .	當我們把這張影像編碼出來 , 把微弱的光線層次放出來 , 我們看到這些噴射機在其他影像中 , 事實上 , 我們看到 , 在土衛二上千英里的太空中 。
my team and i have examined images like this , and like this one , and have thought about the other results from cassini .	我和我的團隊已經檢查過像這樣的圖片 , 就像這個 , 考慮了卡西尼的其他結果 。
and we have arrived at the conclusion that these jets may be erupting from pockets of liquid water under the surface of enceladus .	我們得到的結論是這些噴射機可能是從土衛二表面的液態水中噴出來的 。
so we have , possibly , liquid water , organic materials and excess heat .	所以我們有 , 可能是液態水、有機物質和多餘的熱能 。
in other words , we have possibly stumbled upon the holy grail of modern day planetary exploration , or in other words , an environment that is potentially suitable for living organisms .	換句話說 , 我們可能偶然發現了現代行星探索的聖杯 , 或換句話說 , 一個可能適合生物的環境 。
and i don't think i need to tell you that the discovery of life elsewhere in our solar system , whether it be on enceladus or elsewhere , would have enormous cultural and scientific implications .	我想我不需要告訴各位 , 在太陽系其他地方的生命發現 , 不論是在土衛二或其他地方 , 都會有巨大的文化和科學意涵 。
because if we could demonstrate that genesis had occurred not once , but twice , independently , in our solar system , then that means , by inference , it has occurred a staggering number of times throughout the universe and its 13 . 7 billion year history .	因為如果我們能證明 , 慷慨不曾發生過 , 而是在我們的太陽系中 , 獨立的兩次 , 那就意味著 , 根據推論 , 它在整個宇宙中出現了驚人的數量 , 且它的137億年歷史 。
right now , earth is the only planet still that we know is teeming with life .	現在 , 地球是唯一一個我們所知道的行星 , 地球是充滿生命的 。
it is precious , it is unique , it is still , so far , the only home we've ever known .	它是珍貴的 , 它是獨一無二的 , 到目前為止 , 我們所知唯一的家 。
and if any of you were alert and coherent during the 1960s and we'd forgive you , if you weren't , ok you would remember this very famous picture taken by the apollo 8 astronauts in 1968 .	如果你們當中有人在1960年代發出警告 , 我們會原諒你 , 如果你不是 , 那你會記得1968年阿波羅8號太空人拍的這張著名的照片 。
it was the first time that earth was imaged from space , and it had an enormous impact on our sense of place in the universe , and our sense of responsibility for the protection of our own planet .	這是第一次 , 地球是來自太空的影像 , 它對我們在宇宙中的位置有著巨大的影響 , 我們對地球的保護感知有責任 。
well , we on cassini have taken an equivalent first , a picture that no human eye has ever seen before .	嗯 , 我們在卡西尼拍了一張相同的第一張照片 , 一張從來沒有人看過的照片 。
it is a total eclipse of the sun , seen from the other side of saturn .	它是太陽的完整日蝕 , 從土星的另一側看到 。
and in this impossibly beautiful picture , you see the main rings backlit by the sun , you see the refracted image of the sun and you see this ring created , in fact , by the exhalations of enceladus .	在這張非常美麗的圖片中 , 你可以看到太陽的主要環狀物 , 你可以看到太陽的折射影像 , 你可以看到這個環 , 事實上 , 由土衛二的外表所產生 。
but as if that weren't brilliant enough , we can spot , in this beautiful image , sight of our own planet , cradled in the arms of saturn's rings .	但如果這還不夠聰明 , 我們可以在這個美麗的圖像中看到我們星球的景象 , 在土星的光環中挖掘出來 。
now , there is something deeply moving about seeing ourselves from afar , and capturing the sight of our little , blueocean planet in the skies of other worlds .	現在 , 有件事深深地讓我們看到自己從遠處捕捉到我們小藍綠色的星球在其他世界的天空中捕捉到的景象
and that , and the perspective of ourselves that we gain from that , may be , in the end , the finest reward that we earn from this journey of discovery that started half a century ago .	這樣 , 及我們從中獲得的觀點 , 可能是 , 最終 , 我們從這個發現的旅程中得到最好的獎勵 , 開始了半個世紀 。
as of 2005 , only 15 percent of the world was mapped . this slows the delivery of aid after a disaster and hides the economic potential of unused lands and unknown roads . in this short talk , google's lalitesh katragadda demos map maker , a group mapmaking tool that people around the globe are using to map their world .	2005年 , 只有15%的世界被繪製 。 這緩慢的援助 , 在災難之後 , 隱藏了未知的土地和未知的道路 。 在這個短短的演講中 , 谷歌的拉利特卡德達德達•德莫斯地圖 , 一個團體繪製的地圖工具 , 全世界的人都在用地圖繪製他們的世界 。
collaboration , design , map , technology	合作、設計、地圖、科技、科技合作、合作、合作、合作、設計、地圖、地圖、科技、
lalitesh katragadda: making maps to fight disaster , build economies	拉liteshkatragada:製作地圖來對抗災難 , 建立經濟體 , 建立經濟體 。
in 2008 , cyclone nargis devastated myanmar .	2008年 , 自行車納基人摧毀了緬甸 。
millions of people were in severe need of help .	數百萬人急需幫忙 。
the u . n . wanted to rush people and supplies to the area .	聯合國想要趕人並供應到這個區域 。
but there were no maps , no maps of roads , no maps showing hospitals , no way for help to reach the cyclone victims .	但沒有地圖 , 沒有道路的地圖 , 沒有顯示醫院的地圖 , 無法幫助到cyclo病毒受害者 。
when we look at a map of los angeles or london , it is hard to believe that as of 2005 , only 15 percent of the world was mapped to a geocodable level of detail .	當我們看洛杉磯或倫敦的地圖時 , 很難相信 , 2005年 , 世界上只有15%的地理細節被描繪成可辨識的細節 。
the u . n . ran headfirst into a problem that the majority of the world's populous faces: not having detailed maps .	聯合國執行一個問題:世界上大部分的民眾臉都沒有詳細的地圖 。
but help was coming .	但救援來了 。
at google , 40 volunteers used a new software to map 120 , 000 kilometers of roads , 3 , 000 hospitals , logistics and relief points .	在google , 40位志工用了一套新軟體來繪製十二萬公里的道路 , 三千間醫院、物流和休息點 。
and it took them four days .	他們花了四天的時間 。
the new software they used ? google mapmaker .	他們使用的新軟體 ? 谷歌地圖製造商 。
google mapmaker is a technology that empowers each of us to map what we know locally .	谷歌地圖製作者是一項技術 , 讓我們每個人能夠繪製我們所知的地圖 。
people have used this software to map everything from roads to rivers , from schools to local businesses , and video stores to the corner store .	人們用這個軟體來繪製所有東西 , 從道路到河流 , 從學校到當地企業 , 影片店到角落商店 。
nobel prize nominee hernando de soto recognized that the key to economic liftoff for most developing countries is to tap the vast amounts of uncapitalized land .	諾貝爾獎提名hernandodesto承認 , 大部分發展中國家經濟利益的關鍵是要處理大量未受影響的土地 。
for example , a trillion dollars of real estate remains uncapitalized in india alone .	舉例來說 , 僅僅在印度 , 數兆美元的房地產仍然未被監禁 。
in the last year alone , thousands of users in 170 countries have mapped millions of pieces of information , and created a map of a level of detail never thought viable .	僅僅在去年 , 170個國家數以千計的使用者已經繪製了數百萬個資訊 , 創造出了不可思議的細節地圖 。
and this was made possible by the power of passionate users everywhere .	這使得世界各地熱情使用者的力量 。
let's look at some of the maps being created by users right now .	咱們來看看目前使用者所創造的一些地圖 。
so , as we speak , people are mapping the world in these 170 countries .	所以 , 正如我們所說的 , 在170個國家 , 人們正在繪製這個世界 。
you can see bridget in africa who just mapped a road in senegal .	你可以看到在非洲的橋樑 , 剛在塞內加爾繪製了一條道路 。
and , closer to home , chalua , an n . g . road in bangalore .	離家越近 , 班加羅爾的公路 。
this is the result of computational geometry , gesture recognition , and machine learning .	這是計算幾何學、手勢認可和機器學習的結果 。
this is a victory of thousands of users , in hundreds of cities , one user , one edit at a time .	這是數以千計的使用者的勝利 , 在數百個城市中 , 一個使用者 , 一次編輯 。
this is an invitation to the 70 percent of our unmapped planet .	這是我們未被開發的70%的邀請 。
welcome to the new world .	歡迎來到新世界 。
in 2003 , the palestinian village of budrus mounted a 10monthlong nonviolent protest to stop a barrier being built across their olive groves . did you hear about it ? didn't think so . brazilian filmmaker julia bacha asks why we only pay attention to violence in the israelpalestine conflict and not to the nonviolent leaders who may one day bring peace .	2003年 , 巴勒斯坦村落的巴勒斯坦村落登上了十個月的非暴力抗議活動 , 阻止他們在橄欖的火箭上建造的障礙 。 你們有聽過嗎 ? 巴西的製片人茱莉亞.巴希問:為什麼我們只關注在以色列巴勒斯坦衝突中 , 而非暴力領袖有一天可能會帶來和平 。
arts , communication , compassion , entertainment , film , peace , violence , war	藝術、溝通、同情、娛樂、電影、和平、暴力、戰爭、戰爭、戰爭、戰爭、戰爭、戰爭、戰爭、戰爭、戰爭、暴力、暴力、暴力、暴力、戰爭、戰爭、戰爭、戰爭、戰爭、戰爭、、
julia bacha: pay attention to nonviolence	juliabacha:請注意非暴力事件 。
for the last 8 years , i have dedicated my life to documenting the work of israelis and palestinians who are trying to end the conflict using peaceful means .	過去八年間 , 我致力於記錄以色列和巴勒斯坦人的作品 , 他們試圖用和平的手段來結束衝突 。
when i travel with my work across europe and the united states , one question always comes up: where is the palestinian gandhi ?	當我在歐洲和美國旅行時 , 總是遇到一個問題:巴勒斯坦甘地在哪裡 ?
why aren't palestinians using nonviolent resistance ?	為什麼巴勒斯坦人不用非暴力抗爭 ?
the challenge i face when i hear this question is that often i have just returned from the middle east where i spent my time filming dozens of palestinians who are using nonviolence to defend their lands and water resources from israeli soldiers and settlers .	當我聽到這個問題時 , 我所面臨的挑戰是 , 我剛從中東回來 , 在那裡 , 我花了很多時間拍攝數十位巴勒斯坦人 , 他們用非暴力的方式來保護他們的土地和水資源 , 從以色列士兵和定居者那裡來 。
these leaders are trying to forge a massive national nonviolent movement to end the occupation and build peace in the region .	這些領導人試圖去擁護一個巨大的國家非暴力運動 , 來終止這個地區的職業和平建立 。
yet , most of you have probably never heard about them .	然而 , 大多數人可能從來沒有聽過他們 。
this divide between what's happening on the ground and perceptions abroad is one of the key reasons why we don't have yet a palestinian peaceful resistance movement that has been successful .	在國外發生的事和感知之間 , 這種分歧就是我們尚未擁有的巴勒斯坦和平抗爭運動的關鍵原因之一 。
so i'm here today to talk about the power of attention , the power of your attention , and the emergence and development of nonviolent movements in the west bank , gaza and elsewhere but today , my case study is going to be palestine .	所以我今天要談的是注意力的力量 , 關注的力量 , 以及在西岸、加薩和其他地方的非暴力運動的興起和發展 , 但今天 , 我的案例研究將成為巴勒斯坦 。
i believe that what's mostly missing for nonviolence to grow is not for palestinians to start adopting nonviolence , but for us to start paying attention to those who already are .	我相信大部分的非暴力行為 , 並不是為了巴勒斯坦人開始採用非暴力行為 , 而是為了我們開始注意那些已經存在的人 。
allow me to illustrate this point by taking you to this village called budrus .	讓我用這個名叫布德魯斯的村莊來說明這個觀點 。
about seven years ago , they faced extinction , because israel announced it would build a separation barrier , and part of this barrier would be built on top of the village .	大約七年前 , 他們面臨絕種 , 因為以色列宣布要蓋一個隔離的障礙 , 而這個障礙的部分會在村落上蓋 。
they would lose 40 percent of their land and be surrounded , so they would lose free access to the rest of the west bank .	他們會失去40%的土地 , 被包圍著 , 所以他們會失去西岸其他地方的免費 。
through inspired local leadership , they launched a peaceful resistance campaign to stop that from happening .	透過當地的領導力 , 他們發起了一個和平的抗爭活動 , 阻止這一切發生 。
let me show you some brief clips , so you have a sense for what that actually looked like on the ground .	讓我給你們看一些短片 , 所以你對地面上到底是什麼樣子的感覺 。
palestinian woman: we were told the wall would separate palestine from israel .	巴勒斯坦女子:我們被告知牆會和以色列分開巴勒斯坦 。
here in budrus , we realized the wall would steal our land .	在布德魯斯 , 我們發現牆會偷走我們的土地 。
israeli man: the fence has , in fact , created a solution to terror .	以色列男子:圍籬事實上 , 為恐怖創造了一個解決方案 。
man: today you're invited to a peaceful march .	男子:今天你被邀請去和平遊行 。
you are joined by dozens of your israeli brothers and sisters .	你被幾十位以色列兄弟姐妹加入 。
israeli activist: nothing scares the army more than nonviolent opposition .	以色列的行動主義者:軍隊比非暴力反對更害怕 。
woman: we saw the men trying to push the soldiers , but none of them could do that .	女子:我們看到男人試圖推動士兵 , 但他們沒有人能做到 。
but i think the girls could do it .	但我認為女孩們可以做到 。
fatah party member: we must empty our minds of traditional thinking .	法塔赫派對成員:我們必須忽視傳統思維的思想 。
hamas party member: we were in complete harmony , and we wanted to spread it to all of palestine .	哈馬斯黨員:我們完全和諧 , 我們想要把它傳播到所有的巴勒斯坦 。
chanting: one united nation .	主持人:一個聯合國 。
fatah , hamas and the popular front !	法塔 , 哈馬斯和大眾的前線 !
news anchor: the clashes over the fence continue .	主持人:柵欄的關節持續下去 。
reporter: israeli border police were sent to disperse the crowd .	記者:以色列邊界警察被送去散播群眾 。
they were allowed to use any force necessary .	他們被允許使用任何必要的力量 。
man: these are live bullets .	男子:這些是現場的子彈 。
it's like fallujah . shooting everywhere .	就好像摔角了 。 射擊到處都是 。
israeli activist: i was sure we were all going to die .	以色列活動家:我確信我們都會死 。
but there were others around me who weren't even cowering .	但在我身邊有一些人 , 甚至沒有牛 。
israeli soldier: a nonviolent protest is not going to stop the [unclear] .	以色列的士兵:非暴力抗爭不會阻止他們 。
protester: this is a peaceful march .	普特斯特:這是和平的遊行 。
there is no need to use violence .	不需要使用暴力 。
chanting: we can do it ! we can do it !	主持人:我們能做到 ! 我們可以做到 !
julia bacha: when i first heard about the story of budrus , i was surprised that the international media had failed to cover the extraordinary set of events that happened seven years ago , in 2003 .	朱莉亞•巴奇亞:當我第一次聽到布德魯斯的故事時 , 我很訝異國際媒體沒有報導七年前發生的非凡事件 。
what was even more surprising was the fact that budrus was successful .	更令人驚訝的是布德魯斯成功了 。
the residents , after 10 months of peaceful resistance , convinced the israeli government to move the route of the barrier off their lands and to the green line , which is the internationally recognized boundary between israel and the palestinian territories .	居民在10個月的和平抗爭之後 , 說服以色列政府將他們的土地上的障礙往綠線移動 , 也就是國際認可以色列和巴勒斯坦領土之間的界線 。
the resistance in budrus has since spread to villages across the west bank and to palestinian neighborhoods in jerusalem .	布德魯斯的抗藥性自從傳播到西岸以及耶路撒冷的巴勒斯坦社區 。
yet the media remains mostly silent on these stories .	但媒體仍然沉默在這些故事上 。
this silence carries profound consequences for the likelihood that nonviolence can grow , or even survive , in palestine .	這種沉默會造成嚴重的後果 , 導致非暴力的可能性成長 , 甚至在巴勒斯坦存活下來 。
violent resistance and nonviolent resistance share one very important thing in common ; they are both a form of theater seeking an audience to their cause .	暴力抗爭和非暴力抗爭有一項非常重要的共通點 , 它們都是劇院的一種形式 , 尋求觀眾的成因 。
if violent actors are the only ones constantly getting frontpage covers and attracting international attention to the palestinian issue , it becomes very hard for nonviolent leaders to make the case to their communities that civil disobedience is a viable option in addressing their plight .	如果暴力演員是唯一的先驅者 , 並且吸引國際關注巴勒斯坦議題 , 對非暴力的領導者來說 , 要讓公民不服從是可行的選項 。
the power of attention is probably going to come as no surprise to the parents in the room .	注意力的力量可能對房間裡的父母來說並不意外 。
the surest way to make your child throw increasingly louder tantrums is by giving him attention the first time he throws a fit .	讓孩子們更加大聲的推進方式就是讓他注意到他第一次投入適應的能力 。
the tantrum will become what childhood psychologists call a functional behavior , since the child has learned that he can get parental attention out of it .	幻覺會變成兒童心理學家稱之為功能性行為 , 因為孩子們已經學到 , 他可以從中獲得父母的注意力 。
parents can incentivize or disincentivize behavior simply by giving or withdrawing attention to their children .	父母能激勵或忽視行為 , 僅僅是給予孩子或戒斷的注意力 。
but that's true for adults too .	但對成人也是如此 。
in fact , the behavior of entire communities and countries can be influenced , depending on where the international community chooses to focus its attention .	事實上 , 整個社區和國家的行為會受到影響 , 根據國際社群選擇集中注意力的地方 。
i believe that at the core of ending the conflict in the middle east and bringing peace is for us to transform nonviolence into a functional behavior by giving a lot more attention to the nonviolent leaders on the ground today .	我相信 , 終結中東衝突的核心 , 帶來和平 , 是我們要把非暴力行為轉變成功能性行為 , 讓更多關注現今在地上的非暴力領導人 。
in the course of taking my film to villages in the west bank , in gaza and in east jerusalem , i have seen the impact that even one documentary film can have in influencing the transformation .	在把我的影片帶到西岸、加薩、東耶路撒冷的村莊時 , 我見過一部紀錄片能影響到轉變的影響 。
in a village called wallajeh , which sits very close to jerusalem , the community was facing a very similar plight to budrus .	在一個叫瓦拉雅的村莊 , 離耶路撒冷很近 , 社區正面臨著非常相似的困境 。
they were going to be surrounded , lose a lot of their lands and not have freedom of access , either to the west bank or jerusalem .	他們會被包圍 , 失去很多土地 , 沒有取得自由 , 不論是西岸或耶路撒冷 。
they had been using nonviolence for about two years but had grown disenchanted since nobody was paying attention .	兩年來 , 他們一直在使用非暴力 , 但自從沒有人在注意力時 , 漸漸地被大大的不同 。
so we organized a screening .	所以我們組織了一場篩選 。
a week later , they held the most wellattended and disciplined demonstration to date .	一個禮拜後 , 他們舉辦了最好且最專業的示範 。
the organizers say that the villagers , upon seeing the story of budrus documented in a film , felt that there were indeed people following what they were doing , that people cared .	組織者說 , 村民們 , 看到布德魯斯的故事被記錄在電影中 , 覺得有一些人在追蹤他們在做的事 , 人們在乎的事 。
so they kept on going .	所以他們繼續下去 。
on the israeli side , there is a new peace movement called solidariot , which means solidarity in hebrew .	在以色列 , 有一個新的和平運動 , 叫做slidariot , 意思是希伯來的團結 。
the leaders of this movement have been using budrus as one of their primary recruiting tools .	這個運動的領袖們一直用布德魯斯作為他們主要的招募工具之一 。
they report that israelis who had never been active before , upon seeing the film , understand the power of nonviolence and start joining their activities .	他們報告說 , 以色列從來沒有活躍過 , 看過電影 , 了解非暴力的力量 , 並開始加入他們的活動 。
the examples of wallajeh and the solidariot movement show that even a smallbudget independent film can play a role in transforming nonviolence into a functional behavior .	瓦拉傑和索利德運動的例子顯示 , 即使是一部小型的獨立電影也能扮演一個角色 , 將非暴力變成功能性行為 。
now imagine the power that big media players could have if they started covering the weekly nonviolent demonstrations happening in villages like bil'in , ni'lin , wallajeh , in jerusalem neighborhoods like sheikh jarrah and silwan the nonviolent leaders would become more visible , valued and effective in their work .	想像一下 , 大型媒體播放者的力量 , 如果他們開始報導每週的非暴力演示 , 在村落裡發生 , 比如比利、尼林、華拉雅 , 在耶路撒冷的社區 , 像是希尼克•賈拉和絲瓦 , 非暴力領導人會變得更明顯、更有價值、更有效率 。
i believe that the most important thing is to understand that if we don't pay attention to these efforts , they are invisible , and it's as if they never happened .	我相信最重要的是要了解 , 如果我們不注意這些努力 , 它們是隱形的 , 就好像它們從來沒有發生過一樣 。
but i have seen first hand that if we do , they will multiply .	但我首先看到 , 如果我們做的話 , 它們就會倍增 。
if they multiply , their influence will grow in the overall israelipalestinian conflict .	如果他們倍增 , 他們的影響會在以色列的巴勒斯坦衝突中成長 。
and theirs is the kind of influence that can finally unblock the situation .	他們的影響力終於解開了局面 。
these leaders have proven that nonviolence works in places like budrus .	這些領導人已經證明非暴力在像布德魯斯這樣的地方有用 。
let's give them attention so they can prove it works everywhere .	讓我們給他們注意 , 這樣他們就能證明它無所不在 。
simon sinek has a simple but powerful model for inspirational leadership all starting with a golden circle and the question " why ? " his examples include apple , martin luther king , and the wright brothers . . .	西蒙•海克擁有一個簡單但有力的領導模式 , 全都從黃金圈開始 , 問題是:為什麼 ? 他的例子包括蘋果、馬丁路德金、萊特兄弟......
bullseye , business , entrepreneur , leadership , sales , selling , success	bullseye、商業、企業家、領導力、銷售、成功、成功、成功、企業家、企業家、領導力、銷售、銷售、銷售、銷售、成功、成功、成功 。
simon sinek: how great leaders inspire action	西蒙海克:偉大的領導者鼓舞行動 。
how do you explain when things don't go as we assume ?	你要如何解釋當事情不像我們所想的那樣 ?
or better , how do you explain when others are able to achieve things that seem to defy all of the assumptions ?	或更好 , 你要如何解釋 , 當他人能夠達成看似戰勝所有假設時 , 要如何解釋 ?
for example: why is apple so innovative ?	例如:為什麼蘋果如此創新 ?
year after year , after year , after year , they're more innovative than all their competition .	年復一年 , 年復一年 , 他們比他們所有的競爭都更有創意 。
and yet , they're just a computer company .	然而 , 他們只是一家電腦公司 。
they're just like everyone else .	他們和其他人一樣 。
they have the same access to the same talent , the same agencies , the same consultants , the same media .	他們擁有相同的人才 , 相同的機構 , 相同的顧問 , 同樣的媒體 。
then why is it that they seem to have something different ?	為什麼他們似乎有不同的東西 ?
why is it that martin luther king led the civil rights movement ?	為什麼馬丁•路德•金恩領導民權運動 ?
he wasn't the only man who suffered in a precivil rights america , and he certainly wasn't the only great orator of the day .	他不是唯一一個在美國受苦的人 , 他肯定不是當天最偉大的演說家 。
and why is it that the wright brothers were able to figure out controlled , powered man flight when there were certainly other teams who were better qualified , better funded . . .	為什麼萊特兄弟能夠想出控制權的、有權力的飛機當其他團隊有更好資格、更好的資金時
and they didn't achieve powered man flight , and the wright brothers beat them to it .	他們沒有達成人類飛行 , 萊特兄弟打敗他們 。
there's something else at play here .	這裡還有別的東西 。
about three and a half years ago i made a discovery .	大約三年半前 , 我發現了一項發現 。
and this discovery profoundly changed my view on how i thought the world worked , and it even profoundly changed the way in which i operate in it .	這個發現深深地改變了我對世界運作的方式 , 甚至深深改變了我對它運作的方式 。
as it turns out , there's a pattern .	結果發現 , 有一個模式 。
as it turns out , all the great and inspiring leaders and organizations in the world whether it's apple or martin luther king or the wright brothers they all think , act and communicate the exact same way .	結果發現 , 世界上所有偉大且鼓舞人心的領導人和組織 , 不論是蘋果、馬丁路德金恩或萊特兄弟──他們都認為、行為、溝通的方式都一樣 。
and it's the complete opposite to everyone else .	和其他人完全相反 。
all i did was codify it , and it's probably the world's simplest idea .	我所做的只是編寫它 , 可能是世界上最簡單的想法 。
i call it the golden circle .	我稱它為黃金圈 。
why ? how ? what ?	為什麼 ? 什麼 ?
this little idea explains why some organizations and some leaders are able to inspire where others aren't .	這個小小的點子解釋了為何有些組織和一些領導者能夠啟發別人不在的地方 。
let me define the terms really quickly .	讓我很快地定義這個詞 。
every single person , every single organization on the planet knows what they do , 100 percent .	每個人 , 地球上的每一個組織都知道他們所做的事 , 百分之百 。
some know how they do it , whether you call it your differentiated value proposition or your proprietary process or your usp .	有些人知道他們是如何做到的 , 不論你稱它為你不同的價值觀 , 或你的資產過程 , 或你的usp 。
but very , very few people or organizations know why they do what they do .	但很少人或組織知道他們怎麼做 。
and by " why " i don't mean " to make a profit . "	所謂的 「 為什麼 」 不是為了賺錢 。
that's a result . it's always a result .	這是結果 。 結果總是結果 。
by " why , " i mean: what's your purpose ?	我的意思是:你的目的是什麼 ?
what's your cause ? what's your belief ?	你的成因是什麼 ? 你的信念是什麼 ?
why does your organization exist ?	為什麼你的組織存在 ?
why do you get out of bed in the morning ?	為什麼你早上起床 ?
and why should anyone care ?	為什麼有人要在乎 ?
well , as a result , the way we think , the way we act , the way we communicate is from the outside in .	結果就是 , 我們思考的方式 , 我們溝通的方式來自外界 。
it's obvious . we go from the clearest thing to the fuzziest thing .	很明顯 , 我們從最清楚的事物轉變成最模糊的東西 。
but the inspired leaders and the inspired organizations regardless of their size , regardless of their industry all think , act and communicate from the inside out .	但鼓舞人心的領導人和激勵人心的組織 , 不管他們的大小 , 不管他們的產業都認為 , 行動和溝通來自內部 。
let me give you an example .	讓我舉個例子 。
i use apple because they're easy to understand and everybody gets it .	我用蘋果是因為他們很容易理解 , 每個人都懂 。
if apple were like everyone else , a marketing message from them might sound like this: " we make great computers .	如果蘋果和其他人一樣 , 他們的行銷訊息可能聽起來像這樣: 「 我們會製造出很棒的電腦 。
they're beautifully designed , simple to use and user friendly .	它們設計得很漂亮 , 很簡單 , 很容易使用 , 且很友善 。
want to buy one ? " " meh . "	想要買一台嗎 ? 」
and that's how most of us communicate .	那就是我們大多數人溝通的方式 。
that's how most marketing is done , that's how most sales is done and that's how most of us communicate interpersonally .	這就是大部分的行銷方式 , 大部分的銷售都是如此 , 那就是我們大多數人之間溝通的方式 。
we say what we do , we say how we're different or how we're better and we expect some sort of a behavior , a purchase , a vote , something like that .	我們說我們所做的事 , 我們說我們是如何不同或如何更好 , 我們期待某種行為、購買、投票等等 。
here's our new law firm: we have the best lawyers with the biggest clients , we always perform for our clients who do business with us .	這是我們的新法律公司:我們有最好的律師和最大客戶 , 我們總是為我們的客戶做生意 。
here's our new car: it gets great gas mileage , it has leather seats , buy our car .	這是我們的新車:它有很大的氣體 , 上面有皮革座位 , 買車 。
here's how apple actually communicates .	蘋果是如何溝通的 。
" everything we do , we believe in challenging the status quo .	「 我們所做的一切 , 我們相信挑戰現狀 。
we believe in thinking differently .	我們相信不同的思考方式 。
the way we challenge the status quo is by making our products beautifully designed , simple to use and user friendly .	我們挑戰現狀的方式 , 就是讓我們的產品精美地設計 , 簡單地使用和友善 。
we just happen to make great computers .	我們剛好製造了很棒的電腦 。
want to buy one ? "	想要買一台嗎 ? 」
totally different right ? you're ready to buy a computer from me .	完全不一樣嗎 ? 你準備好跟我買一台電腦 。
all i did was reverse the order of the information .	我所做的只是反轉資訊的順序 。
what it proves to us is that people don't buy what you do ; people buy why you do it .	它向我們證明的是 , 人們不買你做的事 ; 人們買你為什麼做這件事 。
people don't buy what you do ; they buy why you do it .	人們不買你做的事 ; 他們買你為什麼做 。
this explains why every single person in this room is perfectly comfortable buying a computer from apple .	這解釋了為什麼在座的每一個人都很舒服從蘋果電腦購買一台電腦 。
but we're also perfectly comfortable buying an mp3 player from apple , or a phone from apple , or a dvr from apple .	但我們也非常自在地買蘋果電腦的mp3播放器 , 或蘋果電腦的手機 , 或蘋果電腦的dvr 。
but , as i said before , apple's just a computer company .	但 , 就像我之前說過的 , 蘋果只是一家電腦公司 。
there's nothing that distinguishes them structurally from any of their competitors .	沒有任何東西能從他們的競爭者中分辨它們 。
their competitors are all equally qualified to make all of these products .	他們的競爭者都同樣資格做出這些產品 。
in fact , they tried .	事實上 , 他們試了 。
a few years ago , gateway came out with flat screen tvs .	幾年前 , 高速公路出櫃了平面的電視機 。
they're eminently qualified to make flat screen tvs .	他們很有資格製作平面的電視機 。
they've been making flat screen monitors for years .	數年來 , 他們一直在製作平面的螢幕螢幕 。
dell came out with mp3 players and pdas , and they make great quality products , and they can make perfectly welldesigned products and nobody bought one .	戴爾德爾帶著mp3播放器和pdas出櫃 , 他們做出很棒的品質產品 , 他們可以做出完美的設計設計產品 , 沒有人買 。
in fact , talking about it now , we can't even imagine buying an mp3 player from dell .	事實上 , 談到現在 , 我們甚至無法想像從dell上購買mp3播放器 。
why would you buy an mp3 player from a computer company ?	你為什麼要從一家電腦公司買一台mp3播放器 ?
but we do it every day .	但我們每天都這樣做 。
people don't buy what you do ; they buy why you do it .	人們不買你做的事 ; 他們買你為什麼做 。
the goal is not to do business with everybody who needs what you have .	目標不是要和所有需要你的東西的人做生意 。
the goal is to do business with people who believe what you believe .	目標是和相信你所相信的人做生意 。
here's the best part: none of what i'm telling you is my opinion .	最棒的部分是:我告訴你們的意見都沒有 。
it's all grounded in the tenets of biology .	一切都在生物學的10%之內 。
not psychology , biology .	不是心理學、生物學 。
if you look at a crosssection of the human brain , looking from the top down , what you see is the human brain is actually broken into three major components that correlate perfectly with the golden circle .	如果你看一下人類大腦的交叉點 , 從上而下看 , 你看到的是人類的大腦實際上被分解成三個主要元件 , 與黃金圈完全相關 。
our newest brain , our homo sapien brain , our neocortex , corresponds with the " what " level .	我們最新的大腦 , 我們的人類大腦 , 我們的新皮層 , 與 「 什麼 」 的等級有關 。
the neocortex is responsible for all of our rational and analytical thought and language .	新皮層負責所有的理性、分析思考和語言 。
the middle two sections make up our limbic brains , and our limbic brains are responsible for all of our feelings , like trust and loyalty .	中間兩個部分組成了我們的腦 , 我們的邊緣大腦負責我們所有的感覺 , 像是信任和忠誠 。
it's also responsible for all human behavior , all decisionmaking , and it has no capacity for language .	它也負責所有人類的行為 , 所有的決策 , 沒有語言的能力 。
in other words , when we communicate from the outside in , yes , people can understand vast amounts of complicated information like features and benefits and facts and figures .	換句話說 , 當我們從外界溝通時 , 是的 , 人們可以了解很多複雜的資訊 , 比如特徵、利益、事實和數字 。
it just doesn't drive behavior .	它不會驅動行為 。
when we can communicate from the inside out , we're talking directly to the part of the brain that controls behavior , and then we allow people to rationalize it with the tangible things we say and do .	當我們能從內部向外溝通時 , 我們直接和控制行為的部位溝通 , 接著 , 我們允許人們將之合理化為我們所說和做的事 。
this is where gut decisions come from .	這就是腸道決策的來源 。
you know , sometimes you can give somebody all the facts and figures , and they say , " i know what all the facts and details say , but it just doesn't feel right . "	有時候你會給別人所有的事實和數字 , 他們會說: 「 我知道所有事實和細節都說了什麼 , 但感覺不對 。 」
why would we use that verb , it doesn't " feel " right ?	為什麼我們要用那動詞 , 它不會 「 感覺 」 呢 ?
because the part of the brain that controls decisionmaking doesn't control language .	因為大腦控制決策的部分無法控制語言 。
and the best we can muster up is , " i don't know . it just doesn't feel right . "	最好的就是: 「 我不知道 , 感覺不對 。 」
or sometimes you say you're leading with your heart , or you're leading with your soul .	或者有時候你會說你帶著心 , 或是帶著你的靈魂去領導 。
well , i hate to break it to you , those aren't other body parts controlling your behavior .	嗯 , 我不喜歡打破它 , 這些不是身體部位控制你的行為 。
it's all happening here in your limbic brain , the part of the brain that controls decisionmaking and not language .	這一切都發生在你的邊緣大腦中 , 控制決策的部分 , 而非語言 。
but if you don't know why you do what you do , and people respond to why you do what you do , then how will you ever get people to vote for you , or buy something from you , or , more importantly , be loyal and want to be a part of what it is that you do .	但如果你不知道你為什麼做你所做的事 , 人們會回應你為什麼做你所做的事 , 那麼你要如何讓人們投票給你 , 或從你身上買東西 , 或者更重要的是 , 做忠誠 , 想要成為你所做的事的一部分 。
again , the goal is not just to sell to people who need what you have ; the goal is to sell to people who believe what you believe .	同樣的 , 目標並不只是賣給需要的人 ; 目標是賣給那些相信你所相信的人 。
the goal is not just to hire people who need a job ; it's to hire people who believe what you believe .	目標不只是要僱用需要工作的人 ; 而是要僱用相信你所相信的人 。
i always say that , you know , if you hire people just because they can do a job , they'll work for your money , but if you hire people who believe what you believe , they'll work for you with blood and sweat and tears .	我總是這麼說 , 你知道 , 如果你雇用別人 , 只因為他們能做事 , 他們會為你的錢工作 , 但如果你雇用相信你所相信的人 , 他們會用血汗和淚水來幫你工作 。
and nowhere else is there a better example of this than with the wright brothers .	沒有其他地方比萊特兄弟更好的例子 。
most people don't know about samuel pierpont langley .	大部分的人不知道samuelpierpontlangley 。
and back in the early 20th century , the pursuit of powered man flight was like the dot com of the day .	回到二十世紀初 , 追求權力飛行的追求 , 就像是白天的點com 。
everybody was trying it .	每個人都在試 。
and samuel pierpont langley had , what we assume , to be the recipe for success .	我們假設samuelpierpontlangley是成功的配方 。
i mean , even now , you ask people , " why did your product or why did your company fail ? "	我是說 , 即使現在 , 你問別人: 「 為什麼你的產品或為什麼你的公司失敗了 ? 」
and people always give you the same permutation of the same three things: undercapitalized , the wrong people , bad market conditions .	人們總是會給你相同的三項突變:不適合的人、不好的市場條件 。
it's always the same three things , so let's explore that .	總是相同的三件事 , 讓我們來探討一下 。
samuel pierpont langley was given 50 , 000 dollars by the war department to figure out this flying machine .	samuelpierpontlangley被戰爭部門給五萬美金 , 想出這台飛行機器 。
money was no problem .	金錢沒有問題 。
he held a seat at harvard and worked at the smithsonian and was extremely wellconnected ; he knew all the big minds of the day .	他在哈佛舉辦一個座位 , 在史密森尼工作 , 當時非常關聯 , 他知道當時的所有大型思維 。
he hired the best minds money could find and the market conditions were fantastic .	他僱用最好的心資金 , 能找到市場條件很棒 。
the new york times followed him around everywhere , and everyone was rooting for langley .	紐約時報隨處追蹤他 , 每個人都在為langley著手 。
then how come we've never heard of samuel pierpont langley ?	那麼我們怎麼可能從來沒有聽過samuelpierpontlangley ?
a few hundred miles away in dayton ohio , orville and wilbur wright , they had none of what we consider to be the recipe for success .	幾百英哩之外 , 在俄亥俄州 , 奧維爾和威爾布萊特 , 他們沒有我們認為成功的配方 。
they had no money ; they paid for their dream with the proceeds from their bicycle shop ; not a single person on the wright brothers' team had a college education , not even orville or wilbur ; and the new york times followed them around nowhere .	他們沒有錢 , 他們用自行車購物的夢想付錢 ; 沒有一個人在萊特兄弟的隊伍中受過大學教育 , 甚至不是邪惡或威爾布爾 ; 紐約時報追蹤他們到處都沒有 。
the difference was , orville and wilbur were driven by a cause , by a purpose , by a belief .	差別在於 , 奧維爾和威爾布爾被一個目標所驅使 , 一個信念所驅使 。
they believed that if they could figure out this flying machine , it'll change the course of the world .	他們相信如果他們能想出這台飛行機器 , 會改變世界的軌道 。
samuel pierpont langley was different .	samuelpierpontlangley是不同的 。
he wanted to be rich , and he wanted to be famous .	他想變得富有 , 他想變得有名 。
he was in pursuit of the result .	他在追求結果 。
he was in pursuit of the riches .	他在追求富人 。
and lo and behold , look what happened .	看看發生了什麼事 。
the people who believed in the wright brothers' dream worked with them with blood and sweat and tears .	相信萊特兄弟的夢想 , 和他們一起流血、汗水和淚水的人合作 。
the others just worked for the paycheck .	其他人只是為了支付而工作 。
and they tell stories of how every time the wright brothers went out , they would have to take five sets of parts , because that's how many times they would crash before they came in for supper .	他們會說故事 , 每當萊特兄弟出門時 , 他們就得要採取五組零件 , 因為那是他們在供應商前會墜多少次 。
and , eventually , on december 17th , 1903 , the wright brothers took flight , and no one was there to even experience it .	最終 , 在1903年12月17日 , 萊特兄弟飛行 , 甚至沒有人去那裡去體驗它 。
we found out about it a few days later .	幾天後 , 我們發現了 。
and further proof that langley was motivated by the wrong thing: the day the wright brothers took flight , he quit .	更進一步的證據證明雷格利的動機是錯誤的:萊特兄弟飛行的那天 , 他辭掉了 。
he could have said , " that's an amazing discovery , guys , and i will improve upon your technology , " but he didn't .	他可能會說: 「 那是很棒的發現 , 各位 , 我會改善你們的科技 。 」 但他沒有 。
he wasn't first , he didn't get rich , he didn't get famous so he quit .	他不是第一個 , 他沒有富人 , 他沒有得到有名的 , 所以他放棄了 。
people don't buy what you do ; they buy why you do it .	人們不買你做的事 ; 他們買你為什麼做 。
and if you talk about what you believe , you will attract those who believe what you believe .	如果你談到你所相信的 , 你會吸引那些相信你所相信的人 。
but why is it important to attract those who believe what you believe ?	但為什麼吸引那些相信你所相信的人是很重要的 ?
something called the law of diffusion of innovation , and if you don't know the law , you definitely know the terminology .	一個叫做創新的擴散法則 , 如果你不知道法律 , 你絕對知道術語 。
the first two and a half percent of our population are our innovators .	前兩個半數的人口是我們的創新者 。
the next 13 and a half percent of our population are our early adopters .	接下來的13.5%的人口是我們的早期採用者 。
the next 34 percent are your early majority , your late majority and your laggards .	接下來的34%是你最早的大多數 , 你的大多數和你的拉格 。
the only reason these people buy touch tone phones is because you can't buy rotary phones anymore .	人們購買接觸電話的唯一理由是你不能再買不起老舊手機了 。
we all sit at various places at various times on this scale , but what the law of diffusion of innovation tells us is that if you want massmarket success or massmarket acceptance of an idea , you cannot have it until you achieve this tipping point between 15 and 18 percent market penetration , and then the system tips .	我們都坐在這個規模不同的地方 , 但創新的散播法則告訴我們 , 如果你想要大眾市場成功或大眾市場接受一個想法 , 你就不能直到你達成這個臨界點 , 直到你達成了15%到18%的市場滲透率 , 接著 , 系統就要做到了 。
and i love asking businesses , " what's your conversion on new business ? "	我喜歡問企業: 「 你對新生意的轉換是什麼 ? 」
and they love to tell you , " oh , it's about 10 percent , " proudly .	他們很自豪地告訴你: 「 喔 , 大概是10% 。 」
well , you can trip over 10 percent of the customers .	嗯 , 你可以試試超過百分之十的顧客 。
we all have about 10 percent who just " get it . "	我們都有大約10%的人 「 懂 」 。
that's how we describe them , right ?	這就是我們如何描述它們 , 對吧 ?
that's like that gut feeling , " oh , they just get it . "	那就像是那種直覺感覺: 「 喔 , 他們就懂了 。 」
the problem is: how do you find the ones that get it before you're doing business with them versus the ones who don't get it ?	問題是:如何在你和他們做生意之前 , 找到他們 , 而不是那些不懂的人 ?
so it's this here , this little gap that you have to close , as jeffrey moore calls it , " crossing the chasm " because , you see , the early majority will not try something until someone else has tried it first .	這裡是這個 , 你必須關閉的這個小缺口 , 就像jeffreymoore所說的 , 「 跨越混亂 」 一樣 , 因為 , 你看 , 早期大多數人不會嘗試 , 直到別人先試過它 。
and these guys , the innovators and the early adopters , they're comfortable making those gut decisions .	這些人 , 創新者和早期的採用者 , 他們很舒服做出這些直覺決策 。
they're more comfortable making those intuitive decisions that are driven by what they believe about the world and not just what product is available .	他們更舒服地做出那些被他們所相信的世界所驅使的直覺決策 , 而不僅僅是產品可用的 。
these are the people who stood in line for six hours to buy an iphone when they first came out , when you could have just walked into the store the next week and bought one off the shelf .	這些人排隊排隊六小時買iphone , 當他們第一次出櫃時 , 你只要走進商店 , 下週就可以買下一架 。
these are the people who spent 40 , 000 dollars on flat screen tvs when they first came out , even though the technology was substandard .	這些人花了四萬美金在平面的電視上 , 他們剛剛出櫃 , 儘管這項技術很替代 。
and , by the way , they didn't do it because the technology was so great ; they did it for themselves .	順便一提 , 他們並沒有這麼做 , 因為這項技術太棒了 , 他們為自己做這件事 。
it's because they wanted to be first .	因為他們想要成為第一 。
people don't buy what you do ; they buy why you do it and what you do simply proves what you believe .	人們不買你所做的事 ; 他們買你為什麼做的事 , 以及你所做的事 , 證明了你所相信的事 。
in fact , people will do the things that prove what they believe .	事實上 , 人們會做一些證明他們所相信的事 。
the reason that person bought the iphone in the first six hours , stood in line for six hours , was because of what they believed about the world , and how they wanted everybody to see them: they were first .	一個人在前六小時買iphone的理由 , 排行六個小時 , 是因為他們對這個世界的信念 , 以及他們對每個人的看法:他們是第一個 。
people don't buy what you do ; they buy why you do it .	人們不買你做的事 ; 他們買你為什麼做 。
so let me give you a famous example , a famous failure and a famous success of the law of diffusion of innovation .	讓我舉個有名的例子 , 一個有名的失敗和一個有名的成功 , 來說明創新的散播法則 。
first , the famous failure .	首先 , 著名的失敗 。
it's a commercial example .	這是個商業的例子 。
as we said before , a second ago , the recipe for success is money and the right people and the right market conditions , right ? you should have success then .	正如我們之前所說的 , 第二 , 成功的配方是金錢、對的人、對的市場條件 , 對吧 ? 你應該要成功 。
from the time tivo came out about eight or nine years ago to this current day , they are the single highestquality product on the market , hands down , there is no dispute .	從八、九年前到今天 , tivo的時代 , 到目前為止 , 他們是市場上最高品質的產品 , 手上也沒有爭議 。
they were extremely wellfunded .	他們非常有資格 。
market conditions were fantastic .	市場狀況很棒 。
i mean , we use tivo as verb .	我的意思是 , 我們把tivo當作動詞 。
i tivo stuff on my piece of junk time warner dvr all the time .	我隨時都在我的垃圾時間華納dvr上 。
but tivo's a commercial failure .	但tivo是一個商業的失敗 。
they've never made money .	他們從來沒有賺到錢 。
and when they went ipo , their stock was at about 30 or 40 dollars and then plummeted , and it's never traded above 10 .	當他們去ipo時 , 他們的股票大約是30到40元 , 然後倒了 , 從來沒有在10歲以上交易 。
in fact , i don't think it's even traded above six , except for a couple of little spikes .	事實上 , 我不認為在六歲以上交易 , 只不過有幾個小尖刺 。
because you see , when tivo launched their product they told us all what they had .	因為你看 , 當tivo推出他們的產品 , 他們告訴我們他們所擁有的一切 。
they said , " we have a product that pauses live tv , skips commercials , rewinds live tv and memorizes your viewing habits without you even asking . "	他們說: 「 我們有一個暫停現場電視的產品 , 跳過廣告 , 重播現場電視 , 記住你的觀點習慣 , 甚至沒有你問 。 」
and the cynical majority said , " we don't believe you .	憤世嫉俗的多數人說: 「 我們不相信你 。
we don't need it . we don't like it .	我們不需要它 , 我們不喜歡它 。
you're scaring us . "	你害怕我們 。 」
what if they had said , " if you're the kind of person who likes to have total control over every aspect of your life , boy , do we have a product for you .	如果他們說: 「 如果你是那種想要完全掌控你人生的各個層面的人 , 男孩 , 我們有產品給你 。
it pauses live tv , skips commercials , memorizes your viewing habits , etc . , etc . "	它會暫停現場電視 , 跳過廣告 , 記住你的觀點習慣 , 等等 。 」
people don't buy what you do ; they buy why you do it , and what you do simply serves as the proof of what you believe .	人們不買你做什麼 ; 他們買你為什麼做它 , 而你所做的僅僅是證明你所相信的事 。
now let me give you a successful example of the law of diffusion of innovation .	讓我舉個成功的例子 , 說明創新的擴散法則 。
in the summer of 1963 , 250 , 000 people showed up on the mall in washington to hear dr . king speak .	1963年夏天 , 有二十五萬人出現在華盛頓的購物中心 , 聽到金恩博士演說 。
they sent out no invitations , and there was no website to check the date .	他們發出沒有邀請 , 也沒有網站來檢查約會 。
how do you do that ?	要怎麼做呢 ?
well , dr . king wasn't the only man in america who was a great orator .	金恩博士不是美國唯一一個偉大的演說家 。
he wasn't the only man in america who suffered in a precivil rights america .	他不是美國唯一受過處於普通的美國人 。
in fact , some of his ideas were bad .	事實上 , 他的一些想法很糟 。
but he had a gift .	但他有一個禮物 。
he didn't go around telling people what needed to change in america .	他沒有到處告訴人們在美國需要什麼改變 。
he went around and told people what he believed .	他四處走 , 告訴大家他所相信的 。
" i believe , i believe , i believe , " he told people .	「 我相信 , 我相信 , 我相信 , 」 他告訴人們 。
and people who believed what he believed took his cause , and they made it their own , and they told people .	相信他所相信的 , 那些相信他的理念的人 , 並且他們自己化了 , 他們告訴人們 。
and some of those people created structures to get the word out to even more people .	其中一些人創造了結構 , 讓更多人知道這個字 。
and lo and behold , 250 , 000 people showed up on the right day at the right time to hear him speak .	你看 , 25 , 000人在正確的日子中出現 , 聽到他演講的對象 。
how many of them showed up for him ?	有多少人為他出席 ?
they showed up for themselves .	他們為了自己而出 。
it's what they believed about america that got them to travel in a bus for eight hours to stand in the sun in washington in the middle of august .	他們相信美國能讓他們在巴士旅行八小時的路上 , 站在華盛頓8月中間 。
it's what they believed , and it wasn't about black versus white: 25 percent of the audience was white .	這是他們所相信的 , 重點不是黑人對白人:25%的觀眾是白人 。
dr . king believed that there are two types of laws in this world: those that are made by a higher authority and those that are made by man .	金恩博士相信世界上有兩種法律:那些由高權威制定的法律 , 那些由人所制定的法律 。
and not until all the laws that are made by man are consistent with the laws that are made by the higher authority will we live in a just world .	直到人類所制定的所有法則都和較高權威制定的法律一致 , 我們生活在一個公平的世界 。
it just so happened that the civil rights movement was the perfect thing to help him bring his cause to life .	剛好就是民權運動是幫助他終生的完美 。
we followed , not for him , but for ourselves .	我們追隨了 , 不是為了他 , 而是為了我們自己 。
and , by the way , he gave the " i have a dream " speech , not the " i have a plan " speech .	順便說一下 , 他給了 「 我有一個夢想 」 演講 , 而不是 「 我有一個計劃 」 。
listen to politicians now , with their comprehensive 12point plans .	現在 , 聽政治人物 , 用他們全身的12點計畫來聽聽 。
they're not inspiring anybody .	他們沒有鼓舞任何人 。
because there are leaders and there are those who lead .	因為有領導者 , 也有領導者 。
leaders hold a position of power or authority , but those who lead inspire us .	領導者持有權力或權威的立場 , 但那些領導人鼓舞我們的人 。
whether they're individuals or organizations , we follow those who lead , not because we have to , but because we want to .	不論是個人或組織 , 我們追隨領導的人 , 不是因為我們必須這麼做 , 而是因為我們想要 。
we follow those who lead , not for them , but for ourselves .	我們追隨那些領導的人 , 不是為了他們 , 而是為了我們自己 。
and it's those who start with " why " that have the ability to inspire those around them or find others who inspire them .	就是那些從 「 為什麼 」 開始的人 , 能夠鼓舞他們身邊的人 , 或找到啟發他們的人 。
how do you remember where you parked your car ? how do you know if you're moving in the right direction ? neuroscientist neil burgess studies the neural mechanisms that map the space around us , and how they link to memory and imagination .	你如何記得你在哪兒停車 ? 你怎麼知道你是不是在正確的方向 ? 神經科學家neilburges研究我們周遭的神經機制 , 以及它們如何連結記憶和想像力 。
brain , cognitive science , exploration , neuroscience , science	大腦、認知科學、探索、神經科學、科學、科學、科學 。
neil burgess: how your brain tells you where you are	neilburgeges:你的大腦如何告訴你你在哪裡 。
when we park in a big parking lot , how do we remember where we parked our car ?	當我們在一個大停車場停車場時 , 我們要如何記得停車位在哪裡 ?
here's the problem facing homer .	這是面對荷馬的問題 。
and we're going to try to understand what's happening in his brain .	我們會試著了解他的大腦裡發生了什麼事 。
so we'll start with the hippocampus , shown in yellow , which is the organ of memory .	我們先從海馬體開始 , 黃色的就是記憶的器官 。
if you have damage there , like in alzheimer's , you can't remember things including where you parked your car .	如果你有損傷 , 像阿茲海默那樣 , 你就無法記起一些事情 , 包括你停在車子的位置 。
it's named after latin for " seahorse , " which it resembles .	它是以拉丁文為名的 , 它是以拉丁文為名的 , 它是相似的 。
and like the rest of the brain , it's made of neurons .	就像大腦的其餘部分 , 它是由神經元組成 。
so the human brain has about a hundred billion neurons in it .	人類的大腦有大約一千億個神經元 。
and the neurons communicate with each other by sending little pulses or spikes of electricity via connections to each other .	神經元互相溝通 , 藉由發送小脈衝或發送電訊號 , 通過互相連結 。
the hippocampus is formed of two sheets of cells , which are very densely interconnected .	海馬體是由兩種細胞組成 , 非常緊密的相互連結 。
and scientists have begun to understand how spatial memory works by recording from individual neurons in rats or mice while they forage or explore an environment looking for food .	科學家開始了解空間記憶是如何運作的 , 藉由記錄老鼠或老鼠在覓食或探索環境尋找食物的個別神經元 。
so we're going to imagine we're recording from a single neuron in the hippocampus of this rat here .	我們將會想像我們正在從這隻老鼠的海馬體中錄下一個神經元 。
and when it fires a little spike of electricity , there's going to be a red dot and a click .	當它開啟一點電力衝動時 , 會有紅點和點擊 。
so what we see is that this neuron knows whenever the rat has gone into one particular place in its environment .	我們看到的是 , 每當老鼠進入某個特定的環境時 , 這種神經元就會知道 。
and it signals to the rest of the brain by sending a little electrical spike .	它訊號到大腦的其他部位 , 只要發送一個小小的電衝動 。
so we could show the firing rate of that neuron as a function of the animal's location .	所以 , 我們可以把神經元發射的速度呈現成動物的位置 。
and if we record from lots of different neurons , we'll see that different neurons fire when the animal goes in different parts of its environment , like in this square box shown here .	如果我們從許多不同的神經元中記錄下來 , 我們會發現 , 當動物進入環境的不同部位時 , 會產生不同的神經元發射 , 就像這裡的這個方塊 。
so together they form a map for the rest of the brain , telling the brain continually , " where am i now within my environment ? "	所以 , 它們一起組成了一張大腦的地圖 , 不斷地告訴大腦: 「 我現在在我的環境中在哪裡 ? 」
place cells are also being recorded in humans .	位置細胞也被人類記錄下來 。
so epilepsy patients sometimes need the electrical activity in their brain monitoring .	所以癲癇病人有時候需要腦部監控的電活動 。
and some of these patients played a video game where they drive around a small town .	有些病人玩了一場電玩遊戲 , 他們在一個小鎮附近開車 。
and place cells in their hippocampi would fire , become active , start sending electrical impulses whenever they drove through a particular location in that town .	當他們開車穿過某個特定的地點時 , 會開始發送電脈衝 。
so how does a place cell know where the rat or person is within its environment ?	所以 , 一個地方細胞如何知道老鼠或人在其環境中的位置 ?
well these two cells here show us that the boundaries of the environment are particularly important .	這兩個細胞告訴我們 , 環境的界線特別重要 。
so the one on the top likes to fire sort of midway between the walls of the box that their rat's in .	最上方的這個 , 像是在老鼠的牆壁中發火一樣 。
and when you expand the box , the firing location expands .	當你拓展盒子時 , 發射地點會擴張 。
the one below likes to fire whenever there's a wall close by to the south .	下面的那一面 , 每當有一面牆接近南方時 , 都會發出一面牆 。
and if you put another wall inside the box , then the cell fires in both place wherever there's a wall to the south as the animal explores around in its box .	如果你把另一面牆放在盒子裡 , 細胞會在任何一個地方發射一面牆到南邊 , 當動物在盒子裡四處探索時 。
so this predicts that sensing the distances and directions of boundaries around you extended buildings and so on is particularly important for the hippocampus .	因此 , 這個預測會感應你周圍的界線和界線 , 延伸建築物的距離和方向 , 對於海馬體來說 , 特別重要 。
and indeed , on the inputs to the hippocampus , cells are found which project into the hippocampus , which do respond exactly to detecting boundaries or edges at particular distances and directions from the rat or mouse as it's exploring around .	事實上 , 在海馬體輸入的資料中 , 細胞會發現海馬體的專案 , 它會根據特定距離來偵測海馬體的邊界或邊緣 , 特別是從老鼠或老鼠的探測到的方向 。
so the cell on the left , you can see , it fires whenever the animal gets near to a wall or a boundary to the east , whether it's the edge or the wall of a square box or the circular wall of the circular box or even the drop at the edge of a table , which the animals are running around .	左邊的細胞 , 你可以看到 , 每當動物靠近牆壁時 , 它就會發出火焰 , 不論是方形盒子的邊緣 , 或圓形的圍牆 , 或甚至桌邊的滴 , 動物都在跑 。
and the cell on the right there fires whenever there's a boundary to the south , whether it's the drop at the edge of the table or a wall or even the gap between two tables that are pulled apart .	右邊的細胞每當有邊界到南邊 , 不論是桌子的邊緣或牆壁 , 或甚至兩張桌子之間的鴻溝 。
so that's one way in which we think place cells determine where the animal is as it's exploring around .	這是我們認為位置細胞的一種方式 , 決定動物在周圍探索的位置 。
we can also test where we think objects are , like this goal flag , in simple environments or indeed , where your car would be .	我們也可以測試我們認為物體在哪裡 , 比如這個目標 , 在簡單的環境中 , 或在車子的位置 。
so we can have people explore an environment and see the location they have to remember .	所以我們可以讓人們去探索一個環境 , 看看他們需要記得的位置 。
and then , if we put them back in the environment , generally they're quite good at putting a marker down where they thought that flag or their car was .	接著 , 如果我們把它們放回環境中 , 通常它們都很擅長把標記放在他們認為旗幟或車的位置 。
but on some trials , we could change the shape and size of the environment like we did with the place cell .	但在一些試驗中 , 我們可以改變環境的形狀和大小 , 就像我們用安置細胞所做的一樣 。
in that case , we can see how where they think the flag had been changes as a function of how you change the shape and size of the environment .	在這個案例中 , 我們可以看到他們認為旗幟是如何改變環境的形狀和大小 。
and what you see , for example , if the flag was where that cross was in a small square environment , and then if you ask people where it was , but you've made the environment bigger , where they think the flag had been stretches out in exactly the same way that the place cell firing stretched out .	舉例來說 , 你看到的旗幟是在一個小平方的環境中 , 然後如果你問人們在哪裡 , 但你讓環境更大 , 他們認為旗幟在哪裡被伸展 , 完全相同的地方細胞激發的方式 。
it's as if you remember where the flag was by storing the pattern of firing across all of your place cells at that location , and then you can get back to that location by moving around so that you best match the current pattern of firing of your place cells with that stored pattern .	彷彿你還記得旗幟的位置 , 藉由儲存你所有位置細胞的模式 , 然後你就可以回到那個位置 , 這樣你就可以找到最好的位置 , 配合你儲存的位置細胞的模式 。
that guides you back to the location that you want to remember .	那會引導你回到你想要記住的位置 。
but we also know where we are through movement .	但我們也知道我們透過運動來做什麼 。
so if we take some outbound path perhaps we park and we wander off we know because our own movements , which we can integrate over this path roughly what the heading direction is to go back .	所以如果我們採取一些外觀的路徑 , 也許我們停車 , 我們知道 , 因為我們自己的運動 , 我們可以整合這條路 , 走向的路徑 , 走回去 。
and place cells also get this kind of path integration input from a kind of cell called a grid cell .	位置細胞也會得到這種路徑整合 , 來自一種叫做格狀細胞的細胞 。
now grid cells are found , again , on the inputs to the hippocampus , and they're a bit like place cells .	同樣的 , 網格細胞在海馬體輸入的輸入上 , 它們有點像個地方細胞 。
but now as the rat explores around , each individual cell fires in a whole array of different locations which are laid out across the environment in an amazingly regular triangular grid .	但當老鼠四處探索時 , 每個個體細胞會發射一系列不同的位置 , 這些位置在整個環境中 , 以驚人的三角形格向外延伸 。
and if you record from several grid cells shown here in different colors each one has a gridlike firing pattern across the environment , and each cell's gridlike firing pattern is shifted slightly relative to the other cells .	如果你從幾條電網中記錄到這裡的不同顏色 , 每個細胞都有像網格般的旋轉圖案 , 每個細胞的電網圖案都和其他細胞有稍微的關係 。
so the red one fires on this grid and the green one on this one and the blue on on this one .	紅色的這條格子上有紅色 , 綠色的這一條 , 藍色在這上面 。
so together , it's as if the rat can put a virtual grid of firing locations across its environment a bit like the latitude and longitude lines that you'd find on a map , but using triangles .	所以 , 這就像老鼠可以把虛擬的位置放到它的周圍 , 就像你在地圖上找到的緯度和長度線一樣 , 但用三角形 。
and as it moves around , the electrical activity can pass from one of these cells to the next cell to keep track of where it is , so that it can use its own movements to know where it is in its environment .	當它移動時 , 電子活動可以從其中一個細胞傳遞到下一個細胞 , 持續追蹤它所在的位置 , 這樣它就可以用它自己的移動來知道它在環境的位置 。
do people have grid cells ?	人們有電網細胞嗎 ?
well because all of the gridlike firing patterns have the same axes of symmetry , the same orientations of grid , shown in orange here , it means that the net activity of all of the grid cells in a particular part of the brain should change according to whether we're running along these six directions or running along one of the six directions in between .	因為所有的電網圖案都有相同的對稱軸線 , 橘色代表的是所有電網在某個區域的網格活動 , 應該根據我們在這些六個方向進行改變 , 或在中間的六個方向進行相同的對應 。
so we can put people in an mri scanner and have them do a little video game like the one i showed you and look for this signal .	所以 , 我們可以把人放進核磁共振掃描儀中 , 讓他們做個小遊戲 , 就像我剛才展示的一樣 , 尋找這個信號 。
and indeed , you do see it in the human entorhinal cortex , which is the same part of the brain that you see grid cells in rats .	的確 , 你的確在人腦中看到的 , 和老鼠身上看到的電網細胞一樣 。
so back to homer .	回到荷馬 。
he's probably remembering where his car was in terms of the distances and directions to extended buildings and boundaries around the location where he parked .	他可能還記得車子的距離和方向 , 來延伸建築物和界線 , 在他停車的地方 。
and that would be represented by the firing of boundarydetecting cells .	那會被邊界偵測細胞的爆炸所代表 。
he's also remembering the path he took out of the car park , which would be represented in the firing of grid cells .	他還記得他從車子公園走出的路徑 , 路徑會被代表在電網細胞的發射中 。
now both of these kinds of cells can make the place cells fire .	現在這兩種細胞都可以製造地點細胞 。
and he can return to the location where he parked by moving so as to find where it is that best matches the firing pattern of the place cells in his brain currently with the stored pattern where he parked his car .	他可以回到他在移動的位置 , 找到最好的位置 , 配對大腦中的位置細胞的激發模式 , 目前他用儲存的模式 , 把他的車子停在位置上 。
and that guides him back to that location irrespective of visual cues like whether his car's actually there .	那引導他回到那個視覺暗示的位置 , 像他的車真的在那兒 。
maybe it's been towed .	或許它已經被拖延了 。
but he knows where it was , so he knows to go and get it .	但他知道它在哪裡 , 所以他知道要去找它 。
so beyond spatial memory , if we look for this gridlike firing pattern throughout the whole brain , we see it in a whole series of locations which are always active when we do all kinds of autobiographical memory tasks , like remembering the last time you went to a wedding , for example .	所以 , 除了空間記憶之外 , 如果我們在整個大腦中尋找這種網格激發的模式 , 我們會在一系列的位置上看到 , 當我們做各式各樣的自傳記憶任務時 , 總是活躍起來 , 比如 , 記得你上次去婚禮的時候 。
so it may be that the neural mechanisms for representing the space around us are also used for generating visual imagery so that we can recreate the spatial scene , at least , of the events that have happened to us when we want to imagine them .	所以 , 可能是因為我們周遭的神經機制也被用來產生視覺影像 , 這樣我們就可以重建空間場景 , 至少 , 當我們想想像它們時發生的事件 。
