so if this was happening , your memories could start by place cells activating each other via these dense interconnections and then reactivating boundary cells to create the spatial structure of the scene around your viewpoint .	所以 , 如果這發生了 , 你的記憶可以從細胞間的密度互相啟動 , 然後再次啟動邊界細胞 , 創造出你觀點周圍的空間結構 。
and grid cells could move this viewpoint through that space .	網格細胞可以在這個空間中移動這個觀點 。
another kind of cell , head direction cells , which i didn't mention yet , they fire like a compass according to which way you're facing .	另外一種細胞 , 頭部方向細胞 , 我還沒提到 , 它們像同一個指針一樣 , 根據你正在面對的方向 。
they could define the viewing direction from which you want to generate an image for your visual imagery , so you can imagine what happened when you were at this wedding , for example .	他們可以定義你想要創造視覺影像的方向 , 例如你在婚禮上時 , 會發生什麼事 。
so this is just one example of a new era really in cognitive neuroscience where we're beginning to understand psychological processes like how you remember or imagine or even think in terms of the actions of the billions of individual neurons that make up our brains .	這只是一個新的認知神經科學領域的一個例子 , 我們開始了解心理的過程 , 比如你如何記住、想像 , 甚至在數十億個獨立神經元的行動中思考 。
thank you very much .	謝謝大家 。
imagine a global security driven by collaboration among agencies , government , the private sector and the public . that's not just the distant hope of opensource fans , it's the vision of james stavridis , the supreme commander of nato , who shares vivid moments from recent military history to explain why security of the future should be built with bridges rather than walls .	想像一個全球安全驅動力是由政府部門、政府、私營部門和公共事業所驅動 。 這不僅僅是開放源碼粉絲的遠景 , 也是納米斯•史塔維迪斯的最高指揮官 , 他與最近的軍事歷史有著遠見的時光 , 來解釋為何未來的安全性應該要與橋樑建立起來 , 而不是牆壁 。
collaboration , global issues , opensource , peace , politics , social media , violence , war	合作、全球議題、開放資源、和平、政治、社交媒體、暴力、戰爭、戰爭、戰爭、開放、開放、資源、和平、政治、政治、政治、社交媒體、社交媒體、暴力、暴力、暴力、
james stavridis: how nato's supreme commander thinks about global security	詹姆斯•斯特里迪斯:娜塔斯•史托夫•斯多德對全球安全的看法有多大的看法 。
i'm gonna talk a little bit about opensource security , because we've got to get better at security in this 21st century .	我將要談談開放原始碼安全 , 因為在21世紀 , 我們必須更加安全 。
let me start by saying , let's look back to the 20th century , and kind of get a sense of how that style of security worked for us .	首先 , 讓我們回顧一下20世紀 , 關於安全的運作方式 。
this is verdun , a battlefield in france just north of the nato headquarters in belgium .	這是verdun , 一個在法國的戰場 , 位在比利時總部的北方 。
at verdun , in 1916 , over a 300day period , 700 , 000 people were killed , so about 2 , 000 a day .	1916年 , 在verdun , 超過300天的時間 , 70萬人被殺 , 每天大約2000人死亡 。
if you roll it forward 20thcentury security into the second world war , you see the battle of stalingrad , 300 days , 2 million people killed .	如果你把它往前推進二次世界大戰 , 你會看到史達林升三百天的戰役 , 兩百萬人死亡 。
we go into the cold war , and we continue to try and build walls .	我們進入冷戰 , 繼續嘗試建造牆壁 。
we go from the trench warfare of the first world war to the maginot line of the second world war , and then we go into the cold war , the iron curtain , the berlin wall .	我們從第一次世界大戰開始到第二次世界大戰的馬吉尼線 , 然後我們進入冷戰 , 鐵幕 , 柏林牆 。
my thesis for us today is , instead of building walls to create security , we need to build bridges .	我今天的論點是 , 與其建設安全 , 我們不需要建造橋樑 。
this is a famous bridge in europe .	這是歐洲有名的橋 。
it's the bridge over the drina river , the subject of a novel by ivo andrić , and it talks about how , in that very troubled part of europe and the balkans , over time there's been enormous building of walls .	這座橋跨越了戲劇的河流 , 一座小說的主題是伊佛•安德里•安德里 , 它談到 , 在歐洲和巴爾幹非常麻煩的地區 , 經過一段時間 , 已經有很大的牆壁 。
more recently , in the last decade , we begin to see these communities start , hesitatingly , to come together .	最近 , 在過去十年 , 我們開始看到這些社區開始 , 猶豫地團結在一起 。
i would argue , again , opensource security is about connecting the international , the interagency , the privatepublic , and lashing it together with strategic communication , largely in social networks .	我認為 , 同樣的 , 開放原始碼的安全是要把國際網路、國際網路、私人公開的連結在一起 , 並用策略性的溝通 , 大多是在社交網路上 。
so let me talk a little bit about why we need to do that , because our global commons is under attack in a variety of ways , and none of the sources of threat to the global commons will be solved by building walls .	所以 , 讓我來談談為什麼我們需要這樣做 , 因為全球公有物在各方面受到攻擊 , 沒有威脅到全球公有物的來源會被建築牆壁所解決 。
now , i'm a sailor , obviously .	很明顯 , 我是水手 。
this is a ship , a liner , clipping through the indian ocean .	這是一艘船 , 一條線 , 穿過印度洋 。
what's wrong with this picture ?	這張照片有什麼問題 ?
it's got concertina wire along the sides of it .	它沿著它的邊緣有著音樂廳的電線 。
that's to prevent pirates from attacking it .	這是為了防止海盜攻擊 。
piracy is a very active threat today around the world . this is in the indian ocean .	海盜現在是世界上非常活躍的威脅 。 這是在印度洋 。
piracy is also very active in the strait of malacca .	海盜也非常活躍於馬拉加海峽 。
it's active in the gulf of guinea .	它位於幾內亞海灣 。
we see it in the caribbean .	我們在加勒比海看到它 。
it's a $10billionayear discontinuity in the global transport system .	在全球運輸系統中 , 它是10億美元的不連續性 。
last year , at this time , there were 20 vessels , 500 mariners held hostage .	去年 , 在這個時代有20艘船 , 500名海軍陸戰隊主持人 。
this is an attack on the global commons .	這是對全球公有物的攻擊 。
we need to think about how to address it .	我們需要考慮如何處理它 。
let's shift to a different kind of sea , the cyber sea .	讓我們轉移到另一種海洋 , 網路海 。
here are photographs of two young men .	這裡有兩個年輕人的照片 。
at the moment , they're incarcerated .	此刻 , 他們被監禁了 。
they conducted a credit card fraud that netted them over 10 billion dollars .	他們做了一張信用卡詐欺 , 把他們推出超過一百億美金 。
this is part of cybercrime which is a $2trillionayear discontinuity in the global economy .	這是網路犯罪的一部分 , 在全球經濟中 , 是2兆美元的連續性 。
two trillion a year .	一年兩兆美元 。
that's just under the gdp of great britain .	這只是英國的國內生產總值 。
so this cyber sea , which we know endlessly is the fundamental piece of radical openness , is very much under threat as well .	所以這個網路海 , 我們知道無止境是徹底的開放 , 也受到威脅 。
another thing i worry about in the global commons is the threat posed by trafficking , by the movement of narcotics , opium , here coming out of afghanistan through europe over to the united states .	在全球公有物中 , 我擔心的另一件事 , 是人口販賣、毒品、鴉片的運動 , 來自阿富汗 , 從歐洲到美國 。
we worry about cocaine coming from the andean ridge north .	我們擔心來自安地斯山脊的可卡因 。
we worry about the movement of illegal weapons and trafficking . above all , perhaps , we worry about human trafficking , and the awful cost of it .	我們擔心非法武器的運動 , 最重要的是 , 我們擔心人口販賣 , 以及它的成本 。
trafficking moves largely at sea but in other parts of the global commons .	人口販賣運動在海上 , 但在全球公有物的其他地方 。
this is a photograph , and i wish i could tell you that this is a very hightech piece of us navy gear that we're using to stop the trafficking .	這是一張照片 , 我希望我能告訴你們這是一塊非常高科技的我們用海軍船隻來阻止人口販賣 。
the bad news is , this is a semisubmersible run by drug cartels .	壞消息是 , 這是一個由毒品卡特爾負責的半發行者 。
it was built in the jungles of south america .	它是在南美的叢林建造的 。
we caught it with that lowtech raft — — and it was carrying six tons of cocaine .	我們用那低科技的火車抓住它 , 它帶著六噸的古柯鹼 。
crew of four . sophisticated communications sweep .	四個 , 精密的溝通 。
this kind of trafficking , in narcotics , in humans , in weapons , god forbid , in weapons of mass destruction , is part of the threat to the global commons .	這種販賣毒品 , 在人體、武器、上帝禁止大規模毀滅的武器中 , 是對全球公有物的威脅的一部分 。
and let's pull it together in afghanistan today .	今天我們一起在阿富汗 。
this is a field of poppies in afghanistan .	這是阿富汗的一塊餅乾 。
eighty to 90 percent of the world's poppy , opium and heroin , comes out of afghanistan .	世界上有百分之八十到九十的餅乾、鴉片和海洛因來自阿富汗 。
we also see there , of course , terrorism .	當然 , 我們也看到恐怖主義 。
this is where al qaeda is staged from .	這就是基地組織所在的地方 。
we also see a very strong insurgency embedded there .	我們也看到其中一個非常強烈的暴動 。
so this terrorism concern is also part of the global commons , and what we must address .	所以 , 這種恐怖主義的關注也是全球公有物的一部分 , 我們必須解決的問題 。
so here we are , 21st century .	這裡是21世紀 。
we know our 20thcentury tools are not going to work .	我們知道我們20世紀的工具不會成功 。
what should we do ?	我們該怎麼做 ?
i would argue that we will not deliver security solely from the barrel of a gun .	我認為我們不會只從槍的桶子上遞送安全 。
we will not deliver security solely from the barrel of a gun .	我們不會只從槍的桶子上遞送安全 。
we will need the application of military force .	我們需要軍事力量的應用 。
when we do it , we must do it well , and competently .	當我們這樣做時 , 我們必須要做得很好 , 而且要有競爭力 。
but my thesis is , opensource security is about international , interagency , privatepublic connection pulled together by this idea of strategic communication on the internet .	但我的論點是 , 開放資源安全是國際、國際、私人公共的聯繫 , 由網路上的策略通訊的概念結合在一起 。
let me give you a couple of examples of how this works in a positive way .	讓我舉幾個例子來說明這是如何運作的 。
this is afghanistan . these are afghan soldiers .	這是阿富汗 。 這些是阿富汗士兵 。
they are all holding books .	他們都是拿著書 。
you should say , " that's odd . i thought i read that this demographic , young men and women in their 20s and 30s , is largely illiterate in afghanistan . "	你應該說: 「 這很奇怪 。 我想我讀到 , 人口統計學 , 二十、三十歲的年輕男女 , 大部分都是在阿富汗的文盲 。 」
you would be correct .	你會是正確的 。
eightyfive percent cannot read when they enter the security forces of afghanistan .	當他們進入阿富汗安全部隊時 , 85%無法閱讀 。
why ? because the taliban withheld education during the period of time in which these men and women would have learned to read .	為什麼 ? 因為塔利班長期在這些男人和女人都學會閱讀 。
so the question is , so , why are they all standing there holding books ?	所以問題是 , 為什麼他們都站在那裡拿著書 ?
the answer is , we are teaching them to read in literacy courses by nato in partnership with private sector entities , in partnership with development agencies .	答案是 , 我們在教導他們讀書 , 透過nato和私人企業合作 , 和發展機構合作 。
we've taught well over 200 , 000 afghan security forces to read and write at a basic level .	我們教過超過二十萬阿富汗安全部隊閱讀和寫在基本的層面 。
when you can read and write in afghanistan , you will typically put a pen in your pocket .	當你在阿富汗讀書時 , 你通常會把筆放在你的口袋裡 。
at the ceremonies , when these young men and women graduate , they take that pen with great pride , and put it in their pocket .	在儀式裡 , 當這些年輕男女畢業時 , 他們把筆拿到很高的驕傲的筆子 , 把它放在口袋裡 。
this is bringing together international — there are 50 nations involved in this mission — interagency — these development agencies — and privatepublic , to take on this kind of security .	這就把國際組織結合起來 , 有五十個國家涉及到這個任務──國際發展機構──以及私人公共事務 , 來處理這種安全 。
now , we are also teaching them combat skills , of course , but i would argue , opensource security means connecting in ways that create longer lasting security effect .	當然 , 我們也在教他們戰鬥技巧 , 但我認為 , 開放原始碼安全意味著將更長久的安全聯繫起來 , 產生更長的安全效應 。
this is a us navy warship .	這是美國海軍戰艦 。
it's called the comfort .	它叫做舒適感 。
there's a sister ship called the mercy .	有一艘叫做慈悲的姐妹船 。
they are hospital ships .	他們是醫院的船隻 。
this one , the comfort , operates throughout the caribbean and the coast of south america conducting patient treatments .	這個 , 舒適 , 在加勒比海和南美洲的海岸進行病人治療 。
on a typical cruise , they'll do 400 , 000 patient treatments .	在典型的路易斯 , 他們會做四十萬人的治療 。
it is crewed not strictly by military but by a combination of humanitarian organizations: operation hope , project smile .	它並不是由軍方組織所組成 , 而是由人道主義組織組成:營運希望、微笑 。
other organizations send volunteers .	其他組織發送志願者 。
interagency physicians come out .	外科醫生出來了 。
they're all part of this .	他們都是這方面的一部分 。
to give you one example of the impact this can have , this little boy , eight years old , walked with his mother two days to come to the eye clinic put on by the comfort .	舉個例子 , 這個小男孩 , 八歲 , 帶著他的母親走了兩天 , 來到舒適的眼科診所 。
when he was fitted , over his extremely myopic eyes , he suddenly looked up and said , " mama , veo el mundo . "	當他穿著極端的眼睛時 , 他突然抬頭說: 「 媽媽 , 維歐•埃爾普羅 。 」
" mom , i see the world . "	「 媽 , 我看到這個世界 。 」
multiply this by 400 , 000 patient treatments , this privatepublic collaboration with security forces , and you begin to see the power of creating security in a very different way .	乘以四十萬人的治療 , 這種私人的公開合作 , 和安全局合作 , 你開始以非常不同的方式 , 開始看到創造安全的力量 。
here you see baseball players .	這裡你看到棒球選手 。
can you pick out the two us army soldiers in this photograph ?	你能從這張照片中挑出兩位美國軍人嗎 ?
they are the two young men on either side of these young boys . this is part of a series of baseball clinics , where we have explored collaboration between major league baseball , the department of state , who sets up the diplomatic piece of this , military baseball players , who are real soldiers with real skills but participate in this mission , and they put on clinics throughout latin america and the caribbean , in honduras , in nicaragua , in all of the central american and caribbean nations where baseball is so popular , and it creates security .	他們是這兩位年輕男孩兩邊的年輕男孩 。 這是一系列的棒球診所的一部分 , 我們在南加拉大聯盟棒球、國務院、軍隊棒球選手 , 他們是真正的戰士 , 但參與這個任務 , 他們在全美各地和加勒比海 , 在全美洲和加勒比海 , 在全美的宏都加勒比地區 , 創造了保險 。
it shows role models to young men and women about fitness and about life that i would argue help create security for us .	它呈現給年輕人的典範 , 關於健身及生活的典範 , 讓我爭論能為我們創造安全 。
another aspect of this partnership is in disaster relief .	另一方面 , 這種合作關係是鬆了一口氣 。
this is a us air force helicopter participating after the tsunami in 2004 which killed 250 , 000 people .	這是美國空軍直升機 , 在2004年海嘯後進行 , 殺死了25萬人 。
in each of these major disasters — the tsunami in 2004 , 250 , 000 dead , the kashmiri earthquake in pakistan , 2005 , 85 , 000 dead , the haitian earthquake , about 300 , 000 dead , more recently the awful earthquaketsunami combination which struck japan and its nuclear industry — in all of these instances , we see partnerships between international actors , interagency , privatepublic working with security forces to respond to this kind of natural disaster .	在這些重大災難中 , 海嘯在2004年、25萬人死亡 , 2005年巴基斯坦的kamiri地震 , 8萬5千人死去 , 海地地震近來了大約30萬人死亡 , 更近期是日本和其核子產業 , 在所有這些例子中 , 我們看到了國際演員、國際關係、私人合作合作 , 和這種災難 。
so these are examples of this idea of opensource security .	這些是開放資源安全的例子 。
we tie it together , increasingly , by doing things like this .	我們將它連接起來 , 越來越像這樣做 。
now , you're looking at this thinking , " ah , admiral , these must be sea lanes of communication , or these might be fiber optic cables . "	各位現在看到的是這個想法: 「 啊 , 阿富汗 , 這些必定是溝通的海道 , 或這些可能是光纖電纜 。 」
no . this is a graphic of the world according to twitter .	不 。 這是根據推特 , 世界的圖像 。
purple are tweets . green are geolocation .	紫色是推特 , 綠色是地理分配 。
white is the synthesis .	白色是合成 。
it's a perfect evocation of that great population survey , the six largest nations in the world in descending order: china , india , facebook , the united states , twitter and indonesia .	它是大人口調查的完美驅動 , 全世界有六大國以下訂單:中國、印度、臉書、美國、推特和印尼 。
why do we want to get in these nets ?	為什麼我們要進入這些蚊帳 ?
why do we want to be involved ?	為什麼我們要參與 ?
we talked earlier about the arab spring , and the power of all this .	我們先前談到阿拉伯之春 , 以及這一切的力量 。
i'll give you another example , and it's how you move this message .	我再舉另一個例子 , 你如何移動這個訊息 。
i gave a talk like this in london a while back about this point . i said , as i say to all of you , i'm on facebook . friend me .	我在倫敦發表了一場這樣的演講 。 正如我對你們說的 , 我在facebook上 , 朋友們 。
got a little laugh from the audience .	聽眾大笑 。
there was an article which was run by ap , on the wire .	有一篇文章是以ap來經營 。
got picked up in two places in the world: finland and indonesia .	世界上有兩個地方被撿起來:芬蘭和印尼 。
the headline was: nato admiral needs friends .	頭條是:北約的需求需要朋友 。
and the story was a catalyst , and the next morning i had hundreds of facebook friend requests from indonesians and finns , mostly saying , " admiral , we heard you need a friend , and oh , by the way , what is nato ? "	故事是催化劑 , 隔天早上 , 我有數百名來自印尼人和芬蘭人的朋友請求 , 大多是說: 「 農業 , 我們聽說你需要朋友 , 順帶一提 , 哪些是nato ? 」
yeah , we laugh , but this is how we move the message , and moving that message is how we connect international , interagency , privatepublic , and these social nets to help create security .	是的 , 我們笑了 , 但這就是我們如何傳達訊息 , 移動訊息就是我們如何連結國際、國際間、私人的、以及這些社交網絡 , 來協助創造安全 。
now , let me hit a somber note .	現在 , 讓我按下11月的音 。
this is a photograph of a brave british soldier .	這是一張勇敢的英國士兵的照片 。
he's in the scots guards .	他在蘇格蘭警衛裡 。
he's standing the watch in helmand , in southern afghanistan .	他站在阿富汗南部的helmand中 。
i put him here to remind us , i would not want anyone to leave the room thinking that we do not need capable , competent militaries who can create real military effect .	我讓他來這裡提醒我們 , 我不希望任何人離開房間 , 認為我們不需要有能力、有能力的軍隊 , 能夠創造出真正的軍事效應 。
that is the core of who we are and what we do , and we do it to protect freedom , freedom of speech , all the things we treasure in our societies .	這就是我們的核心 , 以及我們所做的事 , 來保護自由、言論自由 , 所有我們在社會中珍惜的東西 。
but , you know , life is not an onandoff switch .	但 , 你知道的 , 生命不是一個徹底的開關 。
you don't have to have a military that is either in hard combat or is in the barracks .	你不需要軍隊 , 要不就在戰鬥中 , 要不就在戰場上 。
i would argue life is a rheostat .	我想說的是 , 生命是場災難 。
you have to dial it in , and as i think about how we create security in this 21st century , there will be times when we will apply hard power in true war and crisis , but there will be many instances , as we've talked about today , where our militaries can be part of creating 21stcentury security , international , interagency , privatepublic , connected with competent communication .	你必須調整它 , 正如我在思考我們如何在21世紀建立安全性 , 將會有時候當我們將在真正的戰爭和危機中使用硬力時 , 會有很多例子 , 如我們今天所說的 , 我們的軍隊可以成為創造21世紀安全、國際、國際、國際、私人公開 , 與互相溝通聯繫 。
i would close by saying that we heard earlier today about wikipedia . i use wikipedia all the time to look up facts , and as all of you appreciate , wikipedia is not created by 12 brilliant people locked in a room writing articles .	最後我會說我們今天早些時候聽到維基百科 。 我常常用維基百科來查事實 , 就像你們所欣賞的 , 維基百科並不是由十二位傑出的人鎖在一個房間寫文章 。
wikipedia , every day , is tens of thousands of people inputting information , and every day millions of people withdrawing that information .	維基百科每天都有成千上萬的人輸入信息 , 每天有數百萬人承受這些信息 。
it's a perfect image for the fundamental point that no one of us is as smart as all of us thinking together .	對根本的觀點而言 , 沒有人像我們所有人一樣聰明 。
no one person , no one alliance , no one nation , no one of us is as smart as all of us thinking together .	沒有一個人 , 沒有一個聯盟 , 沒有一個國家 , 我們沒有一個人像我們所有人一樣聰明 。
the vision statement of wikipedia is very simple: a world in which every human being can freely share in the sum of all knowledge .	維基百科的視覺陳述非常簡單:一個每個人都可以自由地分享的世界 。
my thesis for you is that by combining international , interagency , privatepublic , strategic communication , together , in this 21st century , we can create the sum of all security .	我的論點是 , 透過結合國際、國際、私人的、策略性的溝通 , 在21世紀 , 我們就能創造所有安全的總和 。
thank you very much . thank you . thank you .	非常謝謝 。 謝謝 。
